FR-PR26: Coping selection: high controllability invokes problem-focused coping (plan to change the world); low controllability invokes emotion-focused coping (shift attention, re-appraise, adjust desirability) - with the coping strategy menu of Section 3.11 and the guard that emotion-focused coping may never deny safety-critical facts.

FR-PR26: Appraisals update as the causal interpretation changes; intensity decays over time.

Predicates: pai_appraise/3, pai_cope_select/3.

AC-PR26-001: Given a blocked objective appraised with low controllability, when coping runs, then an emotion-focused strategy is applied and the objective's desirability or priority is adjusted rather than a new plan spawned.

Difficulty: Moderate.

DEP-PR13.


PR 27 - Motivational Modulation (Psi)

Purpose: let urges modulate HOW the whole mind runs, not just what it pursues, and define emotions as regions in modulator space.

FR-PR27: Needs span three categories: physiological (the body's homeostatic variables), cognitive (competence, certainty, exploration), and social (affiliation signals where bodies provide them).

FR-PR27: A global modulator bus (pai_modulator/2) carries three dials read by every actor: arousal, execution speed, and resolution (depth and breadth of processing); strong urgent need raises arousal and speed and narrows resolution; calm lowers arousal and widens resolution.

FR-PR27: A motive is an urge bound to a goal, appetitive or aversive; affective states are named regions in modulator space (pai_affect_region/2), not separate modules.

FR-PR27: Conflicting needs blend their modulation rather than switching abruptly; extreme arousal is clamped so resolution never collapses to zero; modulators decay toward baseline; cognitive needs can drive behavior when physiological needs are satisfied (this is PR 23's curiosity entering the same bus).

Predicates: pai_modulator/2, pai_affect_region/2, pai_motive/3.

AC-PR27-001: Given a battery urge spike, when modulators update, then arousal and speed rise, resolution narrows, and daydream_actor's budget shrinks for that interval.

Difficulty: Moderate.

DEP-PR13, DEP-PR23.


PR 28 - Time-Linear Language (Database Semantics)

Purpose: process language as a stream, one word at a time in arrival order, with one record type supporting hearing, thinking, and speaking.

FR-PR28: Each word's contribution becomes a word_trace: a flat, non-recursive record with a core value and continuation pointers to related word_traces; word_traces sharing a core value are stored in one token line in time-linear arrival order inside a word_bank scope of the Lattice; storage is append-only (sediment), never edited.

FR-PR28: Hearer mode (pai_hear/2) builds content by setting pointers between word_traces as words arrive; ambiguous attachments resolve by compatibility conditions; unknown words are admitted as new word_traces; missing referents leave pointers unbound for later resolution.

FR-PR28: Think mode (pai_think_path/3) navigates word_trace to word_trace along semantic relations, deriving new content by inference; indexicals (I, you, here, now) resolve against the current context parameters (space, time, agent, recipient).

FR-PR28: Speaker mode (pai_speak/2) uses a think-mode navigation as the production plan, emitting surfaces word by word.

Predicates: pai_hear/2, pai_think_path/3, pai_speak/2, pai_word_trace/3.

AC-PR28-001: Given the heard sequence julia is working, when pai_think_path is asked from julia, then a path julia to working exists, and pai_speak over that path emits a grammatical surface.

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR04, DEP-PR31.


PR 29 - Belief Structures and Propagators

Purpose: give every node_fact a scorecard so deciders choose with numbers.

FR-PR29: A belief record per node_fact, per scope and zone, tracks: certainty, coherence (local constraint satisfaction), likelihood, desirability, valence, arousal, and per-action attempt and success counts.

FR-PR29: Propagator specialists (diffuser variants) keep beliefs current: arousal from objective urgency, desirability from objective salience, coherence from local constraint satisfaction over neighbors, likelihood from reliability statistics; dyads receive mirrored negative values where appropriate.

FR-PR29: Updates are incremental and local; global recomputation is forbidden in steady state (global coherence is computationally intractable); occasional scheduled recalculation of old node_facts corrects ordering bias; priors are defined so first-attempt ratios never divide by zero.

FR-PR29: Consumers: deliberation (utility), attention and PR 18 salience, the consolidation forgetting score, and PR 21's evidence truth (which stores its frequency and confidence in this record).

Predicates: pai_belief/3, pai_belief_update/3.

AC-PR29-001: Given a node_fact whose neighbors all support it, when the coherence propagator runs, then its coherence exceeds that of a node_fact with contradicting neighbors.

Difficulty: Moderate to Hard.

DEP-PR04, DEP-PR21.


PR 30 - Perceptual Detector Suite

Purpose: complete the perception front end: specialist detectors that pull structure out of raw percepts, plus place and map building.

FR-PR30: Each detector accepts a percept reference (for example a one-second clip), extracts its kind of features, matches against known features, stores novelties, and returns trait lists: icon_detector (known images), geon_detector (volumetric primitives), shape_detector, object_detector, scene_detector, and image schema detectors (spatial arrangements such as inside, on, beside, path - already bootstrap relations).

FR-PR30: The scene_detector blacks out the foveal center and hashes the background four ways (average, perceptual, difference, and wavelet hashes), using the hash coordinates as facets for matching.

FR-PR30: A locator attaches scenes to venues and venues to locales; a mapper maintains locales within places, areas, regions, and maps, merging venues by scene similarity rather than trusting raw odometry (drift guard); detectors begin tabula rasa where specified, learning their feature inventories from experience.

FR-PR30: Detector disagreement is not an error: all traits are stored and later coordination resolves or tolerates them; concurrent label requests yield one identifier (the lexer insert is a critical section).

Predicates: pai_detect/3, pai_locate/2, pai_map_update/2.

AC-PR30-001: Given two percepts of the same scene from slightly different positions, when the locator runs, then both attach to one venue (merged by scene similarity).

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR04, DEP-PR10.


PR 31 - Developmental Language Acquisition

Purpose: acquire language bottom-up with the same machinery as everything else: sounds chain into words, words ground to experience, and the same chaining repeats up the tiers.

FR-PR31: Phoneme percepts activated in series are linked by tandem relations; branching transitions become choices; categories over them yield word-formation rules (the tandem, series, choice, and category bootstrap relations carry this).

FR-PR31: Words ground to coincident percepts via the existing pai_ground/3 so meanings attach to experience; words heard before their referents persist ungrounded, ready to ground later; homophones carry context in their choice gates for phrase-tier disambiguation.

FR-PR31: The same chaining reapplies one tier up: phrases, then events, then episodes, then scenarios (prototype_actor), frames (frame_actor), lessons, themes, and maxims (maxim_actor); symbolisms and metaphors form where a signifier in present_zone repeatedly evokes a signified in recalled_zone or imagined_zone (metaphor_actor).

FR-PR31: This pipeline runs entirely on the coordination specialist roster (Section 3.11) over the Lattice - language is acquired by the same machinery as everything else, which is the deep point.

Predicates: pai_chain_promote/2, pai_ground/3 (existing), pai_symbolize/3.

AC-PR31-001: Given repeated phoneme series for one word co-occurring with one percept, when the pipeline runs, then a grounded word node_fact exists linking the series to the percept.

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR04, DEP-PR30, with PR 28 as its stream-processing counterpart.


PR 32 - The Attention Economy (ECAN Adaptation)

Purpose: upgrade activation from timestamps-plus-deltas to a full economic attention allocation system, adapting Economic Attention Networks (ECAN) from the OpenCog lineage.

Background definitions: ECAN manages cognition's scarcest resources - processor time and memory - with two currencies per knowledge unit: short-term importance (STI), governing who gets processor attention now, and long-term importance (LTI), governing who keeps occupying memory; atoms earn wages when they prove useful, pay rent for the space they occupy, and spread importance to their associates.

FR-PR32: Every node_fact carries two attention values in a dedicated value channel (Section 3.1): sti (short-term importance) and lti (long-term importance).

FR-PR32: Wages - when a node_fact participates in a successful outcome (a confirmed plan, a fired sentinel that helped, a broadcast-winning coalition, a fulfilled prediction), the attention banker actor credits sti and lti wages proportional to its contribution.

FR-PR32: Rent - on each banker cycle, every node_fact with nonzero attention pays rent (a decay), so importance falls without fresh usefulness; rent runs alongside the activation-window machinery, and kindle_node and quench_node post sti credits and debits respectively.

FR-PR32: Spreading - node_facts spread a fraction of sti to neighbors linked by co-activation association (the Hebbian-style links the linkers already build), so attention flows along learned associations.

FR-PR32: Economic forgetting - the consolidation forgetting sub-pattern (sona_crystallize) SHALL use lti as its primary eviction score: lowest lti is forgotten first, protected flags still inviolable.

FR-PR32: Integration - PR 18 salience consumes sti as an input; PR 21 budgets and the attention economy are reconciled: budgets govern tasks, attention governs knowledge, and the banker converts between them at a configured exchange policy.

FR-PR32: The economy is conserved within configured bounds: total currency in circulation is capped, so attention is genuinely scarce and runaway-importance positive feedback is structurally impossible.

FR-PR32: Before the attention banker's propagation rules are finalized, a prototype compiled onto Constraint Handling Rules (CHR) - the committed-choice forward-chaining rule language already shipped inside the embedded engine - is built and benchmarked, and the bespoke design proceeds only if it beats the CHR prototype on the PR 2 harness measures.

Predicates: pai_attention/3, pai_wage/3, pai_attention_spread/2, pai_attention_metrics/1.

AC-PR32-001: Given two node_facts where one repeatedly contributes to confirmed plans and one never does, when 100 banker cycles run, then the contributor's lti exceeds the idle one's, and under memory pressure the idle one is evicted first.

AC-PR32-002: Given total circulation capped at N units, when wages are paid, then the sum of all sti and lti plus the banker reserve still equals N.

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR04, DEP-PR18, DEP-PR21, DEP-PR29.


PR 33 - Gradual Lattice Types

Purpose: let the mind declare, check, and reason about the types of its own knowledge, gradually - adopted from MeTTa's types-as-atoms-in-the-space design.

FR-PR33: A type declaration is itself a node_fact (relation type_of: subject, type), so types live in the Lattice, are queryable, are learnable (the categorizer specialist MAY induce them), and are themselves typed.

FR-PR33: Typing is gradual: untyped node_facts are always legal; a type_checker actor (off by default, hot-startable) validates typed node_facts and arguments against declarations.

FR-PR33: A violation never crashes anything: the checker inscribes an ill_typed contradiction node_fact (feeding compensation and coping), and the offending structure remains in place for diagnosis.

FR-PR33: Function-style relations MAY declare argument and result types; the chainer (PR 34) and deliberation use type declarations to prune nonsensical candidate inferences and plans early.

FR-PR33: The checker leverages the engine where possible: SWI-Prolog's must_be and dialect type-checking facilities serve as the primitive layer.

Predicates: pai_type_declare/2, pai_type_of/2, pai_type_check/2.

AC-PR33-001: Given type_of(battery_level, number) declared, when a node_fact asserts battery_level with a text argument and the checker runs, then an ill_typed node_fact exists naming the violation, and the system continues running.

Difficulty: Moderate.

DEP-PR04, DEP-PR13.


PR 34 - The Generic Chainer and Meta-Reasoning

Purpose: provide one inference engine - a chainer - that runs forward (from facts toward consequences) and backward (from goals toward support), parameterized by rule bases stored in the Lattice, with its own control policies also stored in the Lattice so the mind can reason about how it reasons.

Background: this adapts the meta-reasoning chaining approach presented for MeTTa at the Conference on Artificial Intelligence and Theorem Proving (AITP) 2024: the chainer is generic; what varies is the rule base (logical rules, causal rules, type rules, analogy schemas) and the control knowledge (which rule to try first, when to stop, what to cache).

FR-PR34: pai_chain(Direction, RuleBase, Start, Result, Options) runs the chainer: Direction is forward or backward; RuleBase names a set of rewrite-rule node_facts (PR 35) or clause references; Options carry the PR 21 budget.

FR-PR34: Backward chaining maps onto the engine's native resolution wherever the rule base is clause-shaped (the unforked engine IS a backward chainer - no reimplementation); forward chaining builds on the sentinel machinery; the chainer's contribution is the uniform interface, the budgeting, and the control layer.

FR-PR34: Inference control knowledge - rule priorities, learned heuristics about which rules pay off in which contexts, caching policies - is stored as control node_facts in the Lattice, updated by regulation from inference outcomes: meta-reasoning, with the refiner (PR 17) free to propose control edits through the constitutional pipeline.

FR-PR34: The reasoner-flavored specialists (Section 3.11, theory_actor and companions) and the thinking experiments of Part 9 (projection, explanation, backcasting, hindcasting) are reorganized as chainer clients: each supplies a rule base and direction rather than its own engine.

FR-PR34: Every chained conclusion records provenance: rule base, rules fired, depth, and budget spent (feeding PR 29 coherence and the introspection trace of Section 3.15).

Predicates: pai_chain/5, pai_rule_base/2, pai_control_policy/3.

AC-PR34-001: Given a causal rule base and a goal state, when pai_chain is run backward within budget, then a chain from current situation to goal is returned with full provenance, or no_chain with the frontier reached.

AC-PR34-002: Given two control policies for one rule base, when 50 mixed problems run under each, then regulation updates the policies' reliability statistics and the chainer prefers the better-performing policy thereafter.

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR15, DEP-PR21, DEP-PR35.


PR 35 - Lattice-Resident Rewrite Rules and the Minimal PrologAI Kernel

Purpose: adopt knowledge-as-code rewrite rules living in the knowledge store (from Reflective Metagraph Rewriting), and a small formal operational semantics defining a compliant implementation (from Meta-MeTTa).

Half 1 - Rewrite rules in the Lattice.

FR-PR35: A rewrite rule is a node_fact (relation rewrites_to: pattern, template, guard) - the PrologAI counterpart of a MeTTa equality atom; an interpreter actor evaluates expressions against the active rule set by unify-substitute-repeat.

FR-PR35: Because rules are node_facts, they carry value channels (attention, reliability, provenance), are queryable and learnable, can be proposed by the refiner (PR 17) and synthesized by the model synthesizer (PR 22), and pass the constitutional pipeline before activation - the reflective foundation with safety preserved.

FR-PR35: Rule sets are scoped: a rewrite rule belongs to a scope and zone, so simulation can try candidate rules in possible_zone without touching live behavior.

Half 2 - The Minimal PrologAI Kernel.

FR-PR35: The .pai language of PR 1 SHALL be given a formal operational semantics: an algebra of states (a grammar of kernel states - the active expression, its bindings, its scope and zone context, and the Lattice - together with a structural congruence) and a small set of labeled transition rules covering: evaluate one step, evaluate in a named scope context, chain a result into a template, unify with success and failure continuations, construct and deconstruct expressions, enter and return from a function frame, and collect or offer nondeterministic alternatives.

FR-PR35: The kernel document is normative: an implementation of PrologAI is compliant if and only if its observable evaluations are derivable from the kernel rules - the specification serving the role the Java Virtual Machine specification serves.

FR-PR35: The reference realization maps kernel transitions onto the unforked engine (unify is unification; the alternatives rules are backtracking; function frames are calls) so compliance costs no fork - the kernel is a specification layer, not a new interpreter, although a strict tiny interpreter MAY be built for verification testing.

Predicates: pai_rewrite_rule/4, pai_interpret/3, pai_kernel_trace/2.

AC-PR35-001: Given a rewrite rule set defining factorial in the Lattice, when pai_interpret evaluates factorial of five, then 120 is returned and pai_kernel_trace yields a derivation using only kernel transition rules.

AC-PR35-002: Given the same .pai program run on the reference realization and on the strict verification interpreter, then observable results agree.

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR01, DEP-PR04, DEP-PR17.


PR 36 - The Hyperon Interoperability Bridge

Purpose: let PrologAI minds and Hyperon systems exchange knowledge - the two closest projects in this field should be able to talk.

FR-PR36: A bidirectional mapping is defined: an Atomese expression maps to a node_fact whose Relation is the expression head and whose Arguments are the mapped children; symbols map to atoms' names through the lexicon; variables map to Prolog variables; grounded atoms map to grounded node_facts (Section 3.1); Hyperon values map to value channels (Section 3.1).

FR-PR36: Import and export: pai_atomese_import/3 reads MeTTa source or an Atomspace export into a chosen scope; pai_atomese_export/3 writes a scope out as MeTTa source.

FR-PR36: A MeTTa space MAY be mounted as a foreign nexus (read-through query, optional write-through) via the MCP Gateway or a direct adapter in prologai-core, budgeted and sandbox-quarantined like any external source: imported knowledge lands in a quarantine scope until normal coordination promotes it.

FR-PR36: Round-trip fidelity: export of an imported scope reproduces the original expressions up to variable renaming.

Predicates: pai_atomese_import/3, pai_atomese_export/3, pai_space_mount/3.

AC-PR36-001: Given a MeTTa file declaring ten expressions, when imported and re-exported, then the round trip preserves all ten up to alpha renaming.

Difficulty: Moderate to Hard.

DEP-PR02, DEP-PR14, DEP-PR35.


PR 37 - The Clause Induction Pattern (Inductive Logic Programming)

Purpose: give the mind the ability to learn genuinely NEW relational structure - new clauses, new recursive competences, new rewrite rules - from its own examples, using inductive logic programming (ILP) natively on the embedded engine; Piagetian accommodation made algorithmic.

Background definitions: ILP learns logic programs from positive examples, negative examples, and background knowledge; meta-interpretive learning (Metagol style) drives induction through a Prolog meta-interpreter and can invent auxiliary predicates and learn recursion; learning from failures (Popper style) generates a candidate hypothesis, tests it on the engine against the examples, and converts each failure into constraints that prune the remaining hypothesis space.

FR-PR37-001: An induction_actor SHALL harvest example sets from the Lattice: positive examples from confirmed outcomes (regulation's confirmations, attained_zone content) and negative examples from disconfirmations (surprises and shocks), each example a ground node_fact with provenance.

FR-PR37-002: Background knowledge for each induction run SHALL be drawn from the bootstrap relations plus a scoped selection of existing causal_plans and rewrite rules, with the PR 21 budget bounding hypothesis search.

FR-PR37-003: The learner SHALL implement the learn-from-failures loop: generate a candidate clause set within a declared hypothesis space (maximum clauses, maximum literals, allowed relations); test it by calling the candidate directly on the embedded engine against all examples; on failure, derive generalization or specialization constraints from the failure kind (a candidate entailing a negative example yields a specialization constraint; one failing a positive example yields a generalization constraint); add the constraints and repeat until a consistent hypothesis or budget exhaustion.

FR-PR37-004: Meta-interpretive mode SHALL be available for recursive targets: induction through metarules (declared second-order clause templates), with predicate invention permitted and invented predicates entering the lexicon as ordinary relations marked invented.

FR-PR37-005: Every induced hypothesis SHALL pass the constitutional RSI pipeline (Section 3.15: propose, sandbox-evaluate against held-out trajectories in possible_zone, constitutional check, commit) before activation as a live causal_plan or rewrite rule (PR 35); reliability tracking then belongs to regulation like any other competence.

FR-PR37-006: Learned failure constraints SHALL be stored as inference control node_facts for the generic chainer (PR 34), so the cost of failed induction is converted into permanent search guidance.

FR-PR37-007: Induced programs SHALL record their examples, metarules or hypothesis-space declaration, and search statistics as provenance, making every learned rule auditable by a human.

Predicates: pai_induce/5 (Examples, Background, HypothesisSpace, Budget, Hypothesis), pai_metarule_declare/2, pai_induction_examples/3.

AC-PR37-001: Given ten positive and ten negative examples of a two-clause target relation expressible in the declared space, when pai_induce runs within budget, then a hypothesis consistent with all examples is returned with full provenance.

AC-PR37-002: Given an induction run that fails on budget, when the chainer next searches a related space, then the stored failure constraints measurably prune its candidate set (verified by search statistics).

AC-PR37-003: Given an induced hypothesis that violates a constitutional principle in sandbox evaluation, then it is rejected and the live system is unchanged.

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR11, DEP-PR17, DEP-PR21, DEP-PR34, DEP-PR35.


PR 38 - Compositional Vector Binding (Vector Symbolic Architectures)

Purpose: let the vector memory represent STRUCTURE, not just similarity, by adopting Vector Symbolic Architecture (VSA) operations - the bridge between the symbolic Lattice and the vector backend.

Background definitions: in a VSA (also called hyperdimensional computing), symbols are high-dimensional vectors; BINDING (for example circular convolution, as in Holographic Reduced Representations) combines a role vector and a filler vector into one vector from which either can be recovered by UNBINDING (circular correlation) plus a cleanup lookup; BUNDLING (vector addition) superposes several bound pairs into one vector representing the whole structure.

FR-PR38-001: The embedding provider (PR 16) SHALL offer a compositional mode: the vector of a compound node_fact is computed by binding each argument's vector to its role vector and bundling the results with the relation's vector, rather than (or in addition to) embedding surface text.

FR-PR38-002: Unbinding queries SHALL be supported: given a compound's vector and a role, return the nearest clean filler vectors (a cleanup memory over the lexicon's vectors), enabling structure-sensitive similarity search - find situations whose AGENT is similar to this one, not merely situations that are similar overall.

FR-PR38-003: The implementation SHALL live in prologai-core with at least two interchangeable algebras (Holographic Reduced Representations and one alternative such as multiply-add-permute), selected by configuration and benchmarked on the PR 2 harness; the torchhd library's model catalogue is the reference for correctness testing.

FR-PR38-004: Dyads and seams interact coherently: the antithesis vector is a declared transform of the thesis vector, and seam connectors (Section 3.1) MAY carry role vectors so connector matching has a vector-side counterpart.

Predicates: pai_bind/3, pai_unbind/3, pai_bundle/2, pai_cleanup/3.

AC-PR38-001: Given compound node_facts give(alice, book, bob) and give(bob, book, alice) embedded compositionally, then their whole-structure vectors differ substantially, while unbinding OBJECT from each returns book.

AC-PR38-002: Given a structure-sensitive query (situations whose INSTRUMENT unbinds near watering_can), then precision against a labeled test set exceeds the same query run on surface-text embeddings.

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR02, DEP-PR16.


PR 39 - Reference Frames and Voting Consensus (the Thousand Brains Pattern)

Purpose: adopt the Thousand Brains theory's two architectural exports: knowledge anchored in reference frames, and consensus by voting among many semi-independent models.

Background: the Thousand Brains Project's Monty system is built from repeating learning modules modeled on cortical columns; each module learns complete object models in spatially structured REFERENCE FRAMES, estimates and effects movement, and communicates with other modules hierarchically and non-hierarchically through a cortical messaging protocol, reaching consensus by VOTING; the theory holds that reference frames serve concepts at every abstraction level, not only spatial objects.

FR-PR39-001: A reference_frame is a new scope subtype in which member node_facts carry coordinates (via pins) relative to the frame's origin and axes; frames are first-class node_facts and may be nested (an object frame within a place frame within a map frame, reusing the PR 30 locator and mapper outputs).

FR-PR39-002: Movement is a frame primitive: pai_frame_move/3 advances a point of attention through a frame (physically, by issuing body commands, or mentally, by traversing coordinates in imagination), and perception SHALL tag incoming features with frame-relative locations when a frame is active - learning object models as feature-at-location associations.

FR-PR39-003: Abstract frames are explicitly supported: conceptual spaces (for example a taxonomy distance frame, a timeline frame, a value-tradeoff frame) declare their axes, and reasoning operations MAY be expressed as movements in such frames, fulfilling the theory's claim that all concepts live in reference frames.

FR-PR39-004: Voting consensus: a voting_actor SHALL collect the concurrent conclusions of multiple specialists or frames about one entity (object identity, situation classification, plan choice), each vote weighted by the voter's reliability and current evidence confidence (PR 21), and inscribe the consensus through the existing vote merge type (Section 3.1), with dissent recorded rather than erased - many columns, one consensus, minority reports preserved.

FR-PR39-005: Frame learning is associative and fast (one-shot anchoring of a feature at a location, Hebbian-style), with consolidation handling later compression - matching Monty's rapid associative learning discipline.

Predicates: pai_frame_create/3, pai_frame_anchor/4, pai_frame_move/3, pai_vote/4.

AC-PR39-001: Given two observation passes over a simulated object from different approach paths, when frame learning runs, then both passes anchor features into ONE object frame (location-consistent), and a third partial observation retrieves the object by frame match.

AC-PR39-002: Given three specialists classifying one percept with conflicting conclusions at differing confidences, when voting_actor runs, then a consensus node_fact exists with weighted tally and preserved dissent records.

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR04, DEP-PR29, DEP-PR30.


PR 40 - Justified Defeasible Reasoning (s(CASP))

Purpose: give the mind rigorous commonsense reasoning with defaults and exceptions, where every conclusion carries a human-readable justification - serving both the chainer and the constitution's transparency principle.

Background: s(CASP) is goal-directed answer set programming - top-down, without grounding - shipped as a package for the embedded engine; it handles non-monotonic negation, defaults, and exceptions, and produces a proof tree for every answer renderable as a natural-language justification.

FR-PR40-001: A defeasible rule base is a declared rule-base flavor for the generic chainer (PR 34): rules MAY carry default conditions and exception clauses with answer-set semantics, evaluated through the s(CASP) engine.

FR-PR40-002: Every defeasible conclusion SHALL carry its justification tree as a provenance value, and pai_justify/2 SHALL render it as readable text - feeding pai_introspection_trace and the constitutional reason-giving of Section 3.16 (vetoes and permissions cite justifications, not just rule identifiers).

FR-PR40-003: Defeasible and classical rule bases coexist: the chainer selects semantics per rule base, and conclusions record which semantics produced them.

Predicates: pai_defeasible_rule/3, pai_justify/2.

AC-PR40-001: Given rules "birds fly by default" and "penguins are birds that do not fly" with a penguin fact, when the chainer queries flight, then the answer is no with a justification tree naming the exception, rendered readably.

Difficulty: Moderate to Hard.

DEP-PR34.


PR 41 - The Distribution Semantics Probabilistic Layer (ProbLog and PITA)

Purpose: put the probabilistic predicates on a rigorous foundation: the distribution semantics of probabilistic logic programming.

Background: under the distribution semantics, probabilistic facts carry probabilities and a program defines a distribution over possible worlds; systems in the ProbLog and PITA lineage compute query probabilities exactly via knowledge compilation (binary decision diagrams) or approximately by sampling, with compact explanation structures - and PITA-style implementations compile to Prolog.

FR-PR41-001: A node_fact MAY be declared probabilistic with a probability in its evidence channel; a probabilistic rule base is a chainer flavor whose query answers are probabilities with explanation structures.

FR-PR41-002: pai_prob_query/3 SHALL return the probability of a query and its explanation set (the worlds or proofs supporting it), with exact computation when tractable within budget and sampling otherwise (the budget from PR 21 governs).

FR-PR41-003: The pai_bayes predicate family (Section 3.15) SHALL be re-specified as the user-facing interface to this layer, and PR 21's frequency-and-confidence evidence values SHALL be the default source of fact probabilities, reconciled by a documented mapping.

Predicates: pai_prob_fact/2, pai_prob_query/3.

AC-PR41-001: Given probabilistic facts rain (0.3) and sprinkler (0.5) with the standard wet-grass rules, when pai_prob_query computes wet_grass, then the returned probability matches the analytically correct value within tolerance, with an explanation set.

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR21, DEP-PR34.


PR 42 - The Attention Schema and the Formal Workspace Correspondence

Purpose: give the mind a model of its own attention (attention schema theory), and tie the workspace cycle to a formal model of consciousness (the Conscious Turing Machine) with testable correspondence.

Background: attention schema theory (Graziano) proposes that awareness is the brain's simplified, controllable MODEL of its own attention, used to predict and steer it; the Conscious Turing Machine (Blum and Blum) is a formal model - short-term memory stage, competing long-term-memory processors, an explicit up-tree competition, global broadcast - whose account of the feeling of consciousness aligns with the attention schema.

FR-PR42-001: An attention_schema scope SHALL be maintained by meta_control_actor: a simplified running model of the workspace's own dynamics - recent winners, suppressed coalitions, habituation state, and a short-horizon prediction of what is likely to win next.

FR-PR42-002: The schema SHALL be usable for control: deliberation and the refiner MAY consult it to pre-empt unwanted capture (raising guard salience), to schedule demanding work for predicted quiet cycles, and to explain attention history in introspection traces.

FR-PR42-003: Correspondence program: the PR 18 cycle SHALL be documented in correspondence with the Conscious Turing Machine - competition function, broadcast, processor set - and CTM-derived behavioral tests SHALL be added to the Part 0.10 proof strategies (alongside the consciousness-indicator coverage reporting of PR 12), making PrologAI's consciousness-related claims formally anchored and falsifiable.

FR-PR42-004: The schema is a model, not the mechanism: corrupting or disabling the schema SHALL degrade prediction and control of attention without halting the workspace cycle itself - and this dissociation is itself a specified test, mirroring the theory's clinical signature.

Predicates: pai_attention_schema/2, pai_attention_predict/2.

AC-PR42-001: Given thirty workspace cycles, when the schema's next-winner predictions are scored, then accuracy exceeds a chance baseline computed from coalition counts.

AC-PR42-002: Given the schema disabled, when an urgent percept and a pinned task compete, then workspace function continues but pre-emptive guarding measurably degrades - the predicted dissociation.

Difficulty: Moderate to Hard.

DEP-PR18, DEP-PR13.


PR 43 - Agent Interoperability Expansion (A2A and Durable Agent Mail)

Purpose: let PrologAI minds participate in the emerging society of agents: speak the Agent2Agent protocol alongside MCP, and exchange durable mail with minds that are not simultaneously awake.

Background: the Agent2Agent (A2A) protocol - now under Linux Foundation stewardship - standardizes inter-agent collaboration among opaque agents: an AGENT CARD (a JSON metadata document declaring identity, capabilities, skills, endpoint, and authentication), stateful TASKS with a defined lifecycle, MESSAGES with role-tagged parts, and ARTIFACTS as outputs, explicitly without exposing internal state, memory, or tools.

FR-PR43-001: The gateway (PR 14) SHALL additionally serve A2A: publish an agent card generated from the mind's enrolled capabilities and configured disclosure policy; accept and issue A2A tasks mapped to objectives (inbound tasks become objective node_facts routed through motivation and the constitutional screen; outbound tasks are dispatched, tracked through the A2A lifecycle, and their artifacts land in a quarantine scope exactly as PR 36 imports do).

FR-PR43-002: Opacity is preserved both ways: the agent card discloses capabilities, never Lattice contents; inbound agents receive task results, never direct queries against the mind's memory.

FR-PR43-003: Durable agent mail: pai_peer_mail_send/3 and pai_peer_mail_fetch/3 provide addressed, persistent mailboxes hosted by the Mind Server, so minds in different sessions exchange messages asynchronously; mail is inscribed to the recipient's quarantine scope on fetch.

FR-PR43-004: The companion protocols (ACP and ANP) have stabilized and are promoted from the research track to production work packages PR 47 (ACP Gateway) and PR 48 (ANP Gateway) respectively; the gateway's protocol layer SHALL be structured so adding a protocol is registration, not redesign.

Predicates: pai_agent_card/1, pai_a2a_task/4, pai_peer_mail_send/3, pai_peer_mail_fetch/3.

AC-PR43-001: Given two PrologAI minds on one Mind Server, when mind A sends an A2A task to mind B requesting a garden forecast, then B's motivation queue shows the screened objective, and A receives the artifact through the task lifecycle without any direct Lattice access.

AC-PR43-002: Given mail sent while the recipient is offline, when the recipient's next session fetches, then the message arrives in quarantine with sender, timestamp, and integrity intact.

Difficulty: Moderate.

DEP-PR14, DEP-PR36.


PR 44 - The Tool Use Pattern (Grounded Tools, Registry, and Invocation)

Purpose: elevate grounded relations (Section 3.1) into a first-class tool-use faculty, so the mind can discover, choose, invoke, and learn from external tools as deliberately as it uses any competence.

Background: a grounded relation already binds a node_fact to an external implementation; this work package adds the registry, the affordance model, the selection step, the gated invocation, and the reliability learning that turn that primitive into the agentic capability the field calls tool use.

FR-PR44: A tool is a grounded node_fact declaring a tool_card: identity, human-readable description, input and output schema, a risk class, the authorization it requires, and its implementation binding - a native foreign predicate (prologai-core), a Model Context Protocol (MCP) server tool (PR 14), an Agent2Agent (A2A) skill (PR 43), or a body capability (PR 10).

FR-PR44: A tool registry holds all enrolled tools as node_facts, queryable by exact match and by similarity, so the mind can discover tools by affordance - asking, in effect, what can fetch a web page or what can send mail - through traverse_nexus.

FR-PR44: Tool selection is a deliberation step (PR 34 and Part 5 Pattern 6): given an objective, the deliberator retrieves candidate tools by affordance match and scores them by reliability statistics (regulation), somatic markers (PR 24), risk class, and budget (PR 21), then chooses.

FR-PR44: Tool invocation is gated and sandboxed: every call passes the constitutional check (Section 3.16) and the oversight monitor (Part 38) appropriate to its risk class; the result lands in a quarantine scope and is validated before promotion; a failed or timed-out call feeds regulation and may raise an impasse (Section 3.11).

FR-PR44: Tool outcomes update reliability statistics like any competence, so the mind learns which tools serve which objectives, and the attention economy (PR 32) lets unused tools fall out of the working set.

FR-PR44: The mind MAY build its own tools: a learned tool is a grounded relation synthesized (PR 22) or induced (PR 37) and bound to a composition of existing tools (the connector mechanic of Section 3.1), entering the registry only through the constitutional pipeline.

Predicates: pai_tool_card/2, pai_tool_register/2, pai_tool_discover/2, pai_tool_select/3, pai_tool_invoke/4.

AC-PR44-001: Given a registered web_search tool and an objective that needs current facts, when the deliberator runs, then web_search is selected, invoked through the constitutional gate, and its result lands in quarantine before any use.

AC-PR44-002: Given a tool whose recent calls have failed and an available alternative, when selection runs, then the alternative is preferred (reliability learning).

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR10, DEP-PR14, DEP-PR21, DEP-PR24, DEP-PR34.


PR 45 - Computer Use (the Screen-and-Input Body)

Purpose: let a PrologAI mind operate a graphical computer as a human does - perceive the screen and actuate mouse, keyboard, and browser - realized through the Mind-Body pattern, so computer use is a body, not a special case.

Background: computer use is the capability that lets an agent work in any application a person can, including those with no Application Programming Interface; PrologAI gains it by treating the screen as a sensor and the input devices as actuators on an enrolled body.

FR-PR45: A computer body is enrolled via manifest_body (PR 10), declaring screen perception and the input capabilities: screenshot, mouse move, click, drag, and scroll, keyboard type and hotkeys, and browser navigation.

FR-PR45: Screen perception flows as percepts: a screenshot is a visual percept processed by the detector suite (PR 30), which extracts interface elements - buttons, fields, links, and text - as node_facts with screen-relative locations, reusing reference frames (PR 39) for the screen's coordinate space.

FR-PR45: Actuation flows as commands: pai_computer_act issues mouse, keyboard, and navigation actions through dispatch_command, each with proprioceptive confirmation - the next screenshot - closing the perception-action loop.

FR-PR45: Browser use is a specialized computer body offering navigation, page-text and Document Object Model extraction, form filling, and tab management as capabilities, preferred over raw pixel control whenever a page exposes structure.

FR-PR45: Computer use is contained by default (Part 38): early minds act only in a sandboxed or simulated desktop with no network beyond an allowlist, real-world control is unlocked only by staged autonomy, and every irreversible on-screen action passes the constitutional check.

FR-PR45: On-screen content and web links from untrusted sources are treated as quarantined input, never as instructions, which guards against prompt injection arriving through the screen.

Predicates: pai_screen_observe/1, pai_computer_act/2, pai_browser_navigate/2, pai_page_extract/2.

AC-PR45-001: Given a sandboxed desktop showing a form, when the mind is asked to fill and submit it, then it observes the screen, locates the fields as node_facts, types the values, submits, and confirms success from the next screenshot.

AC-PR45-002: Given a page containing instruction-like text injected by a third party, when the mind reads the page, then that text lands in quarantine and is not executed as a command.

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR10, DEP-PR30, DEP-PR39, DEP-PR44.


PR 46 - The Robot Operating System Bridge (Embodiment in a Robot)

Purpose: let a PrologAI mind inhabit a physical or simulated robot by bridging to the Robot Operating System, version 2 (ROS 2), so that a robot is enrolled as an ordinary body through the Mind-Body pattern (PR 10).

Background: ROS 2 is the current long-term-support generation of the Robot Operating System (ROS 1 reached end-of-life in 2025); it carries sensor and actuator data over named topics, describes robots in the Uniform Robot Description Format (URDF), and tracks coordinate frames with the TF2 transform system.

FR-PR46-001: A robot, physical or simulated, SHALL be enrolled via manifest_body (PR 10); a small bridge node (written with the rclpy client library) subscribes to the robot's sensor topics and relays them as percepts, and turns the mind's commands into actuator messages - this bridge node is the robot's herald.

FR-PR46-002: Sensor messages (sensor_msgs and geometry_msgs) map to perception_signal percepts processed by the detector suite (PR 30); camera frames become visual percepts; and the TF2 coordinate frames map onto reference frames (PR 39), so the robot's spatial world reuses the existing frame machinery.

FR-PR46-003: Commands map to actuator topics with proprioceptive confirmation closing the loop (the one-hundred-percent command resolution of PR 10); the higher-level stacks Navigation 2 (Nav2) for navigation and MoveIt for manipulation are wrapped as grounded tools (PR 44) rather than reimplemented.

FR-PR46-004: A simulator - Gazebo (the ROS-native default), NVIDIA Isaac Sim (free and Apache-2.0, for photorealistic perception and synthetic data), or Webots (for early work) - provides the virtual robot body for development; the same bridge serves the simulator and a physical robot unchanged, honoring the device-agnostic Mind-Body principle.

FR-PR46-005: Embodiment is staged and contained (Part 38): a mind acts first in simulation only, with no physical actuation and a network allowlist; real-world control is unlocked only by passing the capability evaluations and audits; every irreversible physical action passes the constitutional check, and high-risk actuation is gated by the oversight monitor.

Predicates: pai_robot_enroll/3, pai_ros_bridge/2, pai_robot_observe/1, pai_robot_act/2.

AC-PR46-001: Given a simulated robot in Gazebo or Webots with a camera and a drive base, when the mind is asked to find and approach a colored object, then it observes the scene as percepts, plans a route, issues drive commands, and confirms arrival from proprioceptive feedback.

AC-PR46-002: Given the mind in simulation-only state, when a physical-actuation command is attempted, then it is withheld until staged autonomy and capability evaluation permit it.

Difficulty: Hard.

DEP-PR10, DEP-PR30, DEP-PR39, DEP-PR44.


PR 47 - The Agent Communication Protocol Gateway (ACP)

Purpose: let PrologAI minds participate in the IBM/BeeAI Agent Communication Protocol (ACP) ecosystem, enabling REST-based asynchronous agent task exchange with enterprise agent clients without requiring them to speak the A2A wire format.

Background: the Agent Communication Protocol (ACP), developed by IBM and the BeeAI project and now hosted at agentcommunicationprotocol.dev, is a REST Application Programming Interface (API) specification for asynchronous agent communication. It standardizes how clients create runs, monitor status, and retrieve results via plain Hypertext Transfer Protocol (HTTP); supports streaming responses via Server-Sent Events (SSE); and publishes an agent description card at the well-known Uniform Resource Identifier (URI) path /.well-known/agent.json. ACP graduated from the research track in 2025 and is now a stable specification. The companion protocol note of FR-PR43-004 having been satisfied, ACP is now promoted to a production work package.

FR-PR47-001: The Mind Server SHALL expose an ACP endpoint on a configurable port (default 7476); POST /runs creates a run mapped to an objective node_fact routed through motivation and the constitutional screen; GET /runs/{run_id} returns the current status; and DELETE /runs/{run_id} cancels it; the agent description is served at GET /.well-known/agent.json listing the mind's capabilities without disclosing Lattice contents.

FR-PR47-002: ACP runs support three execution modes selected by the HTTP Accept header of the request: sync (response inline in the HTTP reply body), stream (SSE; the result is streamed token by token), and async (polling; the client calls GET /runs/{run_id} until status is completed or failed); each mode returns the same artifact structure on completion.

FR-PR47-003: Inbound ACP tasks are screened through the constitutional gate (Section 3.16) and routed through motivation (PR 20) as objective node_facts exactly as A2A tasks are (FR-PR43-001); outbound ACP tasks are dispatched through the tool-use faculty (PR 44); opacity is preserved in both directions and the agent description discloses capabilities, not Lattice contents.

FR-PR47-004: The ACP gateway registers itself as a sixth tool source alongside native foreign predicates, Model Context Protocol servers (PR 14), Agent2Agent skills (PR 43), body capabilities (PR 10), and ANP peers (PR 48), so the tool-use faculty can discover and invoke ACP-hosted agents exactly as it invokes any other tool.

Predicates: pai_acp_start/1, pai_acp_stop/0, pai_acp_run/4, pai_acp_status/2, pai_acp_cancel/1, pai_acp_agent_description/1.

AC-PR47-001: Given pai_acp_start(7476) is called, when POST /runs with a valid ACP task body is made, then a run_id is returned and GET /runs/{run_id} shows completed status with an artifact within the timeout.

AC-PR47-002: Given an ACP run in async mode, when the client polls GET /runs/{run_id}, then the status transitions from created to in_progress to completed in the correct order without skipping states.

AC-PR47-003: Given GET /.well-known/agent.json is called, when an ACP client requests it, then a valid ACP agent description JSON is returned listing the mind's capabilities, skills, and supported protocols without exposing Lattice contents.

Difficulty: Moderate.

DEP-PR14, DEP-PR43, DEP-PR44.


PR 48 - The Agent Network Protocol Gateway (ANP)

Purpose: let PrologAI minds participate in decentralized agent networks using the Agent Network Protocol (ANP), enabling peer-to-peer agent discovery and cryptographically authenticated messaging without relying on a central registry.

Background: the Agent Network Protocol (ANP), developed by the agent-network-protocol consortium and now under active community development, is a decentralized protocol for agent identity, discovery, and communication. It uses W3C Decentralized Identifiers (DIDs) for agent identity (one DID per mind, in did:web format), publishes agent descriptions at the well-known URI path /.well-known/agent-descriptions, and authenticates messages with cryptographic signatures derived from the DID key material. ANP supports meta-protocol negotiation (MPN) so agents can discover which communication protocols a peer speaks before initiating contact. ANP graduated from the research track in 2025 and is now a stable specification. The companion protocol note of FR-PR43-004 having been satisfied, ANP is now promoted to a production work package.

FR-PR48-001: Each PrologAI mind SHALL have a DID in did:web format derived from its Mind Server hostname; the DID is generated on first configuration and stored as a constitution-scope node_fact; the associated public key is used to verify inbound ANP messages and to sign outbound ANP messages.

FR-PR48-002: The gateway SHALL serve the ANP agent description at GET /.well-known/agent-descriptions; the description lists the mind's DID, capability set, supported protocols (mcp, a2a, acp, anp) with their respective endpoints, and the public key for message verification; it SHALL NOT expose Lattice contents.

FR-PR48-003: Inbound ANP messages SHALL be verified against the sender's DID-resolved public key before any content is admitted to any scope; messages that fail verification are discarded and a security event is logged in the oversight log.

FR-PR48-004: ANP meta-protocol negotiation (MPN) is supported: when a peer queries which protocols a mind speaks, the gateway returns the set {mcp, a2a, acp, anp} with the appropriate endpoint URL for each, so a peer can select the protocol best suited to its capabilities.

FR-PR48-005: The ANP gateway registers itself as a fifth tool source alongside native foreign predicates, Model Context Protocol servers (PR 14), Agent2Agent skills (PR 43), body capabilities (PR 10), and ACP agents (PR 47), so the tool-use faculty can discover and invoke ANP-addressed peers exactly as it invokes any other tool; every outbound ANP message passes the constitutional gate.

Predicates: pai_anp_did/1, pai_anp_agent_description/1, pai_anp_send/3, pai_anp_receive/3, pai_anp_verify/2, pai_anp_negotiate/2.

AC-PR48-001: Given pai_anp_did(DID) is called, then a valid did:web DID is returned that is stable across calls and stored in the constitution scope.

AC-PR48-002: Given GET /.well-known/agent-descriptions is called, when an ANP client requests it, then a valid ANP agent description is returned listing the mind's DID, capabilities, supported protocols, and public key without exposing Lattice contents.

AC-PR48-003: Given an inbound ANP message whose sender DID cannot be resolved or whose signature does not verify, when pai_anp_receive/3 is called, then the message is discarded and a security event is logged; no content enters any scope.

AC-PR48-004: Given ANP meta-protocol negotiation, when a peer queries supported protocols via pai_anp_negotiate/2, then the set {mcp, a2a, acp, anp} with their endpoint URLs is returned.

Difficulty: Moderate to Hard.

DEP-PR14, DEP-PR43, DEP-PR47.


PART 17 - OVERALL ARCHITECTURE AFTER ALL 48 PRs

Layer 1 - Standard Prolog core (unforked SWI-Prolog dependency): backward chaining, unification, backtracking, all standard predicates, threading, engines, incremental tabling, mature ecosystem.

Layer 2 - Rust FFI Bridge (PR 2): native-speed interface between Prolog on one side and the prologai-core Rust crate (with its pluggable vector backends) on the other.

Layer 3 - The Lattice (PR 3): HNSW-backed persistent shared memory with self-learning topology and cryptographic verified proofs.

Layer 4 - Node Facts (PR 4): structured knowledge units in five memory areas with temporal kindle/quench driven by backend edge weights, embedded by the pluggable provider (PR 16).

Layer 5 - Scopes and Zones (PR 5): microtheory compartmentalization across the nine zones.

Layer 6 - Actor Framework (PRs 6 and 7): cyclic_actor (proactive), receptor (reactive), sentinel (neuro-symbolic opportunistic).

Layer 7 - Subscribe and Publish (PR 8): reactive Lattice coordination and stigmergic actor communication.

Layer 8 - Sentinels (PR 9): forward-chaining rules firing on both exact logical and semantic similarity matches.

Layer 9 - Mind-Body Interface (PR 10): herald, body registration, percept relay, command dispatch, all sensory modalities. (Extended by PR 46, the Robot Operating System version 2 bridge, which enrolls a physical or simulated robot as a body, so robotics is an instance of the Mind-Body interface rather than a new layer.)

Layer 10 - Continuous Learning (PR 11): SONA engine with EWC++ lifelong learning, ReasoningBank episodic recall, and consolidation sub-patterns.

Layer 11 - Intelligence Assessment (PR 12): Bayley, Piagetian, and CHC assessment frameworks, plus consciousness-indicator coverage.

Layer 12 - Reflection Actors (PR 13): the full suite of motivation, daydream, regulation, compensation, coping, exploration, discovery, imitation, play, gating, impasse, and meta-control actors.

Layer 13 - MCP Gateway (PR 14): unified MCP endpoint exposing all PrologAI services to the broader AI agent ecosystem.

Layer 14 - Truth Maintenance (PR 15): incrementally tabled derived knowledge, automatically consistent with the changing Lattice.

Layer 15 - The PrologAI Language Surface (PR 1): the prologai launcher, dialect flags, and the .pai transcompiler.

Layer 16 - Continual Refinement (PR 17): the refiner_actor loop that diagnoses recent trajectories and applies constitutional, sandboxed CRUD edits to the mind's own configuration - reset-free self-improvement.

Layer 17 - Belief and Evidence (PRs 21, 29): budgets, evidence truth values, and per-node_fact belief records with propagators.

Layer 18 - The Workspace Cycle (PR 18): coalitions, salience, one broadcast per cycle, learning attached to the broadcast.

Layer 19 - Predictive Hierarchy (PRs 19, 22): downward predictions, upward precision-weighted errors, and a self-synthesized model population.

Layer 20 - Affective Guidance (PRs 24, 26, 27): somatic markers, staged appraisal, and the global modulator bus.

Layer 21 - Generative Development (PRs 20, 23, 25, 30, 31, 28): spinoff learning, curiosity, steered daydreaming, the detector suite, and the language faculty - the layers by which the mind grows itself.

Layer 22 - Attention Economy (PR 32): two attention currencies per node_fact, wages, rent, importance spreading, and economically driven forgetting.

Layer 23 - Types and the Kernel (PRs 33 and 35): gradual Lattice types, lattice-resident rewrite rules, and the Minimal PrologAI Kernel.

Layer 24 - Chaining and Interoperability (PRs 34 and 36): the generic chainer with meta-reasoning, and the Hyperon interoperability bridge.

Layer 25 - Induction and Composition (PRs 37 and 38): clause induction by inductive logic programming, and compositional vector binding.

Layer 26 - Frames, Justification, and Probability (PRs 39, 40, and 41): reference frames with voting consensus, justified defeasible reasoning, and the distribution-semantics probabilistic layer.

Layer 27 - Self-Awareness and Society (PRs 42 and 43): the attention schema with its formal workspace correspondence, and agent interoperability with durable agent mail.

Layer 28 - Tool Use and Computer Use (PRs 44 and 45): the tool-use faculty that discovers, selects, gates, and learns from external tools across six tool sources, and the computer-use body that operates a screen, keyboard, mouse, and browser - the layer by which the mind reaches into the wider world of tools and applications.

Layer 29 - ACP Gateway (PR 47): the Agent Communication Protocol REST endpoint that lets enterprise HTTP clients create, monitor, and stream agent runs; the ACP agent description at /.well-known/agent.json; and the ACP tool source registration that lets the tool-use faculty invoke ACP-hosted agents as tools.

Layer 30 - ANP Gateway (PR 48): the Agent Network Protocol gateway that gives each mind a decentralized W3C DID identity, serves the ANP agent description at /.well-known/agent-descriptions, verifies inbound messages cryptographically, signs outbound messages, and supports meta-protocol negotiation so peers can discover which protocols a mind speaks.

The result is a constructed language and platform fully backward-compatible with standard SWI-Prolog, enhanced by a verified high-performance vector memory, implementing a complete Piagetian cognitive architecture in PrologAI's own original vocabulary, and participating in all four major agent communication protocols (MCP, A2A, ACP, ANP) - delivered as packs and a launcher on an unforked engine.
