  grid.

END OF PART 98


PART 99 - PROJECT PACK (Layer 88: Axis Projection and Shadow Casting)

Version: v74
What changed: Added the project pack at Layer 88, providing 14 pj_* predicates for shadow casting and axis-projection operations on grids.


PJ-PJ-001: pj_shadow_down/3
Signature: pj_shadow_down(+Grid, +BG, -Grid2)
Contract: Grid2 is Grid with each BG cell replaced by the value of the nearest non-BG cell above it in the same column. Cells with no non-BG cell above remain BG. Non-BG cells are unchanged.

PJ-PJ-002: pj_shadow_up/3
Signature: pj_shadow_up(+Grid, +BG, -Grid2)
Contract: Grid2 is Grid with each BG cell replaced by the value of the nearest non-BG cell below it in the same column. Cells with no non-BG cell below remain BG. Non-BG cells are unchanged.

PJ-PJ-003: pj_shadow_left/3
Signature: pj_shadow_left(+Grid, +BG, -Grid2)
Contract: Grid2 is Grid with each BG cell replaced by the value of the nearest non-BG cell to its right in the same row. Cells with no non-BG cell to the right remain BG. Non-BG cells are unchanged.

PJ-PJ-004: pj_shadow_right/3
Signature: pj_shadow_right(+Grid, +BG, -Grid2)
Contract: Grid2 is Grid with each BG cell replaced by the value of the nearest non-BG cell to its left in the same row. Cells with no non-BG cell to the left remain BG. Non-BG cells are unchanged.

PJ-PJ-005: pj_shadow_dir/4
Signature: pj_shadow_dir(+Grid, +BG, +Dir, -Grid2)
Contract: Dir must be one of the atoms down, up, left, or right. Dispatches to pj_shadow_down, pj_shadow_up, pj_shadow_left, or pj_shadow_right respectively.

PJ-PJ-006: pj_nonbg_rows/3
Signature: pj_nonbg_rows(+Grid, +BG, -Rows)
Contract: Rows is the sorted list of row indices (0-based) for which at least one cell in that row is not equal to BG. The list is in ascending index order with no duplicates.

PJ-PJ-007: pj_nonbg_cols/3
Signature: pj_nonbg_cols(+Grid, +BG, -Cols)
Contract: Cols is the sorted list of column indices (0-based) for which at least one cell in that column is not equal to BG.

PJ-PJ-008: pj_row_counts/3
Signature: pj_row_counts(+Grid, +BG, -Counts)
Contract: Counts is a list of integers, one per row of Grid, where each integer is the number of cells in that row whose value is not BG. The list has the same length as Grid.

PJ-PJ-009: pj_col_counts/3
Signature: pj_col_counts(+Grid, +BG, -Counts)
Contract: Counts is a list of integers, one per column of Grid, where each integer is the number of cells in that column whose value is not BG.

PJ-PJ-010: pj_collapse_rows/3
Signature: pj_collapse_rows(+Grid, +BG, -Row)
Contract: Row is a list of length equal to the number of columns. For each column C, Row[C] is the value of the first (topmost) non-BG cell in column C, scanning rows top to bottom. If all cells in column C are BG, Row[C] is BG.

PJ-PJ-011: pj_collapse_cols/3
Signature: pj_collapse_cols(+Grid, +BG, -Col)
Contract: Col is a list of length equal to the number of rows. For each row R, Col[R] is the value of the first (leftmost) non-BG cell in row R. If all cells in row R are BG, Col[R] is BG.

PJ-PJ-012: pj_col_first/4
Signature: pj_col_first(+Grid, +Col, +BG, -R)
Contract: R is the row index (0-based) of the topmost (minimum row index) non-BG cell in column Col. Fails if column Col contains no non-BG cell.

PJ-PJ-013: pj_col_last/4
Signature: pj_col_last(+Grid, +Col, +BG, -R)
Contract: R is the row index (0-based) of the bottommost (maximum row index) non-BG cell in column Col. Fails if column Col contains no non-BG cell.

PJ-PJ-014: pj_row_first/4
Signature: pj_row_first(+Grid, +Row, +BG, -C)
Contract: C is the column index (0-based) of the leftmost (minimum column index) non-BG cell in row Row. Fails if row Row contains no non-BG cell.


END OF PART 99


PART 100 - DIFF PACK PREDICATES (df_*)

Layer 89. Pack name: diff. Prefix: df_.

This part specifies the 14 predicates of the diff pack, which provide
multi-pair grid difference analysis: finding what changes and what stays
stable within and across training pairs.

A diff term has the form diff(R, C, V1, V2), where R is a row index,
C is a column index, V1 is the old value, and V2 is the new value.

DF-DF-001: df_cell_diff/3
Signature: df_cell_diff(+Grid1, +Grid2, -Diffs)
Contract: Diffs is a list of diff(R, C, V1, V2) terms, one for each cell
position where Grid1[R][C] = V1, Grid2[R][C] = V2, and V1 != V2. Cells are
enumerated in row-major order. The list is empty if the grids are identical.
Both grids must have the same dimensions.

DF-DF-002: df_added/4
Signature: df_added(+Grid1, +Grid2, +BG, -Cells)
Contract: Cells is a list of R-C pairs where Grid1[R][C] = BG and
Grid2[R][C] != BG. These are cells that transitioned from background to
foreground. The list is empty if no cells were added.

DF-DF-003: df_removed/4
Signature: df_removed(+Grid1, +Grid2, +BG, -Cells)
Contract: Cells is a list of R-C pairs where Grid1[R][C] != BG and
Grid2[R][C] = BG. These are cells that transitioned from foreground to
background. The list is empty if no cells were removed.

DF-DF-004: df_recolored/4
Signature: df_recolored(+Grid1, +Grid2, +BG, -Triples)
Contract: Triples is a list of R-C-V1-V2 terms where Grid1[R][C] = V1,
V1 != BG, Grid2[R][C] = V2, V2 != BG, and V1 != V2. These are cells that
kept non-background status but changed their color value.

DF-DF-005: df_stable/3
Signature: df_stable(+Grid1, +Grid2, -Cells)
Contract: Cells is a list of R-C pairs where Grid1[R][C] = Grid2[R][C].
These are cells whose value did not change between the two grids. Both grids
must have the same dimensions.

DF-DF-006: df_palette_change/4
Signature: df_palette_change(+Grid1, +Grid2, -Added, -Lost)
Contract: Added is the sorted list of distinct color values that appear in
Grid2 but not in Grid1. Lost is the sorted list of distinct color values
that appear in Grid1 but not in Grid2. Both lists are sorted ascending.

DF-DF-007: df_common_diffs/2
Signature: df_common_diffs(+Pairs, -CommonCells)
Contract: Pairs is a list of In-Out terms where In and Out are grids.
CommonCells is the intersection of the sets of changed cell positions (R-C
pairs) across all pairs. A cell position is in CommonCells only if it
changed (had different values in In and Out) in every pair. Returns [] if
Pairs is empty.

DF-DF-008: df_common_stable/2
Signature: df_common_stable(+Pairs, -CommonCells)
Contract: Pairs is a list of In-Out terms. CommonCells is the intersection
of the sets of stable cell positions across all pairs. A cell position is in
CommonCells only if its value was identical in In and Out in every pair.
Returns [] if Pairs is empty.

DF-DF-009: df_always_added/3
Signature: df_always_added(+Pairs, +BG, -CommonCells)
Contract: Pairs is a list of In-Out terms. CommonCells is the intersection
of the sets of added cell positions (BG to non-BG) across all pairs. A cell
position is in CommonCells only if it was added in every single pair.
Returns [] if Pairs is empty.

DF-DF-010: df_always_removed/3
Signature: df_always_removed(+Pairs, +BG, -CommonCells)
Contract: Pairs is a list of In-Out terms. CommonCells is the intersection
of the sets of removed cell positions (non-BG to BG) across all pairs.
A cell position is in CommonCells only if it was removed in every pair.
Returns [] if Pairs is empty.

DF-DF-011: df_total_changes/3
Signature: df_total_changes(+Grid1, +Grid2, -N)
Contract: N is the count of cell positions where Grid1 and Grid2 hold
different values. N = 0 when the grids are identical.

DF-DF-012: df_apply_diffs/3
Signature: df_apply_diffs(+Grid, +Diffs, -Grid2)
Contract: Grid2 is the result of applying every diff(R, C, _, V2) in Diffs
to Grid in order. Each application sets Grid[R][C] to V2. If Diffs is
empty, Grid2 equals Grid.

DF-DF-013: df_invert_diffs/2
Signature: df_invert_diffs(+Diffs, -Inverse)
Contract: Inverse is a list of the same length as Diffs where each element
diff(R, C, V1, V2) in Diffs corresponds to diff(R, C, V2, V1) in Inverse.
Applying the inverse to the output grid recovers the input grid.

DF-DF-014: df_filter_diffs/3
Signature: df_filter_diffs(+Diffs, +Goal, -Filtered)
Contract: Filtered is the sublist of Diffs containing only those diff terms
for which call(Goal, Diff) succeeds. Goal is a 1-argument callable.
Filtered preserves the order of elements from Diffs.


END OF PART 100


PART 101 - ORDER PACK PREDICATES (od_*)

Layer 90. Pack name: order. Prefix: od_.

This part specifies the 14 predicates of the order pack, which provide
spatial ordering, ranking, and selection of objects from the obj() term
representation. An object term has the form obj(Color, Cells) where Color
is a non-negative integer and Cells is a sorted list of r(R, C) cells.

OD-OD-001: od_centroid/3
Signature: od_centroid(+Obj, -CR, -CC)
Contract: CR and CC are the integer floor centroids of the cell list in Obj.
CR = floor(sum(R) / N), CC = floor(sum(C) / N) where N is the number of
cells. Fails if the cell list is empty.

OD-OD-002: od_sort_row/2
Signature: od_sort_row(+Objs, -Sorted)
Contract: Sorted is Objs reordered so that objects appear from topmost
centroid row to bottommost. keysort (stable) is used. Ties in centroid row
are broken by original order.

OD-OD-003: od_sort_col/2
Signature: od_sort_col(+Objs, -Sorted)
Contract: Sorted is Objs reordered from leftmost centroid column to
rightmost. keysort (stable) is used.

OD-OD-004: od_reading_order/2
Signature: od_reading_order(+Objs, -Sorted)
Contract: Sorted is Objs reordered by reading order: primary sort by centroid
row ascending, secondary sort by centroid column ascending. Objects with the
same centroid row are ordered left-to-right.

OD-OD-005: od_sort_color/2
Signature: od_sort_color(+Objs, -Sorted)
Contract: Sorted is Objs reordered by color value ascending. keysort (stable)
is used. Objects with the same color keep their original relative order.

OD-OD-006: od_topmost/2
Signature: od_topmost(+Objs, -TopObj)
Contract: TopObj is the object in Objs whose centroid row is the smallest
(nearest to the top of the grid). Fails if Objs is empty. If multiple
objects tie on centroid row, the first in the input list is returned.

OD-OD-007: od_bottommost/2
Signature: od_bottommost(+Objs, -BotObj)
Contract: BotObj is the object whose centroid row is the largest. Fails if
Objs is empty.

OD-OD-008: od_leftmost/2
Signature: od_leftmost(+Objs, -LeftObj)
Contract: LeftObj is the object whose centroid column is the smallest (nearest
to the left edge). Fails if Objs is empty.

OD-OD-009: od_rightmost/2
Signature: od_rightmost(+Objs, -RightObj)
Contract: RightObj is the object whose centroid column is the largest. Fails
if Objs is empty.

OD-OD-010: od_nth_row/3
Signature: od_nth_row(+Objs, +N, -Obj)
Contract: Obj is the N-th object when Objs is sorted by centroid row
ascending. N is 1-indexed. Fails if N is out of range or Objs is empty.

OD-OD-011: od_nth_col/3
Signature: od_nth_col(+Objs, +N, -Obj)
Contract: Obj is the N-th object when Objs is sorted by centroid column
ascending. N is 1-indexed.

OD-OD-012: od_nearest/4
Signature: od_nearest(+Objs, +R, +C, -NearObj)
Contract: NearObj is the object in Objs whose centroid has the minimum
Manhattan distance to the grid position (R, C). Manhattan distance between
centroid (CR, CC) and (R, C) is |CR - R| + |CC - C|. Fails if Objs is empty.
If multiple objects tie on distance, the first in key-sorted order is returned.

OD-OD-013: od_farthest/4
Signature: od_farthest(+Objs, +R, +C, -FarObj)
Contract: FarObj is the object whose centroid has the maximum Manhattan
distance to (R, C). Fails if Objs is empty.

OD-OD-014: od_rank_row/3
Signature: od_rank_row(+Objs, +TargetObj, -Rank)
Contract: Rank is the 1-based position of TargetObj in the row-ascending
ordering of Objs. Rank = 1 means TargetObj is the topmost. Fails if
TargetObj is not in Objs (using == comparison).


END OF PART 101


PART 102 - ASSEMBLE PACK PREDICATES (as_*)

Layer 91. Work Package 112. Prefix as_.
Purpose: Grid assembly, concatenation, and composition operations.
Joins multiple grids horizontally or vertically, assembles grids from 2D
matrices of sub-grids, downscales K x K blocks to single cells, adds colored
borders, centers a grid in a canvas, extracts named quadrants, creates
mirror-concatenations, interleaves columns or rows, pastes sub-grids, applies
mask-based fill, and crops or pads a grid to a target size.

AS-AS-001: as_hcat/2
Signature: as_hcat(+Grids, -Combined)
Contract: Grids is a non-empty list of grids all having the same number of
rows. Combined is the single grid formed by placing them side by side in list
order, preserving the row count and summing the column counts. For a single
grid in the list, Combined equals that grid.

AS-AS-002: as_vcat/2
Signature: as_vcat(+Grids, -Combined)
Contract: Grids is a non-empty list of grids all having the same number of
columns. Combined is the single grid formed by stacking them top-to-bottom in
list order, summing the row counts and preserving the column count.

AS-AS-003: as_grid_of/2
Signature: as_grid_of(+Matrix, -Combined)
Contract: Matrix is a list of rows where each row is a list of grids. All
grids in a row have the same height; all rows produce strips of the same total
width. Combined is the grid formed by horizontally joining each row of grids,
then vertically stacking the resulting strips.

AS-AS-004: as_downscale/3
Signature: as_downscale(+Grid, +K, -Small)
Contract: K is a positive integer. Grid dimensions must be divisible by K in
both directions. Each K x K non-overlapping block in Grid is reduced to a
single cell in Small whose value is the most common value in the block
(majority vote). Small has NR/K rows and NC/K columns.

AS-AS-005: as_border/4
Signature: as_border(+Grid, +W, +Color, -Framed)
Contract: Framed is Grid surrounded on all four sides by a frame of W rows or
columns filled with Color. Framed has NR + 2*W rows and NC + 2*W columns.
The original Grid appears at offset (W, W) within Framed.

AS-AS-006: as_center_in/5
Signature: as_center_in(+Grid, +NR, +NC, +Bg, -Result)
Contract: Result is an NR x NC grid filled with Bg into which Grid is pasted
at the integer floor center offset ((NR - GNR) // 2, (NC - GNC) // 2). If
Grid is larger than the canvas in either dimension, only the visible portion
within the canvas bounds is shown.

AS-AS-007: as_quarter/3
Signature: as_quarter(+Grid, +Q, -Sub)
Contract: Q is one of the atoms tl, tr, bl, br (top-left, top-right,
bottom-left, bottom-right). Sub is the quadrant of Grid containing floor(NR/2)
rows and floor(NC/2) columns at the corresponding corner. Row boundary is at
NR // 2; column boundary is at NC // 2.

AS-AS-008: as_flip_h_cat/2
Signature: as_flip_h_cat(+Grid, -Combined)
Contract: Combined is the horizontal concatenation of Grid and its left-right
mirror (each row reversed). Combined has the same number of rows as Grid and
twice the number of columns.

AS-AS-009: as_flip_v_cat/2
Signature: as_flip_v_cat(+Grid, -Combined)
Contract: Combined is the vertical stack of Grid and its top-bottom mirror
(row list reversed). Combined has twice the number of rows and the same number
of columns.

AS-AS-010: as_zip_h/3
Signature: as_zip_h(+G1, +G2, -Combined)
Contract: G1 and G2 must have the same dimensions. In each row of Combined,
values from the corresponding rows of G1 and G2 are interleaved
column-by-column: G1[R][0], G2[R][0], G1[R][1], G2[R][1], ...
Combined has the same row count and twice the column count.

AS-AS-011: as_zip_v/3
Signature: as_zip_v(+G1, +G2, -Combined)
Contract: G1 and G2 must have the same dimensions. Rows from G1 and G2 are
interleaved: G1[0], G2[0], G1[1], G2[1], ...
Combined has twice the row count and the same column count.

AS-AS-012: as_paste/5
Signature: as_paste(+Base, +Sub, +SR, +SC, -Result)
Contract: Result is Base with Sub unconditionally pasted starting at row SR
and column SC. All cells of Sub within the bounds of Base are copied to the
corresponding positions in Result. Base cells not covered by Sub are unchanged.
Sub cells that fall outside Base bounds are ignored.

AS-AS-013: as_mask_fill/4
Signature: as_mask_fill(+Grid, +Mask, +Fill, -Result)
Contract: Grid and Mask must have the same dimensions. Result[R][C] = Fill
if Mask[R][C] is not 0; otherwise Result[R][C] = Grid[R][C].

AS-AS-014: as_crop_to/5
Signature: as_crop_to(+Grid, +NR, +NC, +Bg, -Result)
Contract: Result is a grid of exactly NR rows and NC columns. Cells at
positions within both Grid's bounds and the target size are copied from Grid.
Cells outside Grid's bounds are filled with Bg. Grid cells beyond the target
size are discarded.


END OF PART 102


PART 103 - REGION PACK PREDICATES (rg_*)

Layer 92. Work Package 113. Prefix rg_.
Purpose: Grid region extraction by separator lines. Divides a grid into
sections using rows or columns where every cell equals a separator value.
Enables finding, measuring, extracting, and navigating the distinct sections
that separator lines create.

RG-RG-001: rg_sep_rows/3
Signature: rg_sep_rows(+Grid, +Sep, -IdxList)
Contract: IdxList is the sorted list of 0-indexed row indices where every cell
in that row equals Sep. Returns [] if no such rows exist.

RG-RG-002: rg_sep_cols/3
Signature: rg_sep_cols(+Grid, +Sep, -IdxList)
Contract: IdxList is the sorted list of 0-indexed column indices where every
cell in that column equals Sep.

RG-RG-003: rg_is_sep_row/3
Signature: rg_is_sep_row(+Grid, +R, +Sep)
Contract: Succeeds if every cell in row R of Grid equals Sep. Fails otherwise.
R is 0-indexed.

RG-RG-004: rg_is_sep_col/3
Signature: rg_is_sep_col(+Grid, +C, +Sep)
Contract: Succeeds if every cell in column C of Grid equals Sep. Fails otherwise.
C is 0-indexed.

RG-RG-005: rg_spans_h/3
Signature: rg_spans_h(+Grid, +Sep, -Spans)
Contract: Spans is a list of R0-R1 inclusive row range pairs, one per horizontal
section of Grid. Sections are the maximal contiguous groups of rows that contain
no separator row. Separator rows are not included in any span. Spans are in
ascending row order.

RG-RG-006: rg_spans_v/3
Signature: rg_spans_v(+Grid, +Sep, -Spans)
Contract: Spans is a list of C0-C1 inclusive column range pairs, one per vertical
section. Separator columns are excluded. Spans are in ascending column order.

RG-RG-007: rg_cut_h/3
Signature: rg_cut_h(+Grid, +Sep, -Parts)
Contract: Parts is a list of sub-grids, one per horizontal section, in top-to-
bottom order. Each sub-grid contains exactly the rows in one horizontal span.
Separator rows are excluded from all sub-grids.

RG-RG-008: rg_cut_v/3
Signature: rg_cut_v(+Grid, +Sep, -Parts)
Contract: Parts is a list of sub-grids, one per vertical section, in left-to-
right order. Each sub-grid contains exactly the columns in one vertical span.

RG-RG-009: rg_sections/3
Signature: rg_sections(+Grid, +Sep, -Matrix)
Contract: Matrix is a list of rows where each element is a list of sub-grids.
Matrix[I][J] is the sub-grid at horizontal section I and vertical section J
(both 0-indexed). Formed by applying rg_cut_h then rg_cut_v to each strip.

RG-RG-010: rg_section_h/4
Signature: rg_section_h(+Grid, +Sep, +N, -Section)
Contract: Section is the N-th horizontal section of Grid (1-indexed). Equivalent
to the N-th element of rg_cut_h/3. Fails if N is out of range.

RG-RG-011: rg_section_v/4
Signature: rg_section_v(+Grid, +Sep, +N, -Section)
Contract: Section is the N-th vertical section of Grid (1-indexed).

RG-RG-012: rg_count_h/3
Signature: rg_count_h(+Grid, +Sep, -N)
Contract: N is the number of horizontal sections. N = length(rg_spans_h result).

RG-RG-013: rg_count_v/3
Signature: rg_count_v(+Grid, +Sep, -N)
Contract: N is the number of vertical sections.

RG-RG-014: rg_region/5
Signature: rg_region(+Grid, +Sep, +R, +C, -Region)
Contract: Region is the sub-grid of the section that contains cell (R, C).
The section is determined by finding the horizontal span containing R and the
vertical span containing C, then extracting the intersection. Fails if (R, C)
lies on a separator row or column.


END OF PART 103


PART 104 - NEIGHBOR PACK SPECIFICATION (Layer 93, nb_* prefix)

Work Package 114

NB-NB-001: nb_4neighbors(+Grid, +R, +C, -Neighbors)
Return a list of nb(Row,Col,Val) terms for each valid 4-connected neighbor
of cell (R, C) in Grid. Directions checked in order: up (-1,0), down (1,0),
left (0,-1), right (0,1). Out-of-bounds directions are omitted. Corner cells
have 2 neighbors, edge cells have 3, interior cells have 4.

NB-NB-002: nb_8neighbors(+Grid, +R, +C, -Neighbors)
Return a list of nb(Row,Col,Val) terms for each valid 8-connected neighbor
of cell (R, C). Covers all 8 surrounding positions including diagonals.
Order: NW, N, NE, W, E, SW, S, SE. Out-of-bounds positions are omitted.

NB-NB-003: nb_is_boundary(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg)
Succeed if cell (R, C) has a value different from Bg and at least one
4-connected neighbor is either out of bounds or has value Bg. Cut after
the first qualifying neighbor so the predicate is deterministic.

NB-NB-004: nb_is_interior(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg)
Succeed if cell (R, C) has a value different from Bg and no 4-connected
neighbor is out of bounds or has value Bg. Uses negation as failure over
the boundary condition check.

NB-NB-005: nb_boundary_cells(+Grid, +Bg, -Cells)
Return a sorted list of R-C pairs for every non-Bg cell in Grid that
satisfies nb_is_boundary/4. Results are sorted lexicographically by row
then column using sort/2.

NB-NB-006: nb_interior_cells(+Grid, +Bg, -Cells)
Return a sorted list of R-C pairs for every non-Bg cell in Grid that
satisfies nb_is_interior/4. Results are sorted by row then column.

NB-NB-007: nb_count_same(+Grid, +R, +C, -N)
Return N as the count of 4-connected neighbors of (R, C) that have the
same color value as (R, C). Uses nb_4neighbors to obtain the neighbor list,
then counts matching values with findall.

NB-NB-008: nb_count_diff(+Grid, +R, +C, -N)
Return N as the count of 4-connected neighbors of (R, C) that have a
different color value from (R, C). Uses nb_4neighbors then counts
non-matching values with findall.

NB-NB-009: nb_adjacent_colors(+Grid, +R, +C, -Colors)
Return a sorted list of distinct color values found among the 4-connected
neighbors of (R, C). Uses nb_4neighbors, extracts values with findall,
and deduplicates with sort.

NB-NB-010: nb_contour(+Grid, +Color, -Cells)
Return a sorted list of R-C pairs for all cells of Color that are adjacent
to at least one cell of a different color or to the grid boundary. These
cells form the visible outline of the Color region in Grid.

NB-NB-011: nb_color_touches(+Grid, +ColorA, +ColorB)
Succeed if any cell of ColorA is 4-adjacent to any cell of ColorB anywhere
in Grid. Uses cut after finding the first adjacency for determinism. Fails
if ColorA and ColorB are never 4-adjacent.

NB-NB-012: nb_touching_pairs(+Grid, +ColorA, +ColorB, -Pairs)
Return a sorted list of (R1-C1)-(R2-C2) pairs where cell (R1,C1) has
ColorA and is 4-adjacent to cell (R2,C2) with ColorB. When ColorA equals
ColorB, both directions of each adjacency appear in the list.

NB-NB-013: nb_flood_fill(+Grid, +R, +C, +FillVal, -Result)
Replace the 4-connected region of cells in Grid containing seed cell (R,C)
with FillVal, producing Result. The seed color is the value at (R,C).
All cells of that color reachable from the seed via 4-connectivity are
replaced. If the seed color already equals FillVal, Result equals Grid.
Uses a worklist-based iterative algorithm; the filled value itself
prevents re-visiting without an explicit visited set.

NB-NB-014: nb_dilate(+Grid, +Bg, +Color, -Result)
Expand the Color region in Grid by one layer: every Bg cell that is
4-adjacent to any Color cell is set to Color in Result. Non-Bg, non-Color
cells are unchanged. Combines findall over all Color cells and their
Bg 4-neighbors with nb_set_cells_ for bulk cell replacement.


END OF PART 104

PART 105 - PERMUTE PACK (Layer 94, pm_* prefix)

Work Package 115

PM-PM-001: pm_permute_rows(+Grid, +Perm, -Result)
Reorder the rows of Grid by the index permutation Perm. The output row at
position i is Grid row Perm[i]. Perm is a list of 0-based row indices.
Implemented using maplist over Perm with nth0 for row extraction.

PM-PM-002: pm_permute_cols(+Grid, +Perm, -Result)
Reorder the columns of Grid by the index permutation Perm. Column j of
Result contains the values from column Perm[j] of Grid. Implemented by
applying an inner maplist per row that picks each column index from Perm.

PM-PM-003: pm_swap_rows(+Grid, +R1, +R2, -Result)
Exchange rows R1 and R2 in Grid. All other rows are unchanged. Extracts
both rows using nth0/3, then rebuilds the grid by mapping each row index
to RowA, RowB, or the original row as appropriate.

PM-PM-004: pm_swap_cols(+Grid, +C1, +C2, -Result)
Exchange columns C1 and C2 in Grid. Implemented by computing a swap
permutation (C1 maps to C2, C2 maps to C1, others unchanged) and passing
it to pm_permute_cols.

PM-PM-005: pm_cycle_rows(+Grid, +N, -Result)
Shift rows cyclically by N positions downward. The last N rows (after
modular reduction) move to the front. N=0 or N mod NR = 0 returns Grid
unchanged. Splits Grid at position NR - (N mod NR) using append.

PM-PM-006: pm_cycle_cols(+Grid, +N, -Result)
Shift columns cyclically by N positions rightward. The last N columns move
to the left. N=0 or N mod NC = 0 returns Grid unchanged. For each row,
splits at NC - (N mod NC) using append then recombines right-then-left.

PM-PM-007: pm_find_row_perm(+Grid1, +Grid2, -Perm)
Find the index permutation such that Grid2[i] = Grid1[Perm[i]] for every
row i. Uses the internal helper pm_first_row_idx_ which locates the first
matching row in Grid1 using nth0 and cut. Fails if any row of Grid2 does
not appear in Grid1.

PM-PM-008: pm_find_col_perm(+Grid1, +Grid2, -Perm)
Find the index permutation such that column j of Grid2 equals column
Perm[j] of Grid1. Extracts each column of Grid2 as a list, then for each
such column finds its first matching column index in Grid1 using the
internal helper pm_first_col_idx_ which iterates with between/3 and cut.

PM-PM-009: pm_sort_rows(+Grid, -Sorted)
Sort the rows of Grid in ascending lexicographic order. Duplicate rows are
preserved. Implemented directly as msort(Grid, Sorted) since SWI-Prolog
compares lists lexicographically by default.

PM-PM-010: pm_sort_cols(+Grid, -Sorted)
Sort the columns of Grid in ascending lexicographic order. Extracts all
columns as lists, sorts the column list with msort, then reconstructs the
grid by reading each row R from the sorted column lists.

PM-PM-011: pm_insert_row(+Grid, +R, +NewRow, -Result)
Insert NewRow before position R in Grid. Rows at and beyond position R
shift down by one. Splits Grid into a Prefix of length R and a Suffix,
then assembles Result = Prefix ++ [NewRow] ++ Suffix using append.

PM-PM-012: pm_delete_row(+Grid, +R, -Result)
Remove row R from Grid. Rows beyond R shift up by one. Uses nth0/4 in
its list-removal mode: nth0(R, Grid, _, Result).

PM-PM-013: pm_insert_col(+Grid, +C, +NewCol, -Result)
Insert a column of values (one per row from NewCol) before position C in
every row of Grid. For each row and its corresponding new column value,
splits the row at C and reassembles. NewCol must be a list with one value
per row. Uses maplist/4 to process pairs of rows and column values.

PM-PM-014: pm_delete_col(+Grid, +C, -Result)
Remove column C from every row of Grid. Uses maplist/3 with nth0/4 in
removal mode on each row: nth0(C, Row, _, ResRow).


PART 106 - GRAVITY PACK (Layer 95, gv_* prefix)

Work Package 116

GV-GV-001: gv_pack_row_left(+Row, +Bg, -Result)
Compact all non-Bg values in Row to the left end. Bg cells fill the right
portion as padding. The relative order of non-Bg values is preserved. Uses
include/3 to separate non-Bg from Bg values, computes padding count by
subtraction, builds a Bg padding list, and appends: NonBg ++ Pad.

GV-GV-002: gv_pack_row_right(+Row, +Bg, -Result)
Compact all non-Bg values in Row to the right end. Bg cells fill the left
portion as padding. The relative order of non-Bg values is preserved. Uses
include/3 to separate values, builds padding, and appends: Pad ++ NonBg.

GV-GV-003: gv_pack_col_up(+Col, +Bg, -Result)
Compact all non-Bg values in the column list Col to the top (start). Bg cells
fill the bottom as padding. Semantically equivalent to gv_pack_row_left but
named for column context. Uses include/3 and append.

GV-GV-004: gv_pack_col_down(+Col, +Bg, -Result)
Compact all non-Bg values in the column list Col to the bottom (end). Bg cells
fill the top as padding. Semantically equivalent to gv_pack_row_right but
named for column context. Uses include/3 and append.

GV-GV-005: gv_fall_left(+Grid, +Bg, -Result)
All non-Bg cells in Grid slide left within their row. Each row is processed
independently using gv_pack_row_left. No inter-row interaction.

GV-GV-006: gv_fall_right(+Grid, +Bg, -Result)
All non-Bg cells in Grid slide right within their row. Each row is processed
independently using gv_pack_row_right. No inter-row interaction.

GV-GV-007: gv_fall_down(+Grid, +Bg, -Result)
All non-Bg cells in Grid fall downward within their column. Implemented by
transposing Grid to column-as-row form, applying gv_pack_row_right to each
transposed row (right = bottom in column space), then transposing back.

GV-GV-008: gv_fall_up(+Grid, +Bg, -Result)
All non-Bg cells in Grid rise upward within their column. Implemented by
transposing Grid, applying gv_pack_row_left to each transposed row (left = top
in column space), then transposing back.

GV-GV-009: gv_fall_dir(+Grid, +Bg, +Dir, -Result)
Dispatch gravity by direction atom. Dir must be one of the atoms down, up,
left, or right. Uses if-then-else for deterministic dispatch to the
corresponding gv_fall_* predicate.

GV-GV-010: gv_fall_color_left(+Grid, +Bg, +Color, -Result)
Only Color cells slide left. Other non-Bg cells act as immovable walls that
bound the gravity segments within each row. Between adjacent walls, Color
cells slide to the left end of the segment and Bg cells fill the right.
Uses gv_split_pack_left_ and gv_take_seg_ internal helpers.

GV-GV-011: gv_fall_color_right(+Grid, +Bg, +Color, -Result)
Only Color cells slide right. Other non-Bg cells act as immovable walls.
Between adjacent walls, Color cells slide to the right end of the segment
and Bg cells fill the left. Uses gv_split_pack_right_ internal helper.

GV-GV-012: gv_fall_color_down(+Grid, +Bg, +Color, -Result)
Only Color cells fall downward. Other non-Bg cells act as immovable walls
within each column. Implemented by transposing, applying gv_split_pack_right_
per transposed row (right = down in column space), then transposing back.

GV-GV-013: gv_fall_color_up(+Grid, +Bg, +Color, -Result)
Only Color cells rise upward. Other non-Bg cells act as immovable walls
within each column. Implemented by transposing, applying gv_split_pack_left_
per transposed row (left = up in column space), then transposing back.

GV-GV-014: gv_fall_color_dir(+Grid, +Bg, +Color, +Dir, -Result)
Dispatch color-specific gravity by direction atom. Dir must be one of the
atoms down, up, left, or right. Uses if-then-else for deterministic dispatch
to the corresponding gv_fall_color_* predicate.



PART 107: COUNT PACK - VALUE COUNTING AND FREQUENCY ANALYSIS

Layer 96 - cn_* prefix

The count pack provides predicates for counting cell values, building frequency
histograms, comparing two grids cell-by-cell, and tallying region colors. All
operations work on any cell value type (integers, atoms, or compound terms) using
structural equality (==/2).

CN-CN-001: cn_by_value(+List, +V, -N)
Count occurrences of value V in a flat list. Uses include/3 with =(V) as the
filter goal; works for any value type via unification. N is the count.

CN-CN-002: cn_color_count(+Grid, +Color, -N)
Count occurrences of Color across all cells of a 2D grid. Flattens the grid
to a single list with append/2, then delegates to cn_by_value/3.

CN-CN-003: cn_histogram(+Grid, -Colors, -Counts)
Build a frequency histogram of all cell values. Returns two parallel lists:
Colors (sorted distinct values) and Counts (their occurrence counts). Uses
msort/2 to sort preserving duplicates, then run-length encoding to group
equal adjacent values.

CN-CN-004: cn_max_color(+Grid, -Color)
Return the value that appears most often in Grid. When counts are tied, returns
the value that sorts first (lowest). Uses cn_histogram/3 and max_list/2.

CN-CN-005: cn_min_color(+Grid, -Color)
Return the value that appears least often in Grid. When counts are tied, returns
the value that sorts first (lowest). Uses cn_histogram/3 and min_list/2.

CN-CN-006: cn_color_rows(+Grid, +Color, -N)
Count the number of rows that contain at least one cell equal to Color.
Uses include/3 with member/2 as the row test.

CN-CN-007: cn_color_cols(+Grid, +Color, -N)
Count the number of columns that contain at least one cell equal to Color.
Enumerates column indices, extracts each column via cn_extract_col_, tests
membership, and counts matching indices.

CN-CN-008: cn_row_distinct(+Grid, +R, -N)
Count the number of distinct values in row R (0-based). Uses sort/2 to
deduplicate the row and returns the length of the sorted result.

CN-CN-009: cn_col_distinct(+Grid, +C, -N)
Count the number of distinct values in column C (0-based). Uses
cn_extract_col_ to collect the column, sort/2 to deduplicate, and returns
the length.

CN-CN-010: cn_grid_total(+Grid, -N)
Return the total number of cells in Grid (rows times columns). Uses the
internal cn_grid_dims_ helper to measure dimensions.

CN-CN-011: cn_equal_cells(+Grid1, +Grid2, -N)
Count cells where Grid1 and Grid2 have the same value. Produces per-row
flag lists (1 for equal, 0 for different), flattens them, then sums.
Both grids must have identical dimensions.

CN-CN-012: cn_diff_cells(+Grid1, +Grid2, -N)
Count cells where Grid1 and Grid2 have different values. Computed as
total cells minus equal cells.

CN-CN-013: cn_region_color(+Grid, +Region, -Color)
Return the color of a region by looking up the grid value at the first
cell of the region. Region is a list of r(R,C) terms as produced by the
connect pack. Color is the value at row R, column C of Grid.

CN-CN-014: cn_regions_per_color(+Grid, +Regions, -Pairs)
Build a Color-Count tally for a list of regions. For each region, looks up
its color via cn_region_color/3. Then folds over the color list with
cn_tally_ to produce a list of Color-N association pairs.

END OF PART 107


PART 108: STRIPE PACK - UNIFORM ROW AND COLUMN STRIPE OPERATIONS

Layer 97 - sr_* prefix

The stripe pack provides predicates for detecting uniform rows and columns
(stripes), listing non-uniform rows and columns, filling individual and
multiple rows or columns with a color, computing row-column intersections, and
filling all cells at those intersections. A stripe is any row or column where
every cell holds the same value.

SR-SR-001: sr_uniform_row(+Grid, +R, -Color)
Row R (0-based) of Grid has all cells equal to Color. Succeeds if and only if
every cell in row R is identical. Fails if the row contains two or more distinct
values.

SR-SR-002: sr_uniform_col(+Grid, +C, -Color)
Column C (0-based) of Grid has all cells equal to Color. Succeeds if and only if
every cell in column C is identical.

SR-SR-003: sr_uniform_rows(+Grid, +Color, -Rows)
Rows is the sorted list of row indices where every cell equals Color. If no row
is uniformly Color, Rows is the empty list.

SR-SR-004: sr_uniform_cols(+Grid, +Color, -Cols)
Cols is the sorted list of column indices where every cell equals Color. If no
column is uniformly Color, Cols is the empty list.

SR-SR-005: sr_all_stripe_rows(+Grid, -Pairs)
Pairs is the list of R-Color pairs, in row-index order, for all rows that are
uniform. Non-uniform rows are omitted. Each pair has the form R-Color where R is
the 0-based row index and Color is the uniform value.

SR-SR-006: sr_all_stripe_cols(+Grid, -Pairs)
Pairs is the list of C-Color pairs, in column-index order, for all columns that
are uniform. Non-uniform columns are omitted.

SR-SR-007: sr_mixed_rows(+Grid, -Rows)
Rows is the sorted list of row indices that are NOT uniform (contain at least
two distinct values). Mixed rows are the complement of uniform rows.

SR-SR-008: sr_mixed_cols(+Grid, -Cols)
Cols is the sorted list of column indices that are NOT uniform. Mixed columns
are the complement of uniform columns.

SR-SR-009: sr_fill_row(+Grid, +R, +Color, -Result)
Result is Grid with every cell in row R replaced by Color. All other rows are
unchanged. Uses the deterministic internal helper sr_fill_row_.

SR-SR-010: sr_fill_col(+Grid, +C, +Color, -Result)
Result is Grid with every cell in column C replaced by Color. All other cells
are unchanged. Uses the deterministic internal helper sr_fill_col_.

SR-SR-011: sr_fill_rows(+Grid, +Rows, +Color, -Result)
Result is Grid with every row index in Rows filled with Color. Rows is
processed in list order; each filling step produces an intermediate grid
consumed by the next. Uses if-then-else for deterministic dispatch.

SR-SR-012: sr_fill_cols(+Grid, +Cols, +Color, -Result)
Result is Grid with every column index in Cols filled with Color. Cols is
processed in list order. Uses if-then-else for deterministic dispatch.

SR-SR-013: sr_cross_cells(+Grid, +Rows, +Cols, -Cells)
Cells is the list of r(R,C) terms for every pair (R,C) where R is in Rows and
C is in Cols (the Cartesian product). Cells are in row-major order: all columns
for the first row, then all columns for the second row, and so on.

SR-SR-014: sr_cross_fill(+Grid, +Rows, +Cols, +Color, -Result)
Result is Grid with all cells at Rows x Cols intersections set to Color. Also
fills all remaining cells in each listed row and each listed column. Implemented
as sr_fill_rows followed by sr_fill_cols on the intermediate grid.

END OF PART 108


PART 109: DIAGONAL PACK - DIAGONAL LINE EXTRACTION AND FILLING

Layer 98 - dg_* prefix

The diagonal pack provides predicates for extracting, testing, and filling
diagonals and anti-diagonals of 2D grids. A diagonal is a set of cells where
C - R is constant (same offset). An anti-diagonal is a set where R + C is
constant (same sum). The main diagonal has offset 0 (C == R). The main
anti-diagonal has sum NC - 1 (passes through the top-right corner).

DG-DG-001: dg_main_diag(+Grid, -Diag)
Extract the values on the main diagonal (cells where C == R). Diag is a list
of values from top-left to bottom-right. For a non-square NR x NC grid, the
main diagonal has min(NR, NC) elements.

DG-DG-002: dg_anti_diag(+Grid, -Diag)
Extract the values on the main anti-diagonal (cells where R + C = NC - 1).
The main anti-diagonal passes through the top-right corner (0, NC-1) and
extends to the lower-left. Diag is listed in increasing R order.

DG-DG-003: dg_nth_diag(+Grid, +N, -Diag)
Extract the values on the N-th diagonal, where C - R = N. N = 0 is the main
diagonal. N > 0 are superdiagonals (above and right of main). N < 0 are
subdiagonals (below and left of main).

DG-DG-004: dg_nth_anti_diag(+Grid, +N, -Diag)
Extract the values on the N-th anti-diagonal, where R + C = N. N = 0 is the
top-left corner. N = NR + NC - 2 is the bottom-right corner.

DG-DG-005: dg_all_diags(+Grid, -Diags)
Diags is the list of all diagonals in offset order from -(NR-1) to NC-1.
Each element is the list of values on one diagonal.

DG-DG-006: dg_all_anti_diags(+Grid, -ADiags)
ADiags is the list of all anti-diagonals in sum order from 0 to NR+NC-2.
Each element is the list of values on one anti-diagonal.

DG-DG-007: dg_fill_main(+Grid, +Color, -Result)
Result is Grid with every cell on the main diagonal set to Color.

DG-DG-008: dg_fill_anti(+Grid, +Color, -Result)
Result is Grid with every cell on the main anti-diagonal set to Color.

DG-DG-009: dg_fill_nth_diag(+Grid, +N, +Color, -Result)
Result is Grid with every cell on the N-th diagonal (C-R = N) set to Color.

DG-DG-010: dg_fill_nth_anti_diag(+Grid, +N, +Color, -Result)
Result is Grid with every cell on the N-th anti-diagonal (R+C = N) set to Color.

DG-DG-011: dg_cell_diag(+R, +C, -N)
N is the diagonal index of cell (R, C). N = C - R. All cells on the same
diagonal share this index.

DG-DG-012: dg_cell_anti_diag(+R, +C, -N)
N is the anti-diagonal index of cell (R, C). N = R + C. All cells on the
same anti-diagonal share this index.

DG-DG-013: dg_uniform_diag(+Grid, +N, -Color)
Succeed if the N-th diagonal (C-R = N) has all cells equal to Color. Fails
if the diagonal is empty or contains two or more distinct values.

DG-DG-014: dg_uniform_anti_diag(+Grid, +N, -Color)
Succeed if the N-th anti-diagonal (R+C = N) has all cells equal to Color.
Fails if the anti-diagonal is empty or contains two or more distinct values.

END OF PART 109

PART 110: RECUR PACK (rc_* prefix, Layer 99, Work Package 120)

The recur pack detects and continues arithmetic progressions and repeating
cycles in numeric and symbolic lists. It provides predicates for generating
arithmetic sequences, finding the minimal repeating period of any list,
continuing either type of sequence by N more terms, cycling through an infinite
repetition, and computing element-wise differences.

RC-RC-001: rc_arith(+Start, +Step, +N, -Seq)
Generate an arithmetic sequence of N terms starting at Start with common
difference Step. Seq = [Start, Start+Step, ..., Start+(N-1)*Step].

RC-RC-002: rc_arith_step(+Seq, -Step)
Extract the common difference Step of an arithmetic sequence Seq. Seq must
have at least 2 elements. Fails if not all consecutive differences are equal.

RC-RC-003: rc_is_arith(+Seq, -Step)
Succeed if Seq is an arithmetic sequence with common difference Step. Requires
at least 2 elements. Fails if Seq is not a valid arithmetic sequence.

RC-RC-004: rc_repeat(+Unit, +N, -Seq)
Generate Seq by repeating Unit exactly N times end-to-end.

RC-RC-005: rc_period(+Seq, -Unit)
Find the minimal repeating unit Unit of Seq. Unit is the shortest list such
that repeating it an integer number of times reproduces Seq exactly. The unit
length must evenly divide the sequence length.

RC-RC-006: rc_is_periodic(+Seq, -Unit)
Succeed if Seq is an exact integer-multiple repetition of some list Unit.
Returns the minimal period unit.

RC-RC-007: rc_next_arith(+Seq, +N, -Next)
Compute the next N terms of arithmetic sequence Seq. Detects the step from Seq
and continues from its last element. Next has exactly N elements.

RC-RC-008: rc_next_repeat(+Seq, +N, -Next)
Compute the next N terms of a periodic sequence Seq. Finds the minimal period
of Seq, determines the current offset, and cycles from that offset. Next has
exactly N elements.

RC-RC-009: rc_extend_arith(+Seq, +N, -Extended, -Step)
Extend arithmetic Seq by N more terms. Extended = Seq ++ Next. Step is the
detected common difference.

RC-RC-010: rc_extend_repeat(+Seq, +N, -Extended, -Unit)
Extend periodic Seq by N more terms. Extended = Seq ++ Next. Unit is the
minimal repeating period.

RC-RC-011: rc_cycle_nth(+Unit, +N, -V)
Return the N-th element (1-based) of the infinite cyclic repetition of Unit.
Uses modular arithmetic: index = (N-1) mod length(Unit).

RC-RC-012: rc_zip_with(+List1, +List2, :Goal, -Result)
Pair-wise application of a 3-argument goal over two same-length lists. Calls
Goal(A, B, C) for each pair (A from List1, B from List2) to produce C in Result.

RC-RC-013: rc_diff_list(+Seq, -Diffs)
Compute consecutive element-wise differences of numeric Seq. Diffs has exactly
length(Seq)-1 elements. Diffs[i] = Seq[i+1] - Seq[i].

RC-RC-014: rc_const_diffs(+Seq, -Step)
Succeed if all consecutive differences in numeric Seq equal the same value Step.
Equivalent to rc_is_arith but named for clarity in difference-computation contexts.

END OF PART 110


PART 111: LINE PACK (Layer 100, li_* prefix)

Work Package 121. Straight-line segment detection and drawing for 2D grids.
Provides cells on horizontal, vertical, and 45-degree diagonal segments; draws
those segments into grids; tests collinearity and shared alignment; and queries
endpoints and interior gaps between two cells on the same line.

Predicate specifications (LI-LI-001 through LI-LI-014):

LI-LI-001: li_hline(+R, +C1, +C2, -Cells)
List of R-C cells on the horizontal segment at row R from column C1 to column
C2. Cells are ordered from min(C1,C2) to max(C1,C2). The endpoints are included.

LI-LI-002: li_vline(+C, +R1, +R2, -Cells)
List of R-C cells on the vertical segment at column C from row R1 to row R2.
Cells are ordered from min(R1,R2) to max(R1,R2). The endpoints are included.

LI-LI-003: li_diag_seg(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -Cells)
List of R-C cells on the 45-degree diagonal from (R1,C1) to (R2,C2). Requires
abs(R2-R1) = abs(C2-C1). Cells are in walk order from (R1,C1) to (R2,C2).
Both endpoints are included.

LI-LI-004: li_draw_h(+Grid, +R, +C1, +C2, +Color, -Result)
Return Grid with all cells on the horizontal segment from (R,C1) to (R,C2)
set to Color. The segment endpoints are both included.

LI-LI-005: li_draw_v(+Grid, +C, +R1, +R2, +Color, -Result)
Return Grid with all cells on the vertical segment from (R1,C) to (R2,C)
set to Color. The segment endpoints are both included.

LI-LI-006: li_draw_diag(+Grid, +R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, +Color, -Result)
Return Grid with all cells on the 45-degree diagonal from (R1,C1) to (R2,C2)
set to Color. Requires abs(R2-R1) = abs(C2-C1). Both endpoints are included.

LI-LI-007: li_same_row(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2)
Succeed if cells (R1,C1) and (R2,C2) are in the same row. Equivalent to R1 =:= R2.

LI-LI-008: li_same_col(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2)
Succeed if cells (R1,C1) and (R2,C2) are in the same column. Equivalent to C1 =:= C2.

LI-LI-009: li_same_diag(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2)
Succeed if cells (R1,C1) and (R2,C2) lie on the same diagonal. Two cells share
a diagonal if C - R is constant: C1 - R1 =:= C2 - R2.

LI-LI-010: li_same_anti(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2)
Succeed if cells (R1,C1) and (R2,C2) lie on the same anti-diagonal. Two cells
share an anti-diagonal if R + C is constant: R1 + C1 =:= R2 + C2.

LI-LI-011: li_collinear(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, +R3, +C3)
Succeed if three cells are collinear: they all share a row, a column, a
diagonal (C-R constant), or an anti-diagonal (R+C constant).

LI-LI-012: li_endpoints(+Cells, -First, -Last)
First and last R-C pairs in a non-empty list of collinear cells. First = head
of the list; Last = last element. Deterministic.

LI-LI-013: li_gap(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -Gap)
Cells strictly between (R1,C1) and (R2,C2) on the same line. The two input
cells must be on the same row, column, diagonal, or anti-diagonal. Gap excludes
both endpoints. If the cells are adjacent, Gap = [].

LI-LI-014: li_line_type(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -Type)
Classify the segment from (R1,C1) to (R2,C2). Type is one of: point (same
cell), horizontal (same row), vertical (same column), diagonal (C-R constant),
anti_diagonal (R+C constant), or other.

END OF PART 111


PART 112: RECT PACK (Layer 101, rt_* prefix)

Work Package 122. Rectangle detection and drawing operations for 2D integer-
coordinate grids. Provides cell enumeration for solid rectangles, frames, and
interiors; grid drawing for each region type; containment tests; bounding box
computation; corner extraction; solid/frame verification; overlap detection; and
scaling.

Predicate specifications (RT-RT-001 through RT-RT-014):

RT-RT-001: rt_cells(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -Cells)
All cells in the solid axis-aligned rectangle with top-left corner (R1,C1) and
bottom-right corner (R2,C2). Cells are returned in row-major order. Both corner
cells are included.

RT-RT-002: rt_border(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -Cells)
The frame cells of the rectangle: all cells on the top row, bottom row, left
column, and right column. Interior cells are excluded. Cells are returned sorted
in row-major order. For a 1x1 rectangle the single cell is the entire border.

RT-RT-003: rt_interior(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -Cells)
Cells strictly inside the frame. Requires at least 3 rows and 3 columns; for
thinner rectangles Interior = [].

RT-RT-004: rt_draw(+Grid, +R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, +Color, -Result)
Return Grid with every cell of the solid rectangle set to Color.

RT-RT-005: rt_draw_border(+Grid, +R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, +Color, -Result)
Return Grid with every frame cell of the rectangle set to Color.

RT-RT-006: rt_draw_interior(+Grid, +R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, +Color, -Result)
Return Grid with every interior cell of the rectangle set to Color. If the
rectangle has no interior, Result = Grid.

RT-RT-007: rt_area(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -Area)
Number of cells in the rectangle: (R2 - R1 + 1) * (C2 - C1 + 1).

RT-RT-008: rt_contains(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, +R, +C)
Succeed if cell (R,C) lies within the rectangle. Inclusion is inclusive on all
four sides: R1 =< R =< R2 and C1 =< C =< C2.

RT-RT-009: rt_corners(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -Corners)
List of four corner cells in the order [top-left, top-right, bottom-left,
bottom-right]: [R1-C1, R1-C2, R2-C1, R2-C2].

RT-RT-010: rt_bbox(+Cells, -MinR, -MinC, -MaxR, -MaxC)
Bounding box of a non-empty list of R-C cells. MinR and MaxR are the minimum
and maximum row indices; MinC and MaxC are the minimum and maximum column indices.

RT-RT-011: rt_is_solid(+Grid, +R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -Color)
Succeed if every cell in the rectangle has the same value Color. The color is
unified with the value of the first cell and then verified across all cells.

RT-RT-012: rt_is_frame(+Grid, +R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -Color)
Succeed if every border cell of the rectangle has the same value Color.

RT-RT-013: rt_overlap(+R1a, +C1a, +R2a, +C2a, +R1b, +C1b, +R2b, +C2b)
Succeed if two axis-aligned rectangles share at least one cell. Two rectangles
overlap iff their row intervals overlap (R1a =< R2b and R2a >= R1b) and their
column intervals overlap (C1a =< C2b and C2a >= C1b).

RT-RT-014: rt_scale(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, +Factor, -R2New, -C2New)
Scale the rectangle by integer Factor from its top-left corner (R1,C1). The
top-left stays fixed. The new bottom-right coordinates are:
R2New = R1 + (R2 - R1) * Factor and C2New = C1 + (C2 - C1) * Factor.

END OF PART 112


PART 113: CLUSTER PACK (Layer 102, cl_* prefix)

Work Package 123. Spatial proximity and grouping operations for sets of R-C cells
in 2D integer-coordinate grids. Provides three distance metrics, proximity
filtering, nearest/farthest cell queries, centroid and spread computation,
color-based grouping, distance-sorted ordering, closest/farthest pair detection,
and band filtering.

Predicate specifications (CL-CL-001 through CL-CL-014):

CL-CL-001: cl_chebyshev(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -D)
Chebyshev (L-infinity) distance between cells (R1,C1) and (R2,C2).
D = max(|R2-R1|, |C2-C1|). Equals the number of king moves on a chessboard.

CL-CL-002: cl_manhattan(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -D)
Manhattan (L-1) distance between cells (R1,C1) and (R2,C2).
D = |R2-R1| + |C2-C1|. Equals the minimum number of 4-connected steps.

CL-CL-003: cl_euclidean_sq(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -DSq)
Squared Euclidean distance between cells (R1,C1) and (R2,C2).
DSq = (R2-R1)^2 + (C2-C1)^2. Integer arithmetic; no square root needed
for distance comparisons.

CL-CL-004: cl_within(+R, +C, +D, +Cells, -Near)
Filter Cells to those whose Chebyshev distance to (R,C) is at most D.
Near is the sublist of Cells within the given radius.

CL-CL-005: cl_nearest(+R, +C, +Cells, -Nearest)
The cell in Cells with the smallest Chebyshev distance to (R,C). Cells must
be non-empty. Ties are broken by first occurrence in Cells.

CL-CL-006: cl_farthest(+R, +C, +Cells, -Farthest)
The cell in Cells with the largest Chebyshev distance to (R,C). Cells must
be non-empty. Ties are broken by first occurrence in Cells.

CL-CL-007: cl_center(+Cells, -CR, -CC)
Integer centroid of a non-empty cell set. CR = round(mean row index);
CC = round(mean column index). Uses SWI-Prolog arithmetic round/1.

CL-CL-008: cl_diameter(+Cells, -D)
Maximum pairwise Chebyshev distance within a non-empty cell set. For a
single-element set, D = 0.

CL-CL-009: cl_spread(+Cells, -DR, -DC)
Bounding box dimensions of a non-empty cell set.
DR = max_row - min_row; DC = max_col - min_col.

CL-CL-010: cl_group_by_color(+Grid, +Cells, -Colors, -Groups)
Group R-C cells by their color value in Grid. Colors is a sorted list of
distinct grid values found in the cells; Groups[i] is the sublist of Cells
whose grid value equals Colors[i]. Colors and Groups are parallel lists.

CL-CL-011: cl_sort_by_dist(+R, +C, +Cells, -Sorted)
Sort Cells by Chebyshev distance to (R,C) in ascending order. keysort/2
(built-in, stable) preserves relative order for equal distances.

CL-CL-012: cl_nearest_pair(+Cells, -Cell1, -Cell2)
The pair of cells from Cells with the minimum pairwise Chebyshev distance.
Cells must have at least 2 elements. Ties resolved by first occurrence in
the pair enumeration order.

CL-CL-013: cl_farthest_pair(+Cells, -Cell1, -Cell2)
The pair of cells from Cells with the maximum pairwise Chebyshev distance.
Cells must have at least 2 elements. Ties resolved by first occurrence.

CL-CL-014: cl_cells_in_band(+R1, +R2, +C1, +C2, +Cells, -Band)
Filter Cells to those whose row is in [R1,R2] and column is in [C1,C2].
Inclusion is inclusive on all four sides. The result preserves the order of
Cells.

END OF PART 113


PART 114: RAY CASTING AND LINE-OF-SIGHT OPERATIONS (ray pack, Layer 103)

Work Package 124 adds the ray pack: 14 predicates (ry_* prefix) for casting
directional rays through 2D integer-coordinate grids, detecting obstacles,
testing line-of-sight, computing distances, reflecting directions, and
launching multi-direction casts.

RY-RY-001: ry_in_bounds(+Grid, +R, +C)
Test whether cell (R,C) is within the bounds of Grid (0-based row and column
indices). Succeeds if 0 =< R < NR and 0 =< C < NC where NR and NC are the
number of rows and columns of Grid respectively.

RY-RY-002: ry_cells_in_dir(+Grid, +R, +C, +DR, +DC, -Cells)
Enumerate all in-bounds cells starting one step beyond (R,C) in direction
(DR,DC), stepping by (DR,DC) until leaving the grid. Cells is the ordered
list of cell coordinates R-C encountered. The origin cell (R,C) is NOT
included. Returns [] if the first step is already out of bounds.

RY-RY-003: ry_first_hit(+Grid, +R, +C, +DR, +DC, +Bg, -Hit)
Find the first cell in direction (DR,DC) from (R,C) whose grid value differs
from Bg (the background color). Hit is the R-C coordinate of that cell.
Fails if all cells in the direction until the grid boundary have value Bg.

RY-RY-004: ry_cast_clear(+Grid, +R, +C, +DR, +DC, +Bg, -Clear)
Collect the maximal prefix of cells in direction (DR,DC) from (R,C) that all
have value Bg. Stops before the first non-Bg cell (the obstacle is not
included). Returns [] if the first cell in direction is already an obstacle.

RY-RY-005: ry_distance_to_hit(+Grid, +R, +C, +DR, +DC, +Bg, -D)
Compute the number of steps from (R,C) to the first non-Bg cell in direction
(DR,DC). D = 1 means the immediately adjacent cell is the obstacle. Fails if
no non-Bg cell exists in that direction within the grid bounds.

RY-RY-006: ry_distance_to_edge(+Grid, +R, +C, +DR, +DC, -D)
Compute the number of in-bounds steps available from (R,C) in direction
(DR,DC) before leaving the grid. D = length(ry_cells_in_dir(...)). Returns 0
if the next step is already out of bounds.

RY-RY-007: ry_is_clear(+Grid, +R, +C, +DR, +DC, +Bg)
Succeed if every cell in direction (DR,DC) from (R,C) until the grid boundary
has value Bg. Trivially succeeds if there are no cells in that direction (the
ray exits immediately).

RY-RY-008: ry_project(+Grid, +R, +C, +DR, +DC, +N, -NewR, -NewC)
Compute the coordinates N steps from (R,C) in direction (DR,DC):
NewR = R + DR*N, NewC = C + DC*N. Fails if (NewR,NewC) is out of grid bounds.

RY-RY-009: ry_dir_to_delta(+Dir, -DR, -DC)
Map a named direction atom to a unit step (DR,DC). Recognized names:
up (-1,0), down (1,0), left (0,-1), right (0,1),
ul (-1,-1), ur (-1,1), dl (1,-1), dr (1,1).

RY-RY-010: ry_reflect_h(+DR, +DC, -RDR, -RDC)
Reflect a direction across a horizontal axis: RDR = -DR, RDC = DC. The row
component of motion reverses; the column component is unchanged.

RY-RY-011: ry_reflect_v(+DR, +DC, -RDR, -RDC)
Reflect a direction across a vertical axis: RDR = DR, RDC = -DC. The column
component of motion reverses; the row component is unchanged.

RY-RY-012: ry_los(+Grid, +R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, +Bg)
Test whether two cells have clear line of sight: succeed if all cells strictly
between (R1,C1) and (R2,C2) on the same line have value Bg. The two cells
must be on the same row, column, main diagonal, or anti-diagonal. Trivially
succeeds for adjacent cells (no interior cells).

RY-RY-013: ry_los_cells(+Grid, +R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -Cells)
Enumerate the cells strictly between (R1,C1) and (R2,C2) on the same line
(same row, column, main diagonal, or anti-diagonal), excluding both endpoints.
Grid is accepted for interface consistency but not accessed during computation.

RY-RY-014: ry_cast_all_4(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg, -Hits)
Cast rays from (R,C) in all 4 compass directions (up, down, left, right).
Hits is a list of 4 terms Dir-Result where Dir is the direction name atom and
Result is the R-C coordinate of the first non-Bg cell encountered, or the atom
none if the direction is clear to the grid boundary.

END OF PART 114


PART 115: 2D INTEGER VECTOR ARITHMETIC AND GEOMETRY (vec2 pack, Layer 104)

Work Package 125 adds the vec2 pack: 14 predicates (vv_* prefix) for 2D
integer vector arithmetic and geometry. Vectors are represented as (DR, DC)
displacement pairs. Operations include offset computation, vector addition,
scaling, negation, three magnitude norms, rotation by multiples of 90 degrees,
dot product, cross product, parallelism testing, and region translation.

VV-VV-001: vv_offset(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -DR, -DC)
Compute the displacement vector from cell (R1,C1) to cell (R2,C2).
DR = R2 - R1, DC = C2 - C1. The vector encodes how many rows and columns
separate the two cells.

VV-VV-002: vv_add(+R, +C, +DR, +DC, -NR, -NC)
Apply displacement vector (DR,DC) to point (R,C) to obtain (NR,NC).
NR = R + DR, NC = C + DC. The inverse of vv_offset when applied from (R1,C1)
using vv_offset(R1,C1,R2,C2,DR,DC).

VV-VV-003: vv_scale(+DR, +DC, +K, -SDR, -SDC)
Scale vector (DR,DC) by integer factor K. SDR = K * DR, SDC = K * DC.
Negative K reverses the direction. K = 0 yields the zero vector.

VV-VV-004: vv_neg(+DR, +DC, -NDR, -NDC)
Negate vector (DR,DC). NDR = -DR, NDC = -DC. The negation points from the
destination back to the origin.

VV-VV-005: vv_len_sq(+DR, +DC, -LSq)
Squared Euclidean length: LSq = DR^2 + DC^2. Integer arithmetic avoids
floating-point computation. Use for distance comparisons; take the square
root externally if the true length is needed.

VV-VV-006: vv_manhattan(+DR, +DC, -M)
L1 (Manhattan) magnitude: M = |DR| + |DC|. The minimum number of 4-connected
steps required to travel the vector.

VV-VV-007: vv_chebyshev(+DR, +DC, -D)
L-infinity (Chebyshev) magnitude: D = max(|DR|, |DC|). The minimum number of
8-connected (king) steps required to travel the vector.

VV-VV-008: vv_rot90_cw(+DR, +DC, -RDR, -RDC)
Rotate vector (DR,DC) 90 degrees clockwise. In row-column coordinates with
the row axis pointing downward: RDR = DC, RDC = -DR.

VV-VV-009: vv_rot90_ccw(+DR, +DC, -RDR, -RDC)
Rotate vector (DR,DC) 90 degrees counter-clockwise. RDR = -DC, RDC = DR.

VV-VV-010: vv_rot180(+DR, +DC, -RDR, -RDC)
Rotate vector (DR,DC) 180 degrees. Equivalent to vv_neg: RDR = -DR, RDC = -DC.

VV-VV-011: vv_dot(+DR1, +DC1, +DR2, +DC2, -D)
Dot product of vectors (DR1,DC1) and (DR2,DC2). D = DR1*DR2 + DC1*DC2.
Positive when vectors point in the same general direction, zero when orthogonal,
negative when they point in opposite directions.

VV-VV-012: vv_cross(+DR1, +DC1, +DR2, +DC2, -C)
Z-component of the 3D cross product for 2D vectors. C = DR1*DC2 - DC1*DR2.
Positive when V2 is counter-clockwise from V1; negative when clockwise; zero
when the vectors are parallel.

VV-VV-013: vv_parallel(+DR1, +DC1, +DR2, +DC2)
Succeed if two vectors are parallel (their 2D cross product is zero). Parallel
includes anti-parallel (opposite directions) and the zero vector case.

VV-VV-014: vv_translate_region(+Cells, +DR, +DC, -NewCells)
Translate a list of R-C cell coordinates by displacement vector (DR,DC).
Each cell R-C in Cells becomes (R+DR)-(C+DC) in NewCells. Preserves order.

END OF PART 115


PART 116: BFS SPREADING, DISTANCE MAPS, AND REACHABILITY (spread pack, Layer 105)

Work Package 126 adds the spread pack: 14 predicates (sd_* prefix) for
Breadth-First Search (BFS) spreading, distance map computation, reachability
queries, ring and zone filtering, Voronoi-style assignment, color spreading,
distance overlay, and single-step BFS expansion over 2D integer-coordinate
grids with a background color. The BFS traverses only cells whose value equals
the specified background color.

SD-SD-001: sd_dist_map(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg, -DistMap)
Compute the BFS distance map from source cell (R,C) through cells with value
Bg. DistMap is a list of Cell-D pairs giving the BFS distance D from (R,C) to
every reachable Bg cell including (R,C) itself at D=0. Returns the empty list
if (R,C) does not have value Bg.

SD-SD-002: sd_dist_multi(+Grid, +Seeds, +Bg, -DistMap)
Multi-source BFS distance map. Seeds is a list of R-C cell coordinates that
serve as simultaneous BFS origins. DistMap gives the minimum BFS distance from
any seed to every reachable Bg cell. Non-Bg seeds are silently filtered before
the search begins.

SD-SD-003: sd_reachable(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg, -Cells)
All Bg cells reachable from (R,C) by 4-connected steps through Bg cells.
Returns a sorted list of R-C cell coordinates.

SD-SD-004: sd_path_dist(+Grid, +R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, +Bg, -D)
BFS shortest path distance from (R1,C1) to (R2,C2) through Bg cells. D is the
minimum number of 4-connected steps. Fails if (R2,C2) is not reachable from
(R1,C1) through Bg cells.

SD-SD-005: sd_path_exists(+Grid, +R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, +Bg)
Succeed if (R2,C2) is reachable from (R1,C1) by 4-connected steps through Bg
cells. Fails otherwise. Derived from sd_path_dist.

SD-SD-006: sd_ring(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg, +D, -Cells)
All Bg cells at exactly BFS distance D from (R,C). Returns a sorted list.

SD-SD-007: sd_zone(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg, +MaxD, -Cells)
All Bg cells at BFS distance at most MaxD from (R,C). Returns a sorted list.

SD-SD-008: sd_dist_to_set(+Grid, +R, +C, +Targets, +Bg, -D)
Minimum BFS distance from (R,C) to any cell in the list Targets through Bg
cells. Fails if no target cell is reachable.

SD-SD-009: sd_farthest(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg, -Cell)
The Bg cell with the greatest BFS distance from (R,C). When multiple cells
share the maximum distance the first in BFS traversal order is returned.

SD-SD-010: sd_expand_once(+Grid, +Frontier, +Visited, +Bg, -NextFrontier)
One BFS expansion step. Frontier is a list of R-C cells at the current BFS
level. Returns the sorted, deduplicated list of Bg 4-neighbors of any Frontier
cell that are not in Frontier or Visited.

SD-SD-011: sd_spread_color(+Grid, +Color, +Bg, +MaxD, -Out)
Spread Color cells outward through Bg cells up to MaxD BFS steps. Cells of
value Color serve as multi-source BFS seeds. Each Bg cell within MaxD steps of
any seed is set to Color in the output grid. Color cells themselves are
unchanged.

SD-SD-012: sd_max_dist(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg, -MaxD)
The maximum BFS distance from (R,C) to any reachable Bg cell. Returns 0 when
(R,C) is the only reachable Bg cell.

SD-SD-013: sd_fill_dist(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg, -Out)
Overlay BFS distances onto the grid. Each Bg cell reachable from (R,C) is set
to its BFS distance in the output. Unreachable Bg cells and non-Bg cells retain
their original values.

SD-SD-014: sd_voronoi(+Grid, +Seeds, +Bg, -Assignment)
Voronoi assignment of Bg cells to the nearest seed. Seeds is a list of R-C
cells; each is assigned a 1-based index. Assignment is a list of Cell-SeedIdx
pairs. Ties (equal distance to two seeds) are broken in favour of the seed with
the lower index. Only Bg cells reachable from at least one seed are included.
Non-Bg seeds are filtered before indexing.

END OF PART 116


PART 117: ENCLOSURE PACK (en_* prefix, Layer 106)
Work Package 127

Overview:
The enclosure pack classifies background (Bg) cells in a 2D integer-coordinate
grid as exterior (reachable from the grid border by 4-connected Bg steps) or
interior (enclosed by non-Bg walls). It also decomposes color regions into
boundary vs. interior subsets and tests spatial surround. All predicates are
deterministic and use the en_* prefix.

EN-EN-001: en_border_cells(+Grid, -Cells)
All cells on the four edges of Grid (row 0, row NR-1, col 0, col NC-1),
returned as a sorted list of R-C pairs.

EN-EN-002: en_outer_cells(+Grid, +Bg, -Cells)
All Bg cells reachable from any border cell of Grid by 4-connected Bg steps.
These are the exterior Bg cells. Returned as a sorted list.

EN-EN-003: en_inner_cells(+Grid, +Bg, -Cells)
All Bg cells NOT reachable from the grid border by 4-connected Bg steps.
These are the enclosed (interior) Bg cells. Returned as a sorted list.
Computed as the set difference of all Bg cells minus exterior Bg cells.

EN-EN-004: en_is_inner(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg)
Succeed if cell (R,C) is a Bg cell that is enclosed (not reachable from
the grid border). Fails if (R,C) is not a Bg cell or is reachable from
the border. Deterministic.

EN-EN-005: en_is_outer(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg)
Succeed if cell (R,C) is a Bg cell that is exterior (reachable from the
grid border). Fails if (R,C) is not a Bg cell or is enclosed. Deterministic.

EN-EN-006: en_fill_inner(+Grid, +Bg, +Color, -Out)
Replace all enclosed Bg cells with Color in the output grid. All other cells
are unchanged. Out equals Grid if there are no enclosed Bg cells.

EN-EN-007: en_inner_count(+Grid, +Bg, -N)
N is the number of enclosed Bg cells in Grid.

EN-EN-008: en_has_inner(+Grid, +Bg)
Succeed if Grid contains at least one enclosed Bg cell. Fails if there
are no enclosed Bg cells. Deterministic.

EN-EN-009: en_inner_components(+Grid, +Bg, -Comps)
Comps is the list of 4-connected components of enclosed Bg cells. Each
element of Comps is a list of R-C cells forming one connected component.
Returns the empty list if there are no enclosed Bg cells.

EN-EN-010: en_outer_components(+Grid, +Bg, -Comps)
Comps is the list of 4-connected components of exterior Bg cells. Each
element of Comps is a list of R-C cells forming one connected component.
Returns the empty list if there are no exterior Bg cells.

EN-EN-011: en_fill_hole(+Grid, +Bg, +R, +C, +Color, -Out)
Fill the enclosed Bg component that contains cell (R,C) with Color.
Fails if (R,C) is not an enclosed Bg cell. Only the component containing
(R,C) is painted; other enclosed components are unchanged.

EN-EN-012: en_boundary_cells(+Grid, +Color, -Cells)
All cells of value Color that lie on the Color region boundary: a Color
cell is a boundary cell if it has fewer than 4 in-bounds neighbors (i.e.,
it is on the grid edge) or if at least one of its 4 in-bounds neighbors
has a value different from Color. Returns a sorted list.

EN-EN-013: en_interior_cells(+Grid, +Color, -Cells)
All cells of value Color that are strictly interior to the Color region:
a Color cell is interior if it has exactly 4 in-bounds neighbors (not on
the grid edge) and all 4 neighbors also have value Color. Returns a sorted
list. An interior cell is the complement of a boundary cell within the
Color region.

EN-EN-014: en_is_surrounded(+Grid, +R, +C, +WallColor)
Succeed if every 4-adjacent neighbor of cell (R,C) is either out of bounds
or has value WallColor. Fails if any in-bounds neighbor has a value other
than WallColor. Deterministic.

END OF PART 117


PART 118 - HULL PACK: Convex Hull and Polygon Geometry

Layer 107. Module: hull. Prefix: hu_.
Work Package 128. Implements Andrew's monotone chain convex hull algorithm
and derived polygon geometry operations on 2D integer-coordinate cell sets.

HU-HU-001: hu_convex_hull(+Cells, -Hull)
Compute the convex hull of Cells using Andrew's monotone chain algorithm.
Hull is a list of R-C vertex cells in clockwise screen order (R increases
downward). Collinear points are excluded. Degenerate inputs: empty list
gives [], single cell gives [that cell].

HU-HU-002: hu_is_convex(+Cells)
Succeed if Cells forms a convex discrete shape: the set of cells equals
the complete set of grid cells inside (or on) its convex hull within the
bounding box. Fails for shapes with missing interior cells or concavities.

HU-HU-003: hu_hull_size(+Cells, -N)
N is the number of vertices in the convex hull of Cells. Collinear points
are not counted. Returns 0 for empty input, 1 for a single cell, 2 for
collinear multi-cell inputs.

HU-HU-004: hu_hull_area2(+Cells, -A2)
A2 is twice the area of the convex hull, computed via the shoelace formula
on the ordered hull vertices. Always a non-negative integer. Returns 0 for
degenerate hulls with fewer than 3 vertices.

HU-HU-005: hu_in_hull(+R, +C, +Hull)
Succeed if cell (R,C) lies inside or on the convex hull Hull. Hull must be
a list of R-C vertices as returned by hu_convex_hull. For a 2-vertex hull
(line segment), the test requires collinearity and bounding-box membership.
For 3+ vertices, all edge cross products must be non-positive.

HU-HU-006: hu_cells_in_hull(+Grid, +Cells, -InHull)
InHull is the sorted list of all cells (R,C) in Grid that lie inside or on
the convex hull of Cells. Grid is used only for its dimensions.

HU-HU-007: hu_fill_hull(+Grid, +Cells, +Color, -Out)
Out is Grid with every cell inside the convex hull of Cells set to Color.
Cells outside the hull are unchanged.

HU-HU-008: hu_concavities(+Grid, +Cells, +Bg, -Missing)
Missing is the sorted list of cells in Grid with value Bg that are inside
the convex hull of Cells but absent from Cells themselves. These represent
the concavities (dents) in the shape.

HU-HU-009: hu_diameter(+Cells, -P1, -P2, -D2)
P1 and P2 are the pair of cells in Cells with the maximum squared
Euclidean distance; D2 is that squared distance. Fails if Cells has fewer
than 2 elements.

HU-HU-010: hu_aspect(+Cells, -H, -W)
H is the row-span (MaxR - MinR) and W is the column-span (MaxC - MinC) of
the convex hull bounding box. Returns H=0, W=0 for an empty Cells list.

HU-HU-011: hu_is_rect(+Cells)
Succeed if the convex hull of Cells has exactly 4 vertices and all four
interior angles are exactly 90 degrees. Handles both axis-aligned and
tilted rectangles. Fails for non-quadrilateral hulls or non-right angles.

HU-HU-012: hu_hull_perim2(+Cells, -P2)
P2 is the sum of squared edge lengths of the convex hull (including the
closing edge back to the first vertex). Approximates the perimeter without
floating-point arithmetic. Returns 0 for hulls with fewer than 2 vertices.

HU-HU-013: hu_centroid(+Cells, -AvgR, -AvgC)
AvgR and AvgC are the integer floor of the average row and column of the
convex hull vertices (not of all cells in Cells). Fails if Cells is empty.

HU-HU-014: hu_hull_contains(+Cells, +SubCells)
Succeed if every cell in SubCells lies inside or on the convex hull of
Cells. Uses hu_in_hull for each element of SubCells.

END OF PART 118


PART 119 - PATCH PACK SPECIFICATION (Layer 108)

Work Package 129: patch pack (pa_* prefix, Layer 108).

Provides sub-grid extraction and template matching for integer-valued grids.
A "patch" is a rectangular sub-grid represented as a list of lists of integers.

PA-PA-001: pa_extract(+Grid, +R0, +C0, +H, +W, -Patch)
Patch is the H x W sub-grid of Grid starting at row R0 (0-based) and column C0.
H rows are taken from R0 to R0+H-1; from each row, W columns starting at C0.
Fails if R0+H or C0+W exceeds the grid dimensions.

PA-PA-002: pa_dims(+Patch, -H, -W)
H is the number of rows and W is the number of columns in Patch.
An empty patch (zero rows) gives H=0, W=0.

PA-PA-003: pa_match(+Grid, +Patch, -R0, -C0)
Non-deterministically enumerate all 0-based top-left positions (R0, C0) where
Patch occurs exactly in Grid. Backtracks over all matching positions in
row-major order. Fails if no match exists.

PA-PA-004: pa_match_all(+Grid, +Patch, -Positions)
Positions is the list of all R0-C0 pairs where Patch occurs exactly in Grid,
in row-major enumeration order. Returns [] if no match exists.

PA-PA-005: pa_match_count(+Grid, +Patch, -N)
N is the count of positions where Patch occurs exactly in Grid. Returns 0 if
Patch does not appear.

PA-PA-006: pa_match_bg(+Grid, +Patch, +Bg, -Positions)
Positions is the list of all R0-C0 pairs where Patch matches Grid with Bg
treated as a wildcard: a Bg cell in Patch matches any cell value in Grid;
non-Bg cells must match exactly.

PA-PA-007: pa_slides(+Grid, +H, +W, -Patches)
Patches is the list of all overlapping H x W sub-patches in row-major order,
each represented as R0-C0-Patch. The number of patches is
(NR-H+1) * (NC-W+1) where NR and NC are the grid dimensions.

PA-PA-008: pa_unique_patches(+Grid, +H, +W, -Unique)
Unique is the sorted list of all distinct H x W patches that appear at least
once in Grid. Sort order is standard Prolog term order on list-of-list terms.

PA-PA-009: pa_most_common_patch(+Grid, +H, +W, -Patch, -Count)
Patch is the H x W sub-patch that appears most often in Grid; Count is its
occurrence count. On ties, the patch first in term sort order wins.
Fails if no H x W patches fit in Grid.

PA-PA-010: pa_diff(+PatchA, +PatchB, -Cells)
Cells is the sorted list of R-C pairs where PatchA and PatchB have different
values. Both patches must have the same dimensions. Returns [] if identical.

PA-PA-011: pa_is_uniform(+Patch, -Color)
Succeed if every cell in Patch has the same value Color. Fails if Patch is
empty or contains more than one distinct value.

PA-PA-012: pa_flip_h(+Patch, -Flipped)
Flipped is Patch with each row reversed (horizontal / left-right mirror).
Each row is individually reversed; row order is unchanged.

PA-PA-013: pa_flip_v(+Patch, -Flipped)
Flipped is Patch with the row order reversed (vertical / top-bottom mirror).
The content of each row is unchanged; only the sequence of rows is reversed.

PA-PA-014: pa_rot90(+Patch, -Rotated)
Rotated is Patch rotated 90 degrees clockwise. For an H x W input the output
is W x H. Formula: Rotated(r', c') = Patch(H-1-c', r').

END OF PART 119


PART 120 - SIGNAL PACK SPECIFICATION (Layer 109)

Work Package 130: signal pack (sg_* prefix, Layer 109).

Provides 1D signal analysis predicates for detecting local extrema, testing
monotone order, computing consecutive differences and slope signs, locating
maximum and minimum positions by index, partitioning values by threshold, and
extracting row, column, and cross-shaped value profiles from grids.

SG-SG-001: sg_peaks(+List, -PeakIdxs)
PeakIdxs is the sorted list of 0-based indices of strict interior local
maxima in List. Index I is a peak if I > 0, I < length(List)-1, and
List[I] > List[I-1] and List[I] > List[I+1]. Returns [] for lists of
length < 3 or when no interior maxima exist.

SG-SG-002: sg_valleys(+List, -ValleyIdxs)
ValleyIdxs is the sorted list of 0-based indices of strict interior local
minima. Index I is a valley if List[I] < both immediate neighbors.

SG-SG-003: sg_argmax(+List, -Idx)
Idx is the 0-based index of the maximum value in List. The first (leftmost)
occurrence wins on ties. Fails if List is empty.

SG-SG-004: sg_argmin(+List, -Idx)
Idx is the 0-based index of the minimum value in List. The first occurrence
wins on ties. Fails if List is empty.

SG-SG-005: sg_diffs(+List, -Diffs)
Diffs is the list of consecutive element-wise differences. Diffs[i] =
List[i+1] - List[i]. Length(Diffs) = length(List) - 1. Returns [] for
lists of length 0 or 1.

SG-SG-006: sg_slope_signs(+List, -Signs)
Signs[i] is 1 if List[i+1] > List[i], -1 if List[i+1] < List[i], 0 if
equal. Uses sg_diffs and maplist over sg_sign_.

SG-SG-007: sg_is_increasing(+List)
Succeed if List is strictly increasing (each element < the next). Vacuously
true for lists of length 0 or 1.

SG-SG-008: sg_is_decreasing(+List)
Succeed if List is strictly decreasing (each element > the next).

SG-SG-009: sg_is_nondecreasing(+List)
Succeed if List is non-strictly increasing (each element =< the next).
Strictly increasing lists also qualify.

SG-SG-010: sg_is_nonincreasing(+List)
Succeed if List is non-strictly decreasing (each element >= the next).

SG-SG-011: sg_threshold(+List, +T, -AboveIdxs, -BelowOrEqIdxs)
AboveIdxs is the sorted list of 0-based indices where List[i] > T.
BelowOrEqIdxs is the sorted list where List[i] =< T.

SG-SG-012: sg_row_profile(+Grid, +R, -Values)
Values is the list of cell values in row R (0-based) of Grid.
Equivalent to nth0(R, Grid, Values).

SG-SG-013: sg_col_profile(+Grid, +C, -Values)
Values is the list of cell values in column C (0-based) of Grid,
from row 0 to the last row.

SG-SG-014: sg_cross_profile(+Grid, +R, +C, -RowVals, -ColVals)
RowVals is the list of values in row R; ColVals is the list of values in
column C. Together they form the cross-shaped value profile of cell (R, C).

END OF PART 120


PART 121 - HISTOGRAM PACK SPECIFICATION (Layer 110)

Work Package 131: histogram pack (hi_* prefix, Layer 110).

Provides 14 predicates for value frequency analysis: counting occurrences,
computing sorted frequency tables, finding the most and least common values,
testing for value presence and uniformity, selecting the top-N most frequent
values, ranking values by frequency, and computing frequency tables and modal
values from 2D integer grids.

HI-HI-001: hi_count(+List, +V, -N)
N is the number of times value V appears in List. Uses include/3 with ==(V)
to collect matching elements, then length/2 to count them. Returns 0 if V
is not present. Works for any list including the empty list.

HI-HI-002: hi_freq(+List, -Pairs)
Pairs is the list of V-Count pairs for every distinct value in List, sorted
by value ascending. An empty list gives []. Computed by sort/2 to get distinct
values, then hi_count for each.

HI-HI-003: hi_mode(+List, -V, -N)
V is the most frequent value in List; N is its occurrence count. On ties,
the value with the smallest sort order wins (first in hi_sorted_by_freq).
Fails if List is empty.

HI-HI-004: hi_rare(+List, -V, -N)
V is the least frequent value in List; N is its occurrence count. On ties,
the value with the largest sort order wins (last in hi_sorted_by_freq).
Fails if List is empty.

HI-HI-005: hi_unique_vals(+List, -Vals)
Vals is the sorted list of distinct values in List. Equivalent to sort/2.

HI-HI-006: hi_unique_count(+List, -N)
N is the number of distinct values in List. Returns 0 for the empty list.

HI-HI-007: hi_sorted_by_freq(+List, -Pairs)
Pairs is the list of V-Count pairs sorted by Count descending. Ties in count
are broken by value ascending. Implemented by negating counts, using keysort
(stable, ascending), then recovering the original counts. The stable sort
preserves the value-ascending order for equal counts.

HI-HI-008: hi_top_n(+List, +N, -TopN)
TopN is the list of the N most frequent V-Count pairs from List. Computed
via hi_sorted_by_freq and prefix extraction with length/2 + append/3.
Fails if List has fewer than N distinct values.

HI-HI-009: hi_has_value(+List, +V)
Succeed if V appears at least once in List. Uses memberchk/2 for determinism.

HI-HI-010: hi_all_equal(+List, -V)
Succeed if every element of List equals V. V is unified with the first
element; forall/2 over member/2 verifies each remaining element with =:=.
Fails for the empty list (no head element to unify).

HI-HI-011: hi_grid_freq(+Grid, -Pairs)
Pairs is the frequency table of all cell values in Grid (a list of rows),
sorted by value ascending. Flattens the grid with append/2, then calls
hi_freq.

HI-HI-012: hi_grid_mode(+Grid, -Color, -Count)
Color is the most frequent cell value in Grid; Count is its occurrence count.
Flattens the grid and calls hi_mode.

HI-HI-013: hi_grid_rare(+Grid, -Color, -Count)
Color is the least frequent cell value in Grid; Count is its occurrence count.
Flattens the grid and calls hi_rare.

HI-HI-014: hi_rank(+List, +V, -Rank)
Rank is the 1-based rank of value V by frequency in List, where Rank 1 is
