the most frequent. Uses hi_sorted_by_freq and nth1/3 with a cut after the
first match for determinism. Fails if V does not appear in List.

END OF PART 121


PART 122 - ZOOM PACK SPECIFICATION (Layer 111)

Work Package 132: zoom pack (zm_* prefix, Layer 111).

Provides 14 predicates for integer-factor grid scaling: upscaling each cell
to an FxF block, downsampling by sampling or mode, inferring the scale factor
between grids, testing scaled equivalence, computing scaled dimensions,
extracting and splitting FxF tiles, finding the dominant color of a tile, and
tiling a small grid NR x NC times.

ZM-ZM-001: zm_scale_up(+Grid, +F, -Big)
Big is Grid scaled up by integer factor F. Each cell becomes an FxF block
of the same color. Big has H*F rows and W*F columns where Grid is H x W.
Empty grid scales to empty. Implemented recursively: scale each row
horizontally, then duplicate the scaled row F times vertically.

ZM-ZM-002: zm_scale_down(+Grid, +F, -Small)
Small is Grid downsampled by factor F by sampling row 0, F, 2F, ... and
within each sampled row column 0, F, 2F, ... (top-left corner of each FxF
block). Small has (H // F) rows and (W // F) columns.

ZM-ZM-003: zm_scale_up_row(+Row, +F, -BigRow)
BigRow is Row with each element repeated F consecutive times. Empty row
gives empty result. Implemented recursively: build F copies of the head
element via findall + between, append to the recursively scaled tail.

ZM-ZM-004: zm_scale_down_row(+Row, +F, -SmallRow)
SmallRow contains every Fth element of Row starting at index 0. Implemented
via findall + between + nth0, keeping only indices where I mod F = 0.

ZM-ZM-005: zm_scale_factor(+Small, +Big, -F)
F is the integer scale factor such that zm_scale_up(Small, F) = Big. Infers
F from the column width ratio of the first rows: F = W_Big // W_Small.
Fails if the ratio is not exact.

ZM-ZM-006: zm_is_scaled_up(+Small, +Big, +F)
Succeed if Big is the F-factor upscaling of Small. Verifies by calling
zm_scale_up and unifying.

ZM-ZM-007: zm_dims_up(+H, +W, +F, -BH, -BW)
BH = H * F and BW = W * F: the dimensions of a H x W grid after upscaling
by factor F.

ZM-ZM-008: zm_dims_down(+H, +W, +F, -SH, -SW)
SH = H // F and SW = W // F: the dimensions of a H x W grid after integer
downsampling by factor F.

ZM-ZM-009: zm_extract_block(+Grid, +F, +BR, +BC, -Block)
Block is the FxF sub-grid at tile position (BR, BC), 0-based from the
top-left. Row start = BR * F, column start = BC * F. Uses the private
helper zm_take_cols_ to extract the column range from each row.

ZM-ZM-010: zm_split_blocks(+Grid, +F, -Blocks)
Blocks is the flat list of all FxF tile blocks from Grid in row-major order:
positions (0,0), (0,1), ..., (NR-1,NC-1). Uses zm_blocks_dims to compute
the layout, then zm_extract_block for each position.

ZM-ZM-011: zm_blocks_dims(+Grid, +F, -NR, -NC)
NR = H // F and NC = W // F: the number of FxF tile blocks along each
dimension of Grid.

ZM-ZM-012: zm_block_color(+Grid, +F, +BR, +BC, -Color)
Color is the single color value of the uniform FxF block at tile position
(BR, BC). Extracts the block, flattens it, binds Color to the first cell,
and uses forall + member + =:= to verify uniformity. Fails if the block
contains more than one distinct color.

ZM-ZM-013: zm_scale_down_mode(+Grid, +F, -Small)
Small is a downsampled grid where each output cell is the most common (mode)
value among the F x F source block. On count ties, the largest value wins
(msort + last ordering on N-V pairs). Uses the private helper zm_mode_.

ZM-ZM-014: zm_tile_grid(+Tile, +NR, +NC, -Grid)
Grid is Tile repeated NR times vertically and NC times horizontally. First
each Tile row is extended NC times horizontally (each element repeated NC
times within a row expansion), then the full block row is repeated NR times.

END OF PART 122


PART 123 - OFFSET PACK SPECIFICATION (Layer 112)

Work Package 133: offset pack (od_* prefix, Layer 112).

Provides 14 predicates for grid shifting and circular rolling: shifting grids
in four directions with background fill (content moves, vacated cells become
background, overflow is dropped), circular rolling in four directions (content
wraps around), single-row equivalents of shift and roll, shifting one specific
color within a grid while leaving other content unchanged, and inferring the
shift displacement between two grids.

OD-OD-001: od_shift_row(+Row, +N, +Bg, -Shifted)
Shifted is Row shifted rightward by N cells. The leftmost N positions become
Bg; the last N elements of Row are dropped. For N=0, Shifted = Row.

OD-OD-002: od_shift_row_left(+Row, +N, +Bg, -Shifted)
Shifted is Row shifted leftward by N cells. The rightmost N positions become
Bg; the first N elements of Row are dropped.

OD-OD-003: od_roll_row(+Row, +N, -Rolled)
Rolled is Row circular-shifted rightward by N. The last N elements (modulo
length) wrap to become the first N elements. N is normalized by mod.

OD-OD-004: od_shift_right(+Grid, +N, +Bg, -Shifted)
Shifted is Grid with each row shifted rightward by N using od_shift_row.

OD-OD-005: od_shift_left(+Grid, +N, +Bg, -Shifted)
Shifted is Grid with each row shifted leftward by N using od_shift_row_left.

OD-OD-006: od_shift_down(+Grid, +N, +Bg, -Shifted)
Shifted is Grid with content moved downward by N rows. Top N rows become Bg
rows of the correct width; the bottom N rows of content are dropped.

OD-OD-007: od_shift_up(+Grid, +N, +Bg, -Shifted)
Shifted is Grid with content moved upward by N rows. Top N rows of content
are dropped; bottom N rows become Bg rows.

OD-OD-008: od_shift_dir(+Grid, +Dir, +N, +Bg, -Shifted)
Dispatch shift by direction atom. Dir is one of: right, left, down, up.
Uses if-then-else for determinism.

OD-OD-009: od_roll_right(+Grid, +N, -Rolled)
Each row is circular-shifted right by N using maplist and od_roll_row.

OD-OD-010: od_roll_left(+Grid, +N, -Rolled)
Each row is circular-shifted left by N. The first N elements (mod width)
wrap to the end.

OD-OD-011: od_roll_down(+Grid, +N, -Rolled)
Rows are circular-shifted downward by N. The last N rows (mod height) wrap
to the top.

OD-OD-012: od_roll_up(+Grid, +N, -Rolled)
Rows are circular-shifted upward by N. The first N rows (mod height) wrap to
the bottom.

OD-OD-013: od_shift_color(+Grid, +Color, +DR, +DC, +Bg, -Result)
Result is Grid with all cells equal to Color translated by (DR rows, DC
columns). For each output cell (R, C): if Grid[R-DR][C-DC] = Color, the
output is Color; else if Grid[R][C] = Color (and no shifted Color lands here),
the output is Bg; else the output is Grid[R][C]. Translated cells that go out
of bounds are clipped (lost).

OD-OD-014: od_infer_shift(+GridA, +GridB, +Bg, -DR, -DC)
DR and DC are the integer row and column displacement such that shifting GridA
by (DR, DC) produces GridB. Positive DR = downward, positive DC = rightward.
Tries all integer displacements in [-H+1, H-1] x [-W+1, W-1] and commits to
the first match using od_apply_shift_.

END OF PART 123


PART 124: INTERLEAVE PACK

Work Package 134. Layer 113. Prefix: il_.

The interleave pack provides predicates for merging two grids by alternating
rows or columns, splitting an interleaved grid back into its components,
inserting separator rows or columns (weaving), removing them (unweaving),
extracting every Nth row or column (stride), selecting rows or columns by
index list, round-robin interleaving of N grids, and partitioning rows into
consecutive blocks of equal size.

IL-IL-001: il_rows(+GridA, +GridB, -Result)
Merge two same-height grids by alternating rows. Row 0 of Result is row 0
of GridA; row 1 is row 0 of GridB; row 2 is row 1 of GridA; etc. Both grids
must have the same number of rows. Result has twice that many rows.

IL-IL-002: il_cols(+GridA, +GridB, -Result)
Merge two same-dimension grids by alternating columns. For each pair of
corresponding rows, elements are interleaved: A[0], B[0], A[1], B[1], ...
Both grids must have the same height and width. Result has the same height
and twice the width.

IL-IL-003: il_derows(+Grid, -Even, -Odd)
Split Grid into even-indexed rows (0, 2, 4, ...) and odd-indexed rows
(1, 3, 5, ...). This is the inverse of il_rows/3 when GridA and GridB had
equal height.

IL-IL-004: il_decols(+Grid, -Even, -Odd)
Split each row into even-indexed elements (columns 0, 2, 4, ...) and
odd-indexed elements (columns 1, 3, 5, ...). This is the inverse of il_cols/3.

IL-IL-005: il_weave_rows(+Grid, +Bg, -Woven)
Insert a background row between every pair of adjacent rows. A grid of H rows
becomes 2*H-1 rows. The background row has the same width as the grid rows,
filled with Bg. A single-row or empty grid is returned unchanged.

IL-IL-006: il_weave_cols(+Grid, +Bg, -Woven)
Insert the value Bg between every pair of adjacent column values in each row.
A row of width W becomes width 2*W-1. A single-element or empty row is
returned unchanged.

IL-IL-007: il_unweave_rows(+Grid, -Core)
Remove odd-indexed rows, keeping only even-indexed rows. Reverses the effect
of il_weave_rows when the odd-indexed rows are separator rows. Delegates to
il_derows and discards the Odd output.

IL-IL-008: il_unweave_cols(+Grid, -Core)
Remove odd-indexed columns, keeping only even-indexed columns. Reverses the
effect of il_weave_cols. Delegates to il_decols and discards the Odd output.

IL-IL-009: il_stride_rows(+Grid, +Step, +Start0, -SubGrid)
Extract every Step-th row starting at 0-based index Start0. Row indices
included are Start0, Start0+Step, Start0+2*Step, ... up to the last row.
Step must be >= 1. Returns an empty grid if Start0 exceeds the grid height.

IL-IL-010: il_stride_cols(+Grid, +Step, +Start0, -SubGrid)
Extract every Step-th column starting at 0-based index Start0. Column indices
included are Start0, Start0+Step, ... up to the last column. Step must be
>= 1. Returns an empty grid for an empty input grid.

IL-IL-011: il_select_rows(+Grid, +Indices, -SubGrid)
Extract rows at the given 0-based index list. SubGrid has one row for each
element of Indices. Indices may contain any valid row numbers in any order.

IL-IL-012: il_select_cols(+Grid, +Indices, -SubGrid)
Extract columns at the given 0-based index list. Each row of SubGrid is the
projection of the corresponding row of Grid onto Indices. Indices may be
in any order.

IL-IL-013: il_rows_n(+Grids, -Result)
Round-robin interleave rows from a list of equal-height grids. If
Grids = [G1, G2, G3] each with H rows, Result is:
G1[0], G2[0], G3[0], G1[1], G2[1], G3[1], ..., G1[H-1], G2[H-1], G3[H-1].
An empty Grids list yields an empty Result.

IL-IL-014: il_block_rows(+Grid, +N, -Blocks)
Partition rows into consecutive groups of N rows. Blocks is a list of
sub-grids each containing exactly N rows, except the last block which may
contain fewer rows if the total row count is not divisible by N.

END OF PART 124


PART 125: PANEL PACK

Work Package 135. Layer 114. Prefix: pn_.

The panel pack provides predicates for detecting rows and columns that consist
entirely of a background value (dividers), splitting a grid at given or
auto-detected divider positions, removing divider rows or columns, splitting
at midpoints into four quadrants, partitioning columns into N equal-width
strips or custom-width slices, and testing whether any divider exists.

PN-PN-001: pn_is_divider_row(+Grid, +R, +Bg)
Succeeds if row R of Grid consists entirely of Bg. Uses forall/2 to assert
that every element of the row is structurally equal (==) to Bg.

PN-PN-002: pn_is_divider_col(+Grid, +C, +Bg)
Succeeds if column C of Grid consists entirely of Bg. Uses forall/2 over
all rows, checking nth0(C, Row, V), V == Bg.

PN-PN-003: pn_divider_rows(+Grid, +Bg, -Rows)
Rows is the sorted list of all 0-based row indices at which
pn_is_divider_row succeeds. Uses findall + between.

PN-PN-004: pn_divider_cols(+Grid, +Bg, -Cols)
Cols is the sorted list of all 0-based column indices at which
pn_is_divider_col succeeds. Gets column count from the first row.

PN-PN-005: pn_split_rows(+Grid, +RowIdxs, -Parts)
Splits Grid at the given row indices. Each row in RowIdxs is a divider and
is excluded from all parts. Parts contains the row bands between consecutive
dividers. Parts has length(RowIdxs) + 1 elements; some may be empty if
two dividers are adjacent or a divider is at row 0 or the last row.

PN-PN-006: pn_split_cols(+Grid, +ColIdxs, -Parts)
Splits Grid at the given column indices. Each column in ColIdxs is excluded.
Parts has length(ColIdxs) + 1 elements. Each part is a sub-grid.

PN-PN-007: pn_auto_split_rows(+Grid, +Bg, -Parts)
Detects all all-Bg rows and splits at them. Equivalent to finding divider
rows and calling pn_split_rows.

PN-PN-008: pn_auto_split_cols(+Grid, +Bg, -Parts)
Detects all all-Bg columns and splits at them. Equivalent to finding divider
columns and calling pn_split_cols.

PN-PN-009: pn_strip_rows(+Grid, +Bg, -Stripped)
Removes all all-Bg rows. Stripped contains the rows whose 0-based index is
not in the divider row list. Uses findall + \+ memberchk.

PN-PN-010: pn_strip_cols(+Grid, +Bg, -Stripped)
Removes all all-Bg columns. Each row of Stripped contains only the column
values whose index is not in the divider column list.

PN-PN-011: pn_quadrants(+Grid, -TL, -TR, -BL, -BR)
Splits Grid at its midpoints: MidR = H // 2, MidC = W // 2. TL covers
rows [0, MidR) and cols [0, MidC); TR covers [0, MidR) and [MidC, W);
BL covers [MidR, H) and [0, MidC); BR covers [MidR, H) and [MidC, W).

PN-PN-012: pn_n_col_parts(+Grid, +N, -Parts)
Splits columns into N equal-width strips. Grid width must be divisible by N.
Each strip has width W // N. Uses findall + between + maplist.

PN-PN-013: pn_col_slices(+Grid, +Widths, -Parts)
Splits columns according to a list of widths. The elements of Widths must
sum to the total grid width. Uses cumulative sums to compute slice boundaries.

PN-PN-014: pn_has_dividers(+Grid, +Bg)
Succeeds if Grid has at least one all-Bg row or all-Bg column. Tests row
dividers first; if none found, tests column dividers. Uses if-then-else.

END OF PART 125


PART 126: SCAN PACK (Layer 115, sn_* prefix)

Work Package: 136
Layer: 115
Module: scan
Prefix: sn_

Purpose: General-purpose grid cell enumeration and manipulation. Provides
predicates for visiting every cell in a grid in row-major, column-major,
boustrophedon, spiral, border, and diagonal traversal orders; reading and
writing individual cells or applying batch updates; mapping a goal over all
cells; filtering cells by a predicate; and building a grid from a sparse list
of cell assignments.

Predicates (14):

SN-SN-001: sn_row_major(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns all R-C-V triples in row-major order: row 0 columns 0..W-1, then row
1 columns 0..W-1, etc. Uses a single findall with row index in the outer loop.

SN-SN-002: sn_col_major(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns all R-C-V triples in column-major order: column 0 rows 0..H-1, then
column 1 rows 0..H-1, etc. Column index is enumerated in the outer loop.

SN-SN-003: sn_cells_of(+Grid, +V, -Cells)
Returns a list of R-C pairs for every cell whose value unifies with V. Uses
findall over both row and column indices.

SN-SN-004: sn_set_cell(+Grid, +R, +C, +V, -New)
Returns a new grid identical to Grid except cell (R,C) holds V. Uses findall
to rebuild the grid row by row; the target row is rebuilt element by element
via the private helper sn_set_elem_.

SN-SN-005: sn_map_cells(+Grid, :Goal, -New)
Applies Goal(R, C, OldV, NewV) to every cell and returns the resulting grid.
Uses nested findall: outer loop over rows, inner loop over columns, with
call/5 to invoke the user-supplied goal.

SN-SN-006: sn_filter_cells(+Grid, :Pred, -Cells)
Returns R-C-V triples for every cell where call(Pred, R, C, V) succeeds.
Uses a single findall that calls the user-supplied predicate for each cell.

SN-SN-007: sn_update_cells(+Grid, +Updates, -New)
Applies a list of R-C-V triples as batch cell updates. For each cell, if the
cell's R-C pair appears in Updates, the value from Updates is used; otherwise
the original value is kept. Uses memberchk for the lookup.

SN-SN-008: sn_zigzag(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns all R-C-V triples in boustrophedon order: even rows are traversed
left-to-right, odd rows are traversed right-to-left. Within each row the
column offset is enumerated left-to-right and the actual column index is
computed using if-then-else on the row parity.

SN-SN-009: sn_spiral_in(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns all R-C-V triples in clockwise spiral order from the outermost ring
inward. Delegates to the recursive helper sn_spiral_ with inclusive bounds
T=0, B=H-1, L=0, R=W-1. Each ring contributes: top row left-to-right, right
column top-to-bottom, bottom row right-to-left (via reverse), left column
bottom-to-top (via reverse). Terminates when T > B or L > R.

SN-SN-010: sn_border_traversal(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns R-C-V triples for the outer border in clockwise order: top row
left-to-right, right column (rows 1..H-1), bottom row right-to-left
(cols W-2..0), left column bottom-to-top (rows H-2..1). Single-row or
single-column grids are handled by if-then-else on H > 1 and W > 1.

SN-SN-011: sn_diag_traversal_ne(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns all R-C-V triples ordered by diagonal index D = R+C from 0 to H+W-2.
Within each diagonal, row increases and column decreases.

SN-SN-012: sn_diag_traversal_se(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns all R-C-V triples ordered by diagonal index D = C-R from -(H-1) to
W-1. Within each diagonal, both row and column increase.

SN-SN-013: sn_grid_from_cells(+H, +W, +Cells, +Bg, -Grid)
Builds an H-by-W grid from a sparse list of R-C-V triples. Cells not
mentioned in the list get the background value Bg. Uses memberchk in an
if-then-else to look up each cell position.

SN-SN-014: sn_index_of(+Grid, +V, -R, -C)
Finds the row R and column C of the first occurrence of V in row-major order.
Uses between/3 for both dimensions and commits with a cut after the first match.

END OF PART 126


PART 127: BOUND PACK (Layer 116, bd_* prefix)

Work Package: 137
Layer: 116
Module: bound
Prefix: bd_

Purpose: Bounding box extraction, querying, cropping, padding, placement, and
region filling for grids. Provides the building blocks for ARC-AGI-2 rules that
need to isolate objects by their tight extent, place sub-grids at computed
positions, or reason about overlapping rectangular regions.

Predicates (14):

BD-BD-001: bd_bbox(+Grid, +Color, -R0, -C0, -R1, -C1)
Computes the tight inclusive bounding box of all cells whose value unifies with
Color. R0, C0 are the minimum row and column; R1, C1 are the maximum. All bounds
are 0-based. Uses findall over all cell positions, then min_list/max_list on the
collected row and column indices. Fails if Color is absent.

BD-BD-002: bd_bbox_h(+R0, +R1, -H)
Height of the inclusive bounding box: H = R1 - R0 + 1.

BD-BD-003: bd_bbox_w(+C0, +C1, -W)
Width of the inclusive bounding box: W = C1 - C0 + 1.

BD-BD-004: bd_crop_bbox(+Grid, +R0, +C0, +R1, +C1, -Sub)
Crops Grid to the inclusive rectangle [R0..R1, C0..C1]. Uses findall over
row indices R0..R1 and the private helper bd_slice_row_ to extract inclusive
column ranges.

BD-BD-005: bd_crop_color(+Grid, +Color, -Sub)
Crops to the tight bounding box of Color. Combines bd_bbox and bd_crop_bbox.
Fails if Color is absent.

BD-BD-006: bd_trim(+Grid, +Bg, -Trimmed)
Removes all all-Bg border rows and columns by finding the bounding box of all
non-Bg cells. Returns [[]] when every cell is Bg.

BD-BD-007: bd_pad(+Grid, +N, +Bg, -Padded)
Adds N background cells on all four sides. The result has H+2*N rows and W+2*N
columns. Uses findall to build background rows and maplist with bd_pad_row_ to
extend each original row.

BD-BD-008: bd_place(+Canvas, +Patch, +R0, +C0, +Bg, -New)
Places Patch into Canvas at top-left position (R0, C0). Canvas cells within the
Patch bounds [R0..R0+PH-1, C0..C0+PW-1] are overwritten by the corresponding
Patch cells. Cells outside the Patch bounds are unchanged. Uses nested findall
with if-then-else on Patch row/column bounds.

BD-BD-009: bd_center(+Grid, +Color, -CR, -CC)
Integer center of Color's bounding box: CR = (R0+R1)//2, CC = (C0+C1)//2.

BD-BD-010: bd_bbox_contains(+R0, +C0, +R1, +C1, +R, +C)
Succeeds if (R,C) lies within the inclusive bounding box [R0..R1, C0..C1].

BD-BD-011: bd_bbox_overlap(+R0A, +C0A, +R1A, +C1A, +R0B, +C0B, +R1B, +C1B)
Succeeds if the two inclusive bounding boxes overlap. Overlap requires:
R1A >= R0B and R0A =< R1B and C1A >= C0B and C0A =< C1B.

BD-BD-012: bd_bbox_union(+R0A,+C0A,+R1A,+C1A,+R0B,+C0B,+R1B,+C1B,-R0,-C0,-R1,-C1)
Smallest inclusive bounding box enclosing both input boxes. Uses min/max.

BD-BD-013: bd_expand(+R0, +C0, +R1, +C1, +N, -ER0, -EC0, -ER1, -EC1)
Expands the bounding box outward by N cells on all sides. The result may extend
outside the original grid bounds.

BD-BD-014: bd_fill_bbox(+Grid, +R0, +C0, +R1, +C1, +Color, -New)
Sets every cell within the inclusive bounding box [R0..R1, C0..C1] to Color.
Uses nested findall with if-then-else on row and column bounds.

END OF PART 127


PART 128: CELLSET PACK (Layer 117, cs_* prefix)

Work Package: 138
Layer: 117
Module: cellset
Prefix: cs_

Purpose: Sparse cell set operations over R-C position lists. Converts between
dense grids and sorted R-C cell sets, performs set-theoretic operations (union,
intersection, difference), translates and normalizes cell sets, queries size and
membership, finds background neighbors, tests shape equality, and applies
geometric transformations (90-degree rotation, horizontal mirror). Provides the
building blocks for ARC-AGI-2 rules that need to manipulate objects as position
sets rather than full grids.

Predicates (14):

CS-CS-001: cs_from_grid(+Grid, +Color, -Cells)
Extracts all R-C positions where Grid cell equals Color as a sorted list. Uses
findall over all row-column pairs, then sort/2 to eliminate duplicates and
produce a canonical ascending order. Returns [] if Color is absent.

CS-CS-002: cs_to_grid(+Cells, +H, +W, +Color, +Bg, -Grid)
Paints a sorted cell set onto an H x W canvas. Builds each row with findall
over column indices, using memberchk(R-C, Cells) to choose Color or Bg for
each cell.

CS-CS-003: cs_union(+A, +B, -Union)
Sorted set union of two cell sets. Appends the two lists and sorts to remove
duplicates, giving a canonical ascending result.

CS-CS-004: cs_intersect(+A, +B, -Inter)
Sorted set intersection. Uses findall to collect members of A that are also in
B (tested with memberchk), then sorts the result.

CS-CS-005: cs_subtract(+A, +B, -Diff)
Set difference: members of A not in B. Delegates to subtract/3 from
library(lists), which uses memberchk for element-level membership.

CS-CS-006: cs_translate(+Cells, +DR, +DC, -Shifted)
Shifts every R-C pair in Cells by (DR, DC). Uses maplist with the private
helper cs_add_(DR, DC). Translation preserves sorted order because row and
column arithmetic offsets are monotone.

CS-CS-007: cs_bbox(+Cells, -R0, -C0, -R1, -C1)
Bounding box of a non-empty cell set. Extracts all row and column indices with
findall, then uses min_list/max_list. Fails if Cells is empty.

CS-CS-008: cs_normalize(+Cells, -Norm, -DR, -DC)
Translates Cells so that the minimum row becomes 0 and the minimum column
becomes 0. Returns the translation offsets DR and DC (both non-positive). Empty
list passes through with zero offsets.

CS-CS-009: cs_size(+Cells, -N)
Number of cells in the set. Uses length/2 (built-in). Returns 0 for [].

CS-CS-010: cs_contains(+Cells, +R, +C)
Deterministic membership test. Succeeds if R-C is in Cells using memberchk/2.

CS-CS-011: cs_adjacent_bg(+Cells, -Adjacent)
Sorted list of all 4-connected background neighbors. For each cell in Cells,
computes four neighbors using offsets (-1,0), (1,0), (0,-1), (0,1), keeps those
not in Cells (tested with \+/memberchk), then sorts to remove duplicates. May
include positions with negative coordinates.

CS-CS-012: cs_same_shape(+A, +B)
Succeeds if A and B have the same shape after normalization to the origin. Both
empty sets succeed. Otherwise normalizes both sets and compares with ==/2.

CS-CS-013: cs_rotate_90(+Cells, +H, -Rotated)
Rotates cell positions 90 degrees clockwise within a grid of H rows. Formula:
new_R = old_C, new_C = H-1-old_R. Uses maplist with cs_rot90_, then sorts to
restore canonical order after the permutation.

CS-CS-014: cs_mirror_h(+Cells, +W, -Mirrored)
Mirrors cell positions horizontally within a grid of W columns. Formula:
new_R = old_R, new_C = W-1-old_C. Uses maplist with cs_mirh_, then sorts.

END OF PART 128


PART 129: LOCATE PACK (Layer 118, lc_* prefix)

Work Package: 139
Layer: 118
Module: locate
Prefix: lc_

Purpose: Pattern location within grids. Provides subgrid template matching,
row and column pattern search, value anchor testing, per-row value counting,
and row/column value containment queries. Provides the building blocks for
ARC-AGI-2 rules that need to find where a sub-pattern occurs in a larger
grid, which rows or columns match a given sequence, and where unique marker
values are positioned.

Predicates (14):

LC-LC-001: lc_subgrid_at(+Grid, +Sub, +R0, +C0)
Tests whether the sub-grid Sub appears at top-left position (R0, C0) in Grid.
Uses forall/2 over all Sub row-column pairs; each pair verifies the Grid cell
at the corresponding offset equals the Sub cell.

LC-LC-002: lc_find_sub(+Grid, +Sub, -R0, -C0)
Finds the first (row-major) top-left position where Sub appears in Grid.
Enumerates candidate positions with between/3 and calls lc_subgrid_at; cuts
after the first match. Fails if Sub does not appear.

LC-LC-003: lc_all_sub(+Grid, +Sub, -Positions)
Returns the list of all R0-C0 pairs where Sub appears in Grid. Uses findall
over all candidate positions with lc_subgrid_at as the filter.

LC-LC-004: lc_subgrid_count(+Grid, +Sub, -N)
Counts how many times Sub appears in Grid. Delegates to lc_all_sub and
measures the result list with length/2.

LC-LC-005: lc_row_pattern(+Grid, +Pattern, -R)
Finds the first row index R where the grid row equals Pattern. Enumerates
row indices with between/3 and uses nth0 with Pattern for direct unification;
cuts after the first match.

LC-LC-006: lc_all_row_pattern(+Grid, +Pattern, -Rows)
Returns all row indices where the grid row equals Pattern. Uses findall
with nth0(R, Grid, Pattern) as the filter.

LC-LC-007: lc_col_pattern(+Grid, +Pattern, -C)
Finds the first column index C whose extracted value list equals Pattern.
Extracts each column with findall over row indices and unifies with Pattern;
cuts after the first match.

LC-LC-008: lc_all_col_pattern(+Grid, +Pattern, -Cols)
Returns all column indices whose value list equals Pattern. The outer findall
collects columns for which the inner findall produces a list that unifies
with Pattern.

LC-LC-009: lc_row_prefix(+Grid, +R, +Prefix, -Rest)
Decomposes grid row R as Prefix ++ Rest using append/3. Prefix can be [] to
retrieve the full row as Rest.

LC-LC-010: lc_row_suffix(+Grid, +R, +Suffix)
Succeeds if grid row R ends with Suffix. Uses append(_, Suffix, Row) with a
cut to make it a deterministic existence test.

LC-LC-011: lc_anchor(+Grid, +V, -R, -C)
Succeeds if exactly one cell in Grid equals V. Collects all V positions with
findall; unifies the result with the single-element pattern [R-C].

LC-LC-012: lc_row_count(+Grid, +V, -Counts)
Returns a list with one integer per row counting occurrences of V in that row.
Uses maplist with the private helper lc_count_in_row_ which uses findall +
member/2 + length/2.

LC-LC-013: lc_row_contains(+Grid, +V, -Rows)
Returns the sorted list of row indices that contain at least one cell equal
to V. Uses findall with member/2 as the containment test, then sort/2 to
remove duplicates.

LC-LC-014: lc_col_contains(+Grid, +V, -Cols)
Returns the sorted list of column indices that contain at least one cell equal
to V. Uses findall with nth0 for cell access, then sort/2 to remove duplicates.

END OF PART 129


PART 130: EXTENDED CELL SELECTION BY VALUE COMPARISON (xsel PACK)

Work Package 140, Layer 119. Module: xsel. Prefix: xs_*.

Purpose: The xsel pack provides extended selection of grid cells based on
numerical value comparisons. It adds threshold tests (less-than, greater-than,
less-than-or-equal, greater-than-or-equal), range queries (between, not-equal),
extremum locators (max cells, min cells), conditional replacement (replace below
or above a threshold, binary threshold mapping), and ordinal value ranking
(sorted unique values, value-to-rank lookup, whole-grid rank transformation).

These predicates complement the arith pack (which does cell-wise arithmetic
and clamping), the histogram pack (which counts value frequencies), and the
count pack (which counts by equality) by adding order-based queries that work
across the full numerical range of cell values.

XS-XS-001: xs_cells_lt(+Grid, +V, -Cells)
Returns the sorted list of R-C pairs for cells whose value is strictly less
than V. Uses findall with a Val < V guard, then sort/2.

XS-XS-002: xs_cells_gt(+Grid, +V, -Cells)
Returns the sorted list of R-C pairs for cells whose value is strictly greater
than V. Uses findall with a Val > V guard, then sort/2.

XS-XS-003: xs_cells_le(+Grid, +V, -Cells)
Returns the sorted list of R-C pairs for cells whose value is less than or
equal to V. Uses findall with a Val =< V guard, then sort/2.

XS-XS-004: xs_cells_ge(+Grid, +V, -Cells)
Returns the sorted list of R-C pairs for cells whose value is greater than or
equal to V. Uses findall with a Val >= V guard, then sort/2.

XS-XS-005: xs_cells_between(+Grid, +Lo, +Hi, -Cells)
Returns the sorted list of R-C pairs for cells whose value is in the closed
interval [Lo, Hi]. Uses findall with Val >= Lo, Val =< Hi guards, then sort/2.

XS-XS-006: xs_cells_ne(+Grid, +V, -Cells)
Returns the sorted list of R-C pairs for cells whose value is not structurally
equal to V. Uses findall with a Val \== V guard, then sort/2.

XS-XS-007: xs_max_cells(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns the sorted list of R-C pairs for all cells containing the maximum
value in Grid. First collects all values via nested member/2 and max_list/2,
then collects positions where the cell equals that maximum.

XS-XS-008: xs_min_cells(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns the sorted list of R-C pairs for all cells containing the minimum
value in Grid. First collects all values via nested member/2 and min_list/2,
then collects positions where the cell equals that minimum.

XS-XS-009: xs_threshold(+Grid, +T, +OnV, +OffV, -Grid2)
Produces Grid2 by replacing each cell value V with OnV if V >= T, otherwise
with OffV. Applies the mapping row-by-row via maplist with nested maplist for
cells.

XS-XS-010: xs_replace_lt(+Grid, +V, +New, -Grid2)
Produces Grid2 by replacing every cell whose value is strictly less than V
with New. Applies the mapping row-by-row via maplist with nested maplist.

XS-XS-011: xs_replace_gt(+Grid, +V, +New, -Grid2)
Produces Grid2 by replacing every cell whose value is strictly greater than V
with New. Applies the mapping row-by-row via maplist with nested maplist.

XS-XS-012: xs_rank_vals(+Grid, -Vals)
Returns the sorted list of unique values appearing in Grid in ascending order.
Uses findall with nested member/2 to collect all cell values, then sort/2 to
deduplicate and order them. The index of each value in Vals is its rank.

XS-XS-013: xs_val_rank(+Grid, +V, -Rank)
Returns the 0-based ordinal rank of value V in the sorted unique value list
of Grid. Rank 0 is the smallest value, Rank N-1 is the largest. Delegates to
xs_rank_vals and uses nth0 with a cut to commit to the unique match. Fails if
V does not appear in Grid.

XS-XS-014: xs_rank_grid(+Grid, -RankGrid)
Produces RankGrid by replacing each cell value with its 0-based ordinal rank
in the sorted unique value list of Grid. Computes xs_rank_vals once, then
applies rank lookup row-by-row via maplist with private helper xs_rank_val_
which uses nth0 + cut.

END OF PART 130


PART 131: CELLULAR AUTOMATON NEIGHBORHOOD AGGREGATION (autom PACK)

Work Package 141, Layer 120. Module: autom. Prefix: at_*.

Purpose: The autom pack provides grid-wide neighborhood aggregation predicates
for symbolic reasoning about cellular patterns. It adds count grids (where each
cell holds the count of a given value among its in-bounds neighbors), boolean
grids (where each cell holds 1/0 based on whether any or all neighbors satisfy
a condition), isolated cell detection, birth rules (where dead cells with
exactly N live neighbors become alive), majority voting (where each cell takes
the value most common among itself and its neighbors), and one step of Conway's
Game of Life.

The pack complements the neighbor pack (nb_*) which operates on individual
cells, and the window pack (wn_*) which counts neighbors for specific cells.
The autom pack applies these operations across the entire grid in a single call,
producing a transformed grid.

AT-AT-001: at_count_nbrs_4(+Grid, +V, -CGrid)
Produces CGrid where each cell contains the count of in-bounds 4-connected
neighbors equal to V. Uses triple-nested findall: outer per-row, middle per-cell,
inner per-direction. Uses at_offs4_ private helper to supply the offset list.

AT-AT-002: at_count_nbrs_8(+Grid, +V, -CGrid)
Produces CGrid where each cell contains the count of in-bounds 8-connected
neighbors equal to V. Same triple-nested findall pattern with at_offs8_.

AT-AT-003: at_count_same_4(+Grid, -CGrid)
Produces CGrid where each cell contains the count of in-bounds 4-connected
neighbors that share its current value. Retrieves the cell value with nth0
and uses it as the filter in the innermost findall.

AT-AT-004: at_count_same_8(+Grid, -CGrid)
Produces CGrid where each cell contains the count of in-bounds 8-connected
neighbors that share its current value.

AT-AT-005: at_any_nbr_4(+Grid, +V, -BGrid)
Produces a 1/0 boolean grid where each cell is 1 if any in-bounds 4-neighbor
equals V, else 0. Uses private helper at_has_nbr_4_ which tries each direction
and cuts on the first V-neighbor found.

AT-AT-006: at_all_nbrs_4(+Grid, +V, -BGrid)
Produces a 1/0 boolean grid where each cell is 1 if every in-bounds 4-neighbor
equals V, else 0. Uses forall/2 over in-bounds 4-directions; vacuously true
for cells with no in-bounds neighbors.

AT-AT-007: at_any_nbr_8(+Grid, +V, -BGrid)
Produces a 1/0 boolean grid where each cell is 1 if any in-bounds 8-neighbor
equals V. Uses private helper at_has_nbr_8_ with the same cut-on-first pattern.

AT-AT-008: at_all_nbrs_8(+Grid, +V, -BGrid)
Produces a 1/0 boolean grid where each cell is 1 if every in-bounds 8-neighbor
equals V. Uses forall/2 over in-bounds 8-directions.

AT-AT-009: at_isolated_4(+Grid, +V, -Cells)
Returns sorted R-C pairs of V-valued cells that have no V-valued 4-neighbor.
Uses findall with \+ at_has_nbr_4_ as the isolation test, then sort/2.

AT-AT-010: at_isolated_8(+Grid, +V, -Cells)
Returns sorted R-C pairs of V-valued cells that have no V-valued 8-neighbor.
Uses findall with \+ at_has_nbr_8_, then sort/2.

AT-AT-011: at_birth_4(+Grid, +Dead, +Live, +N, -Grid2)
Produces Grid2 where each Dead cell with exactly N Live-valued 4-neighbors
becomes Live; all other cells are unchanged. Uses triple-nested findall with
an if-then-else: (V == Dead, count =:= N -> Live ; V).

AT-AT-012: at_birth_8(+Grid, +Dead, +Live, +N, -Grid2)
Produces Grid2 where each Dead cell with exactly N Live-valued 8-neighbors
becomes Live.

AT-AT-013: at_majority_4(+Grid, +Bg, -Grid2)
Produces Grid2 where each cell takes the value most common among itself and
its in-bounds 4-neighbors. Ties are broken by Bg. Delegates to private
helpers at_maj4_cell_ and at_mode_. at_mode_ finds the maximum frequency
using findall + max_list/2, collects all values at that frequency, and
returns the unique winner or Bg on ties.

AT-AT-014: at_step_gol(+Grid, -Grid2)
Produces one step of Conway's Game of Life: 0 = dead, 1 = alive. Uses the
standard B3/S23 rule (born at exactly 3 alive 8-neighbors; survives at 2 or
3 alive 8-neighbors). Delegates to private helper at_gol_next_ which uses
three clauses: survive clause (1 with 2 or 3 alive), birth clause (0 with 3),
and death clause (fallthrough to 0).

END OF PART 131


PART 132: CROSS PACK - 1D CROSS-SECTION EXTRACTION FROM 2D GRIDS

Work Package 142. Layer 121. Module: cross. Prefix: cx_*.

Purpose: Extract and analyze 1D slices of 2D grids: individual rows, columns,
and diagonals, together with aggregate queries (sum, count, unique values, mode)
over those slices. Complements the project pack (shadow casting) and the select
pack (region selection) by providing direct row/column analytics.

CX-CX-001: cx_row(+Grid, +R, -Row)
Extracts row R (0-indexed) from Grid as a list. Delegates directly to nth0/3.

CX-CX-002: cx_col(+Grid, +C, -Col)
Extracts column C (0-indexed) from Grid as a list with one element per row.
Collects the C-th element from every row in order using member/2 + nth0/3
inside findall.

CX-CX-003: cx_diag(+Grid, -Diag)
Extracts the main diagonal (top-left to bottom-right). Length is min(H, W).
For row index R, the diagonal element is Grid[R][R]. Uses between/3 over
row indices 0..H-1 with nth0(R, Row, V).

CX-CX-004: cx_antidiag(+Grid, -Diag)
Extracts the anti-diagonal (top-right to bottom-left). For row index R, the
anti-diagonal column is C = W - 1 - R. Guards C >= 0 to handle non-square
grids where H > W.

CX-CX-005: cx_row_sum(+Grid, +R, -Sum)
Computes the arithmetic sum of all values in row R. Extracts the row via
nth0/3 then delegates to sum_list/2 from library(lists).

CX-CX-006: cx_col_sum(+Grid, +C, -Sum)
Computes the arithmetic sum of all values in column C. Extracts the column
via cx_col/3 then delegates to sum_list/2.

CX-CX-007: cx_row_count(+Grid, +R, +V, -N)
Counts the number of occurrences of value V in row R. Uses findall+member
to collect witnesses then measures length.

CX-CX-008: cx_col_count(+Grid, +C, +V, -N)
Counts the number of occurrences of value V in column C. Extracts the column
via cx_col/3 then counts with findall+member+length.

CX-CX-009: cx_rows_with(+Grid, +V, -Rows)
Returns sorted list of 0-indexed row indices that contain at least one
occurrence of V. Uses between/3 + nth0/3 + member/2 inside findall, then
sort/2 to deduplicate (a row with multiple V cells would appear multiple times
without sort).

CX-CX-010: cx_cols_with(+Grid, +V, -Cols)
Returns sorted list of 0-indexed column indices that contain at least one
occurrence of V. Uses between/3 + member(Row,Grid) + nth0(C,Row,V) inside
findall, then sort/2.

CX-CX-011: cx_row_uniq(+Grid, +R, -Vals)
Returns the sorted set of distinct values present in row R. Extracts the row
via nth0/3 and applies sort/2 (which both sorts and deduplicates).

CX-CX-012: cx_col_uniq(+Grid, +C, -Vals)
Returns the sorted set of distinct values present in column C. Extracts the
column via cx_col/3 and applies sort/2.

CX-CX-013: cx_row_mode(+Grid, +R, +Bg, -Mode)
Returns the most frequently occurring value in row R. On ties, returns Bg.
Extracts the row via nth0/3 and delegates to private helper cx_mode_/3.

CX-CX-014: cx_col_mode(+Grid, +C, +Bg, -Mode)
Returns the most frequently occurring value in column C. On ties, returns Bg.
Extracts the column via cx_col/3 and delegates to cx_mode_/3.

Private helper cx_mode_(+Vals, +Bg, -Mode): builds N-V frequency pairs via
findall, finds MaxN via max_list/2, collects all values at MaxN, returns the
unique winner or Bg on ties.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, sum_list/2, max_list/2.

END OF PART 132


PART 133: MASK PACK - BOOLEAN MASK OPERATIONS ON 2D GRIDS

Work Package 143. Layer 122. Module: mask. Prefix: mk_*.

Purpose: Create, combine, and apply binary (0/1) masks to 2D grids.
A mask is a grid of the same dimensions as the target grid, with each cell
equal to 0 (disabled) or 1 (enabled). Masks allow selective operations:
retain values at enabled positions, fill enabled positions with a constant,
blend two grids by position, or query properties of the enabled set.

MK-MK-001: mk_from_val(+Grid, +V, -Mask)
Creates a binary mask where Mask[R][C] = 1 if Grid[R][C] = V, else 0.
Uses nested maplist/3 with a two-clause helper (match->1, cut, other->0).

MK-MK-002: mk_from_bg(+Grid, +Bg, -Mask)
Creates a binary mask where Mask[R][C] = 0 if Grid[R][C] = Bg, else 1.
Complement of mk_from_val: marks all non-background positions.

MK-MK-003: mk_invert(+Mask, -Mask2)
Inverts every bit: 1 becomes 0, any other value becomes 1. Uses nested
maplist/3 with a two-clause helper (1->0, cut, other->1).

MK-MK-004: mk_and(+MaskA, +MaskB, -MaskC)
Element-wise logical AND: MaskC[R][C] = 1 iff both A and B equal 1.
Uses nested maplist/4 with a two-clause helper (1,1->1, cut, other->0).

MK-MK-005: mk_or(+MaskA, +MaskB, -MaskC)
Element-wise logical OR: MaskC[R][C] = 1 iff at least one of A, B equals 1.
Uses nested maplist/4 with a two-clause helper (0,0->0, cut, other->1).

MK-MK-006: mk_xor(+MaskA, +MaskB, -MaskC)
Element-wise logical XOR: MaskC[R][C] = 1 iff exactly one of A, B equals 1.
Implemented as C is (A + B) mod 2, which generalizes to non-binary integers.

MK-MK-007: mk_apply(+Grid, +Mask, +Bg, -Grid2)
Produces Grid2 where Grid2[R][C] = Grid[R][C] if Mask[R][C] = 1, else Bg.
Uses nested maplist/4 with a two-clause helper (bit 1 keeps value, 0 -> Bg).

MK-MK-008: mk_fill(+Grid, +Mask, +V, -Grid2)
Produces Grid2 where Grid2[R][C] = V if Mask[R][C] = 1, else Grid[R][C].
Complement of mk_apply: fills enabled positions rather than disabling them.

MK-MK-009: mk_overlay(+GridA, +GridB, +Mask, -Grid2)
Produces Grid2 where Grid2[R][C] = GridB[R][C] if Mask[R][C] = 1, else
GridA[R][C]. Uses nested maplist/5 for four-way parallel iteration.

MK-MK-010: mk_where(+Mask, -Cells)
Returns sorted R-C pairs of positions where Mask = 1. Uses between/3 +
nth0/3 inside findall, then sort/2 for canonical order.

MK-MK-011: mk_count(+Mask, -N)
Counts the number of 1-valued cells in Mask. Uses findall + member/2 over
all rows and all cells, then length/2.

MK-MK-012: mk_any(+Mask)
Succeeds iff at least one cell in Mask equals 1. Uses member/2 twice
(over rows then over cells) with cut on the first match. Fails cleanly
if no 1 is found.

MK-MK-013: mk_all(+Mask)
Succeeds iff every cell in Mask equals 1. Uses forall/2 (built-in) with
forall(member(Row,Mask), forall(member(B,Row), B=:=1)).

MK-MK-014: mk_extract(+Grid, +Mask, -Vals)
Returns the sorted set of distinct Grid values at positions where Mask = 1.
Uses between/3 + nth0/3 for both Grid and Mask inside findall, then sort/2
to deduplicate.

Library imports: library(apply): maplist/3, maplist/4, maplist/5.
                 library(lists): member/2, nth0/3.
forall/2 is a built-in and is not imported.

END OF PART 133


PART 134: TABLE PACK - GRID-AS-TABLE OPERATIONS

Work Package 144. Layer 123. Module: table. Prefix: tb_*.

Purpose: Treat a 2D grid as a table (list of rows) and apply set-oriented
tabular operations: transpose, sorting, filtering, grouping, counting, row
deduplication, column selection/insertion/deletion, row insertion/deletion,
row swapping, and column extremum queries.

TB-TB-001: tb_transpose(+Grid, -TGrid)
Produces TGrid where TGrid[C][R] = Grid[R][C]. Implemented by iterating
column indices 0..W-1 and collecting column C of Grid as each new row of
TGrid using member + nth0 inside findall.

TB-TB-002: tb_sort_rows(+Grid, +C, -Sorted)
Sorts rows ascending by the value of column C. Uses findall to build
V-Row key-value pairs keyed by the column C value, then keysort/2 (built-in)
for a stable sort, then unwraps the rows.

TB-TB-003: tb_filter_rows(+Grid, +C, +V, -Filtered)
Keeps only rows where column C equals V. Uses findall with member + nth0
and a structural equality test.

TB-TB-004: tb_group_by(+Grid, +C, -Groups)
Groups rows by their column C value. Groups is a list of V-Rows pairs in
column C value order. Uses sort/2 on the collected column C values to get
unique keys, then one findall per unique key to collect rows.

TB-TB-005: tb_count_by(+Grid, +C, -Counts)
Counts rows per unique column C value. Delegates to tb_group_by/3 then
measures each group with length/2. Counts is a list of V-N pairs.

TB-TB-006: tb_unique_rows(+Grid, -UniqueGrid)
Removes duplicate rows preserving the first occurrence of each. Uses a
recursive helper that accumulates seen rows and skips rows already in the
seen set via \+ member/2.

TB-TB-007: tb_select_cols(+Grid, +ColIdxs, -SubGrid)
Extracts only the columns at the given indices (in the order given by ColIdxs).
Uses findall over member(Row,Grid) and an inner findall over member(C,ColIdxs).
Column reordering is achieved by passing ColIdxs in a different order.

TB-TB-008: tb_drop_col(+Grid, +C, -Grid2)
Removes column C from every row. Uses findall with between/3 over column
indices and a Ci \= C guard to exclude the target column.

TB-TB-009: tb_add_col(+Grid, +NewCol, -Grid2)
Appends list NewCol as a new rightmost column. Uses nth0/3 to pair each row
by index with the corresponding NewCol element, then append/3 to extend.

TB-TB-010: tb_insert_row(+Grid, +Row, +R, -Grid2)
Inserts Row before position R (0-indexed). Uses two recursive clauses: the
base case inserts at position 0 by prepending; the recursive case decrements
R and recurses on the tail.

TB-TB-011: tb_delete_row(+Grid, +R, -Grid2)
Removes the row at position R. Uses findall with nth0/3 and an I \= R guard.

TB-TB-012: tb_swap_rows(+Grid, +R1, +R2, -Grid2)
Swaps rows R1 and R2. Fetches both rows via nth0/3 then rebuilds with
findall using if-then-else to substitute at positions R1 and R2.

TB-TB-013: tb_col_max_row(+Grid, +C, -R)
Returns the 0-indexed row index where column C has its maximum value.
On ties, returns the first (lowest-indexed) matching row. Uses findall to
collect column C values, max_list/2 to find MaxV, then nth0 + nth0 + cut
to locate the first row with MaxV.

TB-TB-014: tb_col_min_row(+Grid, +C, -R)
Returns the 0-indexed row index where column C has its minimum value.
On ties, returns the first matching row. Same pattern as tb_col_max_row
using min_list/2.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, append/3, max_list/2,
  min_list/2.
keysort/2 is a built-in and is not imported.

END OF PART 134


PART 135: NUMSEQ PACK (WP 145)

Layer 124 - Numerical Sequence Operations (nr_* prefix).

This pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for analyzing and
transforming one-dimensional lists of numbers. The predicates complement
the cross pack (Layer 121) which extracts 1D slices from 2D grids; the
numseq pack then processes those extracted slices.

NR-NR-001: nr_diff(+List, -Diffs)
Computes consecutive pairwise differences. Diffs[I] = List[I+1] - List[I].
Uses two-clause recursion: empty and single-element lists produce []; the
recursive clause computes D is B-A and recurses on [B|T].

NR-NR-002: nr_cumsum(+List, -Sums)
Computes prefix cumulative sums. Sums[I] = sum of List[0..I]. The first
element is itself; a recursive helper nr_cumsum_/3 accumulates a running
total S is Acc+H.

NR-NR-003: nr_running_max(+List, -Maxs)
Computes running maximum. Maxs[I] = max(List[0..I]). The first element is
the initial maximum; a recursive helper nr_running_max_/3 updates via
Max1 is max(H, Max0).

NR-NR-004: nr_running_min(+List, -Mins)
Computes running minimum. Mins[I] = min(List[0..I]). Symmetric to
nr_running_max using Min1 is min(H, Min0).

NR-NR-005: nr_zip_add(+A, +B, -C)
Element-wise sum; C[I] = A[I] + B[I]. Uses maplist/3 with a named helper
nr_add_(X,Y,Z) where Z is X+Y.

NR-NR-006: nr_zip_sub(+A, +B, -C)
Element-wise difference; C[I] = A[I] - B[I]. Uses maplist/3 with
nr_sub_(X,Y,Z) where Z is X-Y.

NR-NR-007: nr_zip_mul(+A, +B, -C)
Element-wise product; C[I] = A[I] * B[I]. Uses maplist/3 with
nr_mul_(X,Y,Z) where Z is X*Y.

NR-NR-008: nr_zip_max(+A, +B, -C)
Element-wise maximum; C[I] = max(A[I], B[I]). Uses maplist/3 with
nr_max_(X,Y,Z) where Z is max(X,Y).

NR-NR-009: nr_zip_min(+A, +B, -C)
Element-wise minimum; C[I] = min(A[I], B[I]). Uses maplist/3 with
nr_min_(X,Y,Z) where Z is min(X,Y).

NR-NR-010: nr_scale(+List, +K, -Scaled)
Multiplies every element by scalar K. Uses maplist/3 with
nr_scale_(K,V,S) where S is V*K; K is captured from the outer call.

NR-NR-011: nr_offset(+List, +D, -Shifted)
Adds constant D to every element. Uses maplist/3 with
nr_offset_(D,V,S) where S is V+D; D is captured from the outer call.

NR-NR-012: nr_is_sorted(+List)
Succeeds iff List is non-decreasing (A =< B for each consecutive pair).
Uses three-clause recursion: empty, single-element, and two-element-or-more.

NR-NR-013: nr_is_arith(+List)
Succeeds iff List is an arithmetic sequence (constant pairwise difference).
Computes D is B-A from the first pair, then verifies all subsequent pairs
have the same difference via recursive helper nr_is_arith_/2.

NR-NR-014: nr_period(+List, +MaxP, -P)
Finds the shortest repeating period P in the range 1..MaxP. Uses
between/3 to try periods in ascending order; cuts on the first valid one.
Validity requires Len mod P =:= 0 and nr_check_period_/3 using forall +
nth0 element equality checks.

Library imports: library(apply): maplist/3.
  library(lists): nth0/3, numlist/3.
  length/2, between/3, forall/2 are built-ins and are not imported.

END OF PART 135


PART 136: GRIDMATH PACK (WP 146)

Layer 125 - Cell-Wise Arithmetic on 2D Grids (gm_* prefix).

This pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for applying arithmetic
operations to two-dimensional grids cell by cell. The predicates extend
the concepts from the numseq pack (Layer 124, nr_*) into two dimensions:
where numseq operates on 1D lists, gridmath operates on 2D grids.

GM-GM-001: gm_add(+GridA, +GridB, -GridC)
Cell-wise sum. GridC[R][C] = GridA[R][C] + GridB[R][C]. Uses nested
maplist/4 with named helpers gm_add_row_ and gm_add_.

GM-GM-002: gm_sub(+GridA, +GridB, -GridC)
Cell-wise difference. GridC[R][C] = GridA[R][C] - GridB[R][C]. Uses
nested maplist/4 with helpers gm_sub_row_ and gm_sub_.

GM-GM-003: gm_mul(+GridA, +GridB, -GridC)
Cell-wise product. GridC[R][C] = GridA[R][C] * GridB[R][C]. Uses nested
maplist/4 with helpers gm_mul_row_ and gm_mul_.

GM-GM-004: gm_max(+GridA, +GridB, -GridC)
Cell-wise maximum. GridC[R][C] = max(GridA[R][C], GridB[R][C]). Uses
nested maplist/4 with helpers gm_max_row_ and gm_max_.

GM-GM-005: gm_min(+GridA, +GridB, -GridC)
Cell-wise minimum. GridC[R][C] = min(GridA[R][C], GridB[R][C]). Uses
nested maplist/4 with helpers gm_min_row_ and gm_min_.

GM-GM-006: gm_scale(+Grid, +K, -Grid2)
Multiplies every cell by scalar K. Uses nested maplist/3 with row-level
helper gm_scale_row_(K) that captures K, and cell helper gm_scale_(K).

GM-GM-007: gm_offset(+Grid, +D, -Grid2)
Adds constant D to every cell. Uses nested maplist/3 with row-level
helper gm_offset_row_(D) and cell helper gm_offset_(D).

GM-GM-008: gm_abs(+Grid, -Grid2)
Absolute value of every cell. Uses nested maplist/3 with helpers
gm_abs_row_ and gm_abs_ where A is abs(V).

GM-GM-009: gm_eq_mask(+GridA, +GridB, -Mask)
Produces a 1/0 mask where Mask[R][C] = 1 if GridA[R][C] = GridB[R][C]
and 0 otherwise. Uses nested maplist/4 with a two-clause cut helper
gm_eq_(X,X,1):-!. gm_eq_(_,_,0).

GM-GM-010: gm_diff_mask(+GridA, +GridB, -Mask)
Produces a 1/0 mask where Mask[R][C] = 1 if GridA[R][C] differs from
GridB[R][C] and 0 where they are equal. Symmetric complement of
gm_eq_mask. Uses two-clause cut helper gm_diff_(X,X,0):-!. gm_diff_(_,_,1).

GM-GM-011: gm_clamp(+Grid, +Lo, +Hi, -Grid2)
Clamps each cell to the inclusive range [Lo, Hi]. Uses nested maplist/3
with helper gm_clamp_(Lo,Hi,V,C) where C is max(Lo, min(Hi, V)).

GM-GM-012: gm_modulo(+Grid, +M, -Grid2)
Applies modulo M to every cell. Grid2[R][C] = Grid[R][C] mod M. Uses
nested maplist/3 with helper gm_modulo_(M,V,R) where R is V mod M.

GM-GM-013: gm_sum(+Grid, -Sum)
Computes the sum of all cell values. Uses findall to flatten all cells
into a list via member/2 applied twice, then a recursive sumlist_/2
accumulator. member/2 is imported from library(lists).

GM-GM-014: gm_product(+Grid, -Prod)
Computes the product of all cell values. Uses findall to flatten, then
a recursive prodlist_/2 accumulator.

Library imports: library(apply): maplist/3, maplist/4.
  library(lists): member/2, append/2.

END OF PART 136


PART 137: COLORMAP PACK (WP 147)

Layer 126 - Color Lookup Table and Palette Substitution (cm_* prefix).

This pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for mapping, substituting,
and analyzing color (or value) labels in grids and lists. The predicates
treat a "map" as a list of Old-New pairs and provide operations to apply,
invert, compose, derive, and query such maps.

CM-CM-001: cm_apply(+Map, +Grid, -Grid2)
Applies Map to every cell in Grid. For each cell V, looks up V as a key
in Map using memberchk/2; on miss, the value is left unchanged. Uses
nested maplist/3 with cm_apply_row_ and cm_apply_cell_ helpers.

CM-CM-002: cm_apply_default(+Map, +Bg, +Grid, -Grid2)
Like cm_apply, but replaces unmatched cells with the default value Bg
instead of leaving them unchanged.

CM-CM-003: cm_invert(+Map, +Grid, -Grid2)
Applies the inverse of Map (swapping Old-New to New-Old) to Grid. Uses
findall to build the inverse map, then delegates to cm_apply.

CM-CM-004: cm_compose(+MapA, +MapB, -MapAB)
Composes two maps: MapAB[k] = MapB[MapA[k]]. For each entry K-V1 in MapA,
looks up V1 in MapB; if not found, the intermediate value V1 passes through.
Uses findall to build MapAB.

CM-CM-005: cm_from_grids(+GridA, +GridB, -Map)
Derives a map from the cell-by-cell correspondence between two same-sized
grids. Collects all VA-VB pairs where VA and VB are values at the same
position in GridA and GridB. Deduplicates with sort/2 (built-in).

CM-CM-006: cm_identity(+Palette, -Map)
Builds the identity map V-V for every value in Palette. Uses findall over
member/2.

CM-CM-007: cm_remap(+OldVals, +NewVals, -Map)
Builds a map from two parallel lists of equal length. Uses findall with
nth0/3 to pair corresponding elements.

CM-CM-008: cm_remap_list(+Map, +List, -List2)
Applies Map to a one-dimensional list (rather than a grid). Uses
maplist/3 with cm_apply_cell_; unmatched values are left unchanged.

CM-CM-009: cm_palette(+Map, -Palette)
Returns the sorted list of all source (key) values in Map. Uses findall
to collect keys, then sort/2 to deduplicate.

CM-CM-010: cm_used(+Grid, -UsedVals)
Returns the sorted list of all distinct values that appear in Grid. Uses
nested findall with member/2, then sort/2.

CM-CM-011: cm_has_key(+Map, +K)
Succeeds iff K appears as a key in Map. Uses memberchk/2 for determinism.

CM-CM-012: cm_lookup(+Map, +K, -V)
Looks up the value for key K in Map. Fails if K is not present. Uses
memberchk/2.

CM-CM-013: cm_restrict(+Map, +Keys, +Map2)
Keeps only entries whose key appears in Keys. Uses findall with memberchk
to test key membership.

CM-CM-014: cm_expand(+Map, +Bg, +Palette, -Map2)
Extends Map with K-Bg entries for each palette value that has no entry in
Map. Uses findall + \+ memberchk to find missing keys, then append/3 to
combine. append/3 is imported from library(lists).

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, memberchk/2, nth0/3, append/3.
  library(apply): maplist/3.
  sort/2 is a built-in and is not imported.

END OF PART 137


PART 138: BLOCK PACK (WP 148)

Layer 127 - Rectangular Sub-Grid (Block) Decomposition (bk_* prefix).

This pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for splitting grids into
uniform rectangular blocks and performing block-level operations.

BK-BK-001: bk_extract(+Grid, +R0, +C0, +R1, +C1, -Block)
Extracts the rectangular sub-grid from row R0..R1 and column C0..C1
(inclusive, 0-indexed). Uses nested findall with between/3 and nth0/3.

BK-BK-002: bk_dims(+Grid, +BH, +BW, -NR, -NC)
Computes the number of block rows NR and block columns NC when dividing
a grid into BH-by-BW blocks. NR is H // BH; NC is W // BW (integer
division, exact division assumed).

BK-BK-003: bk_split_h(+Grid, +BH, -Strips)
Splits Grid into horizontal strips of height BH. Uses findall with
between/3 over strip indices to collect rows for each strip.

BK-BK-004: bk_split_v(+Grid, +BW, -Strips)
Splits Grid into vertical strips of width BW. Uses findall with
between/3 over strip indices, with an inner findall to slice each row.

BK-BK-005: bk_tile_h(+Grid, +N, -Tiled)
Tiles Grid N times vertically (stacks N copies top to bottom). Uses
findall over between(1,N,_) and member/2 to replicate rows.

BK-BK-006: bk_tile_v(+Grid, +N, -Tiled)
Tiles Grid N times horizontally (extends each row N times). Uses
maplist/3 with bk_tile_row_/3 helper which replicates cell values.

BK-BK-007: bk_count_h(+Grid, +BH, -N)
Returns the number of complete horizontal strips: N is H // BH.

BK-BK-008: bk_count_v(+Grid, +BW, -N)
Returns the number of complete vertical strips: N is W // BW.

BK-BK-009: bk_map(+Blocks, +Goal, -Blocks2)
Applies a 2-argument predicate Goal to each block in Blocks. Uses
maplist/3 with Goal as the mapping predicate.

BK-BK-010: bk_uniform(+Grid, +R, +C, -V)
Returns the value V at cell (R,C) in Grid. Uses nth0/3 twice.
Useful for checking uniformity by caller: call bk_uniform for all
cells and verify they all return the same V.

BK-BK-011: bk_mode_color(+Grid, +R0, +C0, -V)
Returns the most frequent value V in the 2x2 block starting at (R0,C0).
Uses findall to collect 4 cells, sort/2 for unique values, include/3 to
count each, and max_list/2 + sort/2 to select the lowest-valued winner
on ties. Requires library(lists): include/3, max_list/2 are imported via
include from library(apply) and library(lists) respectively. Actually
uses a private bk_mode_/2 helper with findall+sort+findall pattern.

BK-BK-012: bk_border_color(+Grid, +R0, +C0, -Bg)
Returns the most frequent value among the 8 border cells of the 3x3
neighborhood centered at (R0, C0), excluding the center cell. In-bounds
cells only. Uses findall with negation-as-failure to exclude center.
Delegates to bk_mode_/2.

BK-BK-013: bk_is_solid(+Grid, +Color, -Bool)
Returns Bool=1 iff every cell in Grid equals Color; Bool=0 otherwise.
Uses forall/2 with member/2 twice.

BK-BK-014: bk_is_border(+Grid, +R, +C, -Bool)
Returns Bool=1 iff the cell (R,C) lies on the outer border of Grid
(first row, last row, first column, or last column); Bool=0 otherwise.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/3.
  library(apply): maplist/3.
  Built-ins: length/2, between/3, forall/2, sort/2, max_list/2.

Note: max_list/2 is from library(lists) but is used inside the private
bk_mode_/2 helper. include/3 is from library(apply) used in bk_mode_.
The public API uses only list and apply imports.

END OF PART 138


PART 139: EDGE DETECTION AND BOUNDARY ANALYSIS PACK

Layer 128. Module: edge. File: packs/edge/prolog/edge.pl. Prefix: ed_*.

This pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for detecting boundaries
between regions of different values in a 2D grid. An edge exists wherever
two adjacent cells carry different values. A boundary cell is one that has
at least one 4-connected neighbor with a different value.

The pack covers: collecting horizontal and vertical edge positions, testing
single-cell edge presence, building an edge-labeled mask grid, finding
boundary and inner cells for a specific value, enumerating outer-border
cells, counting edges, detecting smooth (edge-free) grids, and finding
corner positions (2x2 regions with mixed values).

ED-ED-001: ed_h_edges(+Grid, -Edges)
Collects all horizontal edges as R-C pairs. A horizontal edge exists
between row R and row R+1 at column C when Grid[R][C] \= Grid[R+1][C].
Uses findall with between/3 and nth0/3.

ED-ED-002: ed_v_edges(+Grid, -Edges)
Collects all vertical edges as R-C pairs. A vertical edge exists between
column C and column C+1 at row R when Grid[R][C] \= Grid[R][C+1].
Uses findall with between/3 and nth0/3.

ED-ED-003: ed_h_edge(+Grid, +R, +C, -Bool)
Returns Bool=1 iff a horizontal edge exists between (R,C) and (R+1,C),
i.e., Grid[R][C] \= Grid[R+1][C]. Returns 0 otherwise.

ED-ED-004: ed_v_edge(+Grid, +R, +C, -Bool)
Returns Bool=1 iff a vertical edge exists between (R,C) and (R,C+1),
i.e., Grid[R][C] \= Grid[R][C+1]. Returns 0 otherwise.

ED-ED-005: ed_all_edges(+Grid, -Edges)
Collects all edges (horizontal and vertical) as h-R-C and v-R-C terms,
sorted. Merges results of ed_h_edges and ed_v_edges.

ED-ED-006: ed_boundary_cells(+Grid, +Val, -Cells)
Returns R-C pairs (sorted) of all cells with value Val that have at least
one 4-connected neighbor with a different value.

ED-ED-007: ed_outer_boundary(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns R-C pairs (sorted) of all cells on the outer border of the grid
(row 0, last row, column 0, or last column).

ED-ED-008: ed_inner_cells(+Grid, +Val, -Cells)
Returns R-C pairs (sorted) of all cells with value Val that are NOT in
ed_boundary_cells (strictly interior to their uniform region).

ED-ED-009: ed_edge_count(+Grid, -N)
Returns N, the total number of edges in Grid (horizontal plus vertical).

ED-ED-010: ed_is_smooth(+Grid)
Succeeds iff Grid has zero edges (every cell has the same value as all
its neighbors). Equivalent to ed_edge_count(Grid, 0).

ED-ED-011: ed_label_edges(+Grid, +Bg, -Grid2)
Produces a same-size grid Grid2 where each cell is 1 if it is a boundary
cell (has at least one 4-neighbor with a different value) and Bg otherwise.

ED-ED-012: ed_has_edge(+Grid, +R, +C, -Bool)
Returns Bool=1 iff cell (R,C) is a boundary cell; Bool=0 otherwise.
Uses the private helper ed_has_diff_nbr_/6.

ED-ED-013: ed_corners(+Grid, -Corners)
Returns R-C pairs (sorted, 0-indexed top-left corner of each 2x2 block)
where the four cells in the 2x2 block are not all the same value.

ED-ED-014: ed_corner_count(+Grid, -N)
Returns N, the number of corner positions in Grid.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3.
Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3, sort/2.

Note: sort/2 is a SWI-Prolog built-in and is not imported from any library.

END OF PART 139


PART 140: CELL DISTANCE AND PROXIMITY COMPUTATION PACK

Layer 129. Module: distance. File: packs/distance/prolog/distance.pl.
Prefix: dt_*.

This pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for computing distances
between grid cells, building distance transform grids, and performing
proximity queries. Three distance metrics are supported: Manhattan (L1),
Chebyshev (L-inf, also called 8-connected), and squared Euclidean.

DT-DT-001: dt_manhattan(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -D)
Computes the Manhattan (L1) distance D = |R2-R1| + |C2-C1| between two
grid positions (R1,C1) and (R2,C2).

DT-DT-002: dt_chebyshev(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -D)
Computes the Chebyshev (L-inf) distance D = max(|R2-R1|, |C2-C1|).
Corresponds to the number of king-moves on a chess board.

DT-DT-003: dt_euclidean_sq(+R1, +C1, +R2, +C2, -DSq)
Computes the squared Euclidean distance DSq = (R2-R1)^2 + (C2-C1)^2.
Returns an integer, avoiding floating-point square roots.

DT-DT-004: dt_nearest(+Grid, +Val, +R0-C0, -R-C)
Finds the nearest cell (by Manhattan distance) in Grid that has value Val
to the query position R0-C0. On ties, returns the first cell in row-major
order.

DT-DT-005: dt_farthest(+Grid, +Val, +R0-C0, -R-C)
Finds the farthest cell (by Manhattan distance) in Grid that has value Val
from the query position R0-C0. On ties, returns the last in row-major order.

DT-DT-006: dt_all_at(+Grid, +Val, +R0-C0, +D, -Cells)
Finds all cells of value Val at exactly Manhattan distance D from R0-C0.
Returns sorted R-C pairs.

DT-DT-007: dt_within_manhattan(+Grid, +R0, +C0, +D, -Cells)
Returns all in-bounds grid positions within Manhattan distance D of (R0,C0),
sorted as R-C pairs.

DT-DT-008: dt_within_chebyshev(+Grid, +R0, +C0, +D, -Cells)
Returns all in-bounds grid positions within Chebyshev distance D of
(R0,C0), sorted as R-C pairs.

DT-DT-009: dt_map_manhattan(+Grid, +Val, -MapGrid)
Produces a same-size grid where each cell holds the Manhattan distance to
the nearest cell with value Val. Returns -1 if Val is absent.

DT-DT-010: dt_map_chebyshev(+Grid, +Val, -MapGrid)
Produces a same-size grid where each cell holds the Chebyshev distance to
the nearest cell with value Val. Returns -1 if Val is absent.

DT-DT-011: dt_ring_manhattan(+Grid, +R0, +C0, +D, -Cells)
Returns all in-bounds positions at exactly Manhattan distance D from
(R0,C0), sorted as R-C pairs.

DT-DT-012: dt_centroid(+Grid, +Val, -R-C)
Computes the integer centroid (floor of mean row and mean column) of all
cells with value Val. Fails if no such cells exist.

DT-DT-013: dt_diameter_manhattan(+Cells, -D1-D2, -Diam)
Computes the diameter (maximum pairwise Manhattan distance) of a set of
R-C pairs. Returns the two farthest cells D1 and D2 and the distance Diam.

DT-DT-014: dt_diameter_chebyshev(+Cells, -D1-D2, -Diam)
Computes the diameter (maximum pairwise Chebyshev distance) of a set of
R-C pairs.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, min_list/2, max_list/2.
  library(apply): maplist/3.
Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3, abs/1, max/2.

END OF PART 140


PART 141: GRID TOPOLOGY AND CONNECTED COMPONENT ANALYSIS PACK

Layer 130. Module: topology. File: packs/topology/prolog/topology.pl.
Prefix: tp_*.

This pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for flood-fill-based
connected component analysis, enclosed region detection, and topological
classification of grid regions. All connectivity is 4-connected (orthogonal
neighbors only).

TP-TP-001: tp_component(+Grid, +Val, +Seed, -Cells)
Finds all cells of value Val that are 4-connected to Seed. Returns sorted
R-C pairs. Fails if the Seed cell does not have value Val.

TP-TP-002: tp_all_components(+Grid, +Val, -Components)
Returns all 4-connected components of Val in Grid, each as a sorted R-C
pair list. The list is empty if Val does not appear in Grid.

TP-TP-003: tp_component_count(+Grid, +Val, -N)
Returns N, the number of distinct 4-connected components of Val.

TP-TP-004: tp_component_size(+Grid, +Val, +Seed, -N)
Returns N, the cell count of the 4-connected component of Val containing
Seed.

TP-TP-005: tp_largest_component(+Grid, +Val, -Cells)
Returns the cells of the largest 4-connected component of Val. On ties,
returns the first (by sorted component order). Fails if Val is absent.

TP-TP-006: tp_reachable(+Grid, +Val, +Src, +Dst, -Bool)
Returns Bool=1 iff there exists a 4-connected path of Val cells from Src
to Dst; Bool=0 otherwise. Fails if Src does not have value Val.

TP-TP-007: tp_enclosed(+Grid, +Val, +Bg, -Cells)
Returns sorted R-C pairs of all Bg cells that cannot reach the grid border
via 4-connected Bg cells. These are cells completely enclosed by Val.
Val is accepted as an API parameter but the flood fill runs through Bg.

TP-TP-008: tp_has_hole(+Grid, +Val, +Bg, -Bool)
Returns Bool=1 iff Val encloses at least one Bg region; Bool=0 otherwise.

TP-TP-009: tp_hole_count(+Grid, +Val, +Bg, -N)
Returns N, the count of distinct enclosed Bg components (holes).

TP-TP-010: tp_fill_holes(+Grid, +Val, +Bg, -Grid2)
Produces Grid2 by replacing every enclosed Bg cell with Val; all other
cells are left unchanged.

TP-TP-011: tp_border_components(+Grid, +Val, -Components)
Returns all components of Val that have at least one cell on the outer
grid border (row 0, last row, column 0, or last column).

TP-TP-012: tp_interior_components(+Grid, +Val, -Components)
Returns all components of Val that have NO cell on the outer grid border.

TP-TP-013: tp_label_components(+Grid, +Val, -LabelGrid)
Produces a same-size grid where each Val cell is replaced by its 1-based
component index (components are assigned labels in the order they are
discovered) and all non-Val cells become 0.

TP-TP-014: tp_same_component(+Grid, +Val, +P1, +P2, -Bool)
Returns Bool=1 iff P1 and P2 are cells in the same 4-connected component
of Val; Bool=0 otherwise. Delegates to tp_reachable.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, memberchk/2, nth0/3, max_list/2,
  append/3, subtract/3.
Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3, sort/2.

Note: max_list/2 is imported from library(lists) for internal use.
subtract/3 is used to remove processed cells from the pending list.

END OF PART 141


PART 142: ROW AND COLUMN PROJECTION AND PROFILE ANALYSIS PACK (pj_*)

Layer 131. Module: projection. Prefix: pj_*.

This pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for computing 1D summaries
of 2D grids by projecting along rows or columns. It supports sums, counts,
maxima, unique value sets, shadow projections, run-length profiles, and modal
values.

PJ-PJ-001: pj_row_sums(+Grid, -Sums)
Returns Sums, a list of integers, one per row, where each element is the sum
of all cell values in that row.

PJ-PJ-002: pj_col_sums(+Grid, -Sums)
Returns Sums, a list of integers, one per column, where each element is the
sum of all cell values in that column.

PJ-PJ-003: pj_row_counts(+Grid, +Val, -Counts)
Returns Counts, a list of non-negative integers, one per row, where each
element is the number of cells in that row equal to Val.

PJ-PJ-004: pj_col_counts(+Grid, +Val, -Counts)
Returns Counts, a list of non-negative integers, one per column, where each
element is the number of cells in that column equal to Val.

PJ-PJ-005: pj_row_maxes(+Grid, -Maxes)
Returns Maxes, a list of integers, one per row, where each element is the
maximum value in that row.

PJ-PJ-006: pj_col_maxes(+Grid, -Maxes)
Returns Maxes, a list of integers, one per column, where each element is the
maximum value in that column.

PJ-PJ-007: pj_row_uniq(+Grid, -ValLists)
Returns ValLists, a list of sorted lists, one per row, where each sublist
is the sorted unique values that appear in that row.

PJ-PJ-008: pj_col_uniq(+Grid, -ValLists)
Returns ValLists, a list of sorted lists, one per column, where each sublist
is the sorted unique values that appear in that column.

PJ-PJ-009: pj_shadow_h(+Grid, +Val, -ColIndices)
Returns a sorted list of 0-based column indices where at least one cell in
any row has value Val. This is the horizontal shadow of Val onto the column
axis.

PJ-PJ-010: pj_shadow_v(+Grid, +Val, -RowIndices)
Returns a sorted list of 0-based row indices where at least one cell in any
column has value Val. This is the vertical shadow of Val onto the row axis.

PJ-PJ-011: pj_h_profile(+Grid, +Val, -Profile)
Returns Profile, a list of non-negative integers, one per row, where each
element is the length of the longest contiguous run of Val in that row.

PJ-PJ-012: pj_v_profile(+Grid, +Val, -Profile)
Returns Profile, a list of non-negative integers, one per column, where each
element is the length of the longest contiguous run of Val in that column.

PJ-PJ-013: pj_row_modes(+Grid, -Modes)
Returns Modes, a list of values, one per row, where each element is the most
frequently occurring value in that row. On ties, the smallest value wins.

PJ-PJ-014: pj_col_modes(+Grid, -Modes)
Returns Modes, a list of values, one per column, where each element is the
most frequently occurring value in that column. On ties, the smallest value
wins.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2, sum_list/2.
  library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3, include/3.
Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3, sort/2.

END OF PART 142


PART 143: ROW AND COLUMN GRADIENT AND PROGRESSION ANALYSIS PACK (gr_*)

Layer 132. Module: gradient. Prefix: gr_*.

This pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for measuring value
gradients, monotonicity, range, cumulative sums, and second-order
differences in 2D grids.

GR-GR-001: gr_h_diffs(+Grid, -DiffGrid)
Returns DiffGrid where each list holds the adjacent differences of the
corresponding input row: [V1-V0, V2-V1, ...]. A row of length N gives
N-1 differences. An empty or single-element row gives an empty list.

GR-GR-002: gr_v_diffs(+Grid, -DiffGrid)
Returns DiffGrid where each list holds the column-wise differences between
adjacent rows: DiffGrid[i][C] = Grid[i+1][C] - Grid[i][C]. H rows give
H-1 difference lists.

GR-GR-003: gr_h_mono(+Grid, -Flags)
Returns Flags, a list of integers (one per row): 1 if the row is weakly
non-decreasing, -1 if weakly non-increasing (but not non-decreasing), 0
if neither. A constant row returns 1 (trivially non-decreasing).

GR-GR-004: gr_v_mono(+Grid, -Flags)
Returns Flags, a list of integers (one per column): 1 if the column is
weakly non-decreasing, -1 if weakly non-increasing, 0 if neither.

GR-GR-005: gr_h_range(+Grid, -Ranges)
Returns Ranges, a list of integers (one per row), each being the max
minus min of that row's values. Returns 0 for a constant row.

GR-GR-006: gr_v_range(+Grid, -Ranges)
Returns Ranges, a list of integers (one per column), each being the max
minus min of that column's values.

GR-GR-007: gr_h_slope(+Grid, -Slopes)
Returns Slopes, a list of integers (one per row): the net horizontal change
(last element minus first element) of each row.

GR-GR-008: gr_v_slope(+Grid, -Slopes)
Returns Slopes, a list of integers (one per column): the net vertical change
(last element minus first element) of each column.

GR-GR-009: gr_h_const(+Grid, -Bools)
Returns Bools, a list of integers (one per row): 1 if all values in the row
are arithmetically equal, 0 otherwise.

GR-GR-010: gr_v_const(+Grid, -Bools)
Returns Bools, a list of integers (one per column): 1 if all values in the
column are equal, 0 otherwise.

GR-GR-011: gr_h_cum(+Grid, -CumGrid)
Returns CumGrid where each row holds the running cumulative sum of the
corresponding input row: [V0, V0+V1, V0+V1+V2, ...].

GR-GR-012: gr_v_cum(+Grid, -CumGrid)
Returns CumGrid where each cell holds the cumulative sum down the column
to (and including) that row. CumGrid[0] = Grid[0]; CumGrid[i][C] =
CumGrid[i-1][C] + Grid[i][C].

GR-GR-013: gr_h_second(+Grid, -D2Grid)
Returns D2Grid where each list holds the second-order differences
(differences of adjacent differences) of the corresponding row.
A row of length N gives N-2 second-order differences.

GR-GR-014: gr_v_second(+Grid, -D2Grid)
Returns D2Grid holding the second-order vertical differences (computed by
applying gr_v_diffs twice). H rows give H-2 second-order rows.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2, min_list/2, last/2.
  library(apply): maplist/3.
Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3.

END OF PART 143


PART 144: 2D GRID EXTREMA, LOCAL PEAKS, AND THRESHOLD FILTERING PACK (ex_*)

Layer 133. Module: extrema. Prefix: ex_*.

This pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for finding maximum and
minimum values and their positions in 2D grids, detecting local maxima and
minima, computing row and column argmax/argmin, threshold filtering, range
computation, and sparse cell enumeration.

EX-EX-001: ex_max_val(+Grid, -Val)
Returns Val, the maximum value across all cells in Grid.

EX-EX-002: ex_min_val(+Grid, -Val)
Returns Val, the minimum value across all cells in Grid.

EX-EX-003: ex_max_cells(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns Cells, the sorted list of R-C positions whose value equals the
grid maximum. All positions are included if the maximum appears multiple times.

EX-EX-004: ex_min_cells(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns Cells, the sorted list of R-C positions whose value equals the
grid minimum.

EX-EX-005: ex_row_argmax(+Grid, -R)
Returns R, the 0-based index of the row with the maximum row sum.
On ties, the first (lowest-index) row is returned.

EX-EX-006: ex_col_argmax(+Grid, -C)
Returns C, the 0-based index of the column with the maximum column sum.
On ties, the first column is returned.

EX-EX-007: ex_row_argmin(+Grid, -R)
Returns R, the 0-based index of the row with the minimum row sum.
On ties, the first row is returned.

EX-EX-008: ex_col_argmin(+Grid, -C)
Returns C, the 0-based index of the column with the minimum column sum.
On ties, the first column is returned.

EX-EX-009: ex_local_max4(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns Cells, the sorted list of R-C positions that are strictly greater
than every in-bounds 4-connected neighbor. Out-of-bounds directions are
ignored; border and corner cells may qualify if they exceed all neighbors
they do have.

EX-EX-010: ex_local_min4(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns Cells, the sorted list of R-C positions that are strictly less
than every in-bounds 4-connected neighbor.

EX-EX-011: ex_above(+Grid, +Thresh, -Cells)
Returns Cells, the sorted list of R-C positions whose value is strictly
greater than Thresh.

EX-EX-012: ex_below(+Grid, +Thresh, -Cells)
Returns Cells, the sorted list of R-C positions whose value is strictly
less than Thresh.

EX-EX-013: ex_range(+Grid, -Range)
Returns Range, the difference between the maximum and minimum values in Grid.
Returns 0 for a uniform grid.

EX-EX-014: ex_nonzero(+Grid, -Cells)
Returns Cells, the sorted list of R-C positions whose value is not
arithmetically equal to 0. Useful for sparse grid enumeration.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2, min_list/2,
  sum_list/2.
Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3.

END OF PART 144


PART 145: PER-CELL NEIGHBORHOOD VALUE AGGREGATION PACK

Work Package: WP 155
Layer: 134
Module: naggr
Predicate prefix: na_
File: packs/naggr/prolog/naggr.pl

Overview:

The naggr pack provides 14 predicates for computing per-cell aggregate
statistics over in-bounds 4-connected and 8-connected neighborhoods in
2D grids.  Where the automaton pack (at_*, Layer 120) provides count-based
neighbor operations, the naggr pack provides value-based aggregation:
sum, maximum, minimum, mean, range, value spread (distinct-value count),
and difference count.

Every predicate produces an output grid of the same dimensions as the input.
Each output cell holds the aggregate of the in-bounds neighbor values for the
corresponding input cell.  Out-of-bounds neighbors are silently omitted;
this means corner cells have 2 in-bounds 4-neighbors and edge cells have 3,
while interior cells have the full 4 or 8.  Cells with no in-bounds neighbors
(possible only in 1x1 grids) receive sentinel value 0.

Predicate definitions:

NA-NA-001: na_sum4(+Grid, -SumGrid)
SumGrid[R][C] is the sum of the values of all in-bounds 4-neighbors of
cell (R,C).  Returns 0 when no in-bounds 4-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-002: na_sum8(+Grid, -SumGrid)
SumGrid[R][C] is the sum of the values of all in-bounds 8-neighbors of
cell (R,C).  Returns 0 when no in-bounds 8-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-003: na_max4(+Grid, -MaxGrid)
MaxGrid[R][C] is the maximum value among all in-bounds 4-neighbors.
Returns 0 when no in-bounds 4-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-004: na_max8(+Grid, -MaxGrid)
MaxGrid[R][C] is the maximum value among all in-bounds 8-neighbors.
Returns 0 when no in-bounds 8-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-005: na_min4(+Grid, -MinGrid)
MinGrid[R][C] is the minimum value among all in-bounds 4-neighbors.
Returns 0 when no in-bounds 4-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-006: na_min8(+Grid, -MinGrid)
MinGrid[R][C] is the minimum value among all in-bounds 8-neighbors.
Returns 0 when no in-bounds 8-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-007: na_mean4(+Grid, -MeanGrid)
MeanGrid[R][C] is the integer floor of (sum / count) of in-bounds
4-neighbor values.  Returns 0 when no in-bounds 4-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-008: na_mean8(+Grid, -MeanGrid)
MeanGrid[R][C] is the integer floor of (sum / count) of in-bounds
8-neighbor values.  Returns 0 when no in-bounds 8-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-009: na_range4(+Grid, -RangeGrid)
RangeGrid[R][C] is the maximum minus the minimum of in-bounds 4-neighbor
values.  Returns 0 when fewer than 2 in-bounds 4-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-010: na_range8(+Grid, -RangeGrid)
RangeGrid[R][C] is the maximum minus the minimum of in-bounds 8-neighbor
values.  Returns 0 when fewer than 2 in-bounds 8-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-011: na_spread4(+Grid, -SpreadGrid)
SpreadGrid[R][C] is the count of distinct values among all in-bounds
4-neighbors.  Returns 0 when no in-bounds 4-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-012: na_spread8(+Grid, -SpreadGrid)
SpreadGrid[R][C] is the count of distinct values among all in-bounds
8-neighbors.  Returns 0 when no in-bounds 8-neighbors exist.

NA-NA-013: na_diff4(+Grid, -DiffGrid)
DiffGrid[R][C] is the count of in-bounds 4-neighbors whose value is
arithmetically different from the value of cell (R,C) itself.

NA-NA-014: na_diff8(+Grid, -DiffGrid)
DiffGrid[R][C] is the count of in-bounds 8-neighbors whose value is
