arithmetically different from the value of cell (R,C) itself.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2, min_list/2,
  sum_list/2.
Built-ins: sort/2, length/2, between/3, findall/3.

END OF PART 145


PART 146: INTEGER MEDIAN COMPUTATION FOR LISTS AND 2D GRIDS PACK

Work Package: WP 156
Layer: 135
Module: median
Predicate prefix: md_
File: packs/median/prolog/median.pl

Overview:

The median pack provides 14 predicates for computing the lower (floor) integer
median of lists, grid rows, grid columns, and per-cell neighborhoods in 2D grids.

The lower median is defined as the element at 0-based index (N-1)//2 of the
msort-sorted value list.  For odd-length lists this is the unique middle element.
For even-length lists this is the lower of the two middle elements.

msort/2 is used throughout to preserve duplicate values.  sort/2 would remove
duplicates and give incorrect medians when values repeat.

All predicates work on integer-valued 2D grids represented as lists of lists.

Predicate definitions:

MD-MD-001: md_median(+List, -M)
M is the lower median of integer list List.  Requires List to be non-empty.

MD-MD-002: md_row(+Grid, +R, -M)
M is the lower median of row R (0-based) of Grid.

MD-MD-003: md_col(+Grid, +C, -M)
M is the lower median of column C (0-based) of Grid.

MD-MD-004: md_row_medians(+Grid, -Ms)
Ms is the list of lower medians, one per row, in row order.

MD-MD-005: md_col_medians(+Grid, -Ms)
Ms is the list of lower medians, one per column, in column order.

MD-MD-006: md_grid(+Grid, -M)
M is the lower median of all cell values in Grid taken as a flat list.

MD-MD-007: md_filter4(+Grid, -OutGrid)
OutGrid[R][C] is the lower median of the cell value and all in-bounds 4-connected
neighbor values.  The cell itself is always included in the neighborhood.
Typically 3, 4, or 5 values depending on border proximity.

MD-MD-008: md_filter8(+Grid, -OutGrid)
OutGrid[R][C] is the lower median of the cell value and all in-bounds 8-connected
neighbor values.  Typically 4, 6, or 9 values.

MD-MD-009: md_above(+Grid, -Cells)
Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions whose value is strictly greater than
the grid-wide lower median.

MD-MD-010: md_below(+Grid, -Cells)
Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions whose value is strictly less than the
grid-wide lower median.

MD-MD-011: md_row_above(+Grid, +R, -Cells)
Cells is the list of R-C positions in row R whose value is strictly greater than
that row's lower median.

MD-MD-012: md_row_below(+Grid, +R, -Cells)
Cells is the list of R-C positions in row R whose value is strictly less than that
row's lower median.

MD-MD-013: md_col_above(+Grid, +C, -Cells)
Cells is the list of R-C positions in column C whose value is strictly greater
than that column's lower median.

MD-MD-014: md_col_below(+Grid, +C, -Cells)
Cells is the list of R-C positions in column C whose value is strictly less than
that column's lower median.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3.
Built-ins: msort/2, length/2, between/3, findall/3.

END OF PART 146

Part 147: Neighborhood Mode Filter for 2D Grids (nm_* prefix, Layer 136)

This part specifies the nmode pack: 14 predicates for computing the mode
(most frequent value, with smallest-value tie-breaking) of integer lists,
grid rows, columns, entire grids, and per-cell 4-connected and 8-connected
neighborhoods; plus uniform neighborhood detection and outlier detection.

The mode is complementary to the median (md_*) and to per-cell neighbor
aggregates (na_*): where na_* measures sums, maxima, minima, means, and
ranges, and md_* identifies the middle value, nm_* identifies the most
common value in any region.

All predicates use nm_freq_pairs_ internally to build Value-Count association
pairs from an msort-sorted list, then pick the maximum count. Ties in
frequency are resolved by sorting candidates ascending and returning the
first (smallest) value.

Requirement NM-NM-001:
  nm_mode(+List, -M): M is the mode of a non-empty integer list.
  Ties are broken by smallest value.

Requirement NM-NM-002:
  nm_mode_all(+List, -Ms): Ms is the sorted list of all values tied for
  the highest frequency in List.

Requirement NM-NM-003:
  nm_mode_count(+List, -M, -Count): M is the mode and Count is how many
  times M appears in List. Tie-breaking as in NM-NM-001.

Requirement NM-NM-004:
  nm_row(+Grid, +R, -M): M is the mode of row R (0-based) of Grid.

Requirement NM-NM-005:
  nm_col(+Grid, +C, -M): M is the mode of column C (0-based) of Grid.

Requirement NM-NM-006:
  nm_row_modes(+Grid, -Ms): Ms is the list of modes, one per row,
  in row order.

Requirement NM-NM-007:
  nm_col_modes(+Grid, -Ms): Ms is the list of modes, one per column,
  in column order.

Requirement NM-NM-008:
  nm_grid(+Grid, -M): M is the mode of all cell values in Grid.

Requirement NM-NM-009:
  nm_filter4(+Grid, -OutGrid): OutGrid[R][C] is the mode of the cell
  value plus all in-bounds 4-connected neighbor values.

Requirement NM-NM-010:
  nm_filter8(+Grid, -OutGrid): OutGrid[R][C] is the mode of the cell
  value plus all in-bounds 8-connected neighbor values.

Requirement NM-NM-011:
  nm_uniform4(+Grid, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  whose in-bounds 4-connected neighbors all share exactly one distinct value.

Requirement NM-NM-012:
  nm_uniform8(+Grid, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  whose in-bounds 8-connected neighbors all share exactly one distinct value.

Requirement NM-NM-013:
  nm_outlier4(+Grid, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  whose value differs numerically from the mode of their in-bounds
  4-connected neighbors (cell value excluded from the neighborhood mode).

Requirement NM-NM-014:
  nm_outlier8(+Grid, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  whose value differs numerically from the mode of their in-bounds
  8-connected neighbors (cell value excluded from the neighborhood mode).

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, max_list/2.
Built-ins: msort/2, sort/2, length/2, between/3, findall/3.

END OF PART 147

Part 148: Dense Ranking of Integer Values in Lists and 2D Grids (rk_* prefix, Layer 137)

This part specifies the rank pack: 14 predicates for 1-based dense ranking
of integers in lists and 2D grids, 0-based argsort (ascending and descending),
per-row and per-column rank grids, grid-wide rank grid, cell-level rank queries,
top-N and bottom-N cell selection by distinct value, and rank-threshold filtering.

Dense rank: the sorted unique values in ascending order form the rank scale.
The smallest distinct value has rank 1, the second smallest has rank 2, and so on.
All occurrences of the same value receive the same rank. The rank scale has as
many levels as there are distinct values.

Requirement RK-RK-001:
  rk_rank_of(+List, +V, -R): R is the 1-based dense rank of value V in List.
  Fails if V does not appear in List.

Requirement RK-RK-002:
  rk_dense(+List, -Ranks): Ranks is the list of 1-based dense ranks for each
  element of List, in the same order.

Requirement RK-RK-003:
  rk_argsort_asc(+List, -Indices): Indices is the list of 0-based positions
  of List elements sorted in ascending value order. Stable for equal values.

Requirement RK-RK-004:
  rk_argsort_desc(+List, -Indices): Indices sorted in descending value order.
  Stable for equal values.

Requirement RK-RK-005:
  rk_row_dense(+Grid, -RankGrid): each cell replaced with its 1-based dense
  rank within its own row.

Requirement RK-RK-006:
  rk_col_dense(+Grid, -RankGrid): each cell replaced with its 1-based dense
  rank within its own column.

Requirement RK-RK-007:
  rk_grid_dense(+Grid, -RankGrid): each cell replaced with its 1-based dense
  rank among all cell values in Grid.

Requirement RK-RK-008:
  rk_row_rank_of(+Grid, +R, +C, -Rank): 1-based dense rank of cell (R,C)
  within row R.

Requirement RK-RK-009:
  rk_col_rank_of(+Grid, +R, +C, -Rank): 1-based dense rank of cell (R,C)
  within column C.

Requirement RK-RK-010:
  rk_grid_rank_of(+Grid, +R, +C, -Rank): 1-based dense rank of cell (R,C)
  among all cell values in Grid.

Requirement RK-RK-011:
  rk_top_n(+Grid, +N, -Cells): sorted R-C positions of cells whose value is
  among the N largest distinct values. All cells with those values included.

Requirement RK-RK-012:
  rk_bottom_n(+Grid, +N, -Cells): sorted R-C positions of cells whose value
  is among the N smallest distinct values.

Requirement RK-RK-013:
  rk_above_rank(+Grid, +K, -Cells): sorted R-C positions whose grid-wide
  dense rank is strictly greater than K.

Requirement RK-RK-014:
  rk_below_rank(+Grid, +K, -Cells): sorted R-C positions whose grid-wide
  dense rank is strictly less than K.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3.
Built-ins: sort/2, msort/2, length/2, between/3, findall/3.

END OF PART 148

Part 149: Mean, Sum, and Deviation Statistics for Integer Lists and 2D Grids (vt_* prefix, Layer 138)

This part specifies the varstat pack: 14 predicates for integer summation,
floor and rounded arithmetic means, signed and absolute per-element deviation
from the floor mean, per-row and per-column sums and means, global grid mean,
and position lists for cells above or below various means.

All mean computations use floor integer division (sum // count) unless the
predicate name contains _round, which uses floating-point rounding.

Requirement VT-VT-001:
  vt_sum(+List, -Sum): Sum is the integer total of all values in List.

Requirement VT-VT-002:
  vt_mean_floor(+List, -Mean): Mean is the floor of the arithmetic mean of
  List (sum // count). Fails when List is empty.

Requirement VT-VT-003:
  vt_mean_round(+List, -Mean): Mean is the rounded arithmetic mean of List.
  Uses floating-point division and banker's rounding (round/1). Fails when
  List is empty.

Requirement VT-VT-004:
  vt_deviation(+List, -Devs): Devs[I] = List[I] - floor_mean(List).
  Each value is a signed integer deviation from the floor mean.

Requirement VT-VT-005:
  vt_abs_deviation(+List, -AbsDevs): AbsDevs[I] = |List[I] - floor_mean(List)|.
  Each value is a non-negative integer absolute deviation.

Requirement VT-VT-006:
  vt_row_sums(+Grid, -Sums): Sums[R] is the integer sum of all values in row R.

Requirement VT-VT-007:
  vt_col_sums(+Grid, -Sums): Sums[C] is the integer sum of all values in column C.

Requirement VT-VT-008:
  vt_row_means(+Grid, -Means): Means[R] is the floor mean of all values in row R.

Requirement VT-VT-009:
  vt_col_means(+Grid, -Means): Means[C] is the floor mean of all values in column C.

Requirement VT-VT-010:
  vt_global_mean(+Grid, -Mean): Mean is the floor mean of all cell values in Grid.

Requirement VT-VT-011:
  vt_above_mean(+Grid, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  whose value is strictly greater than the global floor mean.

Requirement VT-VT-012:
  vt_below_mean(+Grid, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  whose value is strictly less than the global floor mean.

Requirement VT-VT-013:
  vt_row_above_mean(+Grid, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  whose value is strictly greater than the floor mean of their own row.

Requirement VT-VT-014:
  vt_col_above_mean(+Grid, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  whose value is strictly greater than the floor mean of their own column.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, sum_list/2.
Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3.

END OF PART 149

Part 150: Value Co-Occurrence and Adjacency Analysis in 2D Grids (co_* prefix, Layer 139)

This part specifies the cooccur pack: 14 predicates for collecting ordered
horizontal, vertical, and diagonal adjacent value pairs; counting directed
and undirected adjacent occurrences; testing universal and empty adjacency;
detecting isolated cells; enumerating border values; testing shared borders;
building horizontal transition frequency tables; and finding the most
frequently co-adjacent value.

Requirement CO-CO-001:
  co_h_pairs(+Grid, -Pairs): Pairs is the list of ordered horizontal adjacent
  value pairs A-B where A is immediately left of B in the same row.

Requirement CO-CO-002:
  co_v_pairs(+Grid, -Pairs): Pairs is the list of ordered vertical adjacent
  value pairs A-B where A is immediately above B in the same column.
  Column-major enumeration order.

Requirement CO-CO-003:
  co_d_pairs_dr(+Grid, -Pairs): Pairs is the list of down-right diagonal
  adjacent value pairs A-B: A at (R,C), B at (R+1,C+1).

Requirement CO-CO-004:
  co_d_pairs_dl(+Grid, -Pairs): Pairs is the list of down-left diagonal
  adjacent value pairs A-B: A at (R,C), B at (R+1,C-1).

Requirement CO-CO-005:
  co_count_h(+Grid, +V1, +V2, -N): N is the count of directed horizontal pairs
  where V1 appears immediately to the left of V2.

Requirement CO-CO-006:
  co_count_v(+Grid, +V1, +V2, -N): N is the count of directed vertical pairs
  where V1 appears immediately above V2.

Requirement CO-CO-007:
  co_count_adj4(+Grid, +V1, +V2, -N): N is the count of undirected 4-adjacent
  {V1,V2} pairs. When V1 == V2, counts V1-V1 directed pairs. When V1 \= V2,
  adds the count of V1-V2 and V2-V1 directed pairs.

Requirement CO-CO-008:
  co_always_adj4(+Grid, +V1, +V2): succeeds if every cell with value V1 has
  at least one 4-adjacent cell with value V2.

Requirement CO-CO-009:
  co_never_adj4(+Grid, +V1, +V2): succeeds if no cell with value V1 is
  4-adjacent to any cell with value V2.

Requirement CO-CO-010:
  co_isolated4(+Grid, +V, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  with value V that have no 4-adjacent cell with the same value V.

Requirement CO-CO-011:
  co_border_vals(+Grid, +V, -Vals): Vals is the sorted list of distinct
  values W (W \= V) that 4-neighbor at least one V cell.

Requirement CO-CO-012:
  co_shared_border(+Grid, +V1, +V2): succeeds if some cell with value V1 is
  4-adjacent to some cell with value V2.

Requirement CO-CO-013:
  co_row_transitions(+Grid, -Triples): Triples is the list of A-B-N terms
  for directed horizontal adjacent pair A-B occurring N times, sorted by
  N descending (most frequent first).

Requirement CO-CO-014:
  co_most_common_adj4(+Grid, +V, -W): W is the value most frequently
  4-adjacent to V cells. Ties broken by largest value (msort+last).
  Fails if V has no 4-adjacent cells of any other value.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, last/2, append/3.
Library imports: library(apply): include/3.
Built-ins: sort/2, msort/2, length/2, between/3, findall/3.

END OF PART 150

PART 151: ROWSIG PACK (rs_* prefix, Layer 140)

Work Package 161. General-purpose row and column signature analysis for 2D grids.
Provides predicates for single-column extraction, all-column enumeration, row and
column frequency tables, modal row and column identification, unique row and column
detection, duplicate row and column pair finding, palindrome testing for rows and
columns, and anagram testing for row and column pairs.

Requirement RS-RS-001:
  rs_col_at(+Grid, +C, -Col): Col is the ordered list of values in column C,
  enumerated top-to-bottom (row 0 first).

Requirement RS-RS-002:
  rs_all_cols(+Grid, -Cols): Cols is the list of all column lists in column
  order (column 0 first). Each element is a top-to-bottom list of values.

Requirement RS-RS-003:
  rs_row_freq(+Grid, -Freqs): Freqs is the list of Row-N pairs where N is the
  number of times Row appears in Grid. Sorted by N descending; equal-count rows
  ordered by reverse standard order (largest row last in msort, which becomes
  first after reverse).

Requirement RS-RS-004:
  rs_col_freq(+Grid, -Freqs): Freqs is the list of Col-N pairs where N is the
  number of times column list Col appears. Sorted by N descending.

Requirement RS-RS-005:
  rs_modal_row(+Grid, -Row): Row is the row that appears most often in Grid.
  Ties broken by largest row in standard order (via msort + last). Fails if
  Grid is empty.

Requirement RS-RS-006:
  rs_modal_col(+Grid, -Col): Col is the column list that appears most often.
  Ties broken by largest column list (via msort + last). Fails if Grid has
  no columns.

Requirement RS-RS-007:
  rs_uniq_rows(+Grid, -Pairs): Pairs is the list of R-Row terms for each row
  index R whose row appears exactly once in Grid. Ordered by row index ascending.

Requirement RS-RS-008:
  rs_uniq_cols(+Grid, -Pairs): Pairs is the list of C-Col terms for each column
  index C whose column list appears exactly once. Ordered by column index ascending.

Requirement RS-RS-009:
  rs_dup_row_pairs(+Grid, -Pairs): Pairs is the list of R1-R2 index pairs where
  row R1 equals row R2 and R1 < R2. Ordered by R1 ascending, then R2 ascending.

Requirement RS-RS-010:
  rs_dup_col_pairs(+Grid, -Pairs): Pairs is the list of C1-C2 index pairs where
  column C1 equals column C2 and C1 < C2. Ordered by C1 ascending, then C2.

Requirement RS-RS-011:
  rs_row_palindrome(+Grid, +R): succeeds if row R reads the same left-to-right
  and right-to-left (the row list equals its own reverse).

Requirement RS-RS-012:
  rs_col_palindrome(+Grid, +C): succeeds if column C reads the same top-to-bottom
  and bottom-to-top (the column list equals its own reverse).

Requirement RS-RS-013:
  rs_rows_anagram(+Grid, +R1, +R2): succeeds if rows R1 and R2 in Grid have the
  same multiset of values (msort of both rows produces the same list).

Requirement RS-RS-014:
  rs_cols_anagram(+Grid, +C1, +C2): succeeds if columns C1 and C2 in Grid have
  the same multiset of values (msort of both columns produces the same list).

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, reverse/2, last/2.
Library imports: library(apply): include/3.
Built-ins: sort/2, msort/2, length/2, between/3, findall/3.

END OF PART 151

PART 152: GRIDOPS PACK (go_* prefix, Layer 141)

Work Package 162. General-purpose grid collection operations for reasoning
across multiple 2D integer grids simultaneously.

Requirement GO-GO-001:
  go_always(+Grids, +V, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  at which EVERY grid in Grids contains value V.

Requirement GO-GO-002:
  go_never(+Grids, +V, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  at which NO grid in Grids contains value V.

Requirement GO-GO-003:
  go_sometimes(+Grids, +V, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  at which SOME (>=1) grid has value V but NOT every grid does.

Requirement GO-GO-004:
  go_count_v(+Grids, +V, -CountGrid): CountGrid is a grid of integers where
  each cell (R,C) holds the count of grids in Grids that have value V at (R,C).

Requirement GO-GO-005:
  go_modal(+Grids, -ModalGrid): ModalGrid is a grid where each cell (R,C)
  holds the value appearing most often across all grids at that position.
  Ties broken by smallest value.

Requirement GO-GO-006:
  go_stable(+Grids, -Triples): Triples is the list of R-C-V terms for
  positions where ALL grids in Grids agree on value V.

Requirement GO-GO-007:
  go_unstable(+Grids, -Cells): Cells is the sorted list of R-C positions
  where the grids do NOT all agree on the same value.

Requirement GO-GO-008:
  go_eq(+G1, +G2): succeeds if G1 and G2 are cell-for-cell identical grids.

Requirement GO-GO-009:
  go_add(+G1, +G2, -G): G is the elementwise integer sum of G1 and G2.
  G[R][C] = G1[R][C] + G2[R][C].

Requirement GO-GO-010:
  go_sub(+G1, +G2, -G): G is the elementwise integer difference G1 minus G2.
  G[R][C] = G1[R][C] - G2[R][C].

Requirement GO-GO-011:
  go_emax(+G1, +G2, -G): G is the elementwise integer maximum of G1 and G2.
  G[R][C] = max(G1[R][C], G2[R][C]).

Requirement GO-GO-012:
  go_emin(+G1, +G2, -G): G is the elementwise integer minimum of G1 and G2.
  G[R][C] = min(G1[R][C], G2[R][C]).

Requirement GO-GO-013:
  go_overlay(+Grids, +Bg, -G): G is the overlay of all grids. At each (R,C),
  the result is the first non-Bg value found scanning Grids in order; Bg if
  all are Bg.

Requirement GO-GO-014:
  go_intersect(+Grids, +Bg, -G): G is the intersection of all grids. At each
  (R,C), if ALL grids have the same non-Bg value V, result is V; else Bg.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, last/2.
Library imports: library(apply): maplist/3, maplist/4, include/3.
Built-ins: sort/2, msort/2, length/2, between/3, forall/2, findall/3.

END OF PART 152

PART 153: INDEX PACK - COORDINATE-VALUED GRID GENERATION AND INDEX MASKING (ix_* prefix)

Layer 142. Work Package 163.

Purpose: The index pack generates special 2D grids whose cell values are
derived entirely from cell coordinates (row index, column index, or derived
quantities). These coordinate grids serve as operands in arithmetic operations,
masks for row/column selection, and distance fields for spatial analysis.

Requirement IX-IX-001:
  ix_row_grid(+H, +W, -Grid): Grid is H rows by W cols; cell(R,C) = R.
  Row 0 is all zeros; row H-1 is all H-1.

Requirement IX-IX-002:
  ix_col_grid(+H, +W, -Grid): Grid is H rows by W cols; cell(R,C) = C.
  Every row is [0, 1, 2, ..., W-1].

Requirement IX-IX-003:
  ix_sum_grid(+H, +W, -Grid): Grid is H rows by W cols; cell(R,C) = R+C.
  Cells on the same top-left/bottom-right diagonal share the same value.

Requirement IX-IX-004:
  ix_diff_grid(+H, +W, -Grid): Grid is H rows by W cols; cell(R,C) = R-C.
  Values may be negative. Cells on the same anti-diagonal share a value.

Requirement IX-IX-005:
  ix_prod_grid(+H, +W, -Grid): Grid is H rows by W cols; cell(R,C) = R*C.
  Row 0 and column 0 are all zeros.

Requirement IX-IX-006:
  ix_manhattan_grid(+H, +W, +R0, +C0, -Grid): cell(R,C) = |R-R0|+|C-C0|.
  Manhattan distance from the reference point (R0,C0) to each cell.

Requirement IX-IX-007:
  ix_chebyshev_grid(+H, +W, +R0, +C0, -Grid): cell(R,C) = max(|R-R0|,|C-C0|).
  Chebyshev (king-move) distance from (R0,C0). Cells at distance K form a
  hollow square shell around (R0,C0).

Requirement IX-IX-008:
  ix_mod_grid(+H, +W, +N, -Grid): cell(R,C) = (R+C) mod N.
  Diagonal stripe pattern; period N along diagonals.

Requirement IX-IX-009:
  ix_row_mod_grid(+H, +W, +N, -Grid): cell(R,C) = R mod N.
  Horizontal stripe pattern; period N across rows.

Requirement IX-IX-010:
  ix_col_mod_grid(+H, +W, +N, -Grid): cell(R,C) = C mod N.
  Vertical stripe pattern; period N across columns.

Requirement IX-IX-011:
  ix_mask_rows(+Grid, +Is, +Bg, -Grid2): Grid2 is Grid with rows whose
  0-based index is NOT in Is replaced by all-Bg rows. Rows in Is unchanged.

Requirement IX-IX-012:
  ix_mask_cols(+Grid, +Js, +Bg, -Grid2): Grid2 is Grid with columns whose
  0-based index is NOT in Js replaced by Bg. Columns in Js unchanged.

Requirement IX-IX-013:
  ix_apply(+IxGrid, +Op, +Grid, -Out): Out[R][C] = Grid[R][C] Op IxGrid[R][C].
  Op is one of: add, sub, mul, max_op, min_op.

Requirement IX-IX-014:
  ix_from(+H, +W, +R0, +C0, -Grid): cell(R,C) = (R-R0)*W + (C-C0).
  Linear row-major offset from reference point (R0,C0). May be negative.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3.
Built-ins: length/2, between/3, findall/3.

END OF PART 153


PART 154: FOLD PACK REQUIREMENTS

Layer 143. Module: fold. Prefix: fd_*. Work Package 164.

The fold pack provides predicates for splitting a 2D grid into two halves along a
horizontal or vertical crease, overlaying two same-size grids with a background
priority rule, folding one half onto the other as in paper origami, unfolding a
half-grid into a symmetric full grid, testing whether a grid is symmetric under a
fold crease, finding a fold crease automatically, detecting all-V marker rows or
columns, and composing a double fold (horizontal then vertical). These operations
support visual reasoning tasks where grids are derived from folded symmetric
structures.

Requirement FD-FD-001: fd_split_h(+Grid, +R, -Top, -Bottom).
Split Grid horizontally at crease row R. Top contains rows 0 through R inclusive
(length R+1). Bottom contains rows R+1 through H-1. If R+1 equals H then Bottom is
the empty list. Uses list prefix of length R+1 via length/2 and append/3.

Requirement FD-FD-002: fd_split_v(+Grid, +C, -Left, -Right).
Split Grid vertically at crease column C. Left contains columns 0 through C
inclusive (C+1 columns per row). Right contains columns C+1 through W-1. Each row
is split independently via a helper. Uses maplist/4 and length/2 and append/3.

Requirement FD-FD-003: fd_overlay(+A, +B, +Bg, -Out).
Cell-by-cell overlay of two same-size grids. Out[R][C] equals A[R][C] when
A[R][C] is not equal to Bg; otherwise Out[R][C] equals B[R][C]. Grid A takes
priority: non-background cells of A cover corresponding cells in B. Uses maplist/4
over rows, then maplist/4 over cells.

Requirement FD-FD-004: fd_fold_h(+Grid, +R, +Bg, -Out).
Fold the bottom half of Grid upward with crease after row R. Top = rows 0..R.
Bottom = rows R+1..H-1. For each row index I in 0..R: K = R - I. If K is in range
[0, length(Bottom)-1] then Out[I] = overlay(Top[I], Bottom[K], Bg); otherwise
Out[I] = Top[I]. Output has R+1 rows and same width as Grid.

Requirement FD-FD-005: fd_fold_v(+Grid, +C, +Bg, -Out).
Fold the right half of Grid leftward with crease after column C. Left = cols 0..C.
Right = cols C+1..W-1. For each column index I in 0..C: K = C - I. If K is in
range [0, length(Right_row)-1] then Out[row][I] = overlay(Left[row][I],
Right[row][K], Bg); otherwise Out[row][I] = Left[row][I]. Output has C+1 columns.

Requirement FD-FD-006: fd_unfold_h(+Half, -Grid).
Create a symmetric full grid from a top half by stacking Half above its row-reversed
copy. Grid = append(Half, reverse(Half)). Height of Grid is twice height of Half.

Requirement FD-FD-007: fd_unfold_v(+Half, -Grid).
Create a symmetric full grid from a left half by joining each row with its reverse.
Grid[R] = append(Half[R], reverse(Half[R])). Width of Grid is twice width of Half.

Requirement FD-FD-008: fd_sym_h(+Grid, +R).
Succeed if Grid is symmetric under a horizontal fold with crease after row R.
Mirror formula: row I corresponds to row (2*R + 1 - I). If both I and 2*R+1-I are
in bounds then Grid[I] must equal Grid[2*R+1-I]; otherwise the pair is skipped.
This formula is consistent with fd_fold_h and fd_unfold_h semantics.

Requirement FD-FD-009: fd_sym_v(+Grid, +C).
Succeed if Grid is symmetric under a vertical fold with crease after column C.
Mirror formula: column J corresponds to column (2*C + 1 - J). If both J and
2*C+1-J are in bounds then all cells in column J must equal the corresponding cells
in column 2*C+1-J; otherwise the pair is skipped.

Requirement FD-FD-010: fd_find_fold_h(+Grid, -R).
Find the first row index R (tried in order 0, 1, ..., H-1) around which Grid is
fold-symmetric as defined by fd_sym_h. Fails if no such R exists. Uses between/3
and cuts after the first success.

Requirement FD-FD-011: fd_find_fold_v(+Grid, -C).
Find the first column index C (tried in order 0, 1, ..., W-1) around which Grid is
fold-symmetric as defined by fd_sym_v. Fails if no such C exists.

Requirement FD-FD-012: fd_mark_row(+Grid, +V, -R).
R is the first row index (0-based) such that every cell in that row equals V. Uses
between/3, nth0/3, forall/2, and member/2. Fails if no such row exists.

Requirement FD-FD-013: fd_mark_col(+Grid, +V, -C).
C is the first column index (0-based) such that every cell in that column equals V.
Uses between/3, forall/2, member/2, and nth0/3. Fails if no such column exists.

Requirement FD-FD-014: fd_fold_both(+Grid, +R, +C, +Bg, -Out).
Apply fd_fold_h at row R to get an intermediate grid, then apply fd_fold_v at column
C to that intermediate grid. Output has height R+1 and width C+1.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, append/2, append/3, reverse/2.
Library imports: library(apply): maplist/3, maplist/4.
Built-ins: between/3, forall/2, findall/3, length/2.

END OF PART 154


PART 155: ROTATION PACK REQUIREMENTS

Layer 144. Module: rotation. Prefix: ro_*. Work Package 165.

The rotation pack provides predicates for rotating 2D grids by multiples of 90
degrees clockwise, testing rotational symmetry, rotating cell coordinate sets,
combining grids through rotation-based overlay (spin), and finding which rotation
maps one grid to another. All rotations are clockwise.

Rotation conventions:
  90 CW: (R,C) -> (C, H-1-R). Output is W rows by H cols.
  180: (R,C) -> (H-1-R, W-1-C). Output is H rows by W cols.
  270 CW: (R,C) -> (W-1-C, R). Output is W rows by H cols.

Requirement RO-RO-001: ro_rot90(+Grid, -Out).
Rotate Grid 90 degrees clockwise. Out has W rows and H columns. Each new row C of
Out equals column C of Grid read from the bottom row upward. Uses nested findall
with between/3 and nth0/3.

Requirement RO-RO-002: ro_rot180(+Grid, -Out).
Rotate Grid 180 degrees. Out has the same dimensions as Grid. Implemented as
maplist(reverse, Grid, Temp) followed by reverse(Temp, Out).

Requirement RO-RO-003: ro_rot270(+Grid, -Out).
Rotate Grid 270 degrees clockwise (= 90 counter-clockwise). Out has W rows and H
columns. Each new row index C of Out equals column W-1-C of Grid read top to bottom.

Requirement RO-RO-004: ro_rot_n(+Grid, +N, -Out).
Rotate Grid by N*90 degrees clockwise; N in 0..3. N=0: identity (cut). N=1:
delegates to ro_rot90 (cut). N=2: delegates to ro_rot180 (cut). N=3: delegates to
ro_rot270.

Requirement RO-RO-005: ro_all(+Grid, -Rots).
Produce list [G0, G90, G180, G270] of all four rotations of Grid.

Requirement RO-RO-006: ro_canonical(+Grid, -Canon).
Canon is the lexicographically smallest of the four rotations of Grid under standard
SWI-Prolog term ordering. Uses ro_all and msort/2.

Requirement RO-RO-007: ro_is_rot2(+Grid).
Succeed if Grid is structurally equal to its 180-degree rotation. Checks Grid ==
ro_rot180(Grid).

Requirement RO-RO-008: ro_is_rot4(+Grid).
Succeed if Grid is structurally equal to its 90-degree rotation. Checks Grid ==
ro_rot90(Grid). Requires Grid to be square.

Requirement RO-RO-009: ro_sym_order(+Grid, -N).
N is the smallest order in {1, 2, 4} such that Grid has N-fold rotational symmetry.
N=4 if ro_is_rot4 succeeds; N=2 if ro_is_rot2 succeeds; N=1 otherwise.

Requirement RO-RO-010: ro_rotate_cells(+Cells, +H, +W, +N, -Out).
Rotate a list of R-C cell coordinate pairs by N*90 degrees clockwise within an H by
W bounding box. Uses a private helper ro_apply_cell_/7 with clauses for N=0..3.
N=0: identity. N=1: (R,C) -> (C, H-1-R). N=2: (R,C) -> (H-1-R, W-1-C).
N=3: (R,C) -> (W-1-C, R).

Requirement RO-RO-011: ro_spin2(+Grid, +Bg, -Out).
Overlay Grid with its 180-degree rotation using background-priority semantics.
Non-background cells of Grid take priority over the rotated copy.

Requirement RO-RO-012: ro_spin4(+Grid, +Bg, -Out).
Overlay all four rotations of Grid with background-priority semantics. Applies
overlays in order: Grid, then G90, then G180, then G270.

Requirement RO-RO-013: ro_match_rotation(+GridA, +GridB, -N).
Find the smallest N in 0..3 such that ro_rot_n(GridA, N) equals GridB. Uses
between/3 and cuts after the first match. Fails if no rotation matches.

Requirement RO-RO-014: ro_equiv_rotation(+GridA, +GridB).
Succeed if any rotation of GridA equals GridB. Wraps ro_match_rotation/3.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, reverse/2.
Library imports: library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3.
Built-ins: between/3, length/2, findall/3, msort/2.

END OF PART 155

PART 156: WARP PACK

Work Package 166. Layer 145. Prefix: wr_. Module: warp. File: packs/warp/prolog/warp.pl.

The warp pack provides 14 predicates for shear transformations, cyclic (toroidal)
shifts, per-row arbitrary offset warping, anti-diagonal transposition, and detection
of shear relationships between grids. These predicates extend the fold (Layer 143)
and rotation (Layer 144) packs to cover the non-rigid, progressive-shift family of
grid transformations needed for visual reasoning tasks involving staircase patterns,
toroidal wrapping, and skewed grids.

Requirement WR-WR-001: wr_shift_row(+Grid, +R, +N, +Bg, -Out).
Shift row R right by N cells; fill vacated cells with Bg. N may be negative (shift
left). Formula: Out_row_R[C] = Grid_row_R[C - N] if C-N in [0,W-1], else Bg. All
other rows pass through unchanged.

Requirement WR-WR-002: wr_shift_col(+Grid, +C, +N, +Bg, -Out).
Shift column C down by N cells; fill vacated cells with Bg. N may be negative (shift
up). Formula: Out[R][C] = Grid[R-N][C] if R-N in [0,H-1], else Bg. All other columns
pass through unchanged.

Requirement WR-WR-003: wr_shear_h(+Grid, +Step, +Bg, -Out).
Horizontal shear: row I shifts right by I*Step. Row 0 is unchanged. Formula:
Out[I][C] = Grid[I][C - I*Step] if C - I*Step in [0,W-1], else Bg. Step=0 is
identity; Step>0 shifts rightward with increasing row; Step<0 shifts leftward.

Requirement WR-WR-004: wr_shear_v(+Grid, +Step, +Bg, -Out).
Vertical shear: column J shifts down by J*Step. Column 0 is unchanged. Formula:
Out[R][J] = Grid[R - J*Step][J] if R - J*Step in [0,H-1], else Bg.

Requirement WR-WR-005: wr_unshear_h(+Grid, +Step, +Bg, -Out).
Undo horizontal shear: row I shifts left by I*Step. Equivalent to wr_shear_h with
-Step. Is the perfect inverse of wr_shear_h when no content was lost to boundary
clipping.

Requirement WR-WR-006: wr_unshear_v(+Grid, +Step, +Bg, -Out).
Undo vertical shear: column J shifts up by J*Step. Equivalent to wr_shear_v with
-Step. Is the perfect inverse of wr_shear_v when no content was lost.

Requirement WR-WR-007: wr_cyclic_h(+Grid, +N, -Out).
Cyclically shift all rows right by N with toroidal wrap-around. No fill color needed.
Formula: Out[I][C] = Grid[I][(C-N) mod W]. N=0 or N=W is identity. Uses
wr_cyclic_row_ helper via findall.

Requirement WR-WR-008: wr_cyclic_v(+Grid, +N, -Out).
Cyclically shift all columns down by N with toroidal wrap-around. Formula:
Out[R][C] = Grid[(R-N) mod H][C]. N=0 or N=H is identity.

Requirement WR-WR-009: wr_cyclic_shear_h(+Grid, +Step, -Out).
Cyclic horizontal shear: row I wraps right by I*Step. Formula:
Out[I][C] = Grid[I][(C - I*Step) mod W].

Requirement WR-WR-010: wr_cyclic_shear_v(+Grid, +Step, -Out).
Cyclic vertical shear: column J wraps down by J*Step. Formula:
Out[R][J] = Grid[(R - J*Step) mod H][J].

Requirement WR-WR-011: wr_skew_offsets(+Grid, +Offsets, +Bg, -Out).
Generalized row-warp: row I shifts right by Offsets[I]. Offsets is a list of integers
of the same length as Grid. wr_shear_h(Grid, Step, Bg, Out) is equivalent to
wr_skew_offsets(Grid, [0, Step, 2*Step, ...], Bg, Out).

Requirement WR-WR-012: wr_transpose_anti(+Grid, -Out).
Anti-diagonal transpose. Out has W rows and H columns. Formula:
Out[J][I] = Grid[H-1-I][W-1-J] where J in 0..W-1, I in 0..H-1. For square grids,
applying this twice returns the original grid (involution property).

Requirement WR-WR-013: wr_find_shear_h(+GridA, +GridB, +Bg, -Step).
Find the integer Step in [-(W-1), W-1] such that wr_shear_h(GridA, Step, Bg, GridB).
Returns the first match; fails if no such step exists.

Requirement WR-WR-014: wr_find_shear_v(+GridA, +GridB, +Bg, -Step).
Find the integer Step in [-(H-1), H-1] such that wr_shear_v(GridA, Step, Bg, GridB).
Returns the first match; fails if no such step exists.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/2, reverse/2.
Library imports: library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3.
Built-ins: between/3, length/2, findall/3.

END OF PART 156

PART 157: BORDER PACK

Work Package 167. Layer 146. Prefix: br_. Module: border. File: packs/border/prolog/border.pl.

The border pack provides 14 predicates for concentric ring analysis of 2D grids.
The central concept is the ring depth formula: for a cell (R,C) in an H x W grid,
ring_depth = min(R, H-1-R, C, W-1-C). Ring 0 is the outermost border ring. Ring N
is N steps inward from the outer edge. A 3x3 grid has rings 0 and 1 where ring 1 is
the single center cell. A 5x5 grid has rings 0, 1, 2 where ring 2 is the center cell.
The maximum ring index is (min(H,W)-1)//2. The pack enables ring enumeration,
uniformity testing, border addition and stripping, nested (bullseye) structure
detection, depth mapping, and ring filling.

Requirement BR-BR-001: br_ring_cells(+Grid, +N, -Cells).
Cells is a list of R-C pairs in ring N listed in row-major order. Uses the private
helper br_ring_depth_(H, W, R, C, D) = min(R, H-1-R, C, W-1-C) to test each cell.
Requires H1 is H-1 and W1 is W-1 before between/3 calls.

Requirement BR-BR-002: br_ring_vals(+Grid, +N, -Vals).
Vals is a list of grid values at ring N in row-major order. Uses br_ring_cells to get
cell positions, then nth0/3 to read the value at each position.

Requirement BR-BR-003: br_ring_color(+Grid, +N, -Color).
Uniform color of ring N. Fails if ring N is empty or contains more than one distinct
value. Uses sort/2 on the value list; succeeds only when sort produces a singleton.

Requirement BR-BR-004: br_is_uniform_ring(+Grid, +N).
Succeed if ring N of Grid has a single uniform color. Wraps br_ring_color/3 and
discards the color.

Requirement BR-BR-005: br_add_border(+Grid, +V, -Out).
Add one layer of V cells around Grid. Out has H+2 rows and W+2 columns. The top and
bottom rows contain NewW = W+2 copies of V. Middle rows are produced with findall
using append([V|Row], [V], NewRow) for each original row.

Requirement BR-BR-006: br_strip_border(+Grid, -Inner).
Remove the outermost ring from Grid. Inner is the (H-2) x (W-2) sub-grid. If H < 2
or W < 2 the inner grid is empty and Inner = []. Uses between(1, H2, R) with
H2 is H-2 to select inner rows and between(1, W2, C) with W2 is W-2 to select
inner columns.

Requirement BR-BR-007: br_inner_n(+Grid, +N, -Inner).
Strip N outermost rings from Grid. N=0 returns Grid unchanged via a cut clause.
N>0 strips one ring with br_strip_border then recurses with N1 is N-1. Equivalent
to applying br_strip_border N times.

Requirement BR-BR-008: br_outer_color(+Grid, -V).
Uniform color of the outermost ring (ring 0). Wraps br_ring_color(Grid, 0, V).
Fails if the outermost ring is not uniform.

Requirement BR-BR-009: br_is_uniform_outer(+Grid).
Succeed if the outermost ring of Grid is uniform. Wraps br_outer_color/2 and
discards the color.

Requirement BR-BR-010: br_ring_colors(+Grid, -Colors).
List of uniform ring colors from outside in. The private helper br_ring_colors_/4
collects color at ring N, then recurses for N+1, and stops when N > MaxN or when
a ring is non-uniform. The list terminates at the first non-uniform ring.

Requirement BR-BR-011: br_max_ring(+Grid, -N).
Index of the innermost ring. N = (min(H, W) - 1) // 2. For a 3x3 grid N=1. For
a 5x5 grid N=2. For a 1x1 grid N=0.

Requirement BR-BR-012: br_is_nested(+Grid).
Succeed if every ring of Grid is uniform (concentric bullseye pattern). Uses
forall(between(0, MaxN, N), br_is_uniform_ring(Grid, N)) where MaxN = br_max_ring.

Requirement BR-BR-013: br_depth_map(+Grid, -DepthGrid).
Grid where each cell holds its ring index. DepthGrid[R][C] equals the ring depth
of cell (R,C) in Grid. Requires H1 is H-1 and W1 is W-1 before between/3 calls in
the outer and inner findall.

Requirement BR-BR-014: br_fill_ring(+Grid, +N, +V, -Out).
Replace all cells in ring N with value V; non-ring cells keep their original values.
Uses private helper br_replace_cell_if_/8 which replaces OldV with V when ring depth
equals N and otherwise keeps OldV. Requires H1 is H-1 and W1 is W-1 before between/3.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, numlist/3, append/2, append/3.
Library imports: library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3.
Built-ins: between/3, length/2, findall/3, forall/2, sort/2.

END OF PART 157


PART 158 — SPLICE PACK REQUIREMENTS (sp_* prefix, Layer 147)

Part 158 specifies the splice pack, which provides 14 predicates for structural
editing of 2D grid rows and columns. Unlike cell-level predicates that modify
individual values, splice predicates reshape the grid itself by inserting, deleting,
swapping, reversing, rotating, replicating, or selecting rows and columns.

Prefix: sp_. Module: splice. Layer: 147.

Requirement SP-SP-001: sp_insert_row(+Grid, +R, +NewRow, -Out).
Insert NewRow before row index R. Rows originally at R, R+1, ... shift to R+1,
R+2, ... . R must satisfy 0 =< R =< H where H is the number of rows. R=0 prepends
NewRow. R=H appends NewRow. Implemented with length(Prefix, R), append(Prefix,
Suffix, Grid), append(Prefix, [NewRow|Suffix], Out).

Requirement SP-SP-002: sp_delete_row(+Grid, +R, -Out).
Delete the row at index R. Out has one fewer row than Grid. R must be a valid row
index. Implemented with length(Prefix, R), append(Prefix, [_|Suffix], Grid),
append(Prefix, Suffix, Out).

Requirement SP-SP-003: sp_insert_col(+Grid, +C, +V, -Out).
Insert a column of constant value V before column index C in every row. Columns
originally at C, C+1, ... shift right by one. Implemented by applying the private
helper sp_insert_col_row_/4 to each row via maplist.

Requirement SP-SP-004: sp_delete_col(+Grid, +C, -Out).
Delete the column at index C from every row. Out has one fewer column than Grid.
Implemented by applying the private helper sp_delete_col_row_/3 to each row via
maplist.

Requirement SP-SP-005: sp_swap_rows(+Grid, +R1, +R2, -Out).
Swap the rows at indices R1 and R2. If R1 = R2 the grid is unchanged. Uses findall
with between(0, H1, I) to enumerate indices; row at R1 receives the old R2 row and
vice versa. H1 is H-1.

Requirement SP-SP-006: sp_swap_cols(+Grid, +C1, +C2, -Out).
Swap columns C1 and C2 in every row. If C1 = C2 the grid is unchanged. Implemented
by applying the private helper sp_swap_in_row_/4 to each row via maplist. The helper
uses findall with between(0, W1, C) and W1 is W-1.

Requirement SP-SP-007: sp_reverse_rows(+Grid, -Out).
Reverse the order of rows so that row 0 becomes the last row. Uses reverse/2 from
library(lists) on the top-level row list.

Requirement SP-SP-008: sp_reverse_cols(+Grid, -Out).
Reverse the order of cells in each row. Uses maplist(reverse, Grid, Out) where
reverse/2 is imported from library(lists).

Requirement SP-SP-009: sp_rotate_rows(+Grid, +K, -Out).
Shift rows cyclically so that row K becomes row 0. K is taken modulo H so values
>= H and multiples of H are handled correctly. Implemented with length(Prefix, K1)
where K1 is K mod H, then append(Prefix, Suffix, Grid), append(Suffix, Prefix, Out).

Requirement SP-SP-010: sp_rotate_cols(+Grid, +K, -Out).
Shift columns cyclically so that column K becomes column 0. K is taken modulo W.
Implemented by applying the private helper sp_rotate_row_cols_/3 to each row via
maplist. The helper performs the same cyclic split-and-reassemble as sp_rotate_rows
but on a single row.

Requirement SP-SP-011: sp_replicate_row(+Grid, +R, +N, -Out).
Replace row R with N copies of it in the output. N=1 is identity; N=0 deletes row R;
N=2 inserts one extra copy after R. Implemented with length(Prefix, R), append to
split Grid, length(Copies, N), maplist(=(Row), Copies), append([Prefix, Copies,
Suffix], Out).

Requirement SP-SP-012: sp_replicate_col(+Grid, +C, +N, -Out).
Replace column C with N copies of it in every row. N=1 is identity; N=0 deletes
column C; N=2 inserts one extra copy. Implemented by applying the private helper
sp_replicate_col_in_row_/4 to each row via maplist. The helper uses the same
split-and-reassemble pattern as sp_replicate_row.

Requirement SP-SP-013: sp_select_rows(+Grid, +Indices, -Out).
Keep only the rows at the indices given in Indices, in the order Indices specifies.
Indices may repeat indices or omit any row. Implemented with findall(Row,
(member(I, Indices), nth0(I, Grid, Row)), Out).

Requirement SP-SP-014: sp_select_cols(+Grid, +Indices, -Out).
Keep only the columns at the indices given in Indices, in the order Indices
specifies. Implemented by applying the private helper sp_select_col_from_row_/3
to each row via maplist. The helper uses findall(V, (member(C, Indices),
nth0(C, Row, V)), NewRow).

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, nth0/3, append/2, append/3, reverse/2.
Library imports: library(apply): maplist/2, maplist/3.
Built-ins: length/2, findall/3, between/3.

END OF PART 158


PART 159 — OBJOP PACK REQUIREMENTS (oo_* prefix, Layer 148)

Part 159 specifies the objop pack, which provides 14 predicates for object-level
manipulation within the full 2D grid representation. Where the cellset pack operates
on sparse R-C position lists, objop accepts and returns complete grids, identifying
objects by their color value and applying transformations in place.

Prefix: oo_. Module: objop. Layer: 148.

Requirement OO-OO-001: oo_cells_of(+Grid, +V, -Cells).
Sorted list of R-C pairs where Grid[R][C] = V. Implemented with findall over
between(0, H1, R) and between(0, W1, C) with H1 is H-1 and W1 is W-1, then sort/2
for canonical order. Returns the empty list if V is absent.

Requirement OO-OO-002: oo_bbox(+Cells, -R0, -C0, -R1, -C1).
Bounding box of a non-empty cell list. Extracts all row indices with findall(R,
member(R-_, Cells), Rs) and all column indices with findall(C, member(_-C, Cells),
Cs), then uses min_list/2 and max_list/2 to get the extremes.

Requirement OO-OO-003: oo_count(+Grid, +V, -N).
Number of cells in Grid with value V. Uses oo_cells_of then length/2. Returns 0
when V is absent.

Requirement OO-OO-004: oo_size(+Grid, +V, -H, -W).
Bounding box height H and width W of V cells. Uses oo_cells_of, oo_bbox, then
H is R1-R0+1 and W is C1-C0+1.

Requirement OO-OO-005: oo_center(+Grid, +V, -R, -C).
Center row R and column C of the V cells bounding box, computed with integer
division: R is (R0+R1)//2 and C is (C0+C1)//2.

Requirement OO-OO-006: oo_erase(+Grid, +V, +Bg, -Out).
Replace all V cells in Grid with Bg. Uses oo_cells_of then oo_set_cells_ with Val=Bg.

Requirement OO-OO-007: oo_repaint(+Grid, +V, +NewV, -Out).
Replace all V cells with NewV. Uses oo_cells_of then oo_set_cells_ with Val=NewV.

Requirement OO-OO-008: oo_swap(+Grid, +V1, +V2, -Out).
Exchange all V1 and V2 cells. First sets V1 positions to V2, then sets V2 positions
to V1. Assumes V1 and V2 are non-overlapping colors.

Requirement OO-OO-009: oo_move(+Grid, +V, +DR, +DC, +Bg, -Out).
Translate V cells by (DR, DC). Erases original V cells to Bg, then paints V at
new positions (R+DR, C+DC). Cells translated outside the grid bounds are clipped
and not drawn.

Requirement OO-OO-010: oo_copy(+Grid, +V, +DR, +DC, -Out).
Copy V cells to offset (DR, DC) without erasing the originals. Paints V at
(R+DR, C+DC) for each V cell; in-bounds check applied.

Requirement OO-OO-011: oo_rotate90(+Grid, +V, +Bg, -Out).
Rotate V cells 90 degrees CW around the top-left corner of their bounding box.
Formula in normalized bbox frame: (r, c) → (c, H-1-r) where r=R-R0, c=C-C0.
In absolute coords: NewR = R0+c, NewC = C0+(H-1)-r where H = R1-R0+1. Old cells
are cleared to Bg; rotated cells are painted V. The new bbox top-left is still
(R0, C0) but the bbox may change shape (height becomes old width, width becomes
old height).

Requirement OO-OO-012: oo_rotate180(+Grid, +V, +Bg, -Out).
Rotate V cells 180 degrees around their bounding box center. Formula: NewR =
R0+(H-1)-r, NewC = C0+(W-1)-c where r=R-R0, c=C-C0 and H=R1-R0+1, W=C1-C0+1.
Bounding box shape is unchanged.

Requirement OO-OO-013: oo_mirror_h(+Grid, +V, +Bg, -Out).
Flip V cells horizontally within their bounding box. Formula: NewR = R (unchanged),
NewC = C0+(W-1)-c where c=C-C0 and W=C1-C0+1.

Requirement OO-OO-014: oo_mirror_v(+Grid, +V, +Bg, -Out).
Flip V cells vertically within their bounding box. Formula: NewR = R0+(H-1)-r
where r=R-R0 and H=R1-R0+1, NewC = C (unchanged).

Private helper oo_set_cells_(Grid, Cells, Val, Out): set all R-C positions in
Cells to Val. Scans the full grid with between/3 and memberchk/2 to identify
which cells to change. O(H*W*|Cells|).

Private helper oo_dims_(Grid, H, W): extracts row count H and column count W.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, memberchk/2, nth0/3, min_list/2,
max_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, length/2, between/3.

END OF PART 159


PART 160 — PAIR PACK REQUIREMENTS (pr_* prefix, Layer 149)

Part 160 specifies the pair pack, which provides 14 predicates for object pairing
and scene correspondence. The pack operates on obj(Color, Cells) terms where Cells
is a sorted list of r(R,C) terms representing the occupied positions of an object.
It supports querying individual objects, grouping collections by attribute, finding
unique objects, and cross-scene matching — the three operations most commonly needed
when an ARC-AGI task requires pairing input objects to output objects.

Prefix: pr_. Module: pair. Layer: 149.

Requirement PR-PR-001: pr_obj_shape(+Obj, -Shape).
Extract the D4-canonical shape of Obj. The shape is the lexicographic minimum of
the 8 D4-symmetry transforms of the normalized cell list. Normalization translates
the cell list so that the minimum row coordinate equals 0 and the minimum column
coordinate equals 0. Each of the 8 D4 transforms (identity, 90 CW, 180, 270 CW,
flip horizontal, flip vertical, flip on main diagonal, flip on anti-diagonal) is
applied, the result is normalized to the origin, sorted, and the lexicographic
minimum is taken as the canonical shape.

Requirement PR-PR-002: pr_obj_color(+Obj, -Color).
Extract the color field from an obj(Color, Cells) term. Color is unified with the
first argument of the obj functor.

Requirement PR-PR-003: pr_obj_size(+Obj, -N).
Count the cells in Obj. N is unified with the length of the Cells list in the
obj(Color, Cells) term.

Requirement PR-PR-004: pr_shape_eq(+Obj1, +Obj2).
Succeed if Obj1 and Obj2 have the same D4-canonical shape. Implemented by calling
pr_obj_shape on each object and unifying the results.

Requirement PR-PR-005: pr_color_eq(+Obj1, +Obj2).
Succeed if Obj1 and Obj2 have the same color. Implemented by calling pr_obj_color
on each object and unifying the results.

Requirement PR-PR-006: pr_size_eq(+Obj1, +Obj2).
Succeed if Obj1 and Obj2 have the same cell count. Implemented by calling
pr_obj_size on each object and unifying the results.

Requirement PR-PR-007: pr_group_color(+Objs, -Groups).
Group a list of obj terms by color. Groups is a sorted list of Color-[Obj,...] pairs,
one pair per distinct color, where the Obj sublist contains all objects of that color
in the order they appear in Objs. The pairs are sorted by Color in standard order.

Requirement PR-PR-008: pr_group_size(+Objs, -Groups).
Group a list of obj terms by size (cell count). Groups is a sorted list of N-[Obj,...]
pairs, one pair per distinct size, where the Obj sublist contains all objects of that
size in the order they appear in Objs. The pairs are sorted by N in standard order.

Requirement PR-PR-009: pr_group_shape(+Objs, -Groups).
Group a list of obj terms by D4-canonical shape. Groups is a list of Shape-[Obj,...]
pairs, one pair per distinct canonical shape, where the Obj sublist contains all
objects with that shape in the order they appear in Objs.

Requirement PR-PR-010: pr_unique_color(+Objs, -Obj).
Find the unique object whose color appears exactly once among all objects in Objs.
Uses pr_group_color to partition by color, then selects the singleton group. Fails
if no color appears exactly once or if more than one color appears exactly once.

Requirement PR-PR-011: pr_unique_size(+Objs, -Obj).
Find the unique object whose size appears exactly once among all objects in Objs.
Uses pr_group_size to partition by size, then selects the singleton group. Fails
if no size appears exactly once or if more than one size appears exactly once.

Requirement PR-PR-012: pr_match_color(+Objs1, +Objs2, -Pairs).
Find all same-color pairings between two object lists. Pairs is a list of
Color-Obj1-Obj2 triples where Obj1 is from Objs1, Obj2 is from Objs2, and both
share Color. Generated by findall over the cross-product of Objs1 and Objs2 with
the constraint that both objects have the same color.

Requirement PR-PR-013: pr_match_size(+Objs1, +Objs2, -Pairs).
Find all same-size pairings between two object lists. Pairs is a list of
N-Obj1-Obj2 triples where Obj1 is from Objs1, Obj2 is from Objs2, and both have
the same cell count N. Generated by findall over the cross-product.

Requirement PR-PR-014: pr_match_shape(+Objs1, +Objs2, -Pairs).
Find all D4-equivalent shape pairings between two object lists. Pairs is a list of
Shape-Obj1-Obj2 triples where Obj1 is from Objs1, Obj2 is from Objs2, and both
have the same D4-canonical shape. Generated by findall over the cross-product.

Private helper pr_normalize_(Cells, Norm): translate a sorted r(R,C) cell list so
that min row = 0 and min col = 0. Extracts all R values with findall, finds
min_list, extracts all C values, finds min_list, then maps (R-MinR, C-MinC) over
each cell and sorts the result.

Private helper pr_cell_d4_(Op, H1, W1, r(R,C), r(NR,NC)): apply one of the 8 D4
symmetry operations to a single cell. H1 is the normalized height minus 1 (max row
index after normalization); W1 is the normalized width minus 1 (max col index). The
8 ops are: id (NR=R, NC=C), r90 (NR=C, NC=H1-R), r180 (NR=H1-R, NC=W1-C),
r270 (NR=W1-C, NC=R), fh (NR=R, NC=W1-C), fv (NR=H1-R, NC=C),
fd1 (NR=C, NC=R), fd2 (NR=W1-C, NC=H1-R).

Private helper pr_min_term_(A, B, Min): unify Min with the lexicographically smaller
of A and B using standard order comparison (@<).

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, length/2.

END OF PART 160


PART 161 - WORK PACKAGE 171: ARRANGE PACK (ag_* PREFIX, LAYER 150)

Work Package Number: WP 171
Pack Name: arrange
Module Name: arrange
Prefix: ag_
Layer: 150
PR: 256

Summary: The arrange pack provides 14 predicates for computing centroids of
obj(Color, Cells) terms, comparing and sorting objects by centroid position, detecting
equal spacing between objects, computing group bounding boxes, and finding the nearest
object to a reference. It builds on the pair pack (Layer 149) and the scene pack
(Layer 37) by adding arrangement-level reasoning: not just what an object is, but
where it sits relative to others in a scene.

AG-AG-001: ag_centroid(+Obj, -r(CR,CC))
  Compute the integer (floor-average) centroid of an obj(Color, Cells) term.
  Extract all R values from the cell list with findall, extract all C values,
  divide each sum by the cell count using integer division (//). Fails if Cells is empty.

AG-AG-002: ag_offset(+Obj1, +Obj2, -r(DR,DC))
  Compute the row-column displacement vector from the centroid of Obj1 to the centroid
  of Obj2. DR = CR2 - CR1, DC = CC2 - CC1. Positive DR means Obj2 is below Obj1.

AG-AG-003: ag_row_order(+Obj1, +Obj2)
  Succeed when the centroid row of Obj1 is at most the centroid row of Obj2.
  Obj1 is above or at the same row as Obj2. Equivalent to CR1 =< CR2.

AG-AG-004: ag_col_order(+Obj1, +Obj2)
  Succeed when the centroid column of Obj1 is at most the centroid column of Obj2.
  Obj1 is to the left of or at the same column as Obj2. Equivalent to CC1 =< CC2.

AG-AG-005: ag_row_aligned(+Obj1, +Obj2)
  Succeed when Obj1 and Obj2 have the same centroid row. Uses variable unification on
  the centroid row term to require equality.

AG-AG-006: ag_col_aligned(+Obj1, +Obj2)
  Succeed when Obj1 and Obj2 have the same centroid column. Uses variable unification
  on the centroid column term to require equality.

AG-AG-007: ag_sort_by_row(+Objs, -Sorted)
  Produce a stable sort of an obj list by centroid row, top to bottom. Build R-Obj
  pairs with findall, sort with keysort/2 (stable), then extract the objects. Equal-row
  objects preserve their original relative order.

AG-AG-008: ag_sort_by_col(+Objs, -Sorted)
  Produce a stable sort of an obj list by centroid column, left to right. Build C-Obj
  pairs with findall, sort with keysort/2 (stable), then extract the objects. Equal-column
  objects preserve their original relative order.

AG-AG-009: ag_row_gaps(+Objs, -Gaps)
  Compute the list of consecutive gaps between the sorted distinct centroid rows of all
  objects in Objs. Uses sort/2 to deduplicate and sort, then ag_consec_gaps_ to compute
  differences. An empty list means all objects share the same centroid row.

AG-AG-010: ag_col_gaps(+Objs, -Gaps)
  Compute the list of consecutive gaps between the sorted distinct centroid columns of all
  objects in Objs. Uses sort/2 to deduplicate and sort, then ag_consec_gaps_ to compute
  differences. An empty list means all objects share the same centroid column.

AG-AG-011: ag_equal_row_gaps(+Objs)
  Succeed when all consecutive centroid row gaps are equal. Calls ag_row_gaps to get the
  gap list, requires at least one gap (two or more distinct centroid rows), then calls
  ag_all_equal_ to verify uniformity.

AG-AG-012: ag_equal_col_gaps(+Objs)
  Succeed when all consecutive centroid column gaps are equal. Calls ag_col_gaps to get
  the gap list, requires at least one gap (two or more distinct centroid columns), then
  calls ag_all_equal_ to verify uniformity.

AG-AG-013: ag_group_bbox(+Objs, -R0, -C0, -R1, -C1)
  Compute the bounding box enclosing all cells of all obj terms in the list. Collect
  every row index from every cell of every obj with findall, collect every column index,
  then apply min_list and max_list to find the four bounding box coordinates. Fails if
  Objs is empty or any obj has an empty cell list.

AG-AG-014: ag_nearest(+RefObj, +Objs, -Nearest)
  Find the obj in Objs whose centroid is closest to RefObj's centroid under Manhattan
  distance. Build D-Obj pairs with findall (D = abs(OR-RR) + abs(OC-RC)), sort with
  keysort, and take the first element. Ties broken by the natural key order yield a
  deterministic result.

Private helper ag_consec_gaps_(+SortedList, -Gaps): compute consecutive differences of
a sorted integer list. Base cases: [] -> []; [_] -> [] (with cut to prevent choicepoint).
Recursive case: [A,B|T] -> [B-A | consec_gaps([B|T])].

Private helper ag_all_equal_(+List): all elements of a non-empty list are equal.
Singleton clause has a cut. Recursive clause requires the first two elements to unify.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2, sum_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, keysort/2, length/2.

END OF PART 161


PART 162 - WORK PACKAGE 172: XFORM PACK (xf_* PREFIX, LAYER 151)

Work Package Number: WP 172
Pack Name: xform
Module Name: xform
Prefix: xf_
Layer: 151
PR: 257

Summary: The xform pack provides 14 predicates for applying transformations to
individual obj(Color, Cells) terms and for inferring what transformation connects two
obj terms. Applied transformations include recoloring, translating, normalizing to
origin, and applying named D4 symmetry operations. Inference predicates include cell
offset detection, recolor detection, cell-set arithmetic (added, removed, kept), overlap
counting, D4 operation discovery, scale factor computation, and cell-set merge.

XF-XF-001: xf_recolor(+Obj, +Color, -Out)
  Replace the color of an obj term while keeping the cell list unchanged.
  Implemented as a single head-unification clause: xf_recolor(obj(_, Cells), Color, obj(Color, Cells)).

XF-XF-002: xf_translate(+Obj, +r(DR,DC), -Out)
  Shift every cell of an obj by (DR,DC). Uses findall to build the shifted list and
  sort/2 to maintain canonical order.

XF-XF-003: xf_normalize(+Obj, -Out)
  Translate an obj to the origin. Extract min row and min col via min_list, then
  subtract them from every cell coordinate. Sort the result.

XF-XF-004: xf_d4(+Obj, +Op, -Out)
  Apply a named D4 symmetry operation to the cells of an obj, keeping the result at
  the same top-left corner as the input. Steps: find bbox top-left (MinR,MinC);
  translate to origin; compute H1=max row, W1=max col of normalized cells; apply Op
  using xf_cell_d4_; sort the result; translate back by adding (MinR,MinC).

XF-XF-005: xf_same_cells(+Obj1, +Obj2)
  Succeed if both obj terms have the same sorted cell set. Implemented as
  xf_same_cells(obj(_,Cells), obj(_,Cells)) by unification of the Cells argument.

XF-XF-006: xf_cell_offset(+Obj1, +Obj2, -r(DR,DC))
  Find the translation vector from Obj1 to Obj2. Normalize both to origin; require
  the normalized cell sets to unify (same shape); return DR = min_row(Obj2)-min_row(Obj1),
  DC = min_col(Obj2)-min_col(Obj1). Fails if shapes differ.

XF-XF-007: xf_is_recolor(+Obj1, +Obj2)
  Succeed when Obj1 and Obj2 have identical cells but different colors.
  Implemented as xf_is_recolor(obj(C1,Cells), obj(C2,Cells)) :- C1 \= C2.
  Cell-list unification enforces exact cell identity; \=/2 enforces color difference.

XF-XF-008: xf_cells_added(+Obj1, +Obj2, -Added)
  Cells in Obj2's cell list that are absent from Obj1's cell list (sorted set difference).
  Uses subtract(C2, C1, Added) from library(lists).

XF-XF-009: xf_cells_removed(+Obj1, +Obj2, -Removed)
  Cells in Obj1's cell list that are absent from Obj2's cell list.
  Uses subtract(C1, C2, Removed).

XF-XF-010: xf_cells_kept(+Obj1, +Obj2, -Kept)
  Cells present in both Obj1 and Obj2 (sorted intersection). Uses findall with
  member and memberchk to collect the intersection, then sort.

XF-XF-011: xf_overlap_count(+Obj1, +Obj2, -N)
  Count the cells shared by both obj terms. Calls xf_cells_kept and takes the length.

XF-XF-012: xf_any_d4(+Obj1, +Obj2, -Op)
  Find the first D4 Op in [id, r90, r180, r270, fh, fv, fd1, fd2] such that applying
  Op to Obj1's normalized cell set gives Obj2's normalized cell set. Normalizes both
  objects, computes H1/W1 of Obj1's normalized cells, tries ops via member, applies
  xf_cell_d4_, sorts, and unifies with Obj2's normalized cells. Cuts after first match
  to prevent choicepoints.

XF-XF-013: xf_scale_factor(+Obj1, +Obj2, -N)
  Find integer N >= 1 such that |Obj2.cells| = N * |Obj1.cells|. Requires Obj1 non-empty,
  exact divisibility (0 =:= Len2 mod Len1), and N >= 1.

XF-XF-014: xf_merge(+Obj1, +Obj2, -Out)
  Merge two same-color obj terms by taking the union of their cell lists. Colors must
  unify. Uses append then sort/2 (which removes duplicates) to produce the result.

Private helper xf_cell_d4_(+Op, +R, +C, +H1, +W1, -NR, -NC): same 8-case D4 cell
transform as in the pair pack (pr_cell_d4_), defined locally in xform.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2, subtract/3, memberchk/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, length/2, append/3.

END OF PART 162


PART 163: QUERY PACK (qu_* prefix, Layer 152)

Purpose: Aggregate Queries over Object Lists.
File: packs/query/prolog/query.pl
Module: query
Layer: 152
Prefix: qu_

The query pack provides aggregate statistics and queries over lists of obj(Color, Cells)
terms produced by the scene pack. It covers counting by color/size/exact form, finding
extremes (most/least frequent color, largest/smallest object), computing totals and
averages, testing for uniformity across an object list, and enumerating distinct
attribute values.

"Form" in this pack means the origin-normalized cell list (min row=0, min col=0), which
is an exact structural match. This is deliberately not D4-invariant: two objects with
the same D4 shape but different orientations have different forms. This keeps the query
pack self-contained and avoids importing D4 machinery from the pair pack.

Private helper qu_norm_(+Cells, -Norm): translates the cell list to origin (min row=0,
min col=0) and returns it sorted. Shared by qu_form_, qu_count_by_form, and
qu_all_same_form.

QU-QU-001: qu_count_by_color(+Objs, -Counts)
  Return a sorted list of Color-N pairs where N is the number of obj terms in Objs
  with that Color. Sorted by Color (ascending term order). Uses two-phase
  findall+sort pattern: collect all colors, sort for distinct keys, then findall a
  count per key.

QU-QU-002: qu_count_by_size(+Objs, -Counts)
  Return a sorted list of Size-N pairs where Size is a cell count (integer) and N is
  the number of obj terms with that many cells. Sorted by Size ascending.

QU-QU-003: qu_count_by_form(+Objs, -Counts)
  Return a sorted list of Form-N pairs where Form is the origin-normalized cell list
  and N is the number of obj terms with that exact form. Sorted by Form in standard
  term order. Two objects at different positions but with the same shape contribute
  to the same Form key.

QU-QU-004: qu_most_frequent_color(+Objs, -Color)
  Return the Color that appears in the most obj terms. On ties (multiple colors with
  the same maximum count), return the smallest color value (the one that appears first
  in the sorted Color-N list produced by qu_count_by_color). Deterministic: cuts after
  the first matching color.

QU-QU-005: qu_least_frequent_color(+Objs, -Color)
  Return the Color that appears in the fewest obj terms. On ties, return the smallest
  color value. Deterministic: cuts after the first matching color.

QU-QU-006: qu_largest_obj(+Objs, -Obj)
  Return the obj term with the most cells. On ties (multiple objs with the same maximum
  cell count), return the one that appears first in Objs (input order). Builds a list
  of N-O pairs via findall (preserving input order), finds max, then member+cut to
  return the first occurrence.

QU-QU-007: qu_smallest_obj(+Objs, -Obj)
  Return the obj term with the fewest cells. On ties, return the first in input order.
  Same approach as qu_largest_obj but using min_list.

QU-QU-008: qu_total_cells(+Objs, -N)
  Return the total number of cells across all obj terms in Objs. Collects the length
  of each obj's cell list via findall, then sums with sum_list/2.

QU-QU-009: qu_avg_size(+Objs, -N)
  Return the floor-average cell count per obj in Objs. Computes qu_total_cells and
  divides by length(Objs) using integer division (//). Requires Objs non-empty.

QU-QU-010: qu_all_same_color(+Objs)
  Succeed if every obj term in Objs has the same color. Collects all colors via
  findall, applies sort/2 (deduplication), and requires the result to be a singleton
  list [_].

QU-QU-011: qu_all_same_size(+Objs)
  Succeed if every obj term in Objs has the same cell count. Collects all cell counts
  via findall, applies sort/2, and requires a singleton [_].

QU-QU-012: qu_all_same_form(+Objs)
  Succeed if every obj term in Objs has the same origin-normalized cell list. Collects
  all normalized forms via findall+qu_form_, applies sort/2, and requires a singleton [_].

QU-QU-013: qu_colors(+Objs, -Colors)
  Return a sorted list of distinct color values appearing in Objs. Collects all colors
  with findall, then deduplicates and sorts with sort/2.

QU-QU-014: qu_sizes(+Objs, -Sizes)
  Return a sorted list of distinct cell counts appearing in Objs. Collects all sizes
  with findall, then deduplicates and sorts with sort/2.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2, sum_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, length/2.

END OF PART 163


PART 164: SIFT PACK (si_* prefix, Layer 153)

Purpose: Object List Filtering by Attribute Predicates.
File: packs/sift/prolog/sift.pl
Module: sift
Layer: 153
Prefix: si_

The sift pack filters lists of obj(Color, Cells) terms by various predicates.
All 14 public predicates accept an input Objs list and return Out, the subset of
objects that satisfy the given condition. An empty result list [] is a valid output;
no predicate fails due to an empty result.

Private helper si_norm_(+Cells, -Norm): origin-normalizes the cell list (min row=0,
min col=0, sorted). Used by si_by_form; defined locally to keep the pack self-contained.

Private helper si_on_border_(+R, +C, +H, +W): succeeds if r(R,C) is on the border
of an H-by-W grid. Border means row=0, row=H-1, col=0, or col=W-1. Implemented with
four clauses and cuts for determinism.

SI-SI-001: si_by_color(+Objs, +Color, -Out)
  Keep only obj terms whose Color argument equals Color. Uses findall with O = obj(Color, _)
  pattern unification; no explicit test needed.

SI-SI-002: si_not_color(+Objs, +Color, -Out)
  Keep only obj terms whose Color argument differs from Color. Uses findall with
  C \= Color.

SI-SI-003: si_by_size(+Objs, +N, -Out)
  Keep only obj terms with exactly N cells. Uses findall with length(Cells, N).

SI-SI-004: si_by_form(+Objs, +Form, -Out)
  Keep only obj terms whose origin-normalized cell list (via si_norm_) unifies with
  Form. Form is an exact structural match of the sorted translated cell list.
  Not D4-invariant.

SI-SI-005: si_larger_than(+Objs, +N, -Out)
  Keep only obj terms with strictly more than N cells. Uses findall with S > N.

SI-SI-006: si_smaller_than(+Objs, +N, -Out)
  Keep only obj terms with strictly fewer than N cells. Uses findall with S < N.

SI-SI-007: si_color_in(+Objs, +Colors, -Out)
  Keep only obj terms whose color is a member of the Colors list. Uses memberchk/2
  for efficient non-backtracking membership test.

SI-SI-008: si_color_not_in(+Objs, +Colors, -Out)
  Keep only obj terms whose color is not a member of Colors. Uses \+ memberchk/2.

SI-SI-009: si_max_size(+Objs, -Out)
  Keep all obj terms tied for the maximum cell count. Collects all cell counts with
  findall, finds the maximum with max_list, then selects all objects at that count.
  Unlike qu_largest_obj which returns only the first, si_max_size returns ALL maximal
  objects.

SI-SI-010: si_min_size(+Objs, -Out)
  Keep all obj terms tied for the minimum cell count. Analogous to si_max_size using
  min_list.

SI-SI-011: si_unique_color(+Objs, -Out)
  Keep obj terms whose color appears exactly once in Objs. Computes per-color counts
  using two-phase findall+sort pattern, collects colors with count=1, then filters
  with memberchk.

SI-SI-012: si_shared_color(+Objs, -Out)
  Keep obj terms whose color appears more than once in Objs. Same two-phase count
  approach; collects colors with count > 1.

SI-SI-013: si_on_border(+Objs, +H, +W, -Out)
  Keep obj terms that have at least one cell on the border of an H-by-W grid.
  H = grid height (valid rows 0..H-1), W = grid width (valid cols 0..W-1).
  Border cells: row=0, row=H-1, col=0, or col=W-1. Uses findall with member(r(R,C))
  and si_on_border_(R, C, H, W).

SI-SI-014: si_off_border(+Objs, +H, +W, -Out)
  Keep obj terms with no cell on the grid border. Uses \+ (...member... si_on_border_)
  to negate the border condition.

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, memberchk/2, min_list/2, max_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, length/2.

END OF PART 164


PART 165: PIGMENT PACK (pg_* prefix, Layer 154)

Purpose: Bulk Color Operations on Object Scenes.
File: packs/pigment/prolog/pigment.pl
Module: pigment
Layer: 154
Prefix: pg_

The pigment pack provides scene-level color manipulation over lists of obj(Color, Cells)
terms. It covers uniform recoloring, targeted single-color replacement, color swapping,
color table application (lenient and strict), color table inference from example pairs,
zip-based recoloring, frequency-targeted recoloring (majority/minority/unique/shared),
table inversion, and table validation.

Private helper pg_count_by_color_(+Objs, -Counts): computes sorted Color-N pairs
using the two-phase findall+sort pattern. Used by pg_majority_to, pg_minority_to,
pg_unique_to, and pg_shared_to. Defined locally to keep the pack self-contained.

PG-PG-001: pg_recolor_all(+Objs, +Color, -Out)
  Set every obj's color to Color. All cell lists are preserved unchanged.
  Implemented as findall(obj(Color, Cells), member(obj(_, Cells), Objs), Out).

PG-PG-002: pg_recolor_one(+Objs, +From, +To, -Out)
  Change all objs with color From to To; leave all other objs unchanged.
  Uses if-then-else (C =:= From -> obj(To, Cells) ; obj(C, Cells)) inside findall.

PG-PG-003: pg_swap(+Objs, +C1, +C2, -Out)
  Exchange colors C1 and C2 throughout the scene. Objs with other colors are kept
  unchanged. Uses nested if-then-else inside findall.

PG-PG-004: pg_apply_table(+Objs, +Table, -Out)
  Apply a From-To color table to the scene. Table is a list of From-To pairs (using
  the -/2 functor, e.g. [1-5, 2-6]). Objs whose color has no table entry keep their
  original color. Uses memberchk(C-New, Table) with if-then-else inside findall.

PG-PG-005: pg_apply_table_strict(+Objs, +Table, -Out)
  Apply a color table but exclude objs whose color has no table entry. Only obj terms
  with a matching From-To pair in Table appear in Out. Uses findall with memberchk
  to find both the match condition and the new color in one step.

PG-PG-006: pg_infer_table(+Objs1, +Objs2, -Table)
  Infer a color mapping from two scenes that have the same cell structure. For each
  pair of obj terms (one from Objs1, one from Objs2) with identical cell sets (same
  position in the grid), records the Old-New color pair. sort/2 deduplicates pairs
  that appear multiple times (e.g. when multiple objs share a color mapping). Fails
  if no matching pairs exist.

PG-PG-007: pg_zip_recolor(+Objs, +Colors, -Out)
  Recolor each obj with the corresponding entry in Colors. Stops when either list
  ends (truncation semantics). Implemented with a three-clause recursive predicate
  with cuts on the two base cases.

PG-PG-008: pg_majority_to(+Objs, +Color, -Out)
  Recolor all objs whose color is the most frequent in Objs to Color. Ties broken
  by smallest color value (first in the sorted Color-N list). Non-majority objs
  are kept unchanged. Uses pg_count_by_color_, max_list, and member+cut to identify
  the majority color, then if-then-else findall for the recoloring.

PG-PG-009: pg_minority_to(+Objs, +Color, -Out)
  Recolor all objs whose color is the least frequent in Objs to Color. Ties broken
  by smallest color value. Uses pg_count_by_color_, min_list, and member+cut.

PG-PG-010: pg_unique_to(+Objs, +Color, -Out)
  Recolor objs whose color appears exactly once in Objs to Color. Objs with shared
  colors are kept unchanged. Uses pg_count_by_color_ to find colors with count=1,
  then memberchk with if-then-else inside findall.

PG-PG-011: pg_shared_to(+Objs, +Color, -Out)
  Recolor objs whose color appears more than once in Objs to Color. Objs with unique
  colors are kept unchanged.

PG-PG-012: pg_invert_table(+Table, -Inv)
  Produce the inverse color table by swapping each From-To pair to To-From.
  Uses findall(To-From, member(From-To, Table), Inv).

PG-PG-013: pg_table_from(+Table, -Froms)
  Return the sorted list of From colors appearing in the Table. Collects all From
  values with findall, then sort/2 deduplicates and sorts.

PG-PG-014: pg_consistent(+Table)
  Succeed if the Table is consistent: no From color maps to two different To colors.
  Uses \+ (member(F-T1, Table), member(F-T2, Table), T1 \= T2).

Library imports: library(lists): member/2, memberchk/2, min_list/2, max_list/2.
Built-ins: findall/3, sort/2, length/2.

END OF PART 165


Part 166: Work Package 176 - Delta Pack (dl_* Prefix, Layer 155)

Section 166.1: Purpose

The delta pack provides scene-level delta analysis between two object scenes (lists of obj(Color, Cells) terms). It answers the question "what changed?" when comparing a before-scene to an after-scene. This is a foundational capability for multi-step ARC-AGI-2 reasoning, where understanding what transformation was applied to a scene is the first step toward inducing the general rule.

Section 166.2: Predicate Specification

dl_added(+S1, +S2, -Added): Added is the list of objects in S2 whose exact cell set does not appear in S1. An object is considered added if no object in S1 occupies the same set of grid cells (regardless of color). Empty result ([]) is valid when all S2 cell sets appear in S1.

dl_removed(+S1, +S2, -Removed): Removed is the list of objects in S1 whose exact cell set does not appear in S2. Symmetrical to dl_added with scene arguments swapped.

dl_matched(+S1, +S2, -Pairs): Pairs is a sorted list of O1-O2 terms, one for each pair of objects sharing identical cell sets across scenes. Uses the -/2 functor (same as color table pairs). Deduplicates with sort/2.

dl_recolored(+S1, +S2, -Changes): Changes is a sorted list of C1-C2 pairs recording the From and To colors for every object pair that shares cell sets but has different colors. C1 is the color in S1; C2 is the color in S2. Deduplicates with sort/2.

dl_unchanged(+S1, +S2, -Objs): Objs is the sorted list of objects that appear verbatim (same color and same cell set) in both S1 and S2. Uses term equality via member/2 unification.

dl_color_gain(+S1, +S2, -Colors): Colors lists colors that appear in S2 but not in S1. Computed by set difference on sorted color palettes.

dl_color_loss(+S1, +S2, -Colors): Colors lists colors that appear in S1 but not in S2. Symmetrical to dl_color_gain.

dl_count_diff(+S1, +S2, -N): N is length(S2) - length(S1). Positive when S2 has more objects; negative when fewer; zero when equal.

dl_size_diff(+S1, +S2, -N): N is the total cell count of S2 minus the total cell count of S1. Positive when S2 occupies more cells overall; negative when fewer.

dl_is_added_only(+S1, +S2): Succeeds iff dl_removed gives [] and dl_recolored gives []. The only change is that new objects appeared in S2.

dl_is_removed_only(+S1, +S2): Succeeds iff dl_added gives [] and dl_recolored gives []. The only change is that objects disappeared from S1 to S2.

dl_is_recolor_only(+S1, +S2): Succeeds iff dl_added gives [] and dl_removed gives []. Every cell position in S1 is still present in S2; only colors may have changed.

dl_is_stable(+S1, +S2): Succeeds iff dl_added, dl_removed, and dl_recolored all give []. The two scenes are identical.

dl_scene_diff(+S1, +S2, -Delta): Delta is the compound term delta(Added, Removed, Recolored, Unchanged), aggregating all four components in one call. The four components use the same definitions as dl_added, dl_removed, dl_recolored, and dl_unchanged respectively.

Section 166.3: Matching Semantics

Object matching uses exact cell-set equality: two objects match iff they have the same Cells list under term unification. This definition is consistent with pg_infer_table (pigment pack) and is self-contained: no D4 normalization, no origin normalization, and no approximate matching. The cell-set equality test is implemented via Prolog unification in member/2, which requires both the structure and contents of the r(R,C) terms to match exactly.

Section 166.4: Layer Assignment

Layer 155. Depends on no other packs. Self-contained: uses only member/2 and sum_list/2 from library(lists), plus built-in predicates findall/3, sort/2, length/2, and the negation-as-failure operator \+.


Part 167: Work Package 177 - Group Pack (gp_* Prefix, Layer 156)

Section 167.1: Purpose

The group pack partitions a list of obj(Color, Cells) terms into named groups that share a common property. Groups are represented as sorted Key-[Objs] pairs using the -/2 functor, where Key is the shared property value (color, cell count, row, column, or normalized form). The group pack enables the ARC-AGI-2 reasoning pattern: "divide the scene into subsets sharing a property, then apply different operations to each subset."

Section 167.2: Predicate Specification

gp_by_color(+Objs, -Groups): partition by color. Groups is a sorted list of Color-[ObjsOfColor] pairs covering every distinct color in Objs. Objects within each group preserve original input order.

gp_by_size(+Objs, -Groups): partition by cell count. Groups is a sorted list of N-[ObjsOfSizeN] pairs. Objects with the same number of cells share a group.

gp_by_row(+Objs, -Groups): partition by minimum row of cells. Groups is a sorted list of R-[ObjsWithTopRow R] pairs. The key is the smallest row index among an object's cells.

gp_by_col(+Objs, -Groups): partition by minimum column of cells. Groups is a sorted list of C-[ObjsWithLeftCol C] pairs.

gp_by_form(+Objs, -Groups): partition by origin-normalized cell list (form). Two objects share a form iff their cells, after translation to origin (min row=0, min col=0) and sorting, are identical. Private helper gp_norm_/2 computes the form. Groups is a sorted list of Form-[ObjsOfForm] pairs; Form is itself a sorted list of r(R,C) terms.

gp_size_of(+Groups, -N): N is the number of distinct groups (the length of the Groups list).

gp_flatten(+Groups, -Objs): concatenate all group member lists in key order. Produces a flat list of all objects in the order they appear in Groups.
