gp_largest_group(+Groups, -Largest): Largest is the Key-[Objs] pair whose Objs list is longest. On ties, the group with the smallest Key (earliest in the sorted Groups list) is returned. Uses cut after finding MaxN to ensure determinism. Uses memberchk/2 for the final Key-Grp retrieval to avoid choicepoints.

gp_smallest_group(+Groups, -Smallest): Smallest is the Key-[Objs] pair whose Objs list is shortest. Same tie-breaking and determinism rules as gp_largest_group.

gp_singleton_groups(+Groups, -Singles): Singles is the sub-list of groups containing exactly one object (length = 1). Preserves key order.

gp_shared_groups(+Groups, -Shared): Shared is the sub-list of groups containing more than one object (length > 1). Preserves key order.

gp_group_sizes(+Groups, -Sizes): Sizes is the sorted list of distinct group cardinalities. Deduplicates: if multiple groups have the same number of members, that number appears once.

gp_all_same_size(+Groups): Succeeds iff every group in Groups has the same cardinality. An empty Groups list succeeds vacuously (no counterexample). Implemented by collecting all cardinalities then requiring sort/2 to produce a singleton list.

gp_keys(+Groups, -Keys): Keys is the sorted list of group keys extracted from the Key-[Objs] pairs. Deduplicates with sort/2.

Section 167.3: Group Representation

A group is a Key-[Objs] pair. Key is the shared property value: an integer for color, size, row, or column; or a sorted list of r(R,C) terms for form. The groups list is sorted by key using sort/2 on the first element of each pair.

Section 167.4: Layer Assignment

Layer 156. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, memberchk/2, min_list/2, max_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins findall/3, sort/2, length/2.

Part 168: Proximity Pack Specification (WP 178, Layer 157)

Section 168.1: Purpose

The proximity pack (module proximity, px_* prefix, Layer 157) computes distances and spatial relationships between obj(Color, Cells) terms. It provides object-level distance measures, proximity-based filtering, sorting by distance, and pair-finding predicates. All predicates work directly on obj terms; no grid argument is required.

Section 168.2: Predicate Specifications

px_centroid(+Obj, -R, -C): R and C are the integer-truncated centroid of Obj's cells. Centroid is the sum of all row values divided by the cell count, and the sum of all column values divided by the cell count, both using integer truncation (// operator).

px_centroid_dist(+O1, +O2, -D): D is the Manhattan distance between the centroids of O1 and O2. Manhattan distance = |R1 - R2| + |C1 - C2| where (R1,C1) and (R2,C2) are centroids.

px_min_cell_dist(+O1, +O2, -D): D is the minimum Manhattan distance across all cell pairs, one from O1 and one from O2. Considers the Cartesian product of the two cell lists.

px_touching(+O1, +O2): Succeeds if any cell of O1 is 4-adjacent to any cell of O2. 4-adjacent means Manhattan distance between the two cells equals 1 (cells share an edge, not a corner).

px_nearest(+Objs, +Ref, -Nearest): Nearest is the object in Objs with the minimum centroid distance to Ref. Ties broken by the object appearing earliest in Objs.

px_farthest(+Objs, +Ref, -Farthest): Farthest is the object in Objs with the maximum centroid distance to Ref. Ties broken by earliest in Objs.

px_sort_by_dist(+Objs, +Ref, -Sorted): Sorted is Objs re-ordered ascending by centroid distance from Ref. Equal-distance objects retain their relative order from Objs (stable sort via msort/2).

px_within_dist(+Objs, +Ref, +D, -Near): Near is the sub-list of Objs whose centroid distance from Ref is at most D (inclusive of D).

px_beyond_dist(+Objs, +Ref, +D, -Far): Far is the sub-list of Objs whose centroid distance from Ref is strictly greater than D.

px_closest_pair(+Objs, -O1-O2): O1-O2 is the unordered pair of distinct objects from Objs with the minimum centroid distance. Only index-ordered pairs (I < J) are considered, so each unordered pair is checked once. Ties broken by earliest index pair. Fails if Objs has fewer than two elements.

px_farthest_pair(+Objs, -O1-O2): O1-O2 is the unordered pair with the maximum centroid distance. Same tie-breaking and failure rules as px_closest_pair.

px_touching_objs(+Objs, +Ref, -Touching): Touching is the sub-list of Objs that 4-touch Ref.

px_non_touching_objs(+Objs, +Ref, -NonTouching): NonTouching is the sub-list of Objs that do not 4-touch Ref.

px_dist_rank(+Objs, +Ref, -Ranked): Ranked is a list of D-Obj pairs sorted ascending by centroid distance D. The first element is the nearest object; the last is the farthest. Equal distances retain Objs order (msort stability).

Section 168.3: Distance Convention

All distance measures use Manhattan distance. Centroid distance is used for most predicates (px_centroid_dist, px_nearest, px_farthest, px_sort_by_dist, px_within_dist, px_beyond_dist, px_closest_pair, px_farthest_pair, px_dist_rank). Cell-level minimum distance is provided separately as px_min_cell_dist.

Section 168.4: Layer Assignment

Layer 157. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2, sum_list/2, nth1/3 from library(lists); built-ins msort/2, between/3, findall/3, length/2, abs/1.

Part 169: Link Pack Specification (WP 179, Layer 158)

Section 169.1: Purpose

The link pack (module link, lk_* prefix, Layer 158) builds and manipulates correspondence links between pairs of obj(Color, Cells) terms. A link is an O1-O2 pair where O1 comes from one list and O2 from another. The pack provides predicates for building links by position, proximity, color, size, and form; for extracting and transforming link sets; and for applying correspondence (transferring color or cells from one side to the other).

Section 169.2: Predicate Specifications

lk_by_position(+Objs1, +Objs2, -Links): Links is the element-wise zip of Objs1 and Objs2. The Nth link is Objs1[N]-Objs2[N]. Stops at the shorter list (truncates).

lk_by_nearest(+Objs1, +Objs2, -Links): Each obj in Objs1 is linked to its nearest obj in Objs2 by Manhattan centroid distance. Produces one link per object in Objs1. Ties broken by first appearance in Objs2. Empty Links if Objs2 is empty.

lk_by_color(+Objs1, +Objs2, -Links): All O1-O2 pairs where O1 and O2 share the same color atom. Deduplicates with sort/2.

lk_by_size(+Objs1, +Objs2, -Links): All O1-O2 pairs where O1 and O2 have the same cell count. Deduplicates with sort/2.

lk_by_form(+Objs1, +Objs2, -Links): All O1-O2 pairs where O1 and O2 have the same origin-normalized form (same cell list after translating to origin and sorting). Private helper lk_norm_/2 computes the form. Deduplicates with sort/2.

lk_source(+Links, -Sources): Sources is the list of O1 objects from each O1-O2 link, in link order.

lk_target(+Links, -Targets): Targets is the list of O2 objects from each O1-O2 link, in link order.

lk_invert(+Links, -Inverted): Inverted is the list with O1 and O2 swapped in every link.

lk_count(+Links, -N): N is the number of links (length of the list).

lk_apply_color(+Links, -Result): Result is a list of obj(O2Color, O1Cells) terms — each O1 is recolored with its linked O2's color while keeping its own cells.

lk_apply_cells(+Links, -Result): Result is a list of obj(O1Color, O2Cells) terms — each O1 keeps its own color but gets its linked O2's cells.

lk_filter_same_color(+Links, -Same): Same is the sub-list of links where O1 and O2 have identical color atoms.

lk_filter_diff_color(+Links, -Diff): Diff is the sub-list of links where O1 and O2 have different color atoms.

lk_unlinked(+Objs, +Links, -Unlinked): Unlinked is the sub-list of Objs that do not appear as O1 in any link (by exact term matching).

Section 169.3: Link Representation

A link is an O1-O2 pair using the infix -/2 functor. A links list is a list of such pairs.

Section 169.4: Layer Assignment

Layer 158. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, min_list/2, sum_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins findall/3, sort/2, length/2, abs/1.

Part 170: Layout Pack Specification (WP 180, Layer 159)

Section 170.1: Purpose

The layout pack (module layout, lt_* prefix, Layer 159) analyzes the collective spatial arrangement of a list of obj(Color, Cells) terms. It provides global bounding box, centroid aggregation, row/column range and count, line and diagonal arrangement detection, grid arrangement detection, and uniform spacing checks.

Section 170.2: Predicate Specifications

lt_global_bbox(+Objs, -R1, -C1, -R2, -C2): R1,C1 is the top-left corner and R2,C2 is the bottom-right corner of the bounding box over ALL cells of all objects combined.

lt_bbox_area(+Objs, -Area): Area is (R2-R1+1)*(C2-C1+1) for the global bounding box.

lt_row_range(+Objs, -MinTopR, -MaxTopR): MinTopR and MaxTopR are the minimum and maximum topmost-row values (minimum row of cells) across all objects.

lt_col_range(+Objs, -MinLeftC, -MaxLeftC): MinLeftC and MaxLeftC are the minimum and maximum leftmost-column values across all objects.

lt_all_same_row(+Objs): Succeeds iff all objects share the same topmost row. Vacuously true for empty list.

lt_all_same_col(+Objs): Succeeds iff all objects share the same leftmost column. Vacuously true for empty list.

lt_centroid_of_all(+Objs, -R, -C): R and C are the integer-truncated centroid of all individual object centroids (average of averages, using integer truncation at each step).

lt_row_count(+Objs, -N): N is the number of distinct topmost rows across all objects.

lt_col_count(+Objs, -N): N is the number of distinct leftmost columns.

lt_is_grid(+Objs, -Rows, -Cols): Succeeds iff the objects' centroids form a Rows x Cols grid: Rows distinct centroid row values, Cols distinct centroid col values, every (row, col) combination occupied, and |Objs| = Rows * Cols (no duplicate centroids).

lt_is_diagonal_dr(+Objs): Succeeds iff all object centroids lie on the same downward-right diagonal (R - C is constant). Vacuously true for empty list.

lt_is_diagonal_dl(+Objs): Succeeds iff all centroids lie on the same downward-left diagonal (R + C is constant). Vacuously true for empty list.

lt_gap_h(+Objs, -Gap): Gap is the uniform column gap between consecutive objects sorted by centroid column. Fails if gaps are non-uniform, if Gap = 0, or if fewer than 2 objects.

lt_gap_v(+Objs, -Gap): Gap is the uniform row gap between consecutive objects sorted by centroid row. Fails under the same conditions as lt_gap_h.

Section 170.3: Centroid Convention

Individual object centroids use integer truncation (sum of row values // cell count). The centroid of all objects (lt_centroid_of_all) is the integer-truncated average of individual centroids.

Section 170.4: Layer Assignment

Layer 159. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2, sum_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins msort/2, findall/3, sort/2, length/2.

Part 171: Weave Pack Specification (wv_*, Layer 160)

Section 171.1: Purpose

The weave pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for list interlacing, slicing, and cycling. All predicates operate on any Prolog list; they do not require obj() terms. They are designed for ARC-AGI-2 compositional tasks that require interleaving object sequences, sliding window analysis, rotation, and cyclic repetition of collections.

Section 171.2: Predicate Specifications

wv_alternate(+L1, +L2, -Result): interleave elements of L1 and L2 alternately as [L1[0], L2[0], L1[1], L2[1], ...]. When one list is exhausted, the remaining elements of the other list are appended at the end.

wv_split_even_odd(+List, -Evens, -Odds): split List into elements at even 0-based indices (0, 2, 4, ...) in Evens and elements at odd 0-based indices (1, 3, 5, ...) in Odds.

wv_stride(+List, +Step, -Result): collect every Step-th element starting at index 0. Step must be >= 1. Result contains elements at positions 0, Step, 2*Step, etc.

wv_chunk(+List, +N, -Chunks): split List into consecutive non-overlapping chunks of exactly N elements. Any trailing elements that do not form a complete chunk of N are silently discarded.

wv_pair_wise(+List, -Pairs): produce all consecutive overlapping pairs as [[A,B],[B,C],[C,D],...]. Returns [] for lists with fewer than 2 elements.

wv_triple_wise(+List, -Triples): produce all consecutive overlapping triples as [[A,B,C],[B,C,D],...]. Returns [] for lists with fewer than 3 elements.

wv_rotate_left(+List, +K, -Result): rotate List left by K positions. The element at index K becomes the new head. K is taken modulo list length; empty list returns [].

wv_rotate_right(+List, +K, -Result): rotate List right by K positions. Equivalent to rotating left by (length - K mod length). Empty list returns [].

wv_reflect(+List, -Result): reverse the order of elements (mirror reflection). Delegates to reverse/2.

wv_repeat(+List, +N, -Result): concatenate List with itself N times. N=0 yields [].

wv_take(+List, +N, -Result): return the first N elements of List. If N >= length(List), the entire list is returned.

wv_drop(+List, +N, -Result): discard the first N elements of List and return the remainder. If N >= length(List), returns [].

wv_cycle(+List, +N, -Result): produce a list of exactly N elements by cycling through List repeatedly. Fails if List is empty and N > 0.

wv_zip(+List1, +List2, -Pairs): pair corresponding elements as H1-H2 terms using the -/2 functor. Stops at the shorter list; surplus elements are discarded.

Section 171.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 160. Depends on no other packs. Uses reverse/2, append/3, member/2 from library(lists); built-in length/2.

Part 172: Sizeop Pack Specification (sz_*, Layer 161)

Section 172.1: Purpose

The sizeop pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for size-based sorting and attribute assignment on obj(Color, Cells) collections. All predicates treat "size" as the cell count (length of the Cells list) of an obj term. They enable the common ARC-AGI-2 pattern of sorting objects by size and assigning attributes (such as colors) to them in sorted order.

Section 172.2: Predicate Specifications

sz_of(+Obj, -N): N is the cell count (number of r(R,C) terms in the Cells list) of Obj.

sz_sort_asc(+Objs, -Sorted): Sorted is Objs ordered by cell count ascending (smallest first). Uses stable sort: objects with equal size retain their relative order from the input.

sz_sort_desc(+Objs, -Sorted): Sorted is Objs ordered by cell count descending (largest first). Uses stable sort.

sz_smallest(+Objs, -Obj): Obj is the first object in Objs (by input order) with the fewest cells. Fails if Objs is empty.

sz_largest(+Objs, -Obj): Obj is the first object in Objs (by input order) with the most cells. Fails if Objs is empty.

sz_nth_smallest(+Objs, +N, -Obj): Obj is the Nth object in ascending size order. N is 1-based. Ties are broken by input order (stable sort).

sz_nth_largest(+Objs, +N, -Obj): Obj is the Nth object in descending size order. N is 1-based. Ties are broken by input order (stable sort).

sz_rank_of(+Objs, +Obj, -Rank): Rank is the 1-based position of Obj in the ascending size ordering of Objs. Ties are broken by input order (stable sort).

sz_assign_colors(+Objs, +Colors, -Result): sort Objs by size ascending, then recolor each object with the corresponding color from Colors. Truncates at the shorter of Objs and Colors. Result is a list of obj(NewColor, OriginalCells) terms.

sz_by_size(+Objs, +N, -Filtered): Filtered contains all objects in Objs with exactly N cells.

sz_above(+Objs, +N, -Filtered): Filtered contains all objects in Objs with strictly more than N cells.

sz_below(+Objs, +N, -Filtered): Filtered contains all objects in Objs with strictly fewer than N cells.

sz_unique_sizes(+Objs, -Sizes): Sizes is the sorted list of distinct cell counts across all objects in Objs.

sz_total_cells(+Objs, -N): N is the sum of cell counts across all objects in Objs. Returns 0 for empty Objs.

Section 172.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 161. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, nth1/3, min_list/2, max_list/2, sum_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins length/2, findall/3, sort/2, keysort/2.

Part 173: Posop Pack Specification (po_*, Layer 162)

Section 173.1: Purpose

The posop pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for position-based sorting, filtering, and attribute assignment on obj(Color, Cells) collections. "Position" is derived from the Cells list of r(R,C) terms: topmost row is the minimum R value across all cells; leftmost col is the minimum C value. These predicates enable ARC-AGI-2 patterns that assign attributes to objects based on their spatial location, or that select subsets of objects based on positional thresholds.

Section 173.2: Predicate Specifications

po_row_of(+Obj, -Row): Row is the topmost (minimum) row index of Obj's cells.

po_col_of(+Obj, -Col): Col is the leftmost (minimum) column index of Obj's cells.

po_row_rank(+Objs, +Obj, -Rank): Rank is the 1-based position of Obj when Objs is sorted by topmost row ascending. Ties preserve input order (stable sort).

po_col_rank(+Objs, +Obj, -Rank): Rank is the 1-based position of Obj when Objs is sorted by leftmost col ascending. Ties preserve input order (stable sort).

po_reading_rank(+Objs, +Obj, -Rank): Rank is the 1-based position of Obj in reading order (ascending by topmost row, then by leftmost col within equal rows). Ties preserve input order (stable sort).

po_assign_by_row(+Objs, +Colors, -Result): sort Objs by topmost row ascending, then recolor each with the corresponding color from Colors. Truncates at the shorter of Objs and Colors.

po_assign_by_col(+Objs, +Colors, -Result): sort Objs by leftmost col ascending, then recolor each with the corresponding color from Colors. Truncates at the shorter of Objs and Colors.

po_assign_reading(+Objs, +Colors, -Result): sort Objs in reading order (row then col), then recolor each with the corresponding color from Colors. Truncates at the shorter of Objs and Colors.

po_above_row(+Objs, +R, -Filtered): Filtered contains all objects in Objs whose topmost row is strictly less than R.

po_from_row(+Objs, +R, -Filtered): Filtered contains all objects in Objs whose topmost row is >= R.

po_left_of(+Objs, +C, -Filtered): Filtered contains all objects in Objs whose leftmost col is strictly less than C.

po_from_col(+Objs, +C, -Filtered): Filtered contains all objects in Objs whose leftmost col is >= C.

po_in_row_band(+Objs, +R1, +R2, -Filtered): Filtered contains all objects in Objs whose topmost row is in the inclusive range [R1, R2].

po_in_col_band(+Objs, +C1, +C2, -Filtered): Filtered contains all objects in Objs whose leftmost col is in the inclusive range [C1, C2].

Section 173.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 162. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, nth1/3, min_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins findall/3, keysort/2.

Part 174: Objxf Pack Specification (ox_*, Layer 163)

Section 174.1: Purpose

The objxf pack provides 14 general-purpose predicates for spatial and color transformations of individual obj(Color, Cells) terms. It is the first pack to operate on obj terms as first-class geometric objects: rotating, reflecting, translating, scaling, and combining them without requiring a grid intermediary. This enables compositional transformation rules that work at the object level rather than the grid level.

Section 174.2: Predicate Specifications

ox_bbox(+Obj, -R0, -C0, -R1, -C1): R0 = min row, C0 = min col, R1 = max row, C1 = max col of Obj's cells. Fails if Cells is empty.

ox_size(+Obj, -H, -W): H = R1 - R0 + 1 (height), W = C1 - C0 + 1 (width) of Obj's bounding box.

ox_translate(+Obj, +DR, +DC, -Result): shift every cell by (DR, DC). Result has the same color as Obj. DR and DC may be negative.

ox_to_origin(+Obj, -Result): shift Obj so its topmost row is 0 and its leftmost col is 0. Equivalent to ox_translate(Obj, -R0, -C0, Result) where (R0, C0) is the bounding box anchor.

ox_recolor(+Obj, +NewColor, -Result): replace Obj's color with NewColor. Cells are unchanged.

ox_rot90(+Obj, -Result): rotate 90 degrees clockwise within the bounding box. Each cell r(R, C) maps to r(R0 + Lc, C0 + (H-1) - Lr) where Lr = R - R0, Lc = C - C0, H = bounding box height. After rotation the bounding box is W x H (height and width swap).

ox_rot180(+Obj, -Result): rotate 180 degrees. Each cell r(R, C) maps to r(R0 + R1 - R, C0 + C1 - C). Bounding box dimensions unchanged.

ox_rot270(+Obj, -Result): rotate 270 degrees clockwise (= 90 degrees counter-clockwise). Each cell r(R, C) maps to r(R0 + (W-1) - Lc, C0 + Lr) where Lc = C - C0, Lr = R - R0, W = bounding box width. After rotation the bounding box is W x H.

ox_reflect_h(+Obj, -Result): flip upside-down within the bounding box. Each cell r(R, C) maps to r(R0 + R1 - R, C). Column positions unchanged.

ox_reflect_v(+Obj, -Result): flip left-right within the bounding box. Each cell r(R, C) maps to r(R, C0 + C1 - C). Row positions unchanged.

ox_merge(+Obj1, +Obj2, -Result): Result has Obj1's color. Cells = sorted union of both Cells lists (sort/2 deduplicates).

ox_diff(+Obj1, +Obj2, -Result): Result has Obj1's color. Cells = cells in Obj1 not in Obj2.

ox_intersect(+Obj1, +Obj2, -Result): Result has Obj1's color. Cells = cells in both Obj1 and Obj2.

ox_scale_up(+Obj, +Factor, -Result): scale by a positive integer Factor. Each cell r(R, C) expands to a Factor x Factor block: r(R*Factor + DR, C*Factor + DC) for DR, DC in [0, Factor-1].

Section 174.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 163. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins sort/2, findall/3, between/3.

Part 175: Shrink Pack Specification (sk_*, Layer 164)

Section 175.1: Purpose

The shrink pack provides grid downscaling and block decomposition predicates. It partitions a 2D grid into equal-sized NxN blocks, tests and exploits blocky structure (where every block is uniformly colored), shrinks a blocky grid by factor N (the inverse of ox_scale_up in the objxf pack), finds the scale factor of a scaled-up grid, and downscales obj(Color, Cells) terms. All predicates use 0-indexed row-column coordinates.

Section 175.2: Predicate Specifications

dn_block_dims(+Grid, +N, -BI, -BJ): Count complete NxN blocks. BI = H // N (rows of blocks); BJ = W // N (cols of blocks). Uses integer division on the grid height H and width W.

dn_block_cells(+N, +I, +J, -Cells): r(R,C) pairs covering block (I,J) in NxN partition. Block (I,J) spans rows [I*N .. I*N+N-1] and cols [J*N .. J*N+N-1].

dn_block_color(+Grid, +N, +I, +J, -Color): Unique color of block (I,J). Fails when the block contains two or more distinct values. Uses sort/2 with pattern [Color] to enforce uniqueness.

dn_block_majority(+Grid, +N, +I, +J, -Color): Most frequent value in block (I,J). Ties are broken by standard-order comparison (larger value wins when counts are equal).

dn_is_blocky(+Grid, +N): Succeed if every complete NxN block in Grid is uniform. Uses forall/2 over all block indices.

dn_shrink(+Grid, +N, -Small): Downscale Grid by N using majority vote per block. Small[I][J] = most frequent color in block (I,J). Always succeeds for positive N with at least one complete block.

dn_shrink_strict(+Grid, +N, -Small): Downscale Grid by N; fail if any block is not uniform. Calls dn_is_blocky before building the result.

dn_find_scale(+Grid, -N): Find the smallest N >= 2 such that Grid is N-blocky. Tries divisors of H and W in ascending order; fails if no such N exists up to H.

dn_obj_shrink(+Obj, +N, -Small): Downscale an obj term by dividing all coordinates by N. Each cell r(R,C) maps to r(R//N, C//N); sort/2 removes duplicates that arise when multiple cells map to the same block position.

dn_scale_factor(+Obj1, +Obj2, -N): Find the smallest N >= 2 such that shrinking Obj2 by N yields a normalized cell set matching Obj1 normalized. Tries N from 2 to 30.

dn_uniform_blocks(+Grid, +N, -Pairs): I-J pairs for all uniform NxN blocks (where dn_block_color succeeds).

dn_mixed_blocks(+Grid, +N, -Pairs): I-J pairs for all non-uniform NxN blocks (where dn_block_color fails).

dn_block_grid(+Grid, +N, +I, +J, -Patch): Extract block (I,J) as an NxN sub-grid. Patch is a list of N rows each containing N values.

dn_block_val(+Grid, +N, +I, +J, -Vals): Flat list of all values in block (I,J) in row-major order.

Section 175.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 164. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, nth0/3, min_list/2, last/2 from library(lists); built-ins sort/2, msort/2, findall/3, forall/2, between/3, length/2.

Part 176: Objmorph Pack Specification (om_*, Layer 165)

Section 176.1: Purpose

The objmorph pack provides morphological operations on obj(Color, Cells) terms directly, without requiring a grid. It implements neighborhood generation, boundary and interior extraction under both 4-connectivity and 8-connectivity, single-step and iterated dilation, single-step and iterated erosion, and the compound operations of morphological opening and closing. The pack treats each obj as a cell set and performs standard binary morphology on that set.

Section 176.2: Predicate Specifications

om_neighbors4(+Cell, -Neighbors): Returns the 4 cells directly adjacent (up, down, left, right) to r(R,C). Always returns exactly 4 cells; coordinates may be negative or outside any particular grid boundary.

om_neighbors8(+Cell, -Neighbors): Returns the 8 cells adjacent (including diagonals) to r(R,C). Always returns exactly 8 cells.

om_boundary4(+Obj, -Boundary): Returns an obj with the same Color containing only the boundary cells under 4-connectivity. A cell is a boundary4 cell if at least one of its 4 neighbors is not in the cell set.

om_interior4(+Obj, -Interior): Returns an obj with the same Color containing only the interior cells under 4-connectivity. A cell is interior4 if all 4 of its neighbors are in the cell set.

om_boundary8(+Obj, -Boundary): Returns an obj containing cells that have at least one 8-neighbor outside the cell set.

om_interior8(+Obj, -Interior): Returns an obj containing cells where all 8 neighbors are in the cell set. Stricter than interior4.

om_dilate4(+Obj, -Result): Expands the cell set by one 4-connected step. Each cell contributes its 4 neighbors to the result; original cells are retained. Result = union of original cells and all 4-neighbors of every original cell.

om_erode4(+Obj, -Result): Shrinks the cell set by one 4-connected step. Equivalent to om_interior4: retains only cells fully surrounded on all 4 sides.

om_dilate8(+Obj, -Result): Expands the cell set by one 8-connected step, including diagonal expansion.

om_erode8(+Obj, -Result): Shrinks the cell set by one 8-connected step. Equivalent to om_interior8.

om_dilate4_n(+Obj, +N, -Result): Applies om_dilate4 exactly N times. N=0 is the identity.

om_erode4_n(+Obj, +N, -Result): Applies om_erode4 exactly N times. N=0 is the identity.

om_open4(+Obj, -Result): Morphological opening = erode4 then dilate4. Removes small protrusions and thin connections while preserving bulk shapes.

om_close4(+Obj, -Result): Morphological closing = dilate4 then erode4. Fills small gaps and indentations while preserving bulk shapes.

Section 176.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 165. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2 from library(lists); built-ins sort/2, findall/3, forall/2.

Part 177: Voronoi Pack Specification (vn_*, Layer 166)

Section 177.1: Purpose

The voronoi pack provides nearest-color painting and Voronoi partitioning for 2D grids. Given a grid with non-background colored cells and background cells (identified by a distinguished background value), the pack computes: the nearest non-background color to any background cell by Manhattan distance; the distance transform (distance from each cell to nearest non-background cell); the Voronoi partition (which background cells belong to which color's region); the medial axis (background cells equidistant from two or more colors); and color expansion (background cells reachable within N steps of a specific color).

Section 177.2: Predicate Specifications

vn_non_bg_cells(+Grid, +Bg, -Cells): sorted list of r(R,C) positions whose value differs from Bg.

vn_non_bg_colors(+Grid, +Bg, -Colors): sorted list of distinct non-background values in Grid.

vn_nearest_dist(+Grid, +Bg, +R, +C, -Dist): minimum Manhattan distance from r(R,C) to any non-background cell. Fails if no non-Bg cells exist.

vn_nearest_color(+Grid, +Bg, +R, +C, -Color): color of the non-background cell nearest to r(R,C). Ties broken by standard term order.

vn_paint_bg(+Grid, +Bg, -Painted): replace every Bg cell with the color of the nearest non-Bg cell. Non-Bg cells are unchanged.

vn_dist_map(+Grid, +Bg, -DGrid): same dimensions as Grid. Each Bg cell becomes the Manhattan distance to the nearest non-Bg cell; each non-Bg cell becomes 0.

vn_region_cells(+Grid, +Bg, +Color, -Cells): sorted list of Bg cells whose nearest non-Bg color is Color.

vn_regions(+Grid, +Bg, -Pairs): sorted list of Color-[Cells] pairs for every distinct non-Bg color.

vn_max_dist(+Grid, +Bg, -MaxDist): maximum distance of any Bg cell from its nearest non-Bg cell. Fails if no Bg cells.

vn_at_dist(+Grid, +Bg, +D, -Cells): sorted list of Bg cells whose nearest non-Bg cell is at distance exactly D.

vn_within_dist(+Grid, +Bg, +D, -Cells): sorted list of Bg cells at distance =< D from the nearest non-Bg cell.

vn_medial(+Grid, +Bg, -Cells): sorted list of Bg cells equidistant from non-Bg cells of two or more distinct colors (the Voronoi edge / medial axis).

vn_expand1(+Grid, +Bg, +Color, -Cells): sorted list of Bg cells that are 4-connected to at least one non-Bg cell of Color.

vn_expand_n(+Grid, +Bg, +Color, +N, -Cells): sorted list of Bg cells within Manhattan distance N of any Color cell. N=0 gives an empty list.

Section 177.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 166. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, nth0/3, min_list/2, max_list/2, append/3 from library(lists); built-ins sort/2, findall/3.

Part 178: Objcomp Pack Specification (oc_*, Layer 167)

Section 178.1: Purpose

The objcomp pack provides adjacency and connected-component analysis over collections of obj(Color, Cells) terms. Two objects "touch" when any cell of the first is 4-connected (Manhattan distance 1) to any cell of the second. The pack builds on this touching relation to: enumerate touching pairs, compute adjacency lists, measure touch degree, find isolated objects, compute BFS-connected components, and rank objects by connectivity.

Section 178.2: Predicate Specifications

oc_touches(+Obj1, +Obj2): true when any cell of Obj1 is 4-adjacent to any cell of Obj2. Cuts after the first found adjacent pair.

oc_touching_pairs(+Objs, -Pairs): list of O1-O2 pairs where both are in Objs and oc_touches(O1,O2) is true. Each unordered pair appears once (lower index first).

oc_adj_list(+Objs, -AdjList): Obj-[Neighbors] pairs for every Obj in Objs. Neighbors are all other elements of Objs that touch Obj.

oc_degree(+Obj, +Objs, -N): count of objects in Objs (excluding Obj itself) that touch Obj.

oc_isolated(+Objs, -Isolated): objects in Objs that do not touch any other object in Objs.

oc_connected(+Obj, +Objs, -Component): sorted list of objects reachable from Obj through the touching relation within Objs, including Obj itself. Uses BFS.

oc_components(+Objs, -Components): list of all touching-connected components. Each component is a sorted list of obj terms.

oc_num_components(+Objs, -N): number of touching-connected components in Objs.

oc_largest_component(+Objs, -Component): the component with the most objects. Ties resolved by component order from oc_components.

oc_smallest_component(+Objs, -Component): the component with the fewest objects.

oc_singleton_components(+Objs, -Singles): all components of size exactly 1.

oc_shared_components(+Objs, -Groups): all components of size 2 or more.

oc_max_degree(+Objs, -MaxDeg): maximum touch degree of any object in Objs. Fails if Objs is empty.

oc_sort_by_degree(+Objs, -Sorted): Objs sorted in ascending order of touch degree. Equal-degree objects retain their original relative order.

Section 178.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 167. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, nth0/3, last/2, append/3, subtract/3, max_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins sort/2, findall/3, keysort/2, length/2.

Part 179: Wavefront BFS Propagation Pack (wf_*, Layer 168)

Section 179.1: Purpose

The wavefront pack provides BFS-based wave propagation through a 2D grid, starting from a set of seed cells and spreading through cells matching a designated passable color. Unlike the voronoi pack (which uses Manhattan distance in open space), the wavefront pack uses actual BFS path length, correctly handling obstacles and irregular regions.

Section 179.2: Predicate Specifications

wf_passable(+Grid, +PassColor, -Cells): sorted list of all r(R,C) positions in Grid whose value equals PassColor.

wf_bfs(+Grid, +Seeds, +PassColor, -DistPairs): BFS from all Seeds through PassColor cells. Seeds appear at distance 0 regardless of their own color. DistPairs is a sorted list of D-r(R,C) terms.

wf_reachable(+Grid, +Seeds, +PassColor, -Cells): sorted list of all cells (seeds and PassColor cells) appearing in the BFS distance map.

wf_unreachable(+Grid, +Seeds, +PassColor, -Cells): sorted list of PassColor cells not reachable from Seeds.

wf_at_dist(+DistPairs, +D, -Cells): sorted list of cells at exactly distance D.

wf_within_dist(+DistPairs, +MaxD, -Cells): sorted list of cells at distance <= MaxD.

wf_dist_of(+DistPairs, +Cell, -D): distance D of Cell in DistPairs. Fails if Cell not present.

wf_max_dist(+DistPairs, -MaxD): maximum wave distance in DistPairs. Fails if empty.

wf_all_dists(+DistPairs, -Dists): sorted list of distinct distance values in DistPairs.

wf_path_exists(+Grid, +CellA, +CellB, +PassColor): true when CellB is reachable from CellA via BFS through PassColor cells.

wf_paint_bg(+Grid, +Seeds, +PassColor, +MaxD, -NewGrid): replace each PassColor cell with its BFS distance capped at MaxD. Unreachable cells remain unchanged.

wf_multi_wave(+Grid, +ColoredSeeds, +PassColor, -Painted): paint each PassColor cell with the color of the nearest seed. ColoredSeeds is a list of Color-Seeds pairs. Ties broken by standard term order of Color.

wf_collision(+Grid, +ColoredSeeds, +PassColor, -Cells): sorted list of PassColor cells equidistant from at least two different-colored seed sets.

wf_enclosed(+Grid, +PassColor, -Cells): sorted list of PassColor cells not reachable from any PassColor cell on the grid border.

Section 179.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 168. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, nth0/3, append/3, subtract/3, max_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins sort/2, msort/2, findall/3, memberchk/2, length/2.

Part 180: Object Chain Analysis Pack (ch_*, Layer 169)

Section 180.1: Purpose

The objchain pack provides predicates for detecting and operating on linear chains of obj(Color, Cells) terms connected through 4-adjacency. A chain is a set of objects whose touching graph is a simple path: exactly two objects have touch-degree 1 (endpoints), all others have degree 2. Distinct from objcomp, which handles arbitrary connected components.

Section 180.2: Predicate Specifications

ch_touches(+Obj1, +Obj2): true if any cell of Obj1 is 4-adjacent to any cell of Obj2. Cuts after first found adjacent pair.

ch_degree(+Obj, +Objs, -N): N is the count of objects in Objs (excluding Obj) that 4-touch Obj. The touch-degree of Obj within the universe Objs.

ch_is_chain(+Objs): true when Objs forms a simple linear path. Empty and singleton lists are trivially chains. Two objects form a chain iff they touch. Three or more: exactly two have degree 1 and all others have degree 2.

ch_has_cycle(+Objs): true when Objs forms a closed cycle. Requires N >= 3 and all objects have degree 2 within Objs.

ch_endpoints(+Objs, -E1, -E2): E1 and E2 are the two degree-1 objects. Objs must be a valid chain.

ch_linearize(+Objs, -Ordered): put chain objects in order from one endpoint to the other. Works on an unordered collection.

ch_from_endpoint(+Objs, +Start, -Ordered): linearize starting from Start. Start should be an endpoint for a full traversal.

ch_nth(+Ordered, +N, -Obj): Obj is the Nth element (0-based) of the ordered chain.

ch_color_seq(+Ordered, -Colors): Colors is the list of colors of each object in order.

ch_sub(+Ordered, +I, +J, -Sub): Sub is the sub-chain from index I to J (0-based, inclusive).

ch_reverse(+Ordered, -Rev): Rev is Ordered reversed.

ch_length(+Objs, -N): N is the number of objects in the chain.

ch_is_linear_path(+Ordered): true when each consecutive pair in Ordered touches. Verifies an ordered sequence.

ch_direction(+Ordered, -Dir): Dir is h (horizontal: all same min-row), v (vertical: all same min-col), or other.

Section 180.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 169. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, nth0/3, append/3, reverse/2, min_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins length/2, findall/3, forall/2, memberchk/2.

Part 181: Object Symmetry Analysis Pack (os_*, Layer 170)

Section 181.1: Purpose

The objsym pack provides bounding-box-relative symmetry operations and symmetry tests for individual obj(Color, Cells) terms. It complements the sym pack (grid-level reflections and rotations on list-of-lists) and the symmetry pack (grid-level D4 orbit and canonical form) by working directly on object cell sets. The key distinction: all transforms are computed relative to each object's own bounding box, so an object at any grid position is analyzed correctly without prior normalization.

Section 181.2: Predicate Specifications

os_bbox(+Obj, -MinR, -MinC, -MaxR, -MaxC): minimum and maximum row and column indices of the object's cell set. The bounding box.

os_normalize(+Obj, -NormObj): translate Obj so its bounding box top-left corner is at r(0,0). Subtracts MinR from every row index and MinC from every column index.

os_translate(+Obj, +DR, +DC, -Moved): shift every cell of Obj by (DR, DC). New row = old R + DR; new col = old C + DC.

os_reflect_h(+Obj, -Reflected): reflect Obj left-right about its own vertical center axis. For each cell r(R,C): new C = MinC + MaxC - C; row unchanged.

os_reflect_v(+Obj, -Reflected): reflect Obj top-bottom about its own horizontal center axis. For each cell r(R,C): new R = MinR + MaxR - R; col unchanged.

os_rotate180(+Obj, -Rotated): rotate Obj 180 degrees about its bbox center. Equivalent to applying both reflect_h and reflect_v. For each cell r(R,C): new R = MinR+MaxR-R, new C = MinC+MaxC-C.

os_rotate90(+Obj, -Rotated): rotate Obj 90 degrees clockwise, with result normalized to origin. Formula: for each r(R,C), new r(NR,NC) where NR = C - MinC and NC = MaxR - R.

os_is_hsymm(+Obj): true when the sorted cell set of Obj equals the sorted cell set of os_reflect_h(Obj). Left-right symmetry about the vertical center axis.

os_is_vsymm(+Obj): true when the sorted cell set equals the sorted cell set of os_reflect_v(Obj). Top-bottom symmetry about the horizontal center axis.

os_is_rot180(+Obj): true when the sorted cell set equals the sorted cell set of os_rotate180(Obj). 180-degree rotational symmetry.

os_is_rot90(+Obj): true when the sorted cell set of normalized Obj equals the sorted cell set of normalized os_rotate90(Obj). 90-degree rotational symmetry. Normalization is applied before and after rotation.

os_has_symmetry(+Obj): true when at least one of os_is_hsymm, os_is_vsymm, os_is_rot180, os_is_rot90 holds. Uses cut to stop on first match.

os_symmetries(+Obj, -List): List contains the atoms [h, v, rot180, rot90] for which the corresponding symmetry test holds for Obj.

os_equivalent(+Obj1, +Obj2): true when the normalized cell sets of Obj1 and Obj2 are identical under some D4 orientation. D4 comprises 4 rotations (0, 90, 180, 270 degrees) and 4 flip-then-rotate variants. Color is ignored; only cell positions are compared. Uses cut after first matching orientation.

Section 181.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 170. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins findall/3, msort/2, memberchk/2.

Part 182: Object Shape Classification and Bounding Box Analysis Pack (ob_*, Layer 171)

Section 182.1: Purpose

The objbound pack provides shape classification predicates for obj(Color, Cells) terms. Given an object's cell set, it answers questions about the object's bounding-box dimensions, shape type (rectangle, horizontal line, vertical line, single cell, hollow, frame), interior holes, perimeter (exposed edges), and dense hull (the solid bounding-box rectangle). Complements objmorph (morphological dilation and erosion) and objsym (symmetry tests).

Section 182.2: Predicate Specifications

ob_bbox_h(+Obj, -H): H is the height of the bounding box (MaxR - MinR + 1). Minimum is 1.

ob_bbox_w(+Obj, -W): W is the width of the bounding box (MaxC - MinC + 1). Minimum is 1.

ob_bbox_area(+Obj, -Area): Area is H * W. Total positions spanned by the bounding box including holes.

ob_is_rect(+Obj): true when the object has no holes: cell count equals bbox area. Every grid position in the bbox is occupied.

ob_is_hline(+Obj): true when bbox height is 1. All cells lie in the same row.

ob_is_vline(+Obj): true when bbox width is 1. All cells lie in the same column.

ob_is_single(+Obj): true when H = 1 and W = 1. Exactly one cell.

ob_is_square_bbox(+Obj): true when H = W. The bounding box is square. Does not require the object itself to be a solid square.

ob_holes(+Obj, -HoleCells): HoleCells is the sorted list of cells within the bounding box that are NOT in the object's cell set. Empty for rectangles.

ob_n_holes(+Obj, -N): N is the length of ob_holes(Obj). Zero for rectangles.

ob_is_hollow(+Obj): true when N > 0. The object has at least one gap within its bounding box.

ob_is_frame(+Obj): true when the object is a hollow rectangular frame. Requires H >= 3 and W >= 3; all cells on the bounding box border (row = MinR or MaxR, col = MinC or MaxC) are present; no cell strictly inside the border is present.

ob_perimeter(+Obj, -P): P is the total exposed edge count. For each cell, count 4-adjacent neighbors not in the object's cell set and sum across all cells.

ob_dense_hull(+Obj, -HullObj): HullObj has the same color as Obj and contains every cell in the bounding box (MinR..MaxR x MinC..MaxC). The solid rectangle that encloses Obj.

Section 182.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 171. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, memberchk/2, min_list/2, max_list/2, sum_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins findall/3, between/3, forall/2, length/2.

Part 183: Objrel Pack Specification (or_*, Layer 172)

Section 183.1: Purpose

The objrel pack provides pairwise geometric and spatial relation predicates for obj(Color, Cells) terms. Given two objects, these predicates compute: whether they share cells (overlap, shared_cells, n_shared), whether they are adjacent without overlapping (touch4, touch8), whether one cell set includes the other (contains), the union of their cell sets (union_cells), the Euclidean and Manhattan distances between their centroids (dist, manhattan), the compass direction from one centroid to the other (direction), whether their centroids are row-aligned or column-aligned (aligned_h, aligned_v), and the row and column gaps between their bounding boxes (gap_rows, gap_cols). Colors are ignored in all predicates; only cell positions matter.

Section 183.2: Predicate Specifications

or_overlap(+Obj1, +Obj2): Obj1 and Obj2 share at least one cell position. Colors are irrelevant. Succeeds on the first shared cell found (cut).

or_shared_cells(+Obj1, +Obj2, -Shared): Shared is the list of cell positions appearing in both Obj1 and Obj2, in the order they appear in Obj1's cell list.

or_n_shared(+Obj1, +Obj2, -N): N is the count of shared cell positions.

or_touch4(+Obj1, +Obj2): The objects are 4-adjacent (Manhattan distance 1 between some pair of cells) but do not overlap. Fails if they overlap. Succeeds on the first adjacent pair found (cut).

or_touch8(+Obj1, +Obj2): The objects are 8-adjacent (Chebyshev distance 1 between some pair of cells) but do not overlap. Includes diagonal neighbors. Fails if they overlap. Succeeds on the first adjacent pair found (cut).

or_contains(+Obj1, +Obj2): Every cell of Obj2 is also a cell of Obj1. Uses forall/memberchk. True when Obj2's cell set is a subset of Obj1's.

or_union_cells(+Obj1, +Obj2, -Union): Union is the sorted list of all cells appearing in either Obj1 or Obj2. Duplicates are removed by sort/2.

or_dist(+Obj1, +Obj2, -D): D is the Euclidean distance between the centroids of Obj1 and Obj2. Centroids are sum(rows)/N and sum(cols)/N; D may be a float.

or_manhattan(+Obj1, +Obj2, -D): D is the Manhattan distance between the centroids of Obj1 and Obj2. D may be a float when centroids are non-integer.

or_direction(+Obj1, +Obj2, -Dir): Dir is the compass direction from the centroid of Obj1 to the centroid of Obj2. One of: n, s, e, w, ne, nw, se, sw, or same (when centroids coincide). Row increases southward; column increases eastward.

or_aligned_h(+Obj1, +Obj2): The centroid rows of Obj1 and Obj2 are arithmetically equal. "Horizontally aligned" means both objects share the same row center.

or_aligned_v(+Obj1, +Obj2): The centroid columns of Obj1 and Obj2 are arithmetically equal. "Vertically aligned" means both objects share the same column center.

or_gap_rows(+Obj1, +Obj2, -G): G is the number of empty rows between the bounding boxes of Obj1 and Obj2. G = 0 when bounding boxes touch or overlap in the row dimension. Formula: max(0, max(MinR1,MinR2) - min(MaxR1,MaxR2) - 1).

or_gap_cols(+Obj1, +Obj2, -G): G is the number of empty columns between the bounding boxes of Obj1 and Obj2. Same formula applied to column extremes.

Section 183.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 172. Depends on no other packs. Uses member/2, memberchk/2, append/3 from library(lists); built-ins findall/3, forall/2, sort/2, length/2, min_list/2, max_list/2, sumlist/2.

Part 184: Objfilter Pack Specification (of_*, Layer 173)

Section 184.1: Purpose

The objfilter pack provides filtering, selection, and partitioning predicates for lists of obj(Color, Cells) terms. Given a scene (a list of objects), these predicates select objects by color (of_by_color, of_not_color), by cell count (of_exact_size, of_min_size, of_max_size), and by shape classification (of_is_rect, of_is_hline, of_is_vline, of_is_single, of_is_hollow). Two aggregate predicates find the largest and smallest object (of_largest, of_smallest). A generic meta-predicate (of_filter) and a partitioner (of_partition) complete the set. All shape tests are implemented with private helpers (of_size_, of_bbox_, and five shape testers) so the pack has no cross-pack dependencies.

Section 184.2: Private Helpers

of_size_(+Obj, -N): length of the cell list. Used by size predicates and shape tests.

of_bbox_(+Obj, -MinR, -MinC, -MaxR, -MaxC): bounding box via findall on row and column indices plus min_list/max_list.

of_is_rect_(+Obj): true when cell count = (MaxR-MinR+1)*(MaxC-MinC+1). No holes.

of_is_hline_(+Obj): true when MinR = MaxR (all cells in same row).

of_is_vline_(+Obj): true when MinC = MaxC (all cells in same column).

of_is_single_(+Obj): true when cell count = 1.

of_is_hollow_(+Obj): true when cell count < bbox area.

of_largest_acc_ and of_smallest_acc_: recursive accumulators that compare cell counts and propagate the current best object.

Section 184.3: Predicate Specifications

of_by_color(+Objs, +Color, -Filtered): findall objects matching obj(Color, _). Preserves order.

of_not_color(+Objs, +Color, -Filtered): findall objects with color != Color via C \= Color.

of_exact_size(+Objs, +N, -Filtered): findall objects where of_size_ = N.

of_min_size(+Objs, +N, -Filtered): findall objects where of_size_ >= N.

of_max_size(+Objs, +N, -Filtered): findall objects where of_size_ =< N.

of_is_rect(+Objs, -Filtered): findall objects passing of_is_rect_.

of_is_hline(+Objs, -Filtered): findall objects passing of_is_hline_. Includes single-cell objects (bbox height 1).

of_is_vline(+Objs, -Filtered): findall objects passing of_is_vline_. Includes single-cell objects (bbox width 1).

of_is_single(+Objs, -Filtered): findall objects with cell count = 1.

of_is_hollow(+Objs, -Filtered): findall objects where cell count < bbox area. Includes L-shapes and frames.

of_largest(+Objs, -Obj): linear scan with accumulator; returns the first object with the maximum cell count. Fails on empty Objs.

of_smallest(+Objs, -Obj): linear scan with accumulator; returns the first object with the minimum cell count. Fails on empty Objs.

of_filter(+Objs, :Goal, -Filtered): meta-predicate; wraps include/3 from library(apply). Goal is called as call(Goal, Obj); objects where Goal succeeds are kept.

of_partition(+Objs, :Goal, -In, -Out): meta-predicate; wraps partition/4 from library(apply). In receives objects where Goal succeeds; Out receives objects where Goal fails.

Section 184.4: Layer Assignment

Layer 173. No cross-pack dependencies. Uses member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2 from library(lists); include/3, exclude/3, partition/4 from library(apply); built-ins findall/3, length/2.

Part 185: Canvas Pack Specification (cv_*, Layer 174)

Section 185.1: Purpose

The canvas pack provides predicates for creating grid canvases, painting
obj(Color, Cells) terms onto them, erasing objects, extracting objects from
grids, and compositing subgrids. It bridges the gap between the obj-term
world and the grid world: given a list of obj terms and a desired grid size,
cv_render/5 produces a complete grid. Given a grid, cv_extract_all/3 recovers
the obj list. The pack has no cross-pack dependencies.

Section 185.2: Predicate Specifications

cv_blank(+H, +W, +Bg, -Grid): create an H x W grid where every cell equals Bg.
Grid is a list of H lists each of length W.

cv_size(+Grid, -H, -W): return the height H and width W of a grid.

cv_paint(+Grid, +Obj, -Grid2): paint obj(Color, Cells) onto Grid. All cells in
Cells are set to Color; all other cells are unchanged. Uses a single findall
pass over the grid for efficiency.

cv_paint_all(+Grid, +Objs, -Grid2): paint each obj in Objs onto Grid in list
order. Later objects overwrite earlier ones at shared cell positions.

cv_paint_at(+Grid, +Obj, +DR, +DC, -Grid2): translate each cell r(R,C) in Obj
to r(R+DR, C+DC) then paint. No bounds checking; cells outside the grid are
painted (they do not appear in the output because the grid scan never reaches
them).

cv_paint_clip(+Grid, +Obj, -Grid2): like cv_paint but silently skips cells
with row or column index outside [0, H-1] or [0, W-1].

cv_paint_bg(+Grid, +Obj, +Bg, -Grid2): paint only those cells of Obj whose
current grid value equals Bg. Cells already occupied by a non-Bg value are
left unchanged.

cv_erase(+Grid, +Obj, +Bg, -Grid2): fill all cells of Obj with Bg. The color
field of Obj is ignored.

cv_extract(+Grid, +Color, -Obj): collect all (R,C) positions where the grid
value equals Color into obj(Color, Cells) in row-major order. Cells is empty
if Color does not appear in Grid.

cv_extract_all(+Grid, +Bg, -Objs): collect all non-Bg cells, find the sorted
set of distinct colors, and return one obj(Color, Cells) per color in color-
sorted order. Returns [] if every cell equals Bg.

cv_render(+H, +W, +Bg, +Objs, -Grid): create a blank H x W canvas (cv_blank)
then paint all objects (cv_paint_all). Convenience predicate for the common
scene-to-grid pipeline.

cv_move(+Grid, +Obj, +DR, +DC, +Bg, -Grid2): erase Obj from its current
position (cv_erase) then repaint at offset (DR,DC) (cv_paint_at).

cv_stamp(+Obj, +Bg, -Patch): extract Obj as a minimal bounding-box grid.
Cells are normalized to origin (MinR=0, MinC=0). Non-obj cells within the
bbox are filled with Bg. Patch dimensions equal bbox height x bbox width.

cv_blit(+Canvas, +Patch, +R0, +C0, -Grid2): paste Patch onto Canvas with
its top-left corner at position (R0, C0). Each Patch cell Patch[pr][pc]
overwrites Canvas[R0+pr][C0+pc]. Patch cells that fall outside the canvas
bounds are silently ignored.

Section 185.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 174. No cross-pack dependencies. Uses member/2, nth0/3, memberchk/2
from library(lists); min_list/2, max_list/2 from library(lists); built-ins
findall/3, length/2.


Part 186: Object Sequence and Progression Analysis (objseq Pack, WP 196)

Section 186.1: Purpose

The objseq pack analyses ordered sequences of obj(Color, Cells) terms for
patterns in color, size, and spatial position. It is the companion to the
arrange pack (spatial ordering) and the query pack (aggregate statistics),
focusing specifically on sequence-order relationships: monotone size change,
periodic color or size cycles, equal centroid spacing, collinear arrangement,
and positional projection.

Section 186.2: Predicate Specifications

oq_color_seq(+Objs, -Colors): Colors is the list of colors from each obj in
Objs, in list order. Deterministic.

oq_size_seq(+Objs, -Sizes): Sizes is the list of cell counts from each obj in
Objs, in list order. Deterministic.

oq_centroid_seq(+Objs, -Centroids): Centroids is the list of floor-average
r(R,C) centroids of Objs, in list order. Deterministic.

oq_step_seq(+Objs, -Steps): Steps is the list of consecutive centroid deltas
dr(DR,DC) between adjacent objs in list order. Length is length(Objs)-1.
Deterministic. Succeeds with empty Steps for 0 or 1 objs.

oq_is_growing(+Objs): succeeds if the cell counts in Objs are strictly
increasing in list order. Trivially succeeds for 0 or 1 objs.

oq_is_shrinking(+Objs): succeeds if the cell counts in Objs are strictly
decreasing in list order. Trivially succeeds for 0 or 1 objs.

oq_const_step(+Objs, -DR, -DC): all consecutive centroid steps equal DR and
DC. Fails if Objs has fewer than 2 elements or if any step differs. Binds DR
and DC to the common row and column delta. Deterministic.

oq_const_row_step(+Objs, -DR): all consecutive centroid row differences equal
DR. Column differences may vary. Fails if Objs has fewer than 2 elements or
if any row step differs. Deterministic.

oq_const_col_step(+Objs, -DC): all consecutive centroid column differences
equal DC. Row differences may vary. Fails if Objs has fewer than 2 elements
or if any col step differs. Deterministic.

oq_color_period(+Objs, -P, -Cycle): P is the smallest positive integer such
that Cycle (a list of length P) tiles the color sequence of Objs exactly.
Requires N mod P = 0 where N = length(Objs). Fails if Objs is empty. P
equals length(Objs) when no proper sub-period exists. Deterministic (first
solution only).

oq_size_period(+Objs, -P, -Cycle): same as oq_color_period but for the size
(cell-count) sequence. Deterministic.

oq_collinear(+Objs): succeeds if all centroids of Objs lie on a single
straight line. Uses the 2D cross-product test. Trivially succeeds for 1 or 2
objs. Fails for 0 objs.

oq_next_centroid(+Objs, -r(NR,NC)): predicts the next centroid in the
sequence by projecting the constant step (oq_const_step) one step beyond
the last centroid. Fails if the step is not consistent or Objs has < 2 elems.
Deterministic.

oq_zip_colors(+Objs1, +Objs2, -Pairs): Pairs is the list of C1-C2 terms
pairing the color of each obj in Objs1 with the corresponding obj in Objs2.
Both lists must have the same length. Useful for recording input-to-output
color mappings across a transformation.

Section 186.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 175. No cross-pack dependencies. Uses member/2, append/3, last/2,
sum_list/2 from library(lists); maplist/2, maplist/3 from library(apply);
built-ins findall/3, length/2, between/3.


Part 187: Object-Pair Change Analysis and Rule Application (objdelta Pack, WP 197)

Section 187.1: Purpose

The objdelta pack analyses pairs of obj(Color, Cells) terms (before/after)
to extract what changed: colour, centroid position, or cell count. It
extracts generalisable rules from a list of pairs (a colour map, a constant
displacement) and applies those rules to new objects. Pairs are represented
as O1-O2 terms, consistent with the link pack convention.

Section 187.2: Predicate Specifications

dp_color_delta(+O1, +O2, -C1-C2): C1 is O1's colour; C2 is O2's colour.
Deterministic. C1 and C2 may be equal (no change).

dp_pos_delta(+O1, +O2, -dr(DR,DC)): DR and DC are the centroid displacements
from O1 to O2 (floor-average). Deterministic.

dp_size_delta(+O1, +O2, -D): D = |Cells2| - |Cells1|. Negative means O2 is
smaller. Deterministic.

dp_same_color(+O1, +O2): succeeds if O1 and O2 share the same colour atom.

dp_same_form(+O1, +O2): succeeds if O1 and O2 have the same origin-normalised
cell list (colour ignored). Uses min-row/col translation and sort.

dp_same_pos(+O1, +O2): succeeds if O1 and O2 share the same floor-average
centroid.

dp_color_map(+Pairs, -Map): Map is the sorted distinct list of C1-C2 terms
extracted from the colour of each O1-O2 pair. Empty input yields empty Map.
Deterministic.

dp_apply_color(+C1-C2, +Obj, -Obj2): if Obj's colour equals C1, Obj2 is Obj
with colour C2. Fails otherwise. Preserves the cell list.

dp_apply_color_map(+Map, +Obj, -Obj2): applies the first matching C1-C2 entry
in Map to Obj. Fails if no entry matches. Deterministic (cut after first match).

dp_apply_map_all(+Map, +Objs, -Objs2): applies Map to each obj in Objs.
Objects whose colour is not in Map are left unchanged (no failure).
Deterministic.

dp_const_dr(+Pairs, -DR): DR is the common row centroid delta across all pairs.
Requires at least one pair. Fails if any delta differs.

dp_const_dc(+Pairs, -DC): DC is the common column centroid delta across all
pairs. Requires at least one pair. Fails if any delta differs.

dp_common_cells(+O1, +O2, -Cells): sorted list of r(R,C) positions present in
both O1 and O2 (set intersection). Colour is ignored.

dp_cell_diff(+O1, +O2, -Added, -Removed): Added = positions in O2 not in O1;
Removed = positions in O1 not in O2. Both are sorted. Colour is ignored.

Section 187.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 176. No cross-pack dependencies. Uses member/2, sum_list/2, min_list/2,
subtract/3, intersection/3 from library(lists); maplist/2, maplist/3 from
library(apply); built-ins findall/3, length/2, sort/2.


Part 188: Object Tiling and Multi-Copy Layout (objcopy Pack, WP 198)

Section 188.1: Purpose

The objcopy pack generates multiple copies of obj(Color, Cells) terms at
computed positions. It provides placing an obj at an explicit top-left
position, tiling in rows, columns, and grids, aligning and packing lists of
objs, spreading at fixed intervals, centering within a canvas, and reflecting
within an absolute-frame canvas width.

Section 188.2: Predicate Specifications

tc_place_at(+Obj, +R0, +C0, -Obj2): Obj2 is Obj translated so that its
bounding-box top-left corner is at (R0, C0). Deterministic.

tc_recolor_all(+Color, +Objs, -Objs2): every obj in Objs2 has Color with its
original cells preserved. Deterministic.

tc_tile_row(+Obj, +N, +Step, -Objs): N copies of Obj. Copy I (0-indexed) has
its top-left column = MinCol + I*Step. Row is unchanged. Step may be smaller
than the bbox width (overlapping copies). Deterministic.

tc_tile_col(+Obj, +N, +Step, -Objs): N copies of Obj. Copy I has top-left row
= MinRow + I*Step. Col is unchanged. Deterministic.

tc_tile_grid(+Obj, +NR, +NC, +StepR, +StepC, -Objs): NR*NC copies. Copy
(I,J) has top-left row = MinRow + I*StepR, col = MinCol + J*StepC. Row-major
order (J inner loop). Deterministic.

tc_at_positions(+Obj, +Positions, -Objs): one copy of Obj per r(R,C) in
Positions, placed by top-left. Deterministic.

tc_align_top(+Objs, -Objs2): all objects shifted so their minimum row equals
the global minimum row across all objects. Deterministic.

tc_align_left(+Objs, -Objs2): all objects shifted so their minimum col equals
the global minimum col across all objects. Deterministic.

tc_pack_row(+Objs, +R, +C0, +Gap, -Objs2): objects placed consecutively in a
horizontal row at row R, starting at column C0. Each successive object begins
at the previous object's max-col + 1 + Gap. Deterministic.

tc_pack_col(+Objs, +C, +R0, +Gap, -Objs2): objects placed consecutively in a
vertical column at col C, starting at row R0. Each successive object begins at
the previous object's max-row + 1 + Gap. Deterministic.

tc_spread_h(+Objs, +C0, +Step, -Objs2): Obj I (0-indexed) has its minimum col
set to C0 + I*Step. Rows are preserved from the original objects. Deterministic.

tc_spread_v(+Objs, +R0, +Step, -Objs2): Obj I (0-indexed) has its minimum row
set to R0 + I*Step. Cols are preserved from the original objects. Deterministic.

tc_center(+Obj, +H, +W, -Obj2): Obj2 is Obj placed so that its bounding box
is centered within an H x W canvas. Offsets use floor integer division:
R0 = (H - BH) // 2, C0 = (W - BW) // 2. Deterministic.

tc_flip_h(+Obj, +W, -Obj2): each cell r(R,C) maps to r(R, W-1-C). This is
an absolute-frame horizontal reflection within a canvas of width W (unlike
bounding-box-local reflections). Deterministic.

Section 188.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 177. No cross-pack dependencies. Uses member/2, min_list/2, max_list/2,
nth0/3 from library(lists); maplist/2, maplist/3 from library(apply);
built-ins findall/3, between/3, length/2.

Part 189: Object-List Correspondence and Matching (objmatch Pack, WP 199)

Section 189.1: Purpose

The objmatch pack (mx_* prefix, Layer 178) finds correspondences between two
obj(Color, Cells) term lists. It supports matching by color identity, by cell
count (size), by normalized form (shape), and by nearest centroid (greedy). It
provides unmatched-object extraction, change-type filtering on pairs, per-pair
delta computation (color, position, size), and global uniformity tests on
those deltas. A positional zip predicate rounds out the set.

Section 189.2: Predicate Specifications

mx_by_color(+List1, +List2, -Pairs): each Obj1 in List1 is paired with every
Obj2 in List2 that shares the same color. Result is a list of O1-O2 pairs.
Multiple matches per object are included. Deterministic (findall).

mx_by_size(+List1, +List2, -Pairs): each Obj1 in List1 is paired with every
Obj2 in List2 whose cell count equals Obj1's cell count. Deterministic.

mx_by_form(+List1, +List2, -Pairs): each Obj1 in List1 is paired with every
Obj2 in List2 whose normalized shape equals Obj1's normalized shape. The
normalized shape is the set of cells translated so the bounding box top-left
is at r(0,0), then sorted. Color is ignored. Deterministic.

mx_by_nearest(+List1, +List2, -Pairs): greedy nearest-centroid matching.
Processes Obj1 items in order. Each Obj1 claims the nearest remaining Obj2
by squared Euclidean centroid distance. If List2 runs out, remaining Obj1
items are silently skipped. Deterministic.

mx_unmatched(+Pairs, +List1, +List2, -Unmatched1, -Unmatched2): given a
correspondence Pairs, returns the Obj1 items in List1 not appearing as the
first element of any pair (Unmatched1), and the Obj2 items in List2 not
appearing as the second element of any pair (Unmatched2). Uses subtract/3.
Deterministic.

mx_filter_changed_color(+Pairs, -Changed): keeps only O1-O2 pairs where the
color of O1 differs from the color of O2. Deterministic.

mx_filter_same_color(+Pairs, -Same): keeps only O1-O2 pairs where the color
of O1 equals the color of O2. Deterministic.

mx_color_deltas(+Pairs, -Deltas): maps each O1-O2 pair to a c1-c2 term where
c1 is O1's color and c2 is O2's color. Deterministic.

mx_pos_deltas(+Pairs, -Deltas): maps each O1-O2 pair to a dr(DR,DC) term
where DR = centroid_row(O2) - centroid_row(O1) and DC = centroid_col(O2) -
centroid_col(O1). Centroid uses floor integer division. Deterministic.

mx_size_deltas(+Pairs, -Deltas): maps each O1-O2 pair to an integer N2-N1
where N1 and N2 are the cell counts of O1 and O2. Deterministic.

mx_all_same_color_delta(+Pairs): succeeds iff all O1-O2 pairs share the same
c1-c2 color change. Succeeds trivially on the empty list. Deterministic.

mx_all_same_pos_delta(+Pairs): succeeds iff all O1-O2 pairs share the same
dr(DR,DC) positional delta. Succeeds trivially on the empty list. Deterministic.

mx_all_same_size_delta(+Pairs): succeeds iff all O1-O2 pairs share the same
integer size delta. Succeeds trivially on the empty list. Deterministic.

mx_zip(+List1, +List2, -Pairs): positional pairing — element I of List1 is
paired with element I of List2. Lists must have equal length or the predicate
fails. Deterministic.

Section 189.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 178. No cross-pack dependencies. Uses member/2, subtract/3, nth0/3
from library(lists); maplist/2, maplist/3 from library(apply); built-ins
findall/3, length/2, min_list/2, sum_list/2, msort/2.

Part 190: Object Merging, Set Operations, and Component Splitting (objmerge Pack, WP 200)

Section 190.1: Purpose

The objmerge pack (mg_* prefix, Layer 179) provides cell-set operations on
obj(Color, Cells) terms: union, intersection, difference, and symmetric
difference; horizontal and vertical concatenation; list-level union and
subtraction; bounding-box fill and hollow-frame generation; cell padding; and
splitting into 4-connected or 8-connected components.

Section 190.2: Predicate Specifications

mg_union_cells(+O1, +O2, +Color, -Merged): sorted union of O1's and O2's cell
sets, recolored to Color. Deterministic.

mg_intersect_cells(+O1, +O2, +Color, -Result): sorted intersection of O1's and
O2's cell sets, recolored to Color. Deterministic.

mg_diff_cells(+O1, +O2, +Color, -Result): cells in O1's set but not O2's set,
recolored to Color. Deterministic.

mg_sym_diff_cells(+O1, +O2, +Color, -Result): symmetric difference: cells in
exactly one of the two sets, recolored to Color. Deterministic.

mg_concat_h(+O1, +O2, +Gap, -Merged): O2 is translated so its left (minimum-col)
edge is placed at O1's right (maximum-col) edge + 1 + Gap. All cells from both
objects are combined. Merged uses O1's color. Deterministic.

mg_concat_v(+O1, +O2, +Gap, -Merged): O2 is translated so its top (minimum-row)
edge is placed at O1's bottom (maximum-row) edge + 1 + Gap. All cells from both
objects are combined. Merged uses O1's color. Deterministic.

mg_merge_list(+Objs, +Color, -Merged): sorted union of all cells from all objs
in the list, recolored to Color. Deterministic.

mg_subtract_list(+Base, +RemoveList, +Color, -Result): remove all cells of any
obj in RemoveList from Base's cell set, recolored to Color. Deterministic.

mg_expand_bbox(+Obj, -Expanded): fill the bounding box of Obj with Obj's color.
Expanded contains all r(R,C) where MinR <= R <= MaxR and MinC <= C <= MaxC.
Deterministic.

mg_hollow_bbox(+Obj, -Hollow): replace Obj with only the 1-cell-wide outer frame
of its bounding box. Frame cells are those on the top row, bottom row, leftmost
column, or rightmost column of the bbox. Result is sorted to eliminate
duplicates at corners. Deterministic.

mg_pad(+Obj, +P, +Color, -Padded): generate all cells in the expanded bbox
(MinR-P, MinC-P) to (MaxR+P, MaxC+P), colored Color. Includes the original
cells and P layers of border. Deterministic.

mg_split_cc4(+Obj, -Parts): split Obj into a list of 4-connected component
obj terms, each with Obj's color. Uses BFS flood-fill. Non-deterministic in
order but deterministic in the set of components.

mg_split_cc8(+Obj, -Parts): split Obj into a list of 8-connected component
obj terms. Same structure as mg_split_cc4 but with 8-adjacency neighbors.

mg_n_components4(+Obj, -N): count of 4-connected components. Calls
mg_split_cc4 and takes the length of the result. Deterministic.

Section 190.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 179. No cross-pack dependencies. Uses member/2, subtract/3,
intersection/3, union/3, append/3 from library(lists); maplist/2, maplist/3
from library(apply); built-ins findall/3, between/3, length/2, sort/2,
min_list/2, max_list/2.

Part 191: Object-List Aggregate Attribute Analysis (objattr Pack, WP 201)

Section 191.1: Purpose

The objattr pack (oa_* prefix, Layer 180) computes aggregate statistics and
rankings over a list of obj(Color, Cells) terms. It provides total cell count,
per-color object counts, per-color cell totals, distinct color count, dominant
and rarest colors, unique color detection, size ranking, position ranking,
majority size, and three uniformity tests.

This pack complements the objfilter pack (which selects objects by predicate).
The objattr pack aggregates properties across the full list.

Section 191.2: Predicate Specifications

oa_total_cells(+Objs, -N): sum of all cell counts across the list. N=0 for [].
Deterministic.

oa_color_counts(+Objs, -Pairs): list of Color-Count pairs where Count is the
number of objects with that color. Sorted by color atom. Deterministic.

oa_cell_counts_by_color(+Objs, -Pairs): list of Color-Total pairs where Total
is the sum of cell counts of all objects with that color. Sorted by color.
Deterministic.

oa_n_colors(+Objs, -N): number of distinct color atoms across the list.
N=0 for []. Deterministic.

oa_n_objs_of_color(+Objs, +Color, -N): count of objects with exactly Color.
Deterministic.

oa_dominant_color(+Objs, -Color): color with the most total cells. If tied,
the color that appears first in the sorted result is returned. Fails on [].
Deterministic.

oa_rarest_color(+Objs, -Color): color with the fewest total cells. If tied,
the first in sorted order is returned. Fails on []. Deterministic.

oa_unique_color(+Objs, -Color): color that appears in exactly one object.
Backtracks over all such colors. Fails if none exists. Semi-deterministic.

oa_size_rank(+Objs, -Ranked): objects sorted by cell count descending (largest
first). Equal-sized objects retain their relative order (msort stability).
Deterministic.

oa_pos_rank(+Objs, -Ranked): objects sorted by top-left bounding-box position
in row-major order ascending (top-left first). Uses r(MinR,MinC) as sort key
via msort. Deterministic.

oa_majority_size(+Objs, -N): most frequently occurring cell count. Uses
run-length encoding of the msorted size list. Fails on []. Deterministic.

oa_all_same_color(+Objs): true iff all objects share the same color. Trivially
true on []. Deterministic.

oa_all_same_size(+Objs): true iff all objects have the same cell count.
Trivially true on []. Deterministic.

oa_all_same_form(+Objs): true iff all objects share the same normalized shape
(cells translated to origin, sorted). Trivially true on []. Deterministic.

Section 191.3: Layer Assignment

Layer 180. No cross-pack dependencies. Uses member/2 from library(lists);
maplist/2, maplist/3 from library(apply); built-ins findall/3, length/2,
sum_list/2, min_list/2, msort/2, sort/2.

Part 192: Object-List Grouping by Shared Attribute (objgroup Pack, WP 202)

The objgroup pack (og_* prefix, Layer 181) partitions a list of obj(Color, Cells)
terms into groups that share a common attribute value. It fills the gap between
objfilter (which selects objects individually) and objattr (which aggregates over
all objects): objgroup organizes objects into named bins for downstream reasoning.

A group is represented as a Key-ObjList pair where Key is the shared attribute
value and ObjList contains all objects with that value, in their original input
order.

Grouping operations:

og_by_color(+Objs, -Groups): partition by color atom. Groups are sorted by Color.

og_by_size(+Objs, -Groups): partition by cell count. Groups are sorted by Size
ascending.

og_by_form(+Objs, -Groups): partition by normalized shape. Normalization translates
each object so its top-left cell is at r(0,0), then sorts the cell list. Two objects
fall in the same group iff their normalized cell lists are identical.

og_by_row(+Objs, -Groups): partition by the row of the top-left cell, sorted
ascending.

og_by_col(+Objs, -Groups): partition by the column of the top-left cell, sorted
ascending.

Group inspection operations:

og_n_groups(+Groups, -N): number of groups in the list.

og_n_members(+Groups, +N, -Selected): filter groups to those with exactly N members.

og_singletons(+Groups, -Singletons): specialization of og_n_members for N=1.

og_largest(+Groups, -Group): the group with the most members; alphabetical tiebreak.

og_smallest(+Groups, -Group): the group with the fewest members; alphabetical
tiebreak.

og_all_same_size(+Groups): true iff all groups have the same member count.

og_sort_desc(+Groups, -Sorted): sort groups by member count descending.

og_flat(+Groups, -Objs): flatten all groups into a single list of obj terms,
preserving group order.

og_filter_size(+Groups, +Min, +Max, -Filtered): keep groups with member count
in Min..Max inclusive.

All predicates handle empty input without error. Grouping predicates return an
empty list for empty input. Uniformity predicates succeed vacuously for empty
input. The pack has no cross-pack dependencies.

Part 193: Scene-Level Comparison of Two Object Lists (scenecmp Pack, WP 203)

The scenecmp pack (sm_* prefix, Layer 182) compares two lists of obj(Color, Cells)
terms (a Before scene and an After scene) at the scene level. It answers questions
about what changed between two states without requiring an explicit object-to-object
matching: does the count change, do new colors appear, do new shapes appear?

The pack complements diff (which operates at the grid cell level) and objmatch
(which finds individual object correspondences). The scenecmp pack operates at the
inventory level: comparing color sets, form sets, and object counts.

Introspection predicates (single scene):

sm_n_objs(+Objs, -N): number of objects. Delegates to length/2.

sm_total_cells(+Objs, -N): sum of all cell counts.

sm_colors(+Objs, -Colors): sorted list of distinct colors.

sm_forms(+Objs, -Forms): sorted list of distinct normalized shapes. Normalization
translates each object to the origin and sorts its cell list.

Symmetric comparison predicates (Before vs After):

sm_same_n_objs(+Before, +After): both lists have the same object count.

sm_same_total_cells(+Before, +After): both lists have the same total cell count.

sm_same_colors(+Before, +After): both lists have exactly the same color set.

sm_same_forms(+Before, +After): both lists have exactly the same form set.

Asymmetric comparison predicates:

sm_added_colors(+Before, +After, -Added): colors in After not present in Before.

sm_removed_colors(+Before, +After, -Removed): colors in Before not present in After.

sm_added_forms(+Before, +After, -Added): forms in After not present in Before.

sm_removed_forms(+Before, +After, -Removed): forms in Before not present in After.

sm_n_color_change(+Before, +After, -N): |added colors| + |removed colors|. Zero
means same palette; positive means the palette changed.

sm_any_change(+Before, +After): true iff the object count, color set, or form set
differs. Fails (does not raise an error) when no difference is detected.

All predicates handle empty lists without error. No cross-pack dependencies.

Part 194: Object-List Spatial and Attribute Query Against a Reference (objlocate Pack, WP 204)

The objlocate pack (lq_* prefix, Layer 183) queries a list of obj(Color, Cells) terms
for those satisfying a spatial or attribute relationship to a given reference object.
It applies pairwise relationship tests across a list to produce filtered subsets.

lq_above(+Objs, +Ref, -Found): objects with centroid row strictly less than Ref's.
lq_below(+Objs, +Ref, -Found): objects with centroid row strictly greater than Ref's.
lq_left_of(+Objs, +Ref, -Found): objects with centroid col strictly less than Ref's.
lq_right_of(+Objs, +Ref, -Found): objects with centroid col strictly greater than Ref's.

lq_touching4(+Objs, +Ref, -Found): objects 4-adjacent to Ref. An object is 4-adjacent
if it has a cell at Manhattan distance 1 from any Ref cell and does not overlap Ref.

lq_touching8(+Objs, +Ref, -Found): objects 8-adjacent to Ref. An object is 8-adjacent
if it has a cell at Chebyshev distance 1 from any Ref cell and does not overlap Ref.

lq_overlapping(+Objs, +Ref, -Found): objects sharing at least one cell with Ref.

lq_same_color(+Objs, +Ref, -Found): objects with the same color atom as Ref.

lq_same_form(+Objs, +Ref, -Found): objects with the same normalized shape as Ref.
Normalization translates to the origin and sorts the cell list.

lq_aligned_h(+Objs, +Ref, -Found): objects whose top-left row equals Ref's top-left row.
lq_aligned_v(+Objs, +Ref, -Found): objects whose top-left col equals Ref's top-left col.

lq_nearest(+Objs, +Ref, -Nearest): the single object in Objs with the smallest squared
centroid distance to Ref. Uses msort on D-Obj pairs; first element wins on ties.

lq_farthest(+Objs, +Ref, -Farthest): the single object with the largest squared centroid
distance to Ref.

lq_n_touching4(+Objs, +Ref, -N): count of 4-touching objects.

Centroid computation uses floating-point division of sum-of-coordinates by cell count.
Squared Euclidean distance is used throughout (avoids sqrt, purely integer arithmetic).
All predicates handle empty Objs list without error (returning [] or 0). No cross-pack
dependencies.

Part 195: Scene-Level Uniform Transformation of All Objects (scenexf Pack, WP 205)

Layer 184. Pack prefix: sx_*. Directory: packs/scenexf/.

The scenexf pack applies uniform transformations to every object in a scene
(a list of obj(Color, Cells) terms). Where objxf (ox_*) transforms a single
object, scenexf applies the same operation to the entire list at once.

Exported predicates (14):

sx_recolor(+Scene, +OldColor, +NewColor, -Scene2): replace every object whose
color atom equals OldColor with NewColor. Objects of other colors are unchanged.

sx_recolor_all(+Scene, +NewColor, -Scene2): set every object in Scene to
NewColor, regardless of its current color.

sx_apply_color_map(+Scene, +Map, -Scene2): apply a list of OldColor-NewColor
pairs to the scene. Each object is recolored to NewColor if its color matches
any OldColor in Map; if no pair matches, the object is unchanged.

sx_shift(+Scene, +DR, +DC, -Scene2): translate every object by DR rows and DC
columns. Each cell r(R,C) becomes r(R+DR, C+DC).

sx_to_origin(+Scene, -Scene2): translate the scene so the bounding box
top-left corner is at r(0,0). Computes the scene-wide minimum row and column,
then subtracts them from every cell.

sx_reflect_h(+Scene, +Width, -Scene2): reflect all objects horizontally within
a canvas of the given Width. Each cell r(R,C) becomes r(R, Width-1-C).

sx_reflect_v(+Scene, +Height, -Scene2): reflect all objects vertically within
a canvas of the given Height. Each cell r(R,C) becomes r(Height-1-R, C).

sx_remove_color(+Scene, +Color, -Scene2): remove all objects whose color atom
equals Color. All other objects are retained in order.

sx_keep_color(+Scene, +Color, -Scene2): keep only objects whose color atom
equals Color. All others are discarded.

sx_sort_size_desc(+Scene, -Sorted): sort scene objects by cell count descending.
Uses negated-count key with msort to preserve duplicate ordering.

sx_sort_size_asc(+Scene, -Sorted): sort scene objects by cell count ascending.

sx_sort_pos(+Scene, -Sorted): sort scene objects by top-left position in
row-major order (primary key: min row; secondary: min col).

sx_top_n(+Scene, +N, -TopN): the N largest objects by cell count. If N exceeds
the scene size, all objects are returned sorted by size descending.

sx_dedup_form(+Scene, -Deduped): remove objects with duplicate normalized forms.
The first object of each distinct form is kept. Normalization translates each
object to the origin and sorts its cell list.

No cross-pack dependencies. Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Part 196: Scene-Level Transformation Rule Inference from Object-List Pairs (ruleinfer Pack, WP 206)

Layer 185. Pack prefix: ri_*. Directory: packs/ruleinfer/.

The ruleinfer pack infers which scene-level transformation was applied to a
Before scene to produce an After scene. Inference predicates examine one
Before-After pair; consistency predicates verify a hypothesized rule across
multiple pairs. Pairs are expressed as Before-After terms.

Exported predicates (14):
