ri_infer_recolor(+Before, +After, -Old, -New): infer a single-color substitution.
Old is the color present in Before but absent from After; New is the color
present in After but absent from Before. Succeeds only when exactly one color
changed. Verifies that the count of Old-colored objects in Before equals the
count of New-colored objects in After.

ri_infer_recolor_all(+Before, +After, -New): infer that all objects were set to
the same new color New. Succeeds when the After scene has exactly one distinct
color.

ri_infer_color_map(+Before, +After, -Map): infer a full color substitution map
by comparing position-matched objects. Requires Before and After to have the
same length. Returns Old-New pairs for each position where the color changed.

ri_infer_keep_color(+Before, +After, -Color): infer that a keep_color filter was
applied. After contains only Color objects; After has fewer objects than Before.

ri_infer_remove_color(+Before, +After, -Color): infer that Color was removed.
Color is the single color present in Before but absent from After.

ri_infer_shift(+Before, +After, -DR, -DC): infer a uniform spatial shift. Uses
the first object in Before to compute a candidate DR-DC, then verifies the
entire scene matches when shifted by that amount.

ri_infer_to_origin(+Before, +After): succeed if After equals Before shifted so
the scene bounding box top-left is at r(0,0).

ri_consistent_recolor(+Old, +New, +Pairs): verify that applying recolor(Old, New)
to each Before scene produces the corresponding After scene.

ri_consistent_color_map(+Map, +Pairs): verify that applying the color map to each
Before scene produces the corresponding After scene.

ri_consistent_keep_color(+Color, +Pairs): verify that keeping only Color objects
from each Before scene produces the corresponding After scene.

ri_consistent_remove_color(+Color, +Pairs): verify that removing all Color objects
from each Before scene produces the corresponding After scene.

ri_consistent_shift(+DR, +DC, +Pairs): verify that shifting each Before scene by
(DR, DC) produces the corresponding After scene.

ri_all_same_n_objs(+Pairs): succeed if every pair preserves the object count.

ri_all_same_colors(+Pairs): succeed if every pair preserves the set of distinct
colors.

No cross-pack dependencies. Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Part 197: Scene-Level Rule Term Evaluation Engine (sceneapply Pack, WP 207)

Layer 186. Pack prefix: sa_*. Directory: packs/sceneapply/.

The sceneapply pack applies symbolic rule terms to obj(Color, Cells) scene lists.
It is the evaluation complement to the ruleinfer pack (ri_*): where ruleinfer
infers a rule from examples, sceneapply executes that rule on a scene.

Rule terms and their meanings:

recolor(Old, New): replace all objects of color Old with color New.
recolor_all(New): set all objects to color New.
color_map(Map): apply Old-New color substitution pairs.
shift(DR, DC): translate all objects by (DR, DC).
to_origin: shift scene so bounding box top-left is at r(0,0).
reflect_h(Width): flip all objects horizontally within Width.
reflect_v(Height): flip all objects vertically within Height.
remove_color(Color): discard all objects of Color.
keep_color(Color): keep only objects of Color.
sort_size_desc: sort by cell count descending.
sort_size_asc: sort by cell count ascending.
sort_pos: sort by top-left position row-major.
top_n(N): the N largest objects by cell count.
dedup_form: keep first object of each distinct normalized form.

Exported predicates (14):

sa_apply(+Rule, +Scene, -Scene2): apply one rule term.
sa_apply_seq(+Rules, +Scene, -Scene2): apply a sequence of rules.
sa_verify(+Rule, +Before, +After): rule transforms Before to After (msort).
sa_verify_seq(+Rules, +Before, +After): sequence transforms Before to After.
sa_verify_all(+Rule, +Pairs): rule works on all Before-After pairs.
sa_verify_seq_all(+Rules, +Pairs): sequence works on all pairs.
sa_rule_type(+Rule, -Type): classify as color|spatial|filter|order|dedup.
sa_is_color_rule(+Rule): rule type is color.
sa_is_spatial_rule(+Rule): rule type is spatial.
sa_is_filter_rule(+Rule): rule type is filter.
sa_colors_affected(+Rule, -Colors): color atoms referenced in rule.
sa_compose(+Rule1, +Rule2, -Seq): make two-step sequence [Rule1, Rule2].
sa_seq_len(+Seq, -N): number of steps in a rule sequence.
sa_rule_invertible(+Rule): trivially invertible (recolor, shift, reflect).

No cross-pack dependencies. Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Part 198: Conditional and Selective Scene Transformation (condxf Pack, WP 208)

Layer 187. Pack prefix: xc_*. Directory: packs/condxf/.

The condxf pack applies transformations to a subset of objects in an
obj(Color, Cells) scene list — those satisfying a condition — while leaving
the remaining objects unchanged. It complements the scenexf pack (sx_*), which
applies transformations uniformly to all objects in a scene.

Conditions supported: color match, size comparison (gt/lt/eq/ge/le), identity
(largest, smallest, unique-size), and existence of a unique-size object.

Exported predicates (14):

xc_split_color(+Scene, +Color, -Match, -NoMatch): partition scene into objects
of Color versus all others. Order within each partition is preserved.

xc_merge(+Group1, +Group2, -Scene2): concatenate two object groups into one
scene list (append).

xc_recolor_matching(+Scene, +MatchColor, +NewColor, -Scene2): recolor all
objects whose color is MatchColor to NewColor; other objects are unchanged.

xc_shift_color(+Scene, +Color, +DR, +DC, -Scene2): translate all objects of
Color by (DR, DC); other objects are unchanged.

xc_swap_colors(+Scene, +C1, +C2, -Scene2): swap colors C1 and C2 throughout
the scene; other colors are unchanged.

xc_recolor_by_size(+Scene, +N, +Cmp, +NewColor, -Scene2): recolor each object
whose cell count satisfies the comparison Cmp N (Cmp is gt, lt, eq, ge, or le)
to NewColor; other objects are unchanged.

xc_move_color(+Scene, +Color, +DR, +DC, -Scene2): alias for xc_shift_color.

xc_recolor_largest(+Scene, +NewColor, -Scene2): recolor the single largest
object (by cell count) to NewColor; other objects are unchanged.

xc_recolor_smallest(+Scene, +NewColor, -Scene2): recolor the single smallest
object (by cell count) to NewColor; other objects are unchanged.

xc_largest(+Scene, -Obj): the largest object by cell count. On ties, the object
that sorts first under standard term order is returned (deterministic).

xc_smallest(+Scene, -Obj): the smallest object by cell count. On ties, the object
that sorts first under standard term order is returned (deterministic).

xc_unique_size(+Scene, -Obj): backtrackable; succeeds for each object whose cell
count appears exactly once in the scene.

xc_recolor_unique_size(+Scene, +NewColor, -Scene2): recolor the unique-size
object to NewColor. Fails if no unique-size object exists.

xc_split_size(+Scene, +N, +Cmp, -Match, -NoMatch): partition scene into objects
satisfying size Cmp N (Match) and those not satisfying it (NoMatch).

No cross-pack dependencies. Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Part 199: Holistic Before-After Scene Pair Analysis (scenepair Pack, WP 209)

Layer 188. Pack prefix: ps_*. Directory: packs/scenepair/.

The scenepair pack analyzes a Before scene and an After scene (both lists of
obj(Color, Cells) terms) as a holistic pair. It computes scene-level observables
useful for transformation rule hypothesis ranking: object count change, color set
change, added/removed objects, color delta map, and Boolean detectors for common
transformation types (recolor, recolor-all, uniform shift, shift-to-origin,
size preservation).

Exported predicates (14):

ps_same_n_objs(+Before, +After): Before and After have the same number of objects.

ps_n_added(+Before, +After, -N): count of objects in After that have no
color-and-form match in Before.

ps_n_removed(+Before, +After, -N): count of objects in Before that have no
color-and-form match in After.

ps_added_objs(+Before, +After, -Added): list of objects in After with no match
in Before. Matching uses color atom equality and normalized form equality.

ps_removed_objs(+Before, +After, -Removed): list of objects in Before with no
match in After.

ps_color_set_before(+Before, -Colors): sorted list of distinct color atoms in
the Before scene.

ps_color_set_after(+After, -Colors): sorted list of distinct color atoms in the
After scene.

ps_same_color_set(+Before, +After): Before and After have the same distinct-color
set (sorted msort-based dedup comparison).

ps_color_delta(+Before, +After, -Delta): list of OldColor-NewColor pairs for
position-matched object pairs where the color changed. If lengths differ, Delta
is []. Duplicate pairs are suppressed.

ps_is_recolor(+Before, +After): exactly one color in Before was replaced by
exactly one other color in After (same length; one-element set differences).

ps_is_recolor_all(+Before, +After): all objects in After share a single color
(exactly one distinct color in After).

ps_is_shift(+Before, +After, -DR, -DC): all objects were translated uniformly by
(DR, DC). Uses the first object to derive the candidate shift, then verifies
across the full scene with msort. Deterministic (cuts after first match).

ps_is_to_origin(+Before, +After): After equals Before shifted so the scene
bounding box top-left is at r(0,0).

ps_size_preserved(+Before, +After): same length; each position-matched pair has
the same cell count.

No cross-pack dependencies. Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Part 200: Rule Hypothesis Ranking for obj(Color,Cells) Scene Lists (scenerank Pack, WP 210)

Layer 189. Pack prefix: rk_*. Directory: packs/scenerank/.

The scenerank pack ranks candidate symbolic rule terms by coverage and consistency
across a list of Before-After scene pair training examples. A pair is the term
Before-After where Before and After are obj(Color, Cells) scene lists.

The core concept is coverage: how many pairs does a given rule correctly
explain? A rule explains a pair if applying the rule to Before produces a
result that is order-insensitively equal to After (msort-based comparison).

Exported predicates (14):

rk_n_pairs(+Pairs, -N): number of pairs in the pair list.

rk_coverage_pairs(+Rule, +Pairs, -Covered): list of pairs the rule explains.

rk_coverage(+Rule, +Pairs, -N): count of pairs the rule correctly explains.

rk_consistent(+Rule, +Pairs): rule correctly transforms every pair (full coverage).

rk_inconsistent_pairs(+Rule, +Pairs, -Bad): pairs the rule does not explain.

rk_rule_score(+Rule, +Pairs, -N): alias for rk_coverage.

rk_rank_rules(+Rules, +Pairs, -Ranked): sort Rules by coverage descending.
Tied rules are ordered by standard term order. Returns a list of rule terms.

rk_rank_candidates(+Rules, +Pairs, -CovRulePairs): like rk_rank_rules but
returns Coverage-Rule pairs in descending coverage order.

rk_best_rule(+Rules, +Pairs, -Best): the rule with highest coverage. Fails
if Rules is empty.

rk_all_consistent(+Rules, +Pairs, -Consistent): rules fully consistent with
every pair.

rk_filter_min_coverage(+Rules, +Pairs, +MinN, -Filtered): keep rules with
coverage >= MinN.

rk_perfect_rules(+Rules, +Pairs, -Perfect): rules whose coverage equals the
total pair count.

rk_coverage_ratio(+Rule, +Pairs, -Num/Den): coverage as an integer fraction
Num/Den (Num = coverage, Den = total pairs).

rk_top_n_rules(+Rules, +Pairs, +N, -TopN): the top N rules as Coverage-Rule
pairs. If fewer than N candidates exist, returns all.

No cross-pack dependencies. Implements its own rule application engine (same
dispatch vocabulary as sceneapply but without importing it). Uses library(lists)
and library(apply).

Part 201: Color Substitution Table Learning and Application (colortable Pack, WP 211)

The colortable pack (ct_*, Layer 190) learns a complete color substitution
table from multiple Before-After scene pair training examples and applies it
to new scenes.

Predicates:

ct_infer_from_pair(+Before, +After, -Map): derive the color-to-color mapping
from one Before-After pair. Before and After are obj(Color,Cells) scene lists
of equal length. Matching is positional: the n-th Before object corresponds
to the n-th After object. Map is a list of From-To atom pairs (changed colors
only). Fails if the same source color maps to two different targets.

ct_consistent_map(+Map): succeed if no source color appears with two different
target colors in Map.

ct_merge_maps(+Map1, +Map2, -Merged): merge two color maps. Fails if a source
color maps to two different targets in the combined map.

ct_extend_map(+Base, +Extra, -Extended): alias for ct_merge_maps; extend Base
with new entries from Extra.

ct_learn_map(+Pairs, -Map, -Inconsistent): learn a color map from a list of
Before-After pairs. Map is the merged mapping from all consistent pairs.
Inconsistent is the list of pairs that conflicted with the accumulated map.

ct_mapped_color(+Map, +Color, -Mapped): look up Color in Map. Returns the
target color if found; otherwise returns Color unchanged (identity).

ct_apply_map(+Map, +Obj, -MappedObj): apply a color map to a single
obj(Color,Cells) term.

ct_apply_to_scene(+Map, +Scene, -MappedScene): apply a color map to every
object in a scene list.

ct_map_covers(+Map, +Scene): succeed if Map has an explicit entry for every
color appearing in Scene.

ct_complete_map(+Map, +Scene, -Complete): extend Map with identity entries
for any colors in Scene not already covered.

ct_invert_map(+Map, -Inverted): swap From and To in each entry. Fails if the
inversion is inconsistent.

ct_identity_map(+Colors, -Map): build a map where every color in Colors maps
to itself.

ct_restrict_map(+Map, +Colors, -Restricted): keep only map entries whose
source color appears in Colors.

ct_map_colors(+Map, -Colors): list all source (From) colors in the map.

No cross-pack dependencies. Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Part 202: End-to-End Scene Puzzle Solver (gridsolve Pack, WP 212)

The gridsolve pack (gs_*, Layer 191) integrates rule inference, candidate
ranking, and rule application into a single end-to-end scene puzzle solver.

Predicates:

gs_apply(+Rule, +Scene, -Result): apply a symbolic rule term to an
obj(Color,Cells) scene list. Same dispatch vocabulary as sceneapply:
recolor(Old,New), recolor_all(New), color_map(Map), shift(DR,DC), to_origin,
reflect_h(Width), reflect_v(Height), remove_color(Color), keep_color(Color),
sort_size_desc, sort_size_asc, top_n(N), identity.

gs_coverage(+Rule, +Pairs, -N): count how many Before-After pairs the rule
correctly explains (via msort comparison).

gs_consistent(+Rule, +Pairs): succeed if the rule correctly explains every pair.

gs_rank_rules(+Rules, +Pairs, -Ranked): sort rules by coverage descending.
Ties broken by standard Prolog term order.

gs_best_rule(+Rules, +Pairs, -Best): the rule with the highest coverage.
Fails if Rules is empty.

gs_consistent_rules(+Rules, +Pairs, -Consistent): the subset of Rules fully
consistent with every pair.

gs_valid_rules(+Rules, +Pairs, -Valid): the subset of Rules with coverage > 0.

gs_infer_candidates(+Pairs, -Candidates): infer specific candidate rule terms
from training pairs by pattern matching. Tries recolor, recolor_all, shift,
to_origin, color_map.

gs_default_candidates(-Candidates): a standard broad set of candidate rule
terms for blind enumeration search. Covers common recolor, shift, spatial,
filter, and ordering rules.

gs_solve(+Pairs, +TestInput, -Output): full end-to-end solve. Infer specific
candidates, union with defaults, rank, apply the best rule to TestInput.

gs_solve_n(+Pairs, +N, -TopRules, -BestRule): return the top N rules as
Coverage-Rule pairs and identify the best rule.

gs_explain(+Pairs, -BestRule, -Coverage): return the best rule and its
coverage for the given training pairs.

gs_all_same_output(+Rule, +TestInputs, -Outputs): apply Rule to each test
input, returning the list of results.

gs_n_pairs(+Pairs, -N): count training pairs.

No cross-pack dependencies. Implements its own rule application engine.
Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Part 203: Systematic Generation of Scene Transformation Rule Candidates (transformgen Pack, WP 213)

The transformgen pack (tg_*, Layer 192) systematically generates sets of
candidate rule terms from scene data or training pairs.

Predicates:

tg_scene_colors(+Scene, -Colors): all distinct color atoms in the scene,
sorted.

tg_recolor_candidates(+Scene, -Candidates): all recolor(Old,New) rules
for distinct color pairs in the scene.

tg_recolor_all_candidates(+Scene, -Candidates): all recolor_all(C) rules,
one per color in the scene.

tg_remove_candidates(+Scene, -Candidates): all remove_color(C) rules, one
per color.

tg_keep_candidates(+Scene, -Candidates): all keep_color(C) rules, one per
color.

tg_shift_candidates(+MaxDR, +MaxDC, -Candidates): all shift(DR,DC) rules
with |DR| =< MaxDR and |DC| =< MaxDC, excluding (0,0).

tg_reflect_candidates(+GridH, +GridW, -Candidates): reflect_h and reflect_v
for the given grid dimensions.

tg_top_candidates(+MaxN, +Scene, -Candidates): all top_n(K) rules for K in
1..min(MaxN, |Scene|).

tg_color_map_candidate(+Before, +After, -Rule): derive a color_map rule from
one Before-After pair (positional matching). Fails if no colors change.

tg_from_scenes(+Before, +After, -Candidates): generate all rule candidates
specific to a single Before-After pair (recolor, recolor_all, remove, keep,
color_map, shift, sorting, identity).

tg_from_pairs(+Pairs, -Candidates): generate candidates from a list of
Before-After training pairs. Unions candidates from each pair.

tg_filter_consistent(+Rules, +Pairs, -Consistent): filter to rules fully
consistent with every training pair.

tg_n_candidates(+Candidates, -N): count candidates.

tg_all_scene_candidates(+Scene, +MaxShift, -Candidates): all candidates
from a single scene with given shift bound.

tg_color_map_candidate/3 and tg_filter_consistent/3 are the main building
blocks for targeted search. No cross-pack dependencies.
Uses library(lists) and library(apply).

Part 204: Multi-Color Scene Analysis (multicolor Pack, WP 214)

The multicolor pack (mc_*, Layer 193) queries and partitions obj(Color,Cells)
scenes by color frequency and membership.

Predicates:

mc_color_counts(+Scene, -Counts): sorted Color-N pairs, one per distinct color.

mc_count_of_color(+Scene, +Color, -N): object count for a given color. N=0
if Color not present.

mc_color_present(+Scene, +Color): succeed if Color appears at least once.

mc_dominant_color(+Scene, -Color): color with the most objects. Ties broken
by standard term order.

mc_rarest_color(+Scene, -Color): color with the fewest objects. Ties broken
by standard term order.

mc_singleton_colors(+Scene, -Colors): all colors that appear in exactly one
object.

mc_unique_color(+Scene, -Color): backtrackable; each color with count 1.

mc_color_freq_rank(+Scene, +N, -Color): the Nth most frequent color (1-based).

mc_color_partition(+Scene, -Groups): Color-Objs pairs, one per distinct color.

mc_pair_colors(+Scene, -Pairs): all unordered color pairs as C1-C2 (C1 @< C2).

mc_equal_count_pairs(+Scene, -Pairs): pairs of colors with equal object count.

mc_majority_color(+Scene, -Color): color whose count exceeds half the scene
size. Fails if none exists.

mc_n_distinct_colors(+Scene, -N): number of distinct colors.

mc_color_index(+Scene, +Color, -Index): 1-based rank of Color by descending
frequency.

No cross-pack dependencies. Uses library(lists) and library(apply).


Part 205: sceneinv Pack - Scene Invariant Detection across Training Pairs (si_*, Layer 194)

WP-215-SPEC-001: The sceneinv pack exposes 14 si_* predicates that analyse lists
of Before-After pairs to find structural properties that hold across all training
examples. A pair is represented as Before-After where both sides are lists of
obj(Color, Cells) terms. The predicates cover three invariant families: object-count
invariants (si_n_before, si_n_after, si_all_n_before, si_all_n_after,
si_const_n_before, si_const_n_after, si_n_preserved), color-set invariants
(si_colors_before, si_colors_after, si_const_colors_before, si_const_colors_after,
si_colors_preserved), and cell-count invariants (si_total_cells_before,
si_cells_preserved).

WP-215-SPEC-002: si_const_n_before/2 and si_const_n_after/2 use list_to_set/2 to
reduce the collected count list to its unique values; a single-element set proves
constancy. Both fail on empty Pairs. si_n_preserved/1 uses maplist over a helper
that unifies the Before and After lengths to the same variable.

WP-215-SPEC-003: si_const_colors_before/2 and si_const_colors_after/2 apply
sort/2 within each call to si_colors_before/si_colors_after so that comparison is
order-independent. list_to_set on a list of sorted lists succeeds when all scenes
share the same sorted color atom list.

WP-215-SPEC-004: si_cells_preserved/1 computes the total cell count for Before
and After separately in each pair and requires them to be equal. It uses
sum_list/2 from library(lists). It succeeds vacuously for an empty Pairs list.


Part 206: seqinfer Pack - Sequential Rule Inference for Multi-Step Scene Transformations (sq_*, Layer 195)

WP-216-SPEC-001: The seqinfer pack exposes 14 sq_* predicates that search for
ordered rule sequences that, when applied left-to-right, transform every Before
scene into its corresponding After scene across all training pairs. Pairs are
Before-After terms. The pack extends single-rule solvers by enabling 2-step and
3-step rule compositions to be discovered automatically from candidate rule lists.

WP-216-SPEC-002: sq_apply/3 takes a flat list of rule terms and applies them in
order. Supported base rules: identity, recolor(C1,C2), recolor_all(C), shift(DR,DC),
to_origin, reflect_h, reflect_v, remove_color(C), keep_color(C), sort_size_desc,
sort_size_asc, top_n(N), color_map(Map). The dispatch engine is self-contained
with no cross-pack imports.

WP-216-SPEC-003: sq_infer_2step/3 enumerates all ordered pairs (R1, R2) from the
candidate list, computes coverage for [R1, R2] on all pairs, and returns the pair
with the highest coverage. sq_infer_3step/3 does the same for triples. Both fail
if no candidate combination has positive coverage.

WP-216-SPEC-004: sq_verify/3 applies the rule sequence and compares the result to
After using msort-based equality (order-independent). sq_consistent/2 uses maplist
over sq_verify_pair_/2. sq_coverage/3 uses include/3 to count matching pairs.


Part 207: gridquery Pack - Grid Query and Manipulation (gq_*, Layer 196)

WP-217-SPEC-001: The gridquery pack exposes 14 gq_* predicates for querying and
transforming raw grid format (list-of-lists of color atoms) without converting to
obj(Color, Cells) terms. Positions are 0-indexed (R=row from top, C=column from
left). Predicates: gq_size, gq_at, gq_row, gq_col, gq_colors, gq_n_cells,
gq_most_freq_color, gq_region, gq_diff, gq_n_diff, gq_same_size, gq_transpose,
gq_replace, gq_fill_region.

WP-217-SPEC-002: gq_region/6 takes inclusive bounds (R0,C0)-(R1,C1) and returns
the rectangular sub-grid. It enumerates row indices with numlist, then slices each
row to the column range. gq_diff/3 collects all r(R,C) positions where two same-size
grids have different values. gq_n_diff/3 is the length of that list.

WP-217-SPEC-003: gq_transpose/2 is implemented using gq_col/3: for each column
index 0..W-1, it extracts that column from the grid. This produces a single
deterministic result with no choicepoints.

WP-217-SPEC-004: gq_replace/5 rebuilds the grid row-by-row; only the target row
is modified, and only the target cell within it. gq_fill_region/7 rebuilds similarly
but fills every cell in the rectangular range with the given color.


Part 208: gridparse Pack - Grid Parse and Object Extraction (gp_*, Layer 197)

WP-218-SPEC-001: The gridparse pack exposes 14 gp_* predicates for converting
between raw grid format and obj(Color, Cells) scene representation. A raw grid is
a list of rows, each a list of color atoms. An obj(Color, Cells) term represents
one connected region of a single color. Predicates: gp_bg_color, gp_grid_cells,
gp_color_components, gp_grid_to_scene, gp_scene_to_grid, gp_n_objects,
gp_object_colors, gp_largest_object, gp_smallest_object, gp_objects_by_size,
gp_grid_from_rows, gp_paint_obj, gp_paint_scene, gp_grid_equal.

WP-218-SPEC-002: gp_color_components uses a BFS flood fill. The algorithm starts
with the list of all Color cells (from gp_grid_cells), seeds from the first
unvisited cell, expands to 4-connected neighbors that remain in the Available set,
and returns the component when the queue empties. Remaining Available cells are
passed to the next iteration.

WP-218-SPEC-003: gp_grid_to_scene extracts non-background objects ordered by
color (sort order) and within each color by flood-fill discovery order.
gp_scene_to_grid creates a blank grid with gp_grid_from_rows then calls
gp_paint_scene. gp_paint_obj uses foldl over the cell list, replacing one cell
at a time with private row-replace helpers.

WP-218-SPEC-004: gp_grid_equal uses Prolog term unification (==); it succeeds iff
both grids are structurally identical. gp_bg_color uses the same keyed-msort
pattern as mc_dominant_color (negative count as sort key).


Part 209: gridtask Pack - Grid Task Solver: End-to-End Raw Grid Rule Inference (gt_*, Layer 198)

WP-219-SPEC-001: The gridtask pack exposes 14 gt_* predicates for inferring and
applying transformation rules directly to raw grid format (list-of-lists of color
atoms) without converting to obj(Color, Cells) scenes. Predicates: gt_diff_cells,
gt_n_changed, gt_unchanged_cells, gt_bg_color, gt_infer_color_map,
gt_test_color_map, gt_apply_color_map, gt_color_map_pairs, gt_is_color_sub,
gt_is_identity, gt_is_scale, gt_infer_shift, gt_pair_score, gt_solve.

WP-219-SPEC-002: gt_infer_color_map collects all positionally-aligned From-To
color pairs across every cell of a Before-After pair, deduplicates with
list_to_set, and fails if the same source color maps to two different target
colors. Identity pairs (V-V) are included so that partial recolorings (where only
some cells of a color change) are correctly detected as inconsistent.

WP-219-SPEC-003: gt_color_map_pairs extends gt_infer_color_map across a list of
training pairs using a single findall over all cells of all pairs. The result is
the globally consistent color substitution table; it fails if any source color maps
to two different targets across any pair of cells in the training set.

WP-219-SPEC-004: gt_solve tries four strategies in order: identity (Before == After
for all pairs), color_map (consistent color substitution), scale (integer upscaling,
N >= 2), shift (constant translation with background fill). The first strategy that
explains all training pairs is applied to the test grid. Falls back to identity if
no strategy succeeds.


Part 210: gridnbr Pack - Grid Neighbor Analysis: Cell Adjacency, Morphological Ops, and Neighbor Counts (gn_*, Layer 199)

WP-220-SPEC-001: The gridnbr pack exposes 14 gn_* predicates for analyzing
cell neighborhoods in raw grids (list-of-lists of color atoms) and applying
morphological operations. Predicates: gn_nbr4, gn_nbr8, gn_count4, gn_count8,
gn_count4_grid, gn_count8_grid, gn_any4, gn_all4, gn_mark_border,
gn_mark_isolated, gn_expand_color, gn_shrink_color, gn_majority_nbr4,
gn_conway_step.

WP-220-SPEC-002: gn_nbr4/4 collects the values at the 4-connected (cardinal)
neighbors of a cell at (R,C). gn_nbr8/4 collects values at all 8-connected
(cardinal and diagonal) neighbors. Out-of-bounds positions are omitted; neither
predicate pads with a background value. gn_count4/5 and gn_count8/5 count
occurrences of a given color in the neighbor list.

WP-220-SPEC-003: gn_count4_grid/3 and gn_count8_grid/3 build full grids where
each cell is the count of a specified Color among its 4- or 8-connected
neighbors. These outputs support counting-based ARC transformations.

WP-220-SPEC-004: gn_any4/4 uses memberchk/2 (deterministic) to test that at
least one 4-neighbor has a given color. gn_all4/4 succeeds iff the 4-neighbor
list is non-empty and every element equals Color. gn_mark_border/3 replaces
each non-background cell that has at least one background 4-neighbor with the
atom border. gn_mark_isolated/3 replaces each non-background cell with no
same-color 4-neighbor with the atom isolated.

WP-220-SPEC-005: gn_expand_color/3 implements morphological dilation: every
background cell with at least one Color 4-neighbor is set to Color. The
background is identified as the most frequent color using the keyed-msort
pattern. gn_shrink_color/3 implements morphological erosion: every Color cell
with at least one non-Color 4-neighbor is set to the background color.

WP-220-SPEC-006: gn_majority_nbr4/4 returns the most frequent color among
the 4-connected neighbors using the gn_majority_val_ helper (keyed-msort on
negative counts). Fails if the cell has no 4-neighbors. gn_conway_step/4
applies one step of a Conway-like rule: each Color cell with exactly N Color
4-neighbors is replaced by the background color. All other cells are unchanged.


PART 211 - WORK PACKAGE 221: griddist PACK (LAYER 200, gd_*)

WP-221-SPEC-001: The griddist pack (Layer 200) provides 14 predicates (gd_*
prefix) for computing spatial distances between cells in raw grid format and
for operations derived from those distances. It has no cross-pack dependencies
and uses only library(lists) and built-in predicates.

WP-221-SPEC-002: gd_manhattan/5 computes the Manhattan (L1) distance between
two grid positions as the sum of absolute row and column differences.
gd_chebyshev/5 computes the Chebyshev (L-infinity) distance as the maximum
of absolute row and column differences.

WP-221-SPEC-003: gd_dist_map/3 returns a raw grid (same dimensions as input)
where each cell holds the minimum Manhattan distance from that cell to the
nearest cell whose value equals Color. If Color is absent, all cells get
9999. gd_dist_map8/3 is the Chebyshev-distance variant.

WP-221-SPEC-004: gd_nearest_coord/5 returns the [R2,C2] coordinates of the
nearest Color cell from a given position, using Manhattan distance. Ties are
broken by standard term order. Fails if no Color cell exists.
gd_zone/4 replaces each non-Color cell within Manhattan distance N of any
Color cell with the atom zone; Color cells and far cells are unchanged.
gd_ring/5 returns all in-bounds [R,C] pairs at exactly Manhattan distance D
from a given position.

WP-221-SPEC-005: gd_voronoi/2 replaces each background cell with the color
of its nearest non-background cell (Manhattan distance). Background is the
most frequent color. Ties in distance and frequency are broken by standard
term order. If no foreground cells exist, the grid is unchanged.
gd_bfs_flood/5 computes BFS distances from a start cell treating a specified
Wall color as impassable. Unreachable and Wall cells receive 9999. Fails if
the start cell is a Wall.

WP-221-SPEC-006: gd_recolor_by_dist/4 recolors each Color cell at Manhattan
distance D from the nearest background cell to the D-th element of a
user-supplied Palette list (1-indexed). Color cells beyond the palette length
keep their original Color value. Non-Color cells are unchanged.
gd_expand_n/4 implements N-step morphological dilation: every cell within
Manhattan distance N of any Color cell is set to Color. N=0 is a no-op.
gd_shrink_n/4 implements N-step morphological erosion: every Color cell within
Manhattan distance N of the nearest background cell is replaced by background.
N=0 is a no-op.

WP-221-SPEC-007: gd_equidistant/4 marks each cell where the Manhattan distance
to ColorA equals the Manhattan distance to ColorB with the atom equidist.
ColorA and ColorB cells keep their original values.
gd_max_dist/4 returns the row and column of the cell that is farthest (maximum
Manhattan distance) from any Color cell, resolving ties by row-major order.
Fails if no Color cell exists (all distances are 9999).


PART 212 - WORK PACKAGE 222: gridperiod PACK (LAYER 201, gper_*)

WP-222-SPEC-001: The gridperiod pack (Layer 201) provides 14 predicates
(gper_* prefix) for detecting and exploiting periodic structure in raw grids.
It has no cross-pack dependencies and uses library(lists) and built-in
predicates only.

WP-222-SPEC-002: gper_is_row_periodic/2 succeeds if Grid[r] == Grid[r+P] for
every row pair separated by P. gper_is_col_periodic/2 succeeds if
Grid[r][c] == Grid[r][c+P] for every valid column pair separated by P. Both
are vacuously true when no such pairs exist.

WP-222-SPEC-003: gper_row_period/2 finds the smallest positive integer P for
which gper_is_row_periodic holds; guaranteed within 1..H. gper_col_period/2
finds the smallest P for which gper_is_col_periodic holds; guaranteed within
1..W. gper_tile_dims/3 returns (PH, PW) = (gper_row_period, gper_col_period).

WP-222-SPEC-004: gper_extract_tile/4 returns the top-left TH x TW sub-grid.
gper_tile_grid/4 creates a H x W grid using wrap-around indexing:
Grid[r][c] = Tile[r mod TH][c mod TW].

WP-222-SPEC-005: gper_extend_rows/3 extends to TargetH rows using row mod H.
gper_extend_cols/3 extends to TargetW columns using col mod W.
gper_extend/4 extends to (TargetH, TargetW) in one pass, equivalent to
tiling the grid to the target dimensions.

WP-222-SPEC-006: gper_autocorr_row/3 computes the fraction (0.0 to 1.0) of
row pairs (r, r+P) where Grid[r] == Grid[r+P]; returns 1.0 when no pairs
exist. gper_autocorr_col/3 computes the analogous fraction for column pairs.

WP-222-SPEC-007: gper_shift_wrap_rows/3 returns a grid with rows shifted down
by N positions (wrapping): row R of result = row (R-N) mod H of Grid.
gper_shift_wrap_cols/3 shifts each row's columns right by N positions
(wrapping): column C of result = column (C-N) mod W of Grid.


PART 213 - WORK PACKAGE 223: gridscale PACK (LAYER 202, gsc_*)

WP-223-SPEC-001: The gridscale pack (Layer 202) provides 14 predicates
(gsc_* prefix) for integer block-pixel scaling of raw grids. It operates
on raw grid format (list of rows, each row a list of color atoms, 0-indexed).
"Block size N" partitions the grid into NxN pixel blocks; block (BR, BC)
covers raw rows BR*N..BR*N+N-1 and columns BC*N..BC*N+N-1.
No cross-pack dependencies. Uses library(lists) and library(apply) only.

WP-223-SPEC-002: gsc_upsample/3 scales Grid up by integer factor N: each
source cell becomes an NxN block of the same color in the output, which has
dimensions (H*N) x (W*N). N=1 is a no-op. Fails for N < 1.
gsc_downsample/3 scales Grid down by N: each NxN block must be uniform
(all cells the same color); that color becomes one cell in the output, which
has dimensions (H//N) x (W//N). Fails if any block is not uniform.

WP-223-SPEC-003: gsc_block_majority/3 downsample by N using majority vote per
NxN block (most frequent color, ties broken by term order). Never fails.
gsc_scale_factor/3 finds the integer N such that GridB = gsc_upsample(GridA, N);
requires H_B = H_A * N and W_B = W_A * N. Fails if no exact N exists.
gsc_is_scale_of/3 tests whether GridB = gsc_upsample(GridA, N) using
negation-as-failure across all (R,C) pairs.

WP-223-SPEC-004: gsc_block_at/5 extracts the NxN sub-grid at block position
(BR, BC) (raw rows BR*N..BR*N+N-1, columns BC*N..BC*N+N-1).
gsc_block_uniform/5 succeeds if the NxN block at (BR, BC) is all one Color.
gsc_all_uniform/2 succeeds if every NxN block in Grid is uniform; this is
the necessary and sufficient condition for Grid being an exact N-upsampling.

WP-223-SPEC-005: gsc_infer_tile/2 finds the smallest grid Tile whose
upsampling reproduces Grid, by searching for the largest valid block size N
(largest divisor of both H and W, >= 2, for which gsc_all_uniform holds)
and then downsampling. Fails if no N >= 2 satisfies gsc_all_uniform.
gsc_factors/2 returns the ascending list of all positive integers that divide
both the height and the width of Grid.

WP-223-SPEC-006: gsc_resize/4 resizes Grid to (TargetH, TargetW) using
nearest-neighbor interpolation: Resized[r][c] = Grid[(r*H)//TargetH][(c*W)//TargetW].
gsc_subsample/3 extracts every N-th row and every N-th column (stride-N
sampling): Sub[BR][BC] = Grid[BR*N][BC*N]. Output has (H//N) x (W//N) cells.

WP-223-SPEC-007: gsc_pad/4 surrounds Grid with an N-cell wide border of Color,
producing a (H+2N) x (W+2N) grid. The original occupies rows N..N+H-1 and
columns N..N+W-1. N=0 is a no-op.
gsc_crop_to_factor/3 crops Grid to the largest dimensions divisible by N:
CH = (H//N)*N, CW = (W//N)*N, taking the top-left region. If H and W are
already divisible by N, the full grid is returned.


PART 214 - WORK PACKAGE 224: gridrun PACK (LAYER 203, grl_*)

WP-224-SPEC-001: The gridrun pack (Layer 203) provides 14 predicates
(grl_* prefix) for run-length encoding and stripe analysis of raw grids.
A "run" is a maximal sequence of adjacent identical color values in a row
or column, encoded as the pair Color-Len. No cross-pack dependencies.
Uses library(lists) and library(apply) only.

WP-224-SPEC-002: grl_row_runs/3 encodes row R of Grid as a list of Color-Len
pairs. grl_col_runs/3 encodes column C similarly. grl_all_row_runs/2 and
grl_all_col_runs/2 collect run lists for every row or column respectively.
grl_decode/2 recovers the original flat color list from a run-length list.

WP-224-SPEC-003: grl_run_count/3 returns the number of distinct runs in row R.
grl_uniform_row/3 succeeds (returning Color) if row R has exactly one run.
grl_uniform_col/3 succeeds (returning Color) if column C has exactly one run.

WP-224-SPEC-004: grl_is_striped_h/1 succeeds if every row is uniform (the grid
consists of horizontal solid-color stripes). grl_is_striped_v/1 succeeds if
every column is uniform (vertical solid-color stripes). Both use
negation-as-failure over grl_uniform_row/col.

WP-224-SPEC-005: grl_stripe_colors_h/2 returns the list of row colors for a
horizontally striped grid; fails if any row is not uniform. The length of
Colors equals H. grl_stripe_colors_v/2 returns column colors for a vertically
striped grid; fails if any column is not uniform. Length of Colors equals W.

WP-224-SPEC-006: grl_max_run/4 returns Color and Len for the longest run in row R.
Ties are broken by standard term order on Color (the pair with the smallest
Color atom that has the maximum length). Fails if row R is empty.

WP-224-SPEC-007: grl_alternating/2 succeeds if row R strictly alternates between
exactly two colors: every run has length 1, exactly two distinct colors appear,
and the row has at least 2 cells. Fails for uniform rows, rows with run lengths
greater than 1, or rows with more or fewer than 2 distinct colors.


Part 215 - Work Package 225: gridflood Pack (gf_*, Layer 204)

WP-225-SPEC-001: The gridflood pack (Layer 204) provides fourteen predicates
(gf_* prefix) for flood-fill operations, connected-region analysis, hole
filling, and connected-component enumeration on raw grids. A "region" is a
maximal set of same-color cells connected by 4-adjacency (sharing an edge).
No cross-pack dependencies; uses library(lists) and library(apply) only.

WP-225-SPEC-002: gf_fill/5 replaces the 4-connected same-color region at seed
(R,C) with NewColor using BFS. If the seed color already equals NewColor the
predicate succeeds with Result = Grid (no-op). gf_fill8/5 performs the same
operation using 8-connectivity (diagonal neighbors included). gf_recolor/4
replaces every cell of OldColor with NewColor regardless of connectivity (global
palette swap); differs from gf_fill in that disconnected patches are all changed.

WP-225-SPEC-003: gf_isolate/5 keeps the 4-connected region at (R,C) and sets
all other cells to BgColor, producing a single-region extraction useful for
object-level analysis. gf_region_cells/4 returns the list of R-C coordinates of
the 4-connected same-color region at (R,C) in BFS discovery order. gf_region_size/4
returns the cell count. gf_region_bbox/7 returns the bounding box (MinR, MinC,
MaxR, MaxC) enclosing the 4-connected region.

WP-225-SPEC-004: gf_enclosed_cells/3 finds all BgColor cells not reachable from
any border cell via 4-connected BgColor paths; these are "holes" inside non-BgColor
regions. Seeds BFS from all border cells of BgColor to find reachable cells; the
complement (among BgColor cells) is the enclosed set. gf_fill_enclosed/4 replaces
all enclosed BgColor cells with FillColor.

WP-225-SPEC-005: gf_components/3 enumerates all 4-connected regions of Color as
a list of cell-lists, one per region, in top-left seed order. gf_n_components/3
counts the number of such regions. gf_largest/3 returns the cell-list of the
largest region; ties favor the first encountered region. gf_is_connected/3 succeeds
if all Color cells form at most one region; supports Connectivity = 4 or 8.

WP-225-SPEC-006: gf_boundary_fill/6 flood-fills the 4-connected same-color region
at seed (R,C) with FillColor, treating BoundaryColor cells as impassable walls.
Cells of colors other than the seed color and BoundaryColor also stop the fill.
If the seed cell is itself BoundaryColor, Result = Grid (no-op).

WP-225-SPEC-007: All predicates operate on raw grid format: a list of rows, each
row a list of color atoms, 0-indexed (row 0 = top, col 0 = left). Predicates that
modify grids rebuild the full grid using findall/3; the original Grid is never
destructively updated. BFS is implemented iteratively using an explicit queue
accumulated in a difference-list fashion to avoid stack overflow on large grids.


Part 216 - Work Package 226: gridpath Pack (gpa_*, Layer 205)

WP-226-SPEC-001: The gridpath pack (Layer 205) provides fourteen predicates
(gpa_* prefix) for grid pathfinding: BFS-based shortest path between cells,
distance maps, flood expansion to N steps, wavefront at a fixed distance,
line-of-sight testing, straight-line segment generation, and shortest-path
discovery between colored regions. No cross-pack dependencies; uses
library(lists) only.

WP-226-SPEC-002: gpa_shortest_path/7 finds the shortest 4-connected path from
(R1,C1) to (R2,C2) avoiding ObsColor cells, returning the sequence of R-C
coordinate pairs including both endpoints. gpa_path_length/7 returns the step
count (path length minus 1). gpa_reachable/6 succeeds if a path exists. All
three fail if either endpoint is ObsColor or if no path exists.

WP-226-SPEC-003: gpa_all_reachable/5 returns all R-C cells reachable from a
seed via 4-connected non-ObsColor paths. gpa_distance_map/5 extends this by
returning R-C-Dist triples giving the BFS distance from seed to each reachable
cell. Seed distance is 0. Fails if the seed is ObsColor.

WP-226-SPEC-004: gpa_nearest/6 finds the nearest reachable cell of a specified
color; ties are broken by BFS order (first found at equal distance). Returns
NR-NC. gpa_flood_n/6 returns all cells reachable within N steps. gpa_wavefront/6
returns only cells at exactly distance N (returns [] if none exist at that
distance).

WP-226-SPEC-005: gpa_straight_h/4 generates the list of R-C cells on a
horizontal segment (row R, columns C1..C2 inclusive) in column order from C1
to C2; direction reverses if C1 > C2. gpa_straight_v/4 generates cells on
a vertical segment (col C, rows R1..R2) in row order from R1 to R2.
gpa_between_h/4 and gpa_between_v/4 generate strictly interior cells (endpoints
excluded) of horizontal and vertical segments respectively, always in ascending
index order.

WP-226-SPEC-006: gpa_line_of_sight/6 succeeds if two cells share the same row
or column AND no ObsColor cell lies strictly between them; fails if they are on
different rows and different columns (diagonal). Adjacent cells on the same row
or column have clear line of sight vacuously (no cells between).

WP-226-SPEC-007: gpa_region_path/5 finds the shortest 4-connected path between
any cell of Color1 and any cell of Color2, avoiding ObsColor. Generates all
(Color1, Color2) cell pairs, runs gpa_shortest_path on each pair that has a
valid path, and returns the globally shortest one. Fails if no Color1 or Color2
cells exist or if no path can be found.


Part 217 - Work Package 227: gridmask Pack (gm_*, Layer 206)

WP-227-SPEC-001: The gridmask pack (Layer 206) provides fourteen predicates
(gm_* prefix) for mask-based operations on raw grids: boolean overlay, union,
intersection, difference, inversion, masked extraction, cell-list extraction,
stamp paste, grid comparison, equality, sub-grid extraction, transparent paste,
border mask, and color mask generation. No cross-pack dependencies; uses
library(lists) only. Two grids are compatible only when they share the same
dimensions (same H and W).

WP-227-SPEC-002: gm_overlay/5 overlays GridB on GridA: non-BgColor cells of
GridB replace the corresponding GridA cell; BgColor cells of GridB are
transparent. gm_union/4 produces the union of non-background regions: GridA's
color wins where both are non-BgColor, otherwise the non-BgColor value from
either grid is used. gm_intersect/5 marks every cell FgColor where both grids
are non-BgColor, otherwise BgColor (boolean intersection). gm_difference/5
keeps GridA cells where GridB is BgColor; replaces the others with BgOut.

WP-227-SPEC-003: gm_invert/4 swaps foreground and background: non-BgColor
cells become BgColor, BgColor cells become FgColor. gm_mask_apply/5 uses a
Mask grid to gate Grid: where Mask is non-BgColor, Grid shows through; where
Mask is BgColor the output cell is FillColor. gm_extract/4 produces a copy of
Grid where only the cells in the given R-C list are kept; all others are BgColor.

WP-227-SPEC-004: gm_stamp/5 pastes a Stamp grid onto Grid with its top-left
corner at (OriginR, OriginC); Stamp cells that fall outside Grid bounds are
silently skipped; all Stamp cells overwrite Grid regardless of color.
gm_compare/4 returns the list of R-C positions where two same-dimension grids
differ. gm_equal/2 succeeds if two grids are identical (unified).

WP-227-SPEC-005: gm_sub/6 extracts a Height x Width rectangular sub-grid
starting at (R0, C0); fails if the sub-grid extends outside Grid bounds.
gm_paste/6 pastes a Patch transparently: Patch cells whose color differs from
BgColor overwrite the corresponding Grid cell; BgColor Patch cells leave Grid
unchanged. gm_paste is robust to Patch cells that lie outside Grid bounds.

WP-227-SPEC-006: gm_border_mask/3 produces a binary grid (same dimensions as
Grid) where cells within N layers from any border are marked 'border' and all
other cells are 'interior'. gm_color_mask/4 produces a binary grid where cells
matching the target Color become FgColor and all others become the atom 'bg'.
Both are useful for generating selection masks for spatial or color regions.

WP-227-SPEC-007: The gm_build_/4 private helper generates any H x W grid by
calling a lambda with (R, C, V) for each cell position in row-major order.
All output predicates use gm_build_ to ensure consistent row construction.
Lambdas use the `>>` syntax for clean closure capture of H, W, BgColor, etc.

Part 218 - Work Package 228: gridxform Pack (gx_*, Layer 207)

WP-228-SPEC-001: The gridxform pack (Layer 207) provides fourteen predicates
for geometric transformations of raw grids: three rotations (90, 180, 270
degrees clockwise), two reflections (horizontal, vertical), two diagonal
reflections (main diagonal transpose and anti-diagonal flip), crop to explicit
bounding box, auto-crop to content bounding box, pad with background color,
integer upscale, tile to target dimensions, enumerate all 8 D4 isometries,
and compute the canonical (lexicographically minimum) D4 form.

WP-228-SPEC-002: gx_rotate90/2 rotates an H x W grid 90 degrees clockwise to
produce a W x H grid. The mapping is result[R][C] = original[H-1-C][R]. All
three non-trivial rotations are defined independently; composing any four 90-
degree rotations restores the original grid.

WP-228-SPEC-003: gx_flip_h/2 mirrors columns left-to-right: result[R][C] =
original[R][W-1-C]. gx_flip_v/2 mirrors rows top-to-bottom: result[R][C] =
original[H-1-R][C]. gx_transpose/2 maps (r,c) to (c,r), producing a W x H
grid where result[R][C] = original[C][R]. gx_flip_d2/2 reflects along the
anti-diagonal, producing a W x H grid where result[R][C] = original[H-1-C][W-1-R].

WP-228-SPEC-004: gx_crop/6 extracts rows [R0..R1] x columns [C0..C1]
(inclusive) from Grid, producing a (R1-R0+1) x (C1-C0+1) result.
gx_crop_content/3 auto-crops Grid to the tightest bounding box enclosing all
non-BgColor cells; if no non-BgColor cells exist, the Grid is returned
unchanged.

WP-228-SPEC-005: gx_pad/7 surrounds Grid with BgColor padding: Top rows on
top, Bot rows on bottom, Left columns on the left, Right columns on the right.
gx_scale/3 upscales Grid by integer factor N, making each cell an N x N block.
gx_tile/4 fills an H x W target by tiling Grid using modular indexing.

WP-228-SPEC-006: gx_d4_group/2 enumerates all 8 D4 isometries of Grid in the
order [identity, rotate90, rotate180, rotate270, flip_h, flip_v, transpose,
flip_d2]. gx_normalize/2 sorts these 8 grids by Prolog's standard term order
and returns the lexicographically smallest as the canonical form. Two grids
that are related by any D4 symmetry share the same canonical form.

WP-228-SPEC-007: The private gx_build_/4 helper generates any target H x W
grid by calling a lambda Goal(R,C,V) for each cell position in row-major order.
Unlike gm_build_/4, gx_build_ accepts explicit NewH and NewW parameters that
may differ from the input grid dimensions, enabling non-square output grids for
rotations and transpositions.

Part 219 - Work Package 229: gridsymm Pack (gsm_*, Layer 208)

WP-229-SPEC-001: The gridsymm pack (Layer 208) provides fourteen predicates
for detecting, completing, and measuring symmetry in raw grids. It covers the
six fundamental symmetry types relevant to D4 rectangular grid analysis: top-
bottom (h), left-right (v), main diagonal (d1), anti-diagonal (d2), 90-degree
rotation (rot90), and 180-degree rotation (rot180).

WP-229-SPEC-002: gsm_sym_h/1 tests top-bottom symmetry: Grid[R][C] =
Grid[H-1-R][C] for all R, C. gsm_sym_v/1 tests left-right symmetry:
Grid[R][C] = Grid[R][W-1-C]. Both use a \+ existential check over only the
first half of row or column pairs.

WP-229-SPEC-003: gsm_sym_d1/1 and gsm_sym_d2/1 test main-diagonal and anti-
diagonal symmetry respectively. Both predicates fail for non-square grids.
gsm_sym_rot90/1 tests 90-degree rotational symmetry and also fails for non-
square grids. gsm_sym_rot180/1 tests 180-degree rotational symmetry and works
for any rectangular grid.

WP-229-SPEC-004: gsm_symmetries/2 returns the list of all symmetry types
possessed by Grid in order [h, v, d1, d2, rot90, rot180], omitting types that
are inapplicable (d1, d2, rot90 for non-square grids) or not present.

WP-229-SPEC-005: gsm_complete_h/3 and gsm_complete_v/3 produce grids that are
top-bottom or left-right symmetric by copying one half onto the other. Dir=top
maps result[R][C] = Grid[min(R,H-1-R)][C]; Dir=bottom maps to Grid[max(R,H-1-R)][C].
Similarly for v with left/right directions. gsm_complete_rot180/3 fills
BgColor cells from their 180-rotational mirrors, keeping non-BgColor cells.

WP-229-SPEC-006: gsm_violations_h/2, gsm_violations_v/2, and
gsm_violations_rot180/2 return lists of R-C positions where the grid fails a
given symmetry. An empty result list confirms the symmetry holds. Violations are
reported only from the first half of each pair to avoid duplicates.

WP-229-SPEC-007: gsm_score/3 computes a symmetry score in [0.0..1.0] for
types h, v, or rot180. Score = 1.0 means fully symmetric; score = 0.0 means
no pairs match. Uses float division to ensure a floating-point result.

Part 220 - Work Package 230: gridcolor Pack (gc_*, Layer 209)

WP-230-SPEC-001: The gridcolor pack (Layer 209) provides fourteen predicates
for color analysis and transformation of raw grids: cell counting by color,
histogram generation, most and least frequent color detection, unique color
enumeration, cell position lookup, color presence testing, recoloring,
color mapping, binary thresholding, dominant non-background color, fraction
computation, color count, and frequency-sorted color list.

WP-230-SPEC-002: gc_count/3 counts cells matching a given color atom.
gc_histogram/2 produces a sorted list of Color-Count pairs for every distinct
color in Grid. gc_most_frequent/2 and gc_least_frequent/2 use the histogram
and msort to find the color with the highest or lowest count respectively.

WP-230-SPEC-003: gc_unique_colors/2 returns the sorted list of distinct color
atoms using sort/2. gc_color_cells/3 returns R-C positions of all cells
matching a given color. gc_contains/2 uses memberchk for efficient O(n) presence
testing. gc_count_colors/2 returns the integer count of distinct colors.

WP-230-SPEC-004: gc_recolor/4 replaces all occurrences of OldColor with
NewColor. gc_color_map/3 applies a list of Old-New pair mappings; unmapped
colors pass through unchanged. gc_threshold/5 produces a binary grid where
cells in the Colors list become FgColor and all others become BgColor.

WP-230-SPEC-005: gc_dominant/3 finds the most frequent non-BgColor by
filtering the histogram and selecting the maximum. gc_fraction/3 computes
the fraction of cells matching Color as a float in [0.0..1.0] using float/1
division to avoid integer arithmetic. gc_sorted_by_freq/2 returns colors in
descending frequency order by negating counts before msort.

WP-230-SPEC-006: All predicates use a private gc_all_cells_/2 helper that
collects all cell values via findall in row-major order. This enables histogram
and count operations without re-reading the grid multiple times per predicate.

WP-230-SPEC-007: gc_build_/4 is the standard H x W grid builder using a
lambda Goal(R,C,V). Transformation predicates (gc_recolor, gc_color_map,
gc_threshold) all use gc_build_ for consistent output construction.


Part 221 - Work Package 231: gridstitch Pack (gst_*, Layer 210)

WP-231-SPEC-001: The gridstitch pack (Layer 210) provides fourteen predicates
for assembling and disassembling symbolic grids: horizontal and vertical
concatenation of two grids, list-based horizontal and vertical stacking,
horizontal and vertical splitting at a given index, half-splits, quadrant
extraction, NR x NC tiled arrangement, horizontal and vertical repetition,
border addition, and border removal.

WP-231-SPEC-002: gst_concat_h/3 and gst_concat_v/3 combine exactly two grids.
gst_concat_h requires both grids to have the same number of rows; rows are
zipped by appending corresponding row pairs. gst_concat_v requires matching
column counts; the result is the row-list append of both grids.

WP-231-SPEC-003: gst_hstack/2 and gst_vstack/2 accept a list of grids and
reduce left to right using gst_concat_h and gst_concat_v respectively. Both
handle the empty-list (returns empty grid) and singleton-list (returns the
single grid unchanged) cases deterministically with a cut on the singleton
clause.

WP-231-SPEC-004: gst_split_h/4 splits at a given row index R using list
split: the first R rows become Top, the remainder become Bottom. gst_split_v/4
splits each row at column C using list split per row (maplist over rows).
gst_halves_h/3 and gst_halves_v/3 compute H//2 and W//2 and delegate to the
general split predicates.

WP-231-SPEC-005: gst_quadrants/5 extracts all four quadrants of an even-sized
grid by composing gst_halves_h then gst_halves_v on each half. Reconstruction
is gst_concat_h on top/bottom halves then gst_concat_v.

WP-231-SPEC-006: gst_tile_grid/4 arranges a flat list of NR*NC sub-grids into
a tiled NR x NC layout. It groups sub-grids into NR bands of NC grids using
nth0-based indexing, applies gst_hstack to each band, then gst_vstack on all
bands.

WP-231-SPEC-007: gst_add_border/4 wraps Grid in an N-cell-wide border of
Color by building a (H+2N) x (W+2N) grid: interior cells (OR in [0,H), OC in
[0,W)) copy from Grid; all others are Color. gst_strip_border/3 extracts the
interior by building a (H-2N) x (W-2N) grid offset by N in each direction.
gst_repeat_h/3 and gst_repeat_v/3 create N copies via findall and delegate
to gst_hstack and gst_vstack.


Part 222 - Work Package 232: gridedge Pack (ge_*, Layer 211)

WP-232-SPEC-001: The gridedge pack (Layer 211) provides fourteen predicates
for detecting edges, boundaries, and structural features of symbolic grids.
An edge cell is a cell whose color differs from at least one in-bounds
4-connected (or 8-connected) neighbor. The pack covers 4- and 8-connected
edge detection, bi-color boundary detection, inner and outer border
extraction, edge grid construction, edge counting, neighbor difference
analysis, corner and endpoint detection, smooth cell detection, transition
maps, and color-specific edge counting.

WP-232-SPEC-002: ge_edge_cells/3 collects all FgColor cells that have at
least one 4-connected neighbor of a different color. Each such cell appears
exactly once in the output (findall uses once/1 to prevent duplicates when
multiple neighbors qualify). ge_edge_cells8/3 uses the 8-connected (Moore)
neighborhood. ge_is_edge/3 tests a single cell returning yes or no.

WP-232-SPEC-003: ge_boundary/4 collects Color1 cells that have at least one
4-connected Color2 neighbor, giving the directional boundary of Color1 facing
Color2. ge_inner_border/3 finds BgColor cells adjacent to non-BgColor cells.
ge_outer_border/3 finds non-FgColor cells adjacent to FgColor cells.

WP-232-SPEC-004: ge_edge_grid/4 builds a grid with FgColor edge cells
replaced by EdgeColor; all other cells retain their original color. The edge
cell set is pre-computed and membership-tested with memberchk.

WP-232-SPEC-005: ge_edge_count/3 counts FgColor edge cells. ge_neighbors_diff/4
returns the list of 4-connected neighbor positions where the neighbor color
differs from the reference cell color.

WP-232-SPEC-006: ge_corners/3 collects FgColor cells with 2 or more
differently-colored 4-connected in-bounds neighbors. ge_endpoints/3 collects
FgColor cells with exactly 1 same-color 4-connected in-bounds neighbor.
ge_smooth_cells/3 collects FgColor cells with no differently-colored in-bounds
4-connected neighbor.

WP-232-SPEC-007: ge_transition_map/2 builds a new grid where each cell value
is the count (0..4) of in-bounds 4-connected neighbors with a different color.
ge_edge_color_count/4 counts FgColor cells adjacent to at least one BgColor
cell by delegating to ge_boundary.


Part 223 - Work Package 233: gridmorph Pack (gmo_*, Layer 212)

WP-233-SPEC-001: The gridmorph pack (Layer 212) provides fourteen predicates
for morphological operations on symbolic grids. Morphological operations treat
one color as foreground (FgColor) and all others as background. The pack covers
dilation, erosion, morphological opening and closing, single-step variants,
inner and outer boundary extraction, morphological gradient, top-hat and
bottom-hat transforms, hole filling, border-reachable flood fill, and
connected-component size filtering.

WP-233-SPEC-002: gmo_dilate/4 expands the FgColor region by N layers: in each
step, every non-FgColor cell that has at least one FgColor 4-connected in-bounds
neighbor becomes FgColor. gmo_dilate1/3 applies exactly one dilation step.
gmo_erode/4 shrinks the FgColor region by N layers: in each step, every FgColor
cell that has at least one non-FgColor in-bounds neighbor becomes BgColor (the
background color discovered as the first non-FgColor cell in the grid).
gmo_erode1/3 applies exactly one erosion step. Grid boundary cells behave as if
out-of-bounds positions do not exist; no phantom background is injected.

WP-233-SPEC-003: gmo_open/4 applies N erosion steps then N dilation steps
(morphological opening); removes small isolated FgColor regions while
approximately preserving the shape of large ones. gmo_close/4 applies N dilation
steps then N erosion steps (morphological closing); fills small gaps and holes
within FgColor regions.

WP-233-SPEC-004: gmo_boundary_inner/3 collects FgColor cells that have at
least one non-FgColor 4-connected in-bounds neighbor (the inner border of the
FgColor region). gmo_boundary_outer/3 collects non-FgColor cells that have at
least one FgColor 4-connected in-bounds neighbor (the outer border around the
FgColor region). Both predicates use once/1 inside findall to prevent duplicate
entries when multiple qualifying neighbors exist.

WP-233-SPEC-005: gmo_gradient_cells/3 returns the morphological gradient: the
concatenation of the inner and outer boundaries. This gives all cells in the
border region between FgColor and background, with no duplicates by construction
(inner and outer are disjoint color sets).

WP-233-SPEC-006: gmo_top_hat/4 returns FgColor cells present in the input grid
that are absent after morphological opening with N steps. Highlights small bright
structures (protrusions, isolated spots) that are removed by opening.
gmo_bottom_hat/4 returns cells that become FgColor after morphological closing
but were not FgColor in the input. Highlights small dark holes filled by closing.

WP-233-SPEC-007: gmo_fill_holes/4 fills enclosed holes in the FgColor region.
It uses gmo_connected_border/4 to flood-fill all BgColor cells reachable from
the grid border; any BgColor cell not reached is an enclosed hole and is replaced
by FgColor. gmo_connected_border/4 performs a BFS from all TargetColor cells on
the grid border through TargetColor cells, stopping at BlockColor cells.
gmo_remove_small/5 replaces all FgColor connected components smaller than
MinSize with BgColor, using BFS per unprocessed cell.


Part 224 - Work Package 234: gridconv Pack (gcv_*, Layer 213)

WP-234-SPEC-001: The gridconv pack (Layer 213) provides fourteen predicates
for grid convolution operations: sliding window extraction, window statistics,
density maps, pattern matching, hot spot detection, and square structuring
element morphology. All predicates operate on raw grid format (list of rows,
each a list of color atoms, 0-indexed). Window operations use radius N: the
neighborhood of a cell (R,C) is a (2N+1) x (2N+1) square centered at (R,C).

WP-234-SPEC-002: gcv_window/6 extracts a (2N+1) x (2N+1) subgrid centered at
(R,C), filling out-of-bounds positions with a specified Fill color. This allows
full-square windows even at grid boundaries. gcv_count_in/6 counts cells of a
specified Color in the in-bounds portion of the (2N+1) x (2N+1) window; out-of-
bounds positions are not counted. gcv_density_map/4 produces a grid of the same
dimensions as the input where each cell holds the Color count from its window.

WP-234-SPEC-003: gcv_majority/5 returns the most frequent color among in-bounds
cells in the (2N+1) x (2N+1) window. Ties are broken by term order (via msort).
gcv_majority_map/3 produces a grid where each cell is replaced by its local
majority color. gcv_uniform_at/5 tests whether all in-bounds cells in the window
have the same color, returning yes or no. gcv_uniform_cells/3 collects all grid
positions where the window is uniform.

WP-234-SPEC-004: gcv_find_pattern/3 collects all positions (R,C) where a given
Pattern grid exactly matches as a subgrid of Grid, with (R,C) as the top-left
corner. Pattern and Grid cells are matched atom-by-atom. gcv_count_pattern/3
counts such matching positions. gcv_has_pattern/2 succeeds if at least one match
exists, using once/1 for efficiency.

WP-234-SPEC-005: gcv_hot_spots/5 collects grid positions where the Color count
in the window meets or exceeds a given Threshold. This gives a spatial density
threshold map useful for detecting regions of concentrated color.

WP-234-SPEC-006: gcv_dilate_sq/4 applies square structuring element dilation of
radius N: a non-FgColor cell becomes FgColor if any cell in its (2N+1) x (2N+1)
window is FgColor. Equivalent to gcv_count_in >= 1 for non-FgColor cells.
gcv_erode_sq/4 applies square structuring element erosion: a FgColor cell loses
its color if any in-bounds cell in its window is not FgColor. Implemented by
comparing Color count to total in-bounds count.

WP-234-SPEC-007: gcv_replace_pattern/4 replaces the first-found (row-major)
occurrence of Pattern in Grid with Replacement. If no match exists, Grid is
returned unchanged. Pattern and Replacement must have the same dimensions. The
replacement overwrites the cells at the match position; all other cells are
unchanged.


Part 225 - Work Package 235: gridgraph Pack (ggr_*, Layer 214)

WP-235-SPEC-001: The gridgraph pack (Layer 214) provides fourteen predicates
for region adjacency graph analysis of symbolic grids. A "region" is the set
of all cells of a given color; regions may be disconnected. The pack covers
color pair adjacency, per-color neighbor enumeration, full adjacency graph
construction, adjacency testing, color degree, shared border extraction,
border length, isolated color detection, enclosed color detection, horizontal
and vertical spanning detection, color merging, connected component counting,
and connected component cell partitioning.

WP-235-SPEC-002: ggr_adj_colors/2 collects all sorted pairs (C1-C2, C1 @< C2)
where Color C1 and Color C2 regions share at least one 4-connected boundary.
ggr_adj_of/3 returns the sorted list of distinct colors 4-adjacent to a given
Color. ggr_adj_graph/2 builds the full adjacency list as a list of (Color,
Neighbors) pairs for every distinct color in the grid. ggr_are_adj/3 tests
whether two distinct colors share a boundary, using once/1 for efficiency.

WP-235-SPEC-003: ggr_color_degree/3 counts the number of distinct colors
adjacent to a given Color. ggr_shared_border/4 collects Color1 cells that have
at least one Color2 4-neighbor; uses once/1 to avoid duplicate entries.
ggr_border_length/4 counts such cells. Border length is directional: the count
of C1 cells touching C2 may differ from the count of C2 cells touching C1.

WP-235-SPEC-004: ggr_isolated_colors/2 returns colors with degree 0 (no
differently-colored in-bounds 4-neighbor). ggr_enclosed_colors/3 returns
colors C such that (1) no C cell is on the grid border AND (2) every non-C
4-neighbor of every C cell has the OuterColor. Both conditions are checked by
negation-as-failure.

WP-235-SPEC-005: ggr_spanning_h/2 returns colors with at least one cell in
column 0 AND at least one cell in the last column. ggr_spanning_v/2 returns
colors with at least one cell in row 0 AND at least one cell in the last row.
ggr_merge_colors/4 replaces every occurrence of FromColor with ToColor using
maplist over rows and cells.

WP-235-SPEC-006: ggr_color_components/3 counts the number of 4-connected
components of Color using repeated BFS. ggr_component_cells/3 partitions all
Color cells into a list of cell-lists, one per connected component, ordered by
first cell in row-major order. Both predicates use the internal BFS helper
ggr_bfs_same_ which traverses only same-color cells and uses subtract/3 to
remove visited cells from the remaining set.

WP-235-SPEC-007: All predicates operate on raw grid format (list of rows, each
a list of color atoms, 0-indexed). No cross-pack dependencies. msort/2 is a
SWI-Prolog built-in used internally in ggr_adj_of for deduplication via
list_to_set/2.


Part 226 - Work Package 236: griddiag Pack (gdi_*, Layer 215)

WP-236-SPEC-001: The griddiag pack (Layer 215) provides fourteen predicates
for diagonal analysis of symbolic grids. Two families of diagonals are defined:
main diagonals (cells where column minus row equals K) and anti-diagonals
(cells where row plus column equals K). The pack covers extraction, all-diagonal
enumeration, color counting, uniformity testing, cell modification, uniform
diagonal enumeration, and diagonal length computation.

WP-236-SPEC-002: gdi_main_diag/3 extracts the K-th main diagonal: cells (R,C)
where C - R = K, in ascending R order. K = 0 is the principal diagonal from
(0,0). K > 0 selects diagonals above the principal; K < 0 selects below. For
an H x W grid, K ranges from -(H-1) to W-1. gdi_anti_diag/3 extracts the
K-th anti-diagonal: cells where R + C = K, in ascending C order. K ranges from
0 to H+W-2. gdi_trace/2 returns the principal diagonal (K=0) of length min(H,W).

WP-236-SPEC-003: gdi_all_main_diags/2 collects all main diagonals in ascending
K order; for an H x W grid this produces H+W-1 diagonals. gdi_all_anti_diags/2
similarly collects all anti-diagonals. The total cell count across all main
diagonals (or all anti-diagonals) equals H * W.

WP-236-SPEC-004: gdi_main_count/4 and gdi_anti_count/4 count occurrences of
a given Color on the K-th diagonal of each family. gdi_main_uniform/3 and
gdi_anti_uniform/3 test whether all cells on the K-th diagonal are the same
color, returning yes or no. Both fail on an empty diagonal.

WP-236-SPEC-005: gdi_set_main_diag/4 builds a new grid with all cells on the
K-th main diagonal set to Color; all other cells retain their original color.
gdi_set_anti_diag/4 does the same for the K-th anti-diagonal. Both use
gdi_build_/4 with memberchk for diagonal membership testing.

WP-236-SPEC-006: gdi_uniform_main_diags/2 returns the list of K values (from
-(H-1) to W-1) for which the K-th main diagonal is uniform. Similarly,
gdi_uniform_anti_diags/2 returns the K values (from 0 to H+W-2) for which the
K-th anti-diagonal is uniform.

WP-236-SPEC-007: gdi_diag_length/3 returns the number of cells on the K-th
main diagonal. For a square N x N grid, the principal diagonal has length N;
the K-th diagonal has length N - |K|. For non-square grids the formula
generalizes as min(H, W, H-|K| if K<0, W-K if K>=0).


Part 227 - Work Package 237: gridframe Pack (gfr_*, Layer 216)

WP-237-SPEC-001: The gridframe pack (Layer 216) provides fourteen predicates
for frame-depth analysis of symbolic grids. A frame at depth D is the set of
all cells (R,C) where min(R, H-1-R, C, W-1-C) equals D. Frame 0 is the
outermost border. Deeper frames are inner concentric rings.

WP-237-SPEC-002: gfr_cell_depth/4 computes the frame depth of a specific cell.
gfr_frame/3 collects all cells at a given depth. gfr_max_depth/2 returns the
deepest frame depth: floor((min(H,W)-1)/2). gfr_frame_count/2 returns
max_depth plus one.

WP-237-SPEC-003: gfr_peel/2 returns the (H-2)x(W-2) inner subgrid after
removing the outermost frame. Fails if H<3 or W<3. gfr_all_frames/2 returns
all frame cell-lists in order from depth 0 to max_depth.

WP-237-SPEC-004: gfr_frame_uniform/3 returns yes/no for whether all cells at
depth D are the same color. gfr_frame_colors/3 returns the deduplicated list of
colors at depth D. gfr_count_in_frame/4 counts a specific color at depth D.

WP-237-SPEC-005: gfr_set_frame/4 returns a grid with all cells at depth D set
to a given Color. gfr_fill_frames/3 fills each frame D with Colors[D] from a
supplied list; frames beyond the list length are unchanged.

WP-237-SPEC-006: gfr_uniform_frames/2 returns all depth values with uniform
frames in ascending order. gfr_innermost/2 returns cells at the maximum depth.

WP-237-SPEC-007: gfr_onion_layers/2 returns a list of D-Color pairs for each
uniform frame, in ascending depth order. A grid where all frames are uniform
and each has a distinct color is an "onion" or "target" pattern.


Part 228 - Work Package 238: gridspiral Pack (gsp_*, Layer 217)

WP-238-SPEC-001: The gridspiral pack (Layer 217) provides fourteen predicates
for clockwise spiral traversal of symbolic grids. The spiral starts at cell
(0,0), moves right along the top row, down the right column, left along the
bottom row, and up the left column, then repeats for the next inner frame.

WP-238-SPEC-002: gsp_spiral/2 returns all R-C pairs in spiral order.
gsp_read_spiral/2 reads color values in spiral order. gsp_write_spiral/3 and
gsp_fill_spiral/3 write values into spiral positions; cells beyond the values
list are unchanged. gsp_spiral_length/2 returns H*W.

WP-238-SPEC-003: gsp_spiral_index/4 returns the 0-based position of a cell
in the spiral. gsp_nth_spiral/4 returns the cell at a given position.

WP-238-SPEC-004: gsp_frame_spiral/3 returns the clockwise traversal of a single
frame D. gsp_all_frame_spirals/2 returns frame spirals for all depths in order.

WP-238-SPEC-005: gsp_spiral_uniform/2 returns yes if all cells have the same
color. gsp_spiral_reversed/2 returns cells in reverse (inner-to-outer) order.
gsp_spiral_count/3 counts occurrences of a color.

WP-238-SPEC-006: gsp_rotate_spiral/3 rotates all grid values N steps forward
along the spiral: the value at position I moves to position (I-N) mod (H*W).
Equivalently, position J in the result holds the value from position (J+N) mod len.

WP-238-SPEC-007: gsp_spiral_slice/4 returns the sub-list of spiral cells from
0-based index Start to End inclusive.


Part 229 - Work Package 239: griddelta Pack (gdt_*, Layer 218)

WP-239-SPEC-001: The griddelta pack (Layer 218) provides fourteen predicates for
comparing two same-size grids: finding differing cells, counting changes, mapping
color transitions, applying deltas, and testing identity.

WP-239-SPEC-002: gdt_compatible/2 tests same-size grids. gdt_diff_cells/3 returns
R-C pairs where two grids differ. gdt_diff_count/3 counts them. gdt_same_cells/3
returns agreeing cells.

WP-239-SPEC-003: gdt_changed_pairs/3 returns R-C-(Old->New) terms for each
changed cell. gdt_color_changes/4 counts cells where a specific color was replaced.
gdt_changed_colors/3 collects new colors introduced by the delta.

WP-239-SPEC-004: gdt_apply_delta/4 applies the changes from G1→G2 to a third
grid G3: for each cell where G1 and G2 differ, if G3 has G1's value at that cell,
it receives G2's value. gdt_invert_delta/3 reverses changed cells to G1's values.

WP-239-SPEC-005: gdt_diff_rows/3 returns row indices containing at least one
change. gdt_diff_cols/3 returns column indices with at least one change.

WP-239-SPEC-006: gdt_agree_region/6 tests whether two grids agree in a
rectangular sub-region [RowMin..RowMax] x [ColMin..ColMax].

WP-239-SPEC-007: gdt_overlay/4 overlays G2 onto G1 using a Marker color as
transparent: where G2 equals Marker, G1's value is used; otherwise G2's value
is used. gdt_is_identity/2 succeeds if two grids are identical.

Part 230 - Work Package 240: gridrowcol Pack (grc_*, Layer 219)

WP-240-SPEC-001: The gridrowcol pack (Layer 219) provides fourteen predicates
for extracting, comparing, sorting, and finding matching rows and columns in
a raw grid. Rows and columns are treated as first-class list objects for
direct comparison and lookup. No cross-pack dependencies.

WP-240-SPEC-002: grc_row/3 extracts row R (0-indexed) as a flat list.
grc_col/3 extracts column C as a top-to-bottom list by reading the C-th
element from each row in order.

WP-240-SPEC-003: grc_row_uniform/3 succeeds if all cells in row R share the
same color and binds that color. grc_col_uniform/3 does the same for column C.
Both fail immediately if the row or column contains two or more distinct values.

WP-240-SPEC-004: grc_equal_rows/3 succeeds if rows R1 and R2 of Grid have
identical content. grc_equal_cols/3 succeeds if columns C1 and C2 have
identical content. Both succeed when R1=R2 or C1=C2 (a row/column equals itself).

WP-240-SPEC-005: grc_row_positions/3 returns the sorted list of row indices
whose content unifies with Pattern. grc_col_positions/3 returns the sorted
list of column indices whose content equals Pattern. Both return [] when no
match exists.

WP-240-SPEC-006: grc_matching_rows/2 returns all R1-R2 pairs (R1 < R2) of
row indices that share identical content. grc_matching_cols/2 returns all
C1-C2 pairs (C1 < C2) of column indices that share identical content.

WP-240-SPEC-007: grc_unique_rows/2 returns the list of row indices whose
content appears exactly once in the grid (no other row is identical).
grc_unique_cols/2 returns the list of column indices whose content appears
exactly once. grc_row_sort/2 sorts rows in standard order (msort, duplicates
kept). grc_col_sort/2 reorders columns by the lexicographic order of their
content.

Part 231 - Work Package 241: gridseg Pack (gsg_*, Layer 220)

WP-241-SPEC-001: The gridseg pack (Layer 220) provides fourteen predicates for
detecting uniform-color separator rows and columns, splitting a grid into
non-separator segments, extracting rectangular panels, and trimming border
separators. A separator row is a row whose every cell shares the same color;
a separator column is a column whose every cell shares the same color.
Consecutive separators count as a single boundary. No cross-pack dependencies.

WP-241-SPEC-002: gsg_is_sep_row/3 tests whether row R is entirely one color
and binds that color. gsg_is_sep_col/3 does the same for column C.
gsg_sep_rows/3 returns all separator row indices for a given color.
gsg_sep_cols/3 returns all separator column indices for a given color.

WP-241-SPEC-003: gsg_split_h/3 splits Grid at separator rows of Color into a
list of non-empty sub-grids. gsg_split_v/3 splits at separator columns.
Consecutive separator rows (or cols) are treated as a single boundary: no
empty segment is produced between them. A grid with no separators yields a
single segment containing the whole grid.

WP-241-SPEC-004: gsg_segment_count_h/3 returns the number of horizontal
segments; gsg_segment_count_v/3 returns the number of vertical segments.
gsg_panels/3 splits by both separator rows and columns and returns a flat
row-major list of all rectangular panels. gsg_panel_count/3 returns the
total number of panels.

WP-241-SPEC-005: gsg_trim_h/3 removes leading and trailing separator rows from
a grid. gsg_trim_v/3 removes leading and trailing separator columns.
gsg_trim/3 removes both. All three treat consecutive separator borders as one.

WP-241-SPEC-006: gsg_sep_color/2 succeeds if exactly one color is used as a
separator row or column in Grid and binds that color. Fails when zero or
multiple distinct separator colors exist.

WP-241-SPEC-007: All predicates use the private helpers gsg_uniform_/2 (list
uniformity), gsg_col_/3 (column extraction), gsg_transpose_/2 (grid
transposition via findall), gsg_split_rows_/4 (accumulator-based row
grouping), and gsg_drop_sep_/3 (leading separator removal). gsg_split_v uses
transpose-split_h-transpose. gsg_trim_v uses transpose-trim_h-transpose.

Part 232 - Work Package 242: gridhist Pack (ghst_*, Layer 221)

WP-242-SPEC-001: The gridhist pack (Layer 221) provides fourteen predicates for
per-row and per-column color frequency analysis. Histogram format is a sorted
list of Color-Count pairs in ascending color order. No cross-pack dependencies.

WP-242-SPEC-002: ghst_row_hist/3 returns the color frequency histogram for a
specific row. ghst_col_hist/3 does the same for a specific column.
ghst_all_row_hists/2 returns the list of histograms for all rows in row-index
order. ghst_all_col_hists/2 returns the list for all columns.

WP-242-SPEC-003: ghst_modal_row/3 returns the most frequent color in row R.
Ties are broken by last-in-ascending-sort order (highest alphabetically).
ghst_modal_col/3 does the same for column C.

WP-242-SPEC-004: ghst_row_count/4 counts occurrences of a specific color in
row R. ghst_col_count/4 does the same for column C. Both return 0 if the
color is absent.

WP-242-SPEC-005: ghst_row_entropy/3 returns the number of distinct colors in
row R (color diversity). ghst_col_entropy/3 does the same for column C.
Both equal the length of the corresponding histogram.

WP-242-SPEC-006: ghst_max_row/3 returns the row index with the highest count
of a given color. Ties resolved by highest row index. Fails if Color does not
appear in any row. ghst_min_row/3 returns the row index with the lowest
non-zero count. Ties resolved by lowest row index.

WP-242-SPEC-007: ghst_rows_with/4 returns all row indices where the given
color appears at least N times. ghst_cols_with/4 does the same for columns.
Both return [] when no row or column satisfies the threshold.

Part 233 - Work Package 243: gridpos Pack (gps_*, Layer 222)

WP-243-SPEC-001: The gridpos pack (Layer 222) provides fourteen predicates for
positional sub-grid extraction and cell identification. Operations cover halves,
