quadrants, even/odd rows and columns, checkerboard patterns, center cell, corner
cells, and the horizontal/vertical cross through the center.

WP-243-SPEC-002: gps_top_half/2 returns rows [0, H//2) as a sub-grid.
gps_bottom_half/2 returns rows [H//2, H). For odd H the bottom half has one more
row than the top. For H=1 the top half is empty.

WP-243-SPEC-003: gps_left_half/2 returns columns [0, W//2) as a sub-grid.
gps_right_half/2 returns columns [W//2, W). For odd W the right half has one more
column. For W=1 the left half contains one empty row per row of the grid.

WP-243-SPEC-004: gps_quadrant/3 takes a quadrant atom (tl, tr, bl, br) and
returns the corresponding rectangular sub-grid. tl: rows [0,HMid), cols [0,WMid).
tr: rows [0,HMid), cols [WMid,W). bl: rows [HMid,H), cols [0,WMid).
br: rows [HMid,H), cols [WMid,W).

WP-243-SPEC-005: gps_even_rows/2 returns the sub-grid of rows at even 0-indexed
positions (0, 2, 4, ...). gps_odd_rows/2 returns rows at odd indices. For a 1-row
grid, even_rows returns [[row]], odd_rows returns [].

WP-243-SPEC-006: gps_even_cols/2 returns columns at even 0-indexed positions
(0, 2, 4, ...) per row. gps_odd_cols/2 returns columns at odd indices per row.
For W=1 the even grid retains the single column; the odd grid contains empty rows.

WP-243-SPEC-007: gps_checkerboard/3 takes Parity (0 or 1) and returns the list
of R-C pairs where (R+C) mod 2 = Parity. Parity must be bound. Order is
row-major: R ascending, then C ascending within each row.

Part 234 - Work Package 244: gridgrav Pack (gv_*, Layer 223)

WP-244-SPEC-001: The gridgrav pack (Layer 223) provides fourteen predicates for
simulating gravity within a raw grid. Non-background (non-bg) cells are those
whose color differs from a user-specified BgColor. Gravity causes non-bg cells to
settle toward one edge of their row or column.

WP-244-SPEC-002: gv_fall_down/3 settles non-bg cells to the bottom of each column,
filling the vacated top positions with BgColor. gv_fall_up/3 settles non-bg cells
to the top. gv_fall_left/3 settles non-bg cells to the left of each row.
gv_fall_right/3 settles non-bg cells to the right. All four operations preserve
the count and relative order of non-bg cells within each row or column.

WP-244-SPEC-003: gv_col_pile_h/4 returns the count of non-bg cells in column C.
gv_row_pile_w/4 returns the count of non-bg cells in row R. gv_all_col_piles/3
returns the list of pile heights for all columns in index order.
gv_all_row_piles/3 returns the list of pile widths for all rows in index order.

WP-244-SPEC-004: gv_floating_cells/3 returns R-C pairs for non-bg cells that have
a BgColor cell directly below them in the same column; these are the cells that
would move under downward gravity in one step. gv_settled/2 succeeds if and only
if no floating cells exist (gv_floating_cells returns []).

WP-244-SPEC-005: gv_col_gap_above/4 returns the count of BgColor cells at the top
of column C before the first non-bg cell (the gap that would exist after
fall_down). Returns the full column height if the column is entirely BgColor.

WP-244-SPEC-006: gv_max_col_pile/3 returns the index of the column with the most
non-bg cells; ties are broken by lowest column index. gv_min_col_pile/3 returns
the index of the column with the fewest non-bg cells; ties by lowest index;
includes zero-pile columns.

WP-244-SPEC-007: gv_non_bg_count/3 returns the total count of non-BgColor cells
in the entire grid. The count is invariant under any gravity operation.

Part 235 - Work Package 245: gridtile Pack (gti_*, Layer 224)

WP-245-SPEC-001: The gridtile pack (Layer 224) provides fourteen predicates for
detecting, extracting, verifying, and constructing tiling patterns in raw grids.
A grid has vertical period P if H mod P = 0 and every row R equals row R mod P.
A grid has horizontal period P if W mod P = 0 and every column C equals col C mod P.

WP-245-SPEC-002: gti_h_period/2 returns the smallest valid vertical period.
gti_w_period/2 returns the smallest valid horizontal period. gti_tile_size/3
returns both periods. These predicates always succeed since H divides H and W
divides W (trivial period = full dimension).

WP-245-SPEC-003: gti_is_tiling/3 checks that a given (TH, TW) pair is a valid
tiling period. gti_extract_tile/4 returns the top-left TH x TW sub-grid.
gti_tile_to_grid/4 builds an H x W grid by tiling a given pattern so that
cell (R,C) = Tile[R mod TH][C mod TW].

WP-245-SPEC-004: gti_row_is_periodic/3 checks if a row of given length has period P.
gti_col_is_periodic/3 checks if a column in the grid has vertical period P.
gti_tile_count_h/3 returns H div TH; gti_tile_count_w/3 returns W div TW.

WP-245-SPEC-005: gti_matches_tile/4 checks if the TH x TW sub-grid at (R0,C0) equals
a given tile. gti_tile_offset/5 maps a cell (R,C) to its position (TileR-TileC)
within the tile given periods (TH, TW). gti_all_tiles/4 lists all tile sub-grids
in row-major order when the grid is tiled by (TH, TW).

WP-245-SPEC-006: gti_crop_to_tile/2 extracts the minimal tile by computing
h_period and w_period and returning the top-left sub-grid of that size. This
is the inverse of gti_tile_to_grid applied to the minimal periods.

Part 236 - Work Package 246: gridmark Pack (gmk_*, Layer 225)

WP-246-SPEC-001: The gridmark pack (Layer 225) provides fourteen predicates for
creating annotated copies of a grid with specific cells overwritten by a mark color.
All operations are non-destructive: the input Grid is unchanged and Marked is a
new grid.

WP-246-SPEC-002: gmk_mark_cell/5 marks a single cell (R,C). gmk_mark_cells/4
marks a list of R-C pairs. gmk_mark_row/4 marks all cells in row R.
gmk_mark_col/4 marks all cells in column C. gmk_mark_rect/7 marks all cells
in the rectangle rows [R0..R1], cols [C0..C1].

WP-246-SPEC-003: gmk_mark_border/3 marks all outer-ring cells (row 0, row H-1,
col 0, col W-1). gmk_mark_diagonal/3 marks cells where R = C (main diagonal, for
R and C both in range). gmk_mark_anti_diagonal/3 marks cells where R + C = W - 1.
gmk_mark_corners/3 marks the four corner cells.

WP-246-SPEC-004: gmk_mark_cross/3 marks the center row (H//2) and center column
(W//2), forming a cross. gmk_mark_checkerboard/3 marks all cells where (R+C) mod 2 = 0.

WP-246-SPEC-005: gmk_marked_cells/3 returns the list of R-C pairs for all cells
with MarkColor, in row-major order. gmk_is_marked/4 checks if a single cell has
MarkColor. gmk_erase/4 replaces all cells with MarkColor by BgColor, reversing
any marking operation.

Part 237 - Work Package 247: gridcrop Pack (gcr_*, Layer 226)

WP-247-SPEC-001: The gridcrop pack (Layer 226) provides fourteen predicates for
cropping, trimming, padding, centering, and expanding grids. All operations are
non-destructive and return new grids. Raw grid format: list of rows, each a list
of color atoms, 0-indexed.

WP-247-SPEC-002: gcr_bbox/3 returns the bounding box R0-C0-R1-C1 of all non-BgColor
cells. It fails if every cell equals BgColor. gcr_crop_bbox/3 crops a grid to that
bounding box. gcr_trim/3 removes all outer uniform-BgColor rows and columns and is
equivalent to gcr_crop_bbox/3. gcr_trim_rows/3 removes only leading and trailing
uniform-BgColor rows (columns unchanged). gcr_trim_cols/3 removes only leading and
trailing uniform-BgColor columns (rows unchanged).

WP-247-SPEC-003: gcr_crop/6 extracts the sub-grid at rows R0..R1 and columns C0..C1
(0-indexed, inclusive). gcr_pad_to/5 extends a grid with BgColor to at least TargetH
rows and TargetW columns, adding extra rows at the bottom and extra columns on the right;
dimensions already meeting the target are not changed.

WP-247-SPEC-004: gcr_center_in/5 places a grid in the center of a TargetH x TargetW
BgColor frame. Vertical offset is floor((TargetH-H)/2); horizontal offset is
floor((TargetW-W)/2). gcr_add_border/4 adds N rows and N columns of Color on all four
sides. gcr_remove_border/4 removes N rows and columns from all four sides.

WP-247-SPEC-005: gcr_expand_down/4 appends N new rows of Color at the bottom.
gcr_expand_right/4 appends N new columns of Color at the right. gcr_content_h/3
returns the height of the non-BgColor bounding box (MaxR-MinR+1). gcr_content_w/3
returns the width of the non-BgColor bounding box (MaxC-MinC+1).

Part 238 - Work Package 248: gridpatch Pack (gpt_*, Layer 227)

WP-248-SPEC-001: The gridpatch pack (Layer 227) provides fourteen predicates for
extracting, placing, overlaying, searching, tiling, scattering, and inpainting
sub-grid regions (patches). All operations are non-destructive. A patch is itself
a grid: a list of rows, each a list of color atoms, 0-indexed.

WP-248-SPEC-002: gpt_extract/6 extracts a sub-grid from rows R0..R1 and columns
C0..C1. gpt_place/5 pastes a Patch at position (R0,C0), overwriting cells in
the Grid. gpt_overlay/6 pastes a Patch at (R0,C0) with transparency: Patch cells
with color TranspColor are not copied, leaving the Grid cell intact.

WP-248-SPEC-003: gpt_match_at/4 checks if a Patch exactly matches the sub-grid
of Grid starting at (R0,C0). gpt_find_all/3 returns all R0-C0 positions (row-major)
where Patch matches. gpt_count/3 counts the number of matching positions.
gpt_replace_first/4 replaces the first (top-left) matching occurrence of OldPatch
with NewPatch.

WP-248-SPEC-004: gpt_scatter/4 places Patch at every R0-C0 position in a list,
applying placements left to right. gpt_tile_fill/4 builds an H x W grid by tiling
Patch so that cell (R,C) = Patch[R mod PH][C mod PW].

WP-248-SPEC-005: gpt_h/2 returns the row count of a patch. gpt_w/2 returns the
column count. gpt_size/3 returns both. gpt_eq/2 checks if two patches are identical.
gpt_inpaint/7 fills the rectangle [R0..R1] x [C0..C1] in Grid with a Color value.

Part 239 - Work Package 249: gridscan Pack (gsn_*, Layer 228)

WP-249-SPEC-001: The gridscan pack (Layer 228) provides fourteen predicates for
scanning rows and columns in four cardinal directions (right, left, down, up).
Predicates detect the nearest non-background cell in a direction, measure the
distance to it, collect all non-background cells in a row or column, and test
whether any non-background cell exists in a direction.

WP-249-SPEC-002: gsn_scan_row/4 returns all non-BgColor cells in row R as
C-V pairs (column-value) ordered by column. gsn_scan_col/4 returns all non-BgColor
cells in column C as R-V pairs (row-value) ordered by row.

WP-249-SPEC-003: gsn_first_right/5 returns the first non-BgColor cell going right
from column C0 in row R as C-V. gsn_first_left/5 returns the nearest non-BgColor
cell going left from C0. gsn_first_down/5 returns the first non-BgColor cell going
down from row R0 in column C as R-V. gsn_first_up/5 returns the nearest cell going
up. All four predicates fail if no such cell exists.

WP-249-SPEC-004: gsn_dist_right/5 returns D = C_hit - C0 (minimum 1) for the
first non-BgColor cell going right; fails if none. gsn_dist_left/5 returns
D = C0 - C_hit. gsn_dist_down/5 returns D = R_hit - R0. gsn_dist_up/5 returns
D = R0 - R_hit.

WP-249-SPEC-005: gsn_blocked_right/4, gsn_blocked_left/4, gsn_blocked_down/4,
and gsn_blocked_up/4 succeed if any non-BgColor cell exists in the named direction
from the given position. They are defined as wrappers around the corresponding
gsn_first_* predicates.

Part 240 - Work Package 250: gridwave Pack (gwv_*, Layer 229)

WP-250-SPEC-001: The gridwave pack (Layer 229) provides fourteen predicates for
color wave propagation, frontier detection, single-color expansion, directional
shadow casting, and interior contraction on symbolic grids.

WP-250-SPEC-002: gwv_step/3 applies one wave-expansion step: each background cell
adjacent (4-connected) to exactly one non-background color takes that color.
Cells adjacent to two or more different non-background colors remain background
(conflict). gwv_fill/3 repeats gwv_step until the grid reaches a fixed point.
gwv_fill_n/4 applies exactly N steps.

WP-250-SPEC-003: gwv_frontier/3 returns the list of R-C positions of background
cells that border at least one non-background cell (4-connected). gwv_color_frontier/4
returns only cells adjacent to a specific color. gwv_equidistant_front/3 returns
cells adjacent to two or more different non-background colors (conflict boundary cells).

WP-250-SPEC-004: gwv_color_expand/4 expands a single named color one step: each
background cell adjacent to that color becomes that color; other colors are unchanged.
gwv_color_expand_n/5 applies exactly N single-color expansion steps.

WP-250-SPEC-005: gwv_shadow_right/4, gwv_shadow_down/4, gwv_shadow_left/4, and
gwv_shadow_up/4 cast directional shadows: each background cell that lies downstream
of any non-background cell (in the named direction, with no non-background cell
between them) becomes ShadowColor. Non-background cells keep their value.
gwv_contract/3 removes non-background cells that have at least one in-bounds
4-connected background neighbor. gwv_contract_n/4 applies N contraction steps.

Part 241 - Work Package 251: gridshift Pack (gsh_*, Layer 230)

WP-251-SPEC-001: The gridshift pack (Layer 230) provides fourteen predicates for
shifting, rolling, and offsetting symbolic grids. Four predicates perform linear
(non-wrapping) shifts in the four cardinal directions; vacated cells fill with a
background color. Four predicates perform cyclic (toroidal) rolls of the entire
grid. Two predicates roll individual rows or columns cyclically.

WP-251-SPEC-002: gsh_shift_right/4 shifts each row right by N cells; the leftmost N
cells become BgColor. gsh_shift_left/4 shifts left. gsh_shift_down/4 shifts all rows
down by N; N new BgColor rows appear at the top. gsh_shift_up/4 shifts up. In all
four directional shifts, cells that move beyond the grid boundary are lost.

WP-251-SPEC-003: gsh_roll_right/3 and gsh_roll_left/3 cyclically roll each row by N
cells (toroidal). gsh_roll_down/3 and gsh_roll_up/3 cyclically roll the entire row list
by N rows. All four roll predicates are identity operations when N equals the grid width
or height respectively.

WP-251-SPEC-004: gsh_roll_row/4 cyclically rolls a single named row right by N positions.
gsh_roll_col/4 cyclically rolls a single named column down by N positions (implemented
via grid transpose). gsh_shift_row/5 shifts a single row horizontally by N cells
(positive = right, negative = left) with bg fill. gsh_shift_col/5 shifts a single
column vertically.

WP-251-SPEC-005: gsh_shift_color/6 shifts all cells of a given Color by (DR, DC);
cells that move out-of-bounds disappear; vacated positions become BgColor; non-Color
non-BgColor cells are unchanged. gsh_offset/5 shifts the entire grid by (DR, DC):
Result[R][C] = Grid[R-DR][C-DC] if in bounds, else BgColor.

Part 242 - Work Package 252: gridmap Pack (gmp_*, Layer 231)

WP-252-SPEC-001: The gridmap pack (Layer 231) provides fourteen predicates for
color mapping and substitution operations on symbolic grids. The pack covers
atomic cell remapping, color swapping, replacement and merging, canonical
normalization, palette extraction, foreground recoloring, color masking, palette
inversion and cycling, mapping construction from aligned grids, map inversion,
map composition, and mapped-cell counting.

WP-252-SPEC-002: gmp_remap/3 applies a list of From-To color pairs to every cell
in a grid; cells whose color does not appear as a From key are left unchanged.
gmp_swap/4 swaps two specific colors throughout the grid (bidirectional single-step
remap). gmp_replace/4 replaces one specific color with another. gmp_merge/4
replaces a list of colors with a single target color.

WP-252-SPEC-003: gmp_normalize/3 assigns integer rank labels (1, 2, 3, ...) to
non-BgColor cells in the order they first appear in row-major scan order; BgColor
cells remain BgColor. gmp_palette/3 returns the ordered list of distinct non-BgColor
colors in first-occurrence row-major order.

WP-252-SPEC-004: gmp_recolor_fg/4 replaces all non-BgColor cells with a single
FgColor; BgColor cells remain unchanged. gmp_mask_color/4 keeps cells of one
specified Color and replaces all other cells with BgColor.

WP-252-SPEC-005: gmp_invert/3 reverses palette assignments given an explicit
Palette list: color at position i maps to color at position (n+1-i). gmp_cycle/4
cyclically advances each cell's palette index by N positions modulo the palette
length. gmp_build_map/4 derives a From-To mapping from two same-sized grids by
collecting positions where both grids have non-BgColor values that differ.
gmp_invert_map/2 reverses all From-To pairs to To-From. gmp_compose_maps/3 chains
two mappings by finding all From-Mid-To paths. gmp_map_count/3 counts cells whose
color appears as a From key in a mapping.

Part 243 - Work Package 253: gridrefl Pack (grf_*, Layer 232)

WP-253-SPEC-001: The gridrefl pack (Layer 232) provides fourteen predicates for
geometric reflection and rotation of symbolic grids. The pack covers horizontal
and vertical flips, clockwise rotations by 90, 180, and 270 degrees, main-diagonal
and anti-diagonal transpositions, symmetry detection on all four axes, enumeration
of all symmetry axes, and symmetry completion in both directions.

WP-253-SPEC-002: grf_flip_h/2 reverses each row (left-right mirror). grf_flip_v/2
reverses the list of rows (top-bottom mirror). grf_rot90/2 rotates 90 degrees
clockwise (transpose then flip_h). grf_rot180/2 rotates 180 degrees (flip_v then
flip_h). grf_rot270/2 rotates 270 degrees clockwise / 90 degrees counter-clockwise
(flip_h then transpose). Four successive rot90 steps return the original grid.

WP-253-SPEC-003: grf_transpose/2 swaps rows and columns (main-diagonal reflection).
grf_antidiag/2 reflects across the anti-diagonal (rot180 then transpose); for a
square NxN grid, AntiDiag[R][C] = Grid[N-1-C][N-1-R]. Both operations are
self-inverse (applying twice gives the original grid).

WP-253-SPEC-004: grf_is_sym_h/1 succeeds if the grid equals its horizontal flip.
grf_is_sym_v/1 succeeds if the grid equals its vertical flip. grf_is_sym_d/1
succeeds if the grid equals its own transpose (meaningful only for square grids).
grf_is_sym_a/1 succeeds if the grid equals its own anti-diagonal reflection.
grf_sym_axes/2 returns the subset of [h, v, d, a] for which the corresponding
symmetry test succeeds.

WP-253-SPEC-005: grf_make_sym_h/3 makes a grid horizontally symmetric by merging
each row with its reversal: for each position, if the original cell is non-BgColor
it keeps its value; if it is BgColor and the mirror cell is non-BgColor, the mirror
value is used; otherwise BgColor. grf_make_sym_v/3 applies the same logic row-wise,
merging row R with row (H-1-R).

Part 244 - Work Package 254: gridlogic Pack (ggl_*, Layer 233)

WP-254-SPEC-001: The gridlogic pack (Layer 233) provides fourteen predicates for
cell-wise logical and set-theoretic operations on symbolic grids. All operations
treat one designated BgColor as the logical "false" or background value; all other
colors are treated as "true" or foreground. Fourteen predicates cover pairwise
binary operations, list-wide reductions, conditional selection, and color filtering.

WP-254-SPEC-002: ggl_and/4 produces a cell where both grids are non-bg; ggl_or/4
produces a cell where at least one grid is non-bg (first wins on overlap); ggl_xor/4
produces a cell where exactly one grid is non-bg; ggl_not/4 inverts: bg→FgColor and
non-bg→bg. ggl_subtract/4 keeps Grid1 cells that are absent from Grid2 (Grid1 non-bg
and Grid2 bg). ggl_common/4 keeps cells where both grids agree on the same non-bg
color. ggl_differ/4 keeps Grid1 cells where both are non-bg but values differ.

WP-254-SPEC-003: ggl_any/3 takes a list of grids and produces the cell-wise OR: the
first non-bg value across all grids wins. ggl_all/3 produces the cell-wise AND across
a list: non-bg value if all grids agree on the same non-bg color; else bg.
ggl_majority/3 uses plurality voting: the most frequent non-bg color at each position
if it appears more than N/2 times (where N is the list length); else bg.

WP-254-SPEC-004: ggl_unanimous/3 requires all grids (including bg cells) to agree at
each position; any disagreement yields bg. Unlike ggl_all, unanimous considers bg/non-bg
agreement: [[b,b],[b,b]] and [[r,b],[b,b]] disagree at (0,0) so output is bg there.

WP-254-SPEC-005: ggl_mask/5 keeps Grid's cell values where MaskGrid equals MaskColor;
all other cells become BgColor. ggl_if/5 selects ThenGrid's cell value where CondGrid
equals CondColor; otherwise ElseGrid's value. ggl_filter/4 keeps only cells whose
color appears in a given list; all others become BgColor.

Part 245 - Work Package 255: gridchain Pack (gch_*, Layer 234)

WP-255-SPEC-001: The gridchain pack (Layer 234) provides fourteen predicates for
structural manipulation of sequences (lists) of grids. It covers consecutive
pairing (gch_pairs), sliding windows (gch_window), element-wise zipping (gch_zip),
prefix/suffix extraction (gch_take, gch_drop), indexed access (gch_nth), sameness
testing (gch_all_same), deduplication (gch_dedup), repetition (gch_cycle),
interleaving (gch_interleave), splitting (gch_split_at), reversal (gch_reverse),
per-pair change counts (gch_diff_counts), and first-vs-last change masks
(gch_changes_mask). All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-255-SPEC-002: gch_pairs/2 produces a list of consecutive two-element sublists
from a sequence of grids. An empty or single-element sequence yields an empty
result. gch_window/3 generalises this to overlapping windows of width W;
W > length(Grids) yields an empty result. Both predicates use findall with
nth0-based indexing for clean, deterministic output.

WP-255-SPEC-003: gch_zip/3 pairs two sequences element-wise, stopping at the
shorter. gch_take/3 and gch_drop/3 both clamp to the actual list length rather
than failing when the requested index exceeds it. gch_split_at/4 uses the
length/append idiom to split cleanly without arithmetic.

WP-255-SPEC-004: gch_dedup/2 removes duplicate grids while preserving the order of
first occurrence. It uses an accumulator (Seen list) identical in structure to
gmp_unique_ordered_ in gridmap. gch_all_same/1 matches [G,G|Rest] recursively and
fails immediately on any pair that differs.

WP-255-SPEC-005: gch_diff_counts/3 delegates to gch_pairs and then counts differing
positions using recursive cell-level helpers with a cut on the equal-cell clause.
gch_changes_mask/4 compares only the first and last grids (using last/2), producing
a binary mask with MarkColor at changed positions and BgColor elsewhere. A
single-element sequence returns an all-BgColor mask of the same dimensions.

Part 246 - Work Package 256: gridblend Pack (gbld_*, Layer 235)

WP-256-SPEC-001: The gridblend pack (Layer 235) provides ten predicates for
blending and compositing grids using layered priority, transparency, spatial
patterns, and voting. All operations treat one designated BgColor as transparent.
The pack covers gbld_overlay/4, gbld_underlay/4, gbld_stencil/4, gbld_priority/3,
gbld_checker_blend/5, gbld_stripe_blend/5, gbld_threshold_replace/5,
gbld_merge_many/3, gbld_dominant/3, and gbld_composite/4. All 44 tests pass.

WP-256-SPEC-002: gbld_overlay/4 places a Top grid over a Bottom grid: non-bg
cells in Top show; bg cells in Top are transparent and reveal Bottom. gbld_underlay
is the inverse: Bottom wins over Top. gbld_stencil/4 keeps Source cells only at
positions where a Stencil grid equals StencilColor; other positions output
StencilColor as the "erased" value.

WP-256-SPEC-003: gbld_priority/3 folds a list of grids with the first as topmost
layer, reducing by repeated gbld_overlay. gbld_merge_many/3 folds with the last
as topmost, reducing by accumulating from the bottom up. Both produce a single
composite grid where the first or last non-bg value at each position wins.

WP-256-SPEC-004: gbld_checker_blend/5 blends two grids by checkerboard parity:
positions where (R+C) mod 2 = Parity take from Grid1; all others from Grid2.
gbld_stripe_blend/5 blends by horizontal row stripes of StripeWidth rows each,
alternating between Grid1 and Grid2 within even/odd stripe bands.

WP-256-SPEC-005: gbld_threshold_replace/5 replaces all non-bg cells in rows where
the non-bg count meets or exceeds a threshold. gbld_dominant/3 performs a
per-cell plurality vote across a list of grids, selecting the most frequent non-bg
value (all-bg positions remain bg). gbld_composite/4 dispatches to overlay,
underlay (merge_many), or dominant based on a Mode atom.

Part 247 - Work Package 257: gridextract Pack (gxt_*, Layer 236)

WP-257-SPEC-001: The gridextract pack (Layer 236) provides fourteen predicates for
collecting cells, computing bounding boxes, extracting crops, and building object
registries from symbolic grids. Predicates: gxt_nonbg_cells/3, gxt_color_cells/3,
gxt_bbox/4, gxt_crop_bbox/5, gxt_object_at/5, gxt_all_colors/3,
gxt_color_count/4, gxt_largest_color/3, gxt_smallest_color/3,
gxt_centered_crop/5, gxt_row_cells/4, gxt_col_cells/4, gxt_region_count/4,
gxt_registry/3. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-257-SPEC-002: gxt_nonbg_cells/3 and gxt_color_cells/3 collect non-bg or
specific-color cells as r(R,C,V) triples in row-major order. gxt_bbox/4 computes
the tight bounding box over all non-bg cells and returns bb(MinR,MinC,MaxR,MaxC);
it fails if the grid is all-bg. gxt_crop_bbox/5 extracts the sub-grid for a given
bounding box and returns an off(R1,C1) origin offset.

WP-257-SPEC-003: gxt_object_at/5 finds the bounding box of the 4-connected region
of same-color cells reachable from a given starting cell, using BFS flood fill.
gxt_region_count/4 counts distinct 4-connected same-color regions by repeatedly
flood-filling and removing visited cells from the worklist.

WP-257-SPEC-004: gxt_largest_color/3 and gxt_smallest_color/3 return the non-bg
color with the most and fewest cells respectively, using msort on count-color pairs
for deterministic tie-breaking. gxt_centered_crop/5 computes the centroid of all
non-bg cells, clamps a crop window of the requested size to the grid boundaries,
and extracts the sub-grid.

WP-257-SPEC-005: gxt_registry/3 builds an obj(Color,Count,BBox) record for each
unique non-bg color, sorted by color in msort order. gxt_row_cells/4 and
gxt_col_cells/4 return non-bg cells in a specified 0-indexed row or column as
r(R,C,V) triples. gxt_all_colors/3 returns a sorted unique list of all non-bg
colors present.

Part 248 - Work Package 258: gridgrav Pack (gra_*, Layer 237)

WP-258-SPEC-001: The gridgrav pack (Layer 237) provides fourteen predicates for
making non-bg cells fall or slide toward edges of rows and columns. Predicates:
gra_fall_down/3, gra_fall_up/3, gra_fall_left/3, gra_fall_right/3, gra_fall/4,
gra_col_nonbg/4, gra_row_nonbg/4, gra_set_col_bottom/5, gra_set_col_top/5,
gra_set_row_left/5, gra_set_row_right/5, gra_blocked_fall/5, gra_is_settled/2,
gra_gravity_score/3. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-258-SPEC-002: gra_fall_down/3, gra_fall_up/3, gra_fall_left/3, and
gra_fall_right/3 apply gravity in a named direction to the whole grid. Each
predicate works column-by-column (for down/up) or row-by-row (for left/right),
collecting non-bg values and packing them to the target edge while filling the
vacated positions with the background color. Relative order among non-bg values
within each column or row is preserved.

WP-258-SPEC-003: gra_fall/4 dispatches to the four directional predicates by a
direction atom (down, up, left, right) using deterministic cuts. gra_col_nonbg/4
and gra_row_nonbg/4 extract non-bg values from a specified column or row in
row-major order, returning them as a simple list without position information.

WP-258-SPEC-004: gra_set_col_bottom/5, gra_set_col_top/5, gra_set_row_left/5,
and gra_set_row_right/5 replace a single column or row in a grid with a supplied
list of values packed to the specified edge; remaining positions become the
background color. These predicates are composable with gra_col_nonbg and
gra_row_nonbg for extract-transform-insert workflows.

WP-258-SPEC-005: gra_blocked_fall/5 applies gravity in a named direction but
treats a specified BlockColor as an immovable wall: non-bg non-block cells fall
within each segment delimited by BlockColor positions, stopping at the wall face.
gra_is_settled/2 tests whether gra_fall_down leaves the grid unchanged.
gra_gravity_score/3 returns the number of cell positions that would differ between
the grid and its fall_down result; a score of 0 means already settled.

Part 249 - Work Package 259: gridstamp Pack (gst_*, Layer 238)

WP-259-SPEC-001: The gridstamp pack (Layer 238) provides fourteen predicates for
placing patterns on grids, finding matches, manipulating grid borders and
dimensions, and creating blank canvases. Predicates: gst_stamp/6, gst_stamp_all/5,
gst_scatter/5, gst_find_matches/4, gst_stamp_count/4, gst_pad/5, gst_unpad/3,
gst_replicate_h/4, gst_replicate_v/4, gst_border/5, gst_center/5, gst_extract/6,
gst_replace/5, gst_canvas/4. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-259-SPEC-002: gst_stamp/6 pastes a Stamp grid at a given (R,C) position in a
Grid, using the background color as transparency: non-bg cells in Stamp overwrite;
bg cells in Stamp leave the original Grid cell unchanged. Stamp cells that fall
outside the Grid boundary are silently ignored. gst_stamp_all/5 applies the same
stamp at each position in a list, accumulating results left to right.

WP-259-SPEC-003: gst_scatter/5 places a single Color value at every (R,C)
position in a list, unconditionally overwriting whatever was there. gst_find_matches/4
finds all top-left positions where a Pattern grid matches the corresponding Grid
subgrid exactly (cell by cell). gst_stamp_count/4 wraps gst_find_matches to return
a count. Both find_matches and stamp_count handle patterns larger than the Grid by
returning zero matches.

WP-259-SPEC-004: gst_pad/5 pads a Grid to at least H rows and W columns using the
background color, anchored at the top-left. gst_unpad/3 removes all-bg border rows
and columns, returning the tight bounding rectangle of non-bg content; an all-bg
grid yields []. gst_extract/6 extracts an H x W subgrid at (R,C). gst_replace/5
places a Patch opaquely at (R,C), overwriting all cells including bg.

WP-259-SPEC-005: gst_replicate_h/4 and gst_replicate_v/4 repeat a Grid N times
side by side or stacked. gst_border/5 surrounds a Grid with a colored border of
given thickness T, producing a grid of height GH+2T and width GW+2T. gst_center/5
places a Grid at the center of an H x W bg canvas using integer division for
alignment. gst_canvas/4 creates a blank all-bg grid of the given dimensions.

Part 250 - Work Package 260: gridalign Pack (gal_*, Layer 239)

WP-260-SPEC-001: The gridalign pack (Layer 239) provides fourteen predicates for
computing alignment properties of symbolic grids: center of mass, bounding box,
bounding box center, translation, overlap counting and scoring, intersection-over-
union, offset search, center alignment, bbox-center alignment, centroid offset
vector, placement at a position, anchor-based placement, and any-overlap offset
search. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-260-SPEC-002: gal_center_of_mass/3 returns the integer-floor average (R,C) of
all non-bg cell indices. gal_nonbg_bbox/3 returns the tight bounding box r0(R0,C0,R1,C1)
or the atom none for all-bg grids. gal_bbox_center/3 returns the floor center of the
bounding box. All three predicates fail gracefully on all-bg inputs.

WP-260-SPEC-003: gal_translate/5 shifts every non-bg cell by (DR,DC) within the
same grid dimensions; cells that move out of bounds become Bg. gal_overlap_count/4
counts positions where both grids have non-bg cells. gal_overlap_score/4 normalises
by Grid1's non-bg count. gal_iou/4 computes intersection-over-union of non-bg regions
using negation to avoid double-counting the disjunction.

WP-260-SPEC-004: gal_find_offset/5 searches all (DR,DC) in [-SearchR,SearchR]^2,
shifts Grid2's non-bg cells by each candidate, and selects the offset maximising
overlap with Grid1's non-bg cells (ties broken by minimum Manhattan distance).
gal_align_centers/4 and gal_align_bbox_centers/4 apply gal_translate after computing
the required shift; both return Grid2 unchanged if either grid has no non-bg cells.

WP-260-SPEC-005: gal_place_at/6 pastes Grid2 transparently onto a canvas at (R0,C0)
using the same transparency model as gridstamp. gal_anchor_to/8 computes (R0,C0)
from a given cell-to-cell alignment (PR,PC) in Grid2 to (QR,QC) in Canvas and
delegates to gal_place_at. gal_match_any_offset/4 finds all (DR,DC) offsets where
at least one non-bg cell of Grid2, after translation, lands on a non-bg cell of Grid1.


Part 251: Work Package 261 - gridcolorop Pack (gco_*, Layer 240)

WP-261-SPEC-001: The gridcolorop pack (Layer 240) provides fourteen predicates
for querying, transforming, and analyzing colors in symbolic grids. The pack
covers color counting, distinct-color listing, Nth-color selection, color
swapping, color replacement, map-based substitution, keep-only masking, color
removal, palette cycling, frequency-rank replacement, palette application,
most/least frequent color query, and binary inversion. All 44 acceptance
tests pass.

WP-261-SPEC-002: gco_color_counts/3 returns cc(Color,Count) pairs for all
non-bg colors sorted by count descending. gco_distinct_colors/3 extracts the
color list from those pairs. gco_nth_color/4 returns the Nth most frequent
non-bg color (0-indexed). gco_count_distinct/3 returns the count of distinct
non-bg colors.

WP-261-SPEC-003: gco_swap/5 exchanges Color1 and Color2 throughout a grid;
all other cells including Bg are unchanged. gco_replace/5 replaces every
occurrence of OldColor with NewColor (including Bg cells if OldColor=Bg).
gco_apply_map/4 applies a list of OldColor-NewColor pairs; cells not matching
any key are unchanged.

WP-261-SPEC-004: gco_keep_only/4 keeps cells matching Color and replaces all
others with Bg. gco_remove_color/4 replaces Color cells with Bg while keeping
all others unchanged. gco_cycle/5 advances each palette-member cell N steps
through the Palette list (modular, supports negative N for backward cycling);
cells not in Palette are unchanged.

WP-261-SPEC-005: gco_rank_grid/3 replaces each non-bg cell with the 0-indexed
frequency rank of its color (0 = most frequent); Bg cells remain Bg.
gco_apply_palette/4 replaces the Kth most frequent non-bg color with the Kth
entry in a Palette list; colors beyond Palette length are unchanged.
gco_most_least/4 returns the most and least frequent non-bg colors.
gco_invert/4 is a binary invert: non-bg cells become Bg and Bg cells become
FgColor. Critically, gco_sort_by_count_desc_ uses Neg is -N (arithmetic
evaluation) to compute integer negation, not the term -N which would create
the compound -(N) and sort in the wrong direction.


Part 252: Work Package 262 - gridresize Pack (grs_*, Layer 241)

WP-262-SPEC-001: The gridresize pack (Layer 241) provides fourteen predicates
for scaling, resizing, tiling, cropping, and fitting symbolic grids. The pack
covers integer scale up and down, mode-based downsampling, double and halve
shortcuts, nearest-neighbor resize to arbitrary dimensions, modular tiling,
rectangular cropping, border cropping, aspect-ratio-preserving fit into a canvas,
centering a grid in a larger canvas, dimension querying, aspect ratio, and
square test. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-262-SPEC-002: grs_scale_up/3 expands each cell into an F x F block; the
output is (H*F) x (W*F). grs_scale_down/4 samples the top-left cell of each
F x F block, producing a floor(H/F) x floor(W/F) result. grs_scale_down_mode/4
takes the mode (most common value) of each block; ties are broken by msort order
(lexicographically first atom). Returns [] when the scaled result would be 0x0.

WP-262-SPEC-003: grs_double/2 and grs_halve/3 are shorthands for F=2.
grs_resize/5 performs nearest-neighbor resizing: output[r][c] =
input[floor(r*H/NewH)][floor(c*W/NewW)]. Returns [] for NewH=0 or NewW=0.
grs_tile_to/4 fills a target H x W grid by modular repetition of the source.

WP-262-SPEC-004: grs_crop/6 extracts rows [R0,R1] x cols [C0,C1] with clamping
to grid bounds; returns [] for an empty range. grs_border_crop/4 removes N rows
and columns from all four borders; returns [] when the result would be empty.
grs_embed_in/5 centers a grid on a Bg canvas of specified dimensions.

WP-262-SPEC-005: grs_fit_in/5 scales a grid to fit within H x W while preserving
aspect ratio (letterbox), then centers it on a Bg canvas. It uses float arithmetic
to compute the scale factor and rounds to the nearest integer pixel.
grs_grid_size/3 and grs_aspect_ratio/4 report dimensions. grs_is_square/1 tests
whether H = W. Critical design note: all if-then-else blocks that follow a
grs_dims_ call must be wrapped in explicit outer parentheses, because without them
SWI-Prolog parses the preceding comma-chain as part of the condition, leaving H
and W unbound in the else branch.


Part 253: Work Package 263 - gridobj Pack (gob_*, Layer 242)

WP-263-SPEC-001: The gridobj pack (Layer 242) provides fourteen predicates for
4-connected component analysis, extraction, and manipulation in symbolic grids.
The pack covers component cell enumeration, color and size query, bounding box,
binary mask, subgrid extraction, full object inventory, count, largest/smallest
component selection, flood fill, enclosed-region fill, object removal, and object
movement. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-263-SPEC-002: gob_object_cells/4 enumerates all cells in the 4-connected
component at (R,C) using BFS. gob_object_color/4 returns the color at (R,C).
gob_object_size/4 returns the count of cells in the component. gob_object_bbox/4
returns the tight bounding box r0(R0,C0,R1,C1). gob_object_mask/5 produces a
full-grid mask with the component's color at component positions and Bg elsewhere.

WP-263-SPEC-003: gob_extract_object/5 returns the bounding-box subgrid of the
component, with non-component cells filled with Bg. gob_all_objects/3 returns a
list of ob(Color,Cells,BBox) for all non-Bg connected components in scan order.
gob_object_count/3 returns the count of such components.

WP-263-SPEC-004: gob_largest_object/3 returns the cells of the component with
the most cells; gob_smallest_object/3 returns the cells of the component with
the fewest cells. Both fail if Grid has no non-Bg cells. gob_flood_fill/5
replaces a component with a new color. gob_fill_enclosed/4 fills all Bg regions
that have no 4-connected path to the grid border.

WP-263-SPEC-005: gob_remove_object/5 replaces a component with Bg.
gob_move_object/7 moves a component by computing the offset from the component's
bounding-box top-left to the target (NewR,NewC), removes the original, and places
the component at the new position. Cells that would fall outside grid bounds are
clipped. The BFS in gob_bfs_ checks both the Visited set and the current frontier
(Rest) to prevent any cell from being added to the frontier twice.


Part 254: Work Package 264 - gridgroupby Pack (ggb_*, Layer 243)

WP-264-SPEC-001: The gridgroupby pack (Layer 243) provides fourteen predicates for
grouping, filtering, sorting, pairing, and counting ob(Color,Cells,BBox) object terms
produced by gob_all_objects/3. All operations are general-purpose list transformations
over object lists and do not depend on any specific grid representation. All 44
acceptance tests pass.

WP-264-SPEC-002: ggb_group_by_color/2 groups objects by their shared color into
grp(Color,ObjList) terms. ggb_group_by_size/2 groups objects by shared cell count.
ggb_group_by_row/2 groups objects by the top row of their bounding box.
ggb_group_by_col/2 groups objects by the left column of their bounding box. All four
group-by predicates return groups in ascending key order.

WP-264-SPEC-003: ggb_filter_by_color/3 returns the sub-list of objects matching a
given color. ggb_filter_by_size/3 returns objects whose cell count equals a given
value. ggb_filter_larger/3 returns objects whose cell count is strictly greater than N.
ggb_filter_smaller/3 returns objects whose cell count is strictly less than N.

WP-264-SPEC-004: ggb_sort_by_size_asc/2 sorts objects by cell count, smallest first.
ggb_sort_by_size_desc/2 sorts objects by cell count, largest first. ggb_sort_by_row/2
sorts objects by the top row of their bounding box. ggb_sort_by_col/2 sorts objects
by the left column of their bounding box.

WP-264-SPEC-005: ggb_pair_by_color/2 returns a list of pair(Color,Obj1,Obj2) for
each color that has exactly two objects; colors with one or three or more objects are
omitted. ggb_count_per_color/2 returns a list of cnt(Color,N) for each distinct color,
in descending count order.


Part 255: Work Package 265 - gridrelation Pack (grl_*, Layer 244)

WP-265-SPEC-001: The gridrelation pack (Layer 244) provides fourteen predicates for
computing spatial relations between ob(Color,Cells,BBox) object terms produced by
gob_all_objects/3. The pack covers touching, adjacency, minimum distance, strict
positional relations (above, below, left-of, right-of), bounding box containment,
bounding box overlap, cell overlap, row/column range overlap, primary direction, and
a comprehensive all-relations query. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-265-SPEC-002: grl_touching/2 succeeds if two objects share a 4-adjacent cell edge.
grl_adjacent/3 succeeds if any pair of cells from the two objects is within Manhattan
distance N. grl_min_distance/3 returns the minimum Manhattan distance between any
cell of ObjA and any cell of ObjB.

WP-265-SPEC-003: grl_above/2 succeeds if ObjA's last row is strictly less than ObjB's
first row. grl_below/2 succeeds if ObjA's first row is strictly greater than ObjB's
last row. grl_left_of/2 and grl_right_of/2 are the column analogues.

WP-265-SPEC-004: grl_bbox_contains/2 succeeds if ObjA's bbox fully contains ObjB's
bbox on all four sides. grl_bbox_overlap/2 succeeds if the two bbox row ranges overlap
AND the two col ranges overlap. grl_cells_overlap/2 succeeds if any cell position
appears in both objects' cell lists.

WP-265-SPEC-005: grl_same_rows/2 and grl_same_cols/2 succeed if the respective bbox
ranges overlap. grl_direction/3 returns the primary direction from ObjA to ObjB
(above, below, left, right, or overlap) by comparing doubled bbox centroids.
grl_all_relations/3 returns the list of all true relation atoms between two objects.


Part 256: Work Package 266 - gridtransform Pack (gtr_*, Layer 245)

WP-266-SPEC-001: The gridtransform pack (Layer 245) provides fourteen predicates for
detecting color mappings between two grids, computing cell-level differences, and
applying transformations. All predicates require both grids to have the same
dimensions. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-266-SPEC-002: gtr_color_map/3 detects the consistent color mapping from GridA to
GridB as a sorted list of cm(OldColor,NewColor) pairs. It fails if any source color
maps to more than one destination color at different positions. gtr_apply_color_map/3
applies a color map to a grid; unmapped colors pass through unchanged.

WP-266-SPEC-003: gtr_diff_cells/3 returns positions where the grids differ.
gtr_diff_count/3 counts them. gtr_same_cells/3 returns matching positions.
gtr_changed_colors/3 returns chg(R,C,OldColor,NewColor) for each changed position.

WP-266-SPEC-004: gtr_invert_map/2 inverts a color map; fails if the map is not
injective. gtr_compose_maps/3 composes two maps; only colors present in both appear
in the result. gtr_is_identity_map/1 succeeds if every entry has the same source and
target. gtr_apply_changes/3 applies a list of chg/4 terms to a grid.

WP-266-SPEC-005: gtr_delta_grid/4 produces a grid showing only changed cells.
gtr_overlay/4 pastes non-Bg cells of a delta grid onto a base grid. gtr_common_grid/4
keeps cells that match between two grids; others become Bg. gtr_is_color_permutation/2
succeeds if GridB is a bijective color permutation of GridA.


Part 257: Work Package 267 - gridobjmatch Pack (gom_*, Layer 246)

WP-267-SPEC-001: The gridobjmatch pack (Layer 246) provides fourteen predicates for
matching ob(Color,Cells,BBox) object terms between two lists and detecting what
changed from one list to the other. The pack covers color-based matching, nearest-
centroid matching, size-based matching, unmatched-object extraction, color-difference
partitioning, movement-vector computation, constant-move detection, color-map
inference, appeared/disappeared detection, structural equality, and object-count
change. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-267-SPEC-002: gom_match_color/3 pairs each object in Objs1 with the first object
in Objs2 sharing the same color; unmatched objects on either side are dropped silently.
gom_match_nearest/3 pairs each object in Objs1 with the nearest object in Objs2 by
doubled-centroid Manhattan distance; objects in Objs2 are consumed greedily.
gom_match_size/3 pairs objects by shared cell count (number of cells).

WP-267-SPEC-003: gom_unmatched_a/3 returns objects in Objs1 that have no partner in
any match/2 term. gom_unmatched_b/3 does the same for Objs2. gom_color_diff/3
partitions a match list into a Same sub-list (both objects share color) and a Diff
sub-list (objects have different colors).

WP-267-SPEC-004: gom_move_vector/2 computes the mv(DR,DC) displacement from the
top-left bounding-box corner of O1 to that of O2. gom_move_vectors/2 maps this over
a list of match pairs. gom_constant_move/2 succeeds if every pair in the list has the
same move vector; fails for an empty list.

WP-267-SPEC-005: gom_infer_color_map/2 collects cm(OldColor,NewColor) terms from
color-changing matched pairs and returns a deduplicated sorted list.
gom_appeared/3 returns objects in Objs2 whose color does not appear in Objs1.
gom_disappeared/3 returns objects in Objs1 whose color does not appear in Objs2.
gom_same_structure/2 succeeds if the two lists share the same multiset of colors.
gom_count_change/3 returns length(Objs2) minus length(Objs1).


Part 258: Work Package 268 - symtab Pack (st_*, Layer 247)

WP-268-SPEC-001: The symtab pack (Layer 247) provides fourteen predicates for
learning symbol-to-value mappings from training pairs. A symbol table is a list
of sym(Feature, Value) terms where Feature identifies an observable property of
an input object and Value is what that feature encodes in the output. The pack
addresses the in-context symbol definition problem: some objects in a task stand
for something other than themselves, and their meaning is defined only by the
task's own training pairs. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-268-SPEC-002: st_build_table/2 takes a list of pair(InputObjs, OutputObjs)
training pairs and returns the most specific symbol table consistent with all pairs.
st_identify_symbols/2 finds objects whose observable features co-vary with output
changes. st_contrastive_learn/2 performs cross-pair analysis to find features that
consistently predict output values.

WP-268-SPEC-003: st_apply_table/3 applies a learned symbol table to a list of input
objects and returns a color map (list of cm(OldColor, NewColor) terms). st_hole_count/2
estimates the number of enclosed gaps in an object's bounding box.
st_lookup/3 retrieves the value for a given feature from a symbol table.

WP-268-SPEC-004: st_entry_consistent/2 checks that a proposed sym entry does not
conflict with existing table entries. st_color_feature/2 and st_size_feature/2 extract
color and size features from ob/3 terms. st_position_feature/3 extracts the grid
quadrant (tl/tr/bl/br) from an ob/3 term given grid dimensions.

WP-268-SPEC-005: st_is_symbol/2 checks whether an object is plausibly a symbol by
heuristic (smaller than content objects or unique color). st_candidate_symbols/2
extracts the smallest quartile of objects as symbol candidates.
st_score_table/3 scores a table against training pairs. st_best_table/3 selects the
highest-scoring table from a list of candidates.


Part 259: Work Package 269 - invariant Pack (iv_*, Layer 248)

WP-269-SPEC-001: The invariant pack (Layer 248) provides fourteen predicates for
extracting what stays constant across all training pairs. Invariants reduce the
hypothesis search space by eliminating entire rule classes before any search begins.
Training pairs are pair(InputGrid, OutputGrid) terms. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-269-SPEC-002: iv_grid_invariants/2 finds grid-level properties (dimensions) that
are identical in every input grid across all training pairs. iv_output_invariants/2
does the same for output grids. iv_object_invariants/2 finds object-level properties
(stable color set) constant across inputs.

WP-269-SPEC-003: iv_variant_features/2 returns the complementary list of features
that DO change across training inputs, identifying candidate rule parameters.
iv_consistent_delta/2 finds input-to-output changes consistent across all pairs,
such as dims_preserved or color_set_preserved.

WP-269-SPEC-004: iv_all_grids/2 and iv_no_grids/2 are meta-predicates that test
a goal against all grids or verify its failure on all grids respectively.
iv_color_set/3 extracts non-background colors from a grid. iv_same_color_sets/2
and iv_same_dims/1 check structural equality across a list of grids.

WP-269-SPEC-005: iv_preserves_dims/1, iv_preserves_colors/1, and
iv_preserves_count/2 check cross-pair structural invariants at the pair level.
iv_stable_color_map/2 finds cell-level color mappings consistent across all pairs
by intersecting the per-pair color maps.


Part 260: Work Package 270 - contrast Pack (ca_*, Layer 249)

WP-270-SPEC-001: The contrast pack (Layer 249) provides fourteen predicates for
contrastive pair analysis across training pairs. It identifies which input features
co-vary with output changes - the key causal signal in grid transformation tasks.
Training pairs are pair(InputGrid, OutputGrid) terms. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-270-SPEC-002: ca_pairwise_delta/2 computes a delta(I, Changes) term for each
training pair, where Changes is a list of chg(R,C,OldV,NewV) terms recording every
cell that changed. ca_feature_profile/2 extracts a feature profile for a single
grid as a list of feat(Name, Value) terms covering dims, color_count, and
dominant_color.

WP-270-SPEC-003: ca_stable_features/2 returns input features constant across all
training examples. ca_unstable_features/2 returns features that vary. These two
sets are disjoint and complement each other. ca_profile_diff/3 computes the set
difference between two feature profiles.

WP-270-SPEC-004: ca_covarying_features/2 finds input features present in ALL
changing pairs but absent from stable pairs - the strongest evidence for a causal
link between feature and transformation. ca_rank_features/2 sorts all candidate
features by their correlation with output changes.

WP-270-SPEC-005: ca_context_gate/2 returns the top-ranked co-varying feature as
the rule-triggering context. ca_change_count/3 counts changing pairs containing a
given feature. ca_common_context/3, ca_correlated_features/3, ca_separates/4, and
ca_minimal_features/2 provide additional contrastive analysis tools.


Part 261: Work Package 271 - legend Pack (lg_*, Layer 250)

WP-271-SPEC-001: The legend pack (Layer 250) provides fourteen predicates for
detecting and parsing "legend" regions in grid tasks. A legend region is a small,
isolated part of the grid that acts as a code key mapping visual features to
semantic meanings. Training pairs are pair(InputGrid, OutputGrid) terms. Regions
are lists of r(Row, Col) cell coordinates. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-271-SPEC-002: lg_detect_legend/3 finds the most likely legend region in a grid
by selecting small, isolated, structurally distinct connected color regions.
lg_all_regions/3 finds all connected color regions using BFS flood-fill.
lg_region_area/2 returns the cell count of a region.

WP-271-SPEC-003: lg_is_legend/2 succeeds if a region is more likely a legend than
content (small relative to content, not touching content). lg_is_small/3 tests if
a region is at most one-quarter of the total grid area.

WP-271-SPEC-004: lg_legend_entries/2 parses a legend region into entry/2 terms by
row band. lg_color_map/3 maps each row band to the color at its first cell in the
source grid. lg_entry_boundaries/2 returns sorted unique row indices.

WP-271-SPEC-005: lg_consistent_legend/2 finds a legend structure appearing in every
training pair input. lg_same_shape/2 tests shape equivalence via normalization.
lg_position/3 classifies a region's spatial position as top, bottom, left, right,
or center. lg_separated/2 tests that two regions are not 4-connected adjacent.


Part 262: Work Package 272 - multipair Pack (mp_*, Layer 251)

WP-272-SPEC-001: The multipair pack (Layer 251) provides fourteen predicates for
tracking object identity and correspondence across multiple training pairs
simultaneously. Objects are identified by color (bg=0). Training pairs are
pair(InputGrid, OutputGrid) terms. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-272-SPEC-002: mp_track_objects/2 assigns tracked(Idx, Color, PairIdxList)
identity terms to each non-bg color across all training pair inputs.
mp_all_input_objects/2 extracts po(PairIdx, Color) terms for every non-bg color
in each pair's input. Indexing is 1-based.

WP-272-SPEC-003: mp_invariant_objects/2 finds tracked colors that appear in EVERY
training pair input. mp_role_objects/3 splits tracked objects into content
(invariant) and markers (variable). mp_cross_pair_match/2 builds match(I,J,Colors)
terms for every pair of training pair indices.

WP-272-SPEC-004: mp_universal_colors/2 and mp_variable_colors/2 find colors present
in all or some pair inputs respectively. These two sets are guaranteed disjoint.
mp_consistent_count/1 verifies that all inputs have the same number of distinct
non-bg colors. mp_modal_object_count/2 finds the most common such count.

WP-272-SPEC-005: mp_disappeared_objects/2 finds universal colors absent from all
outputs. mp_appeared_objects/2 finds colors in outputs but no inputs.
mp_stable_color_objects/2 finds universal colors with the same cell count in every
input. mp_singleton_color/2 finds colors in exactly one training pair input.


Part 263: Work Package 273 - taskcat Pack (tc_*, Layer 252)

WP-273-SPEC-001: The taskcat pack (Layer 252) provides fourteen predicates for
classifying grid transformation tasks by type and selecting solving strategies.
The four task categories are: single_rule, multi_step, context_gated, symbol_table.
Training pairs are pair(InputGrid, OutputGrid) terms. All 44 acceptance tests pass.

WP-273-SPEC-002: tc_categorize/2 implements a Chain of Responsibility pattern:
try single_rule first, then multi_step, then context_gated, then symbol_table as
the fallback. tc_suggest_strategies/2 returns an ordered strategy list for each
category, enabling fallback through seqinfer_2step, seqinfer_3step, and others.

WP-273-SPEC-003: tc_is_single_rule/1 checks for consistent change counts, uniform
change patterns, and preserved dimensions - the hallmarks of a single repeating rule.
tc_is_multi_step/1 detects tasks requiring multiple sequential steps by looking for
high max change counts relative to average, or multiple distinct change patterns.

WP-273-SPEC-004: tc_has_context_gate/1 detects tasks where some input color
consistently separates pairs by change count (the hallmark of a contextual gate).
tc_has_symbol_table/1 detects tasks where inputs have more distinct colors than
outputs (suggesting some colors are symbols, not content).

WP-273-SPEC-005: tc_is_fill_task/1 and tc_is_deletion_task/1 detect pure fill and
deletion tasks respectively. tc_preserves_dims/1 and tc_preserves_colors/1 check
structural constraints across all pairs. tc_confidence/2 returns a 0.0-1.0
confidence score for the primary category based on dims, count, and pattern stability.


Part 264: Work Package 274 - seqinfer Enhancement (sq_arc2_candidates/1)

WP-274-SPEC-001: The seqinfer pack (Layer 195) is enhanced with sq_arc2_candidates/1,
an extended rule candidate list optimized for ARC-AGI-2's four difficulty flavors:
multi-rule compositional, multi-step sequential, context-gated, and symbol-defined.
The predicate returns a list of 66 scene-level rule terms using integer colors 0-9.

WP-274-SPEC-002: sq_arc2_candidates/1 is a superset of sq_default_rules/1, adding
numeric color recolor pairs for colors 1-6, larger shift variants (2 and 3 steps),
additional remove_color and keep_color variants for colors 4-6, and top_n(1/2/3)
operators. All 52 acceptance tests (44 existing + 8 new) pass.


Part 265: Work Package 275 - hyp Enhancement (hy_spatial_hyp, hy_structural_hyp, hy_sequence_hyp)

WP-275-SPEC-001: The hyp pack (Layer 74) is enhanced with three new predicates for
grid-level hypothesis generation beyond color substitution. All 43 tests pass.

WP-275-SPEC-002: hy_spatial_hyp/3 finds a shift(DR, DC) hypothesis explaining all
training pairs by verifying that non-zero cells shifted by (DR, DC) match the output.
Candidates are tried in the order of the Moves list; the first consistent shift wins.

WP-275-SPEC-003: hy_structural_hyp/3 finds a structural(Pattern) hypothesis for
named structural properties including dims_preserved, colors_preserved,
total_nonzero_preserved, monotone_output, output_subset_of_input, and
input_subset_of_output. Returns the first pattern consistent with all pairs.

WP-275-SPEC-004: hy_sequence_hyp/4 finds a seq(Map1, Map2) two-step color-map
hypothesis: applying Map1 then Map2 to each input grid must produce the output.
Both Map1 and Map2 are color substitution maps (lists of Old-New pairs).


Part 266: Work Package 276 - condxf Enhancement (xc_infer_gate/3)

WP-276-SPEC-001: The condxf pack (Layer 187) is enhanced with xc_infer_gate/3,
which infers the gate color that separates training pairs into groups with distinct
change signatures. All 45 tests pass (41 existing + 4 new).

WP-276-SPEC-002: xc_infer_gate/3 accepts a list of pair(SceneIn, SceneOut) scene
pairs and a Variants list (reserved for future use). It returns gate_color(Color)
for the first color in sorted order that, when used to partition pairs into
"has Color in input" vs "does not have Color in input", produces distinct change
signatures in the two groups. Change signature is lost(Colors)-gained(Colors).


Part 267: Work Package 277 - induction Enhancement (id_cross_pair_invariants/2, id_cross_pair_variants/2)

WP-277-SPEC-001: The induction pack (Layer 59) is enhanced with id_cross_pair_invariants/2
and id_cross_pair_variants/2 for aggregating analysis across multiple training pairs.
All 46 tests pass (37 existing + 9 new).

WP-277-SPEC-002: id_cross_pair_invariants/2 accepts a list of pair(InGrid, OutGrid)

Properties tested: dims_preserved, colors_preserved, total_nonzero_preserved,
