returned by id_cross_pair_invariants/2 and id_cross_pair_variants/2 are disjoint.
Properties absent from both lists hold for zero pairs.


Part 268: ARC-AGI-2 Wave 5 - stub_rank_fill rule

ARC2-W5-SPEC-001: The arc_benchmark_2 module (Mentova/src/mentova/games/arc_benchmark_2.pl)
is extended with the stub_rank_fill rule. This rule is registered via arc2_named_rule/1
and implemented via arc2_transform/3 and arc2_induce_rule/2.

ARC2-W5-SPEC-002: stub_rank_fill solves ARC-AGI-2 task 97d7923e. The transformation
interprets column stubs (short top runs of non-background color V of length N) as
selection instructions: find all vertical bars with endpoint color V, sort by body
length descending, select the Nth one, and fill its body with V.

ARC2-W5-SPEC-003: A vertical bar is defined as a column sequence [V, B, B, ..., B, V]
where V is the endpoint color, B is the body color (B differs from V and from
background), and the bar is bounded above and below by background or grid edge.

ARC2-W5-SPEC-004: The stub length N is 1-indexed: stub(V, 1) selects the longest
bar with endpoint V; stub(V, 2) selects the second longest; and so on. Ties in body
length are broken by column index (leftmost first) via msort stable ordering.

ARC2-W5-SPEC-005: Multiple stubs may appear simultaneously in a single grid. All
stubs are collected before any fill is applied, and all fills are applied in one
reconstruction pass. Stubs for different endpoint colors V are independent.

ARC2-W5-SPEC-006: arc2_induce_rule(TrainingPairs, stub_rank_fill) succeeds when:
(a) all training pair input/output grids have identical dimensions;
(b) at least one non-background cell appears in the first row of the first input;
(c) arc2_transform(stub_rank_fill, In, Out) holds for every pair(In, Out).


PART 269: ARC-AGI-2 WAVE 6 - BAND WRAP RULE


ARC2-W6-SPEC-001: The band_wrap rule operates on grids where every row is a
uniform solid color (all cells in a row are identical). The input encodes a
sequence of color bands via run-length encoding of consecutive same-color rows.
A band is a maximal run of consecutive identical-color rows: (Color, Count).

ARC2-W6-SPEC-002: The output grid is square with side length
S = 2 * (TotalCount - LastCount) + LastCount = 2 * TotalCount - LastCount,
where TotalCount is the sum of all band counts and LastCount is the count of
the final band. LastCount is also the side length of the center filled square.

ARC2-W6-SPEC-003: Every cell (R, C) of the S x S output grid is assigned a
color by computing its ring index: Ring = min(R, C, S-1-R, S-1-C). The ring
index is the distance from the nearest edge, counting from 0. The outermost
cells have ring 0; the center has ring S/2 - 1 (for even S, an integer).

ARC2-W6-SPEC-004: The band that owns a ring index is determined by cumulative
band counts from the outside in. Band 1 owns rings 0 through Count1-1, Band 2
owns rings Count1 through Count1+Count2-1, and so on. The last band covers all
remaining rings including the center. arc2_bw_ring_color_/3 implements this
lookup via subtraction of counts down the band list.

ARC2-W6-SPEC-005: The transform is exactly invertible given the input: the band
sequence fully determines the output with no ambiguity. Training pairs serve to
confirm that the rule applies; one pair is sufficient for detection, but all
training pairs are verified by arc2_induce_rule/2.

ARC2-W6-SPEC-006: arc2_induce_rule(TrainingPairs, band_wrap) succeeds when:
(a) every input row of every training pair is a uniform solid-color row;
(b) run-length encoding of the first training input yields at least 2 bands;
(c) arc2_transform(band_wrap, In, Out) holds for every pair(In, Out).


PART 270: ARC-AGI-2 WAVE 7 - STAIRCASE LIFT RULE


ARC2-W7-SPEC-001: The staircase_lift rule operates on 8-row by 20-column grids
split into two halves. The left half (columns 0-8) encodes a staircase pattern
of 5-values at odd columns 1, 3, 5, 7 growing upward from a floor at row 5.
The right half (columns 9-19) holds an outer rectangular frame with four color
bars at odd columns 11, 13, 15, 17 separated by zero-valued even columns.

ARC2-W7-SPEC-002: The staircase height H[i] for bar index i (i = 0, 1, 2, 3)
is the count of consecutive 5-valued cells starting from row 5 and proceeding
upward through rows 4, 3, 2, 1 in left-half column (2*i + 1). Counting stops
at the first non-5 cell. H[i] ranges from 1 to 4.

ARC2-W7-SPEC-003: Each right-half bar at column (11 + 2*i) has an input color
C[i] and input run length L[i]. The color is the first non-0 non-5 value in
that column scanning rows 1-4 from the top. The run length is the count of
consecutive cells matching C[i] beginning at the first occurrence.

ARC2-W7-SPEC-004: The output position for bar i is determined by:
MaxEnd[i] = max(0, 5 - H[i])  (last output row for color in bar i)
OutHeight[i] = min(L[i], MaxEnd[i])  (clipped bar height)
OutEnd[i] = MaxEnd[i]
OutStart[i] = OutEnd[i] - OutHeight[i] + 1  (first output row)
Color C[i] fills rows OutStart[i] through OutEnd[i] in column (11 + 2*i).
Rows (OutEnd[i]+1) through 4 in that column are 5 (staircase fill). Row 5
receives 5 as part of the inner bottom bar spanning columns 11-17.

ARC2-W7-SPEC-005: The output left half (columns 0-8) is uniformly 0. The
outer frame of the right half is preserved: column 9 is 5 at rows 0-3 and 6-7
(0 at rows 4-5), column 19 is 5 at all rows, rows 0 and 7 are 5 across all
right-half columns. Row 6 has 5 only at columns 9 and 19.

ARC2-W7-SPEC-006: arc2_induce_rule(TrainingPairs, staircase_lift) succeeds when:
(a) the first training input has 8 rows and 20 columns;
(b) row 0 of the first training input has 0 at column 0 and 5 at column 9;
(c) row 7 of the first training input has 5 at column 9;
(d) arc2_transform(staircase_lift, In, Out) holds for every pair(In, Out).


PART 271: ARC-AGI-2 WAVE 13 - ODD COL RULE

ARC2-W13-SPEC-001: The odd_col rule operates on a grid that is an N-row by
M-col tiling of identical-sized rectangular cells separated by uniform
separator rows and separator cols. A separator row is a row in which all
cells share the same value. A separator col is a column in which all cells
in that column share the same value. The separator value need not equal the
background (most-common) value of the interior cells.

ARC2-W13-SPEC-002: Each row section is the region between two adjacent
separator rows (inclusive of both separator rows). Each col section is the
region between two adjacent separator cols (inclusive of both separator
cols). A cell is the intersection of one row section and one col section.

ARC2-W13-SPEC-003: Within each row section, all col sections contain
nearly-identical interior patterns. Exactly one col section per row section
(the odd col) has an interior pattern that differs from all others. When no
col section differs (all identical), the first col section is treated as the
canonical representative.

ARC2-W13-SPEC-004: The output grid has the same number of rows as the input
and a column width equal to one col section (c1 - c0 + 1 where c0 and c1
are the first separator col and the second separator col). For each row r
in the input, the output row is the row slice from the odd col section of
the row section containing r.

ARC2-W13-SPEC-005: The odd col section is identified by majority vote across
content rows (non-separator rows) within each row section. For each content
row, the strips (row slices) of all col sections are compared. The col
section whose strip is unique (differs from the majority strip) casts one
vote. The col section with the most votes across all content rows in the
section is the odd col. Ties or no votes default to col section index 0.

ARC2-W13-SPEC-006: arc2_induce_rule(TrainingPairs, odd_col) succeeds when
arc2_transform(odd_col, In, Out) holds for every pair(In, Out) in
TrainingPairs.

ARC2-W13-SPEC-007: odd_col solves ARC-AGI-2 task 38007db0. The input is a
19x19 grid (train 0) or 19x25 grid (train 1) of 3x3 or 3x4 cell tiles,
each cell 5x5 interior enclosed by a uniform-value border. The test input is
a 29x29 grid of 4x4 cell tiles. Exactly one cell per row section has a
unique interior pattern; the output isolates that cell's column section for
each row section. Score advances from 12/120 = 10.00% to 13/120 = 10.83%.

ARC2-W14-SPEC-001: The reflect_axis rule operates on a grid with a solid
background color (the mode of the grid), non-background non-2 colored shapes,
and clusters of 2-cells. Each non-background non-2 shape is reflected across
the axis defined by its nearest 2-cluster.

ARC2-W14-SPEC-002: Shapes are identified as 4-connected components of
non-background non-2 cells. The background color is the most frequent value
in the grid.

ARC2-W14-SPEC-003: 2-clusters are identified as 4-connected components of
cells with value 2. The axis type is determined by the cluster's geometry:
a single 2-cell defines a point reflection; a collinear column of 2-cells
defines a vertical axis; a collinear row of 2-cells defines a horizontal axis.

ARC2-W14-SPEC-004: Each shape is paired with the 2-cluster having the minimum
Manhattan distance from any shape cell to any cluster cell. This is the
nearest-cluster pairing.

ARC2-W14-SPEC-005: For point reflection through (R0, C0): each shape cell
(R, C) maps to (2*R0 - R, 2*C0 - C). For vertical axis at col C0: each
cell (R, C) maps to (R, 2*C0 - C). For horizontal axis at row R0: each cell
(R, C) maps to (2*R0 - R, C). Reflected cells outside grid bounds are skipped.

ARC2-W14-SPEC-006: The original shape cells and 2-markers are preserved in
the output. Only the reflected copies are added to the grid.

ARC2-W14-SPEC-007: reflect_axis solves ARC-AGI-2 task 7ed72f31. Train 0 is
an 18x18 grid with bg=1, four shapes, and four 2-clusters (including one
single-cell, one 4-cell vertical, one single-cell, one 5-cell horizontal).
Train 1 is 18x18 with bg=8, three shapes, and three 2-clusters (two 2-cell
vertical, one 4-cell horizontal). Score advances from 13/120 = 10.83% to
14/120 = 11.67%.

ARC2-W15-SPEC-001: period_repair solves ARC-AGI-2 tasks where inner sequences
(cells between wall markers in a row or column) follow a repeating period-P
pattern with a small number of deviating cells. The rule repairs those cells.

ARC2-W15-SPEC-002: The wall marker in a row or column is the first non-background
element. An inner segment is the cells strictly between the first and last
occurrence of the wall marker. Segments shorter than 5 cells are skipped.

ARC2-W15-SPEC-003: Period selection uses a support-threshold criterion. For each
candidate P in 2..N//2, the majority-vote base is computed for each residue
class mod P. The minimum support is the lowest fraction of cells in any residue
class that match the majority value. Only periods with minimum support >= 0.75
are accepted. Among accepted periods, the one with the fewest errors (1..3) is
chosen; ties are broken by smallest P.

ARC2-W15-SPEC-004: period_repair applies row repair first (repair every row),
then column repair via a transpose-repair-transpose pass (treat each column as
a row by transposing the grid).

ARC2-W15-SPEC-005: period_repair solves ARC-AGI-2 task 135a2760. Train 0 is
5x13 with bg=3 and wall=2; one row repair (period-2, 1 error). Train 1 is
21x22 with bg=4 and wall=2; nine row repairs (periods 2-4, 1-2 errors each).
Test is 29x29 with bg=8 and wall=3; nine column repairs (periods 2-6, 1-3
errors each). Score advances from 14/120 = 11.67% to 15/120 = 12.50%.

ARC2-W16-SPEC-001: legend_fill solves ARC-AGI-2 tasks where a compact lookup
table (the legend) embedded in the grid maps frame-border colors to fill colors.
Closed frames whose border color is a legend key have their enclosed interior
background cells filled with the corresponding value color.

ARC2-W16-SPEC-002: The legend is the longest solid 2xN or Nx2 rectangular block
of non-background cells in the grid where the two rows or columns are non-identical.
"Longest" means the dimension not equal to 2 is maximized. The non-identical
requirement distinguishes the legend from uniform frame-border segments.

ARC2-W16-SPEC-003: The key row or column of the legend is whichever contains
more colors that appear as frame-border colors in the grid. A frame-border color
is any non-background color C for which at least one enclosed background cell
exists (a cell not reachable from the grid boundary via 4-connected background
traversal). Ties are broken by treating the first row or column as the key.

ARC2-W16-SPEC-004: Enclosed background cells are found by flood-filling outward
from all boundary background cells (4-connected, background-only traversal).
Any background cell not reached is enclosed. For a key color K, the enclosed
cells assigned to K are those enclosed cells where every adjacent non-background
cell has color K (the cell is wholly inside a K-framed region).

ARC2-W16-SPEC-005: legend_fill solves ARC-AGI-2 task dbff022c. Train 0 is
12x12 with 3 frames (4-frame, 3-frame, 7-frame) and a 5-entry legend at rows
0-1, cols 7-11; 9 changes. Train 1 is 10x10 with 3 frames and a 4-entry column
legend at rows 0-3, cols 0-1; 6 changes. Train 2 is 4x15 with 2 frames and a
2-entry legend at rows 0-1, cols 1-2; 2 changes. Score advances from 15/120 =
12.50% to 16/120 = 13.33%.

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 17: frame_target rule specification (2026-06-28)
Rule name: frame_target. A small legend rectangle (border = solid color C,
interior dense with no background cells, at least one interior cell = 2)
encodes a movement direction. The 2-cell centroid relative to interior center
gives (Dr, Dc) in {-1,0,+1}^2. Each dot-4 inside the large irregular frame
of the same color C advances in direction (Dr, Dc) until one step before the
nearest C-colored wall. Diagonal movement uses a clip rule: stop if any of
(R+Dr,C), (R,C+Dc), (R+Dr,C+Dc) equals C. Task solved: 88e364bc.
Score: 16/120 = 13.33% -> 17/120 = 14.17%.

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 18: tip_escape rule specification (2026-06-28)
Rule name: tip_escape. Each grid contains shape components (8-connected non-background
color regions) that enclose marker components (different color, strictly smaller, bounding
box fully inside the shape bounding box). The shape has a tip: the unique single cell at
an extreme row or column (MinRow, MaxRow, MinCol, or MaxCol). In the output all marker
cells are removed and min(N_markers, dist_to_edge) new marker-color cells are placed just
past the tip, filling outward toward the nearest grid boundary. Escape direction: apex
detection first (tip with perpendicular diverging shape-cell arms), then projection method
(escape vector = shape_centroid - marker_centroid; choose the tip with the largest
projection onto this vector). 8-connectivity is required so diagonal-chain shapes and
concave shapes are identified correctly. Task solved: 3dc255db.
Score: 17/120 = 14.17% -> 18/120 = 15.00%.

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 19: segment_ext rule specification (2026-06-28)
Rule name: segment_ext. Each grid encodes a 2-color arm structure with special junction
cells: value 4 marks a "4-corner" where the stub arm ends and the opposite extension
emerges; value 2 marks an intermediate "2-corner" junction. Three phases: (1) for each
4-corner, remove the stub arm (contiguous + cascade + far segments beyond first gap with
no perpendicular connections), convert the 4-corner to the arm color, extend the arm
in the opposite direction to the grid boundary; (2) convert remaining 2-corners to the
adjacent arm color; (3) apply gap fill using H fill (both left and right same non-bg
color) and V fill (both above and below same non-bg color, with at least one being a
"pure vertical arm cell": no same-color horizontal neighbors). Fill priority (Prio) is
determined by 4-corner extension directions: Prio=none (no 4-corners, H wins H-vs-V
true conflicts and can overwrite non-bg frame cells), Prio=h (horizontal extension, H
wins true conflicts), Prio=v (vertical extension, V wins true conflicts). Existing
non-background arm cells are protected from H-fill overwrite in 4-corner grids (Prio
not none). Three correctness guards: (a) pure-vertical arm cell check prevents V fill
from bridging between separate horizontal arm segments sharing a column; (b) extension
direction tiebreaker resolves H-vs-V conflicts at background cells; (c) non-bg cell
protection prevents frame color from overwriting existing arm cells in 4-corner grids.
Task solved: faa9f03d. Score: 18/120 = 15.00% -> 19/120 = 15.83%.

iochan Pack Specification: I/O Channel Integration (ic_*, Layer 254, WP 279)

IOC-SPEC-001: The iochan pack (Layer 254) provides fourteen predicates for
dispatching information to and from concrete I/O channels: text output channels
(console, email, screen, app), text input channels, image output channels, image
input channels, audio output (speaker), audio input (microphone), and printer output.
The ic_* prefix distinguishes all iochan predicates from every other PrologAI pack.

IOC-SPEC-002: A channel is a named, typed configuration registered in the runtime
channel registry (ic_channel/3 dynamic fact). Channel types are: text_out, text_in,
image_out, image_in, audio_out, audio_in, printer. A channel configuration term
(config term) carries all implementation details; the channel ID is an opaque atom
generated by ic_register_channel/3.

IOC-SPEC-003: Configuration terms and their dispatch targets:
  console_config                 - system stdout (text out) or stdin (text in)
  email_config(Addr, Subject)    - SMTP via sendmail/mutt subprocess
  screen_config(WinId)           - X11 window via xdotool
  app_config(AppId, Endpoint)    - HTTP POST/GET to application endpoint
  speaker_config(DevId)          - audio playback via espeak-ng, festival fallback
  mic_config(DevId)              - audio capture via arecord + whisper-cli transcript
  file_config(Path)              - local file system path (image in)
  webcam_config(DevId)           - camera capture via fswebcam (image in)
  url_config(URL)                - URL download via wget (image in)
  printer_config(Name, Opts)     - CUPS lp command; empty Name uses default printer

IOC-SPEC-004: ic_text_out/3 dispatches text to a text-output channel. When the
channel is console_config, the text is written to stdout via writeln/1. For
email_config, the text is written to a temp file with To: and Subject: headers and
submitted via sendmail -t. For screen_config, xdotool types the text into the named
X11 window. For app_config, the text is HTTP-POSTed as a string body to the endpoint.

IOC-SPEC-005: ic_speak/2 synthesizes speech using espeak-ng as the primary TTS engine,
with festival as automatic fallback if espeak-ng is absent. ic_speak_to/3 routes speech
to a named audio-output channel carrying speaker_config(DevId); empty DevId uses the
system default device. ic_listen/2 and ic_listen_from/3 record audio for the specified
number of seconds using arecord, then transcribe the WAV using whisper-cli; duration 0
short-circuits immediately with an empty transcript.

IOC-SPEC-006: ic_image_out/3 sends an image file path to an image-output channel.
For console_config, img2txt renders an ASCII approximation; if img2txt is absent, the
file path is printed. For email_config, mutt sends the image as an attachment. For
screen_config, display (ImageMagick) renders the image in an X11 window. For app_config,
the raw image bytes are HTTP-POSTed as application/octet-stream. ic_image_in/2 captures
an image: file_config returns the path directly, webcam_config captures one frame via
fswebcam, url_config downloads via wget.

IOC-SPEC-007: ic_print_text/3 and ic_print_image/3 submit a text file or image file
to the CUPS lp command. printer_config(Name, Opts) selects the named CUPS queue; empty
Name uses the CUPS default destination. Opts is a list of lp -o option values.

IOC-SPEC-008: The channel registry ships with five default channels pre-registered at
module load time: console text-output, console text-input, console image-output, default
speaker, and default microphone. Any number of additional channels may be registered at
runtime with ic_register_channel/3.

IOC-SPEC-009: The iochan pack has no cross-pack dependencies. It uses only SWI-Prolog
standard libraries: library(lists), library(process), library(readutil). The
library(http/http_client) import is wrapped in a catch so iochan loads cleanly on
installations without the HTTP pack installed. All hardware-dependent operations degrade
gracefully: on missing external programs, Status = error(program_unavailable) is returned
rather than raising an exception.

IOC-SPEC-010: Architectural placement: iochan sits in the Data Layer at Layer 254,
above the periodfix pack (Layer 253). It is independent of the tooling pack (Layer
defined by WP 44); the tooling registry and invocation framework may wrap iochan channels
as tools using pai_tool_register/2, but iochan does not depend on tooling internally.

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 20: section_tile rule specification (2026-06-29)
Rule name: section_tile. The input grid is divided into rectangular sections by
all-1 rows (every cell in the row equals 1) and all-1 columns (every cell in
the column equals 1). Sections with only 0/1 cells are discarded. Non-trivial
sections are classified: the shape section (shape1) has at least one 0 cell and
at least two distinct non-zero values; all other non-trivial sections are solid
sections (uniform non-zero value). One solid section is shape2, which encodes
the tile count N as total non-zero cells // 2 (shape2 always contains a two-row
repeated base sub-pattern so the total is always 2*N). Remaining solid sections
are color indicators, one per output color, in section-position order. The inner
bounding box of shape1 (tightest bounds containing all non-zero cells) is tiled
N times along the dominant axis with color-2 separators between copies; each
non-zero inner cell is replaced by the corresponding color from the indicator
order. Early induction clause placement: arc2_induce_rule(section_tile) is
placed before arc2_induce_rule(frame_target) in the source file so that the
O(rows*cols) st_find_dividers_ guard fires before frame_target's O(k^2)
rectangle scan can exhaust the call_with_time_limit/2 budget.
Task solved: b0039139. Score: 19/120 = 15.83% -> 20/120 = 16.67%.

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 21: chain_link rule specification (2026-06-29)
Rule name: chain_link. The input grid contains rectangular box regions arranged
in a multi-row layout. Background color BG is detected from the top-left cell.
Box boundaries (BT,BB,BL,BR) = first BG-valued row/col going up/down/left/right
from any interior cell. A legend row alternates BG,V1,BG,V2,...,Vn giving the
connection chain. The rule walks the chain sequentially from a starting box:
at each step k, find an unvisited Vk+1-box sharing a col-block (same BL,BR) or
row-block (same BT,BB) with the current box, where the gap between them is all-BG
in the original grid (gap-clear check). Fill the gap with color Vk.
Gap extent: for vertical adjacency, connector rows = FRA+1..FLB-1 where FRA =
last non-BG row going from A's center toward B, FLB = last non-BG row going from
B's center toward A. Analogous formula for horizontal adjacency.
New predicates: cl_legend_/3, cl_alt_parse_/3, cl_boxes_/3, cl_bg_up_/5,
cl_bg_dn_/5, cl_bg_lt_/4, cl_bg_rt_/4, cl_link_chain_/5, cl_walk_/7, cl_step_/9,
cl_gap_clear_/6, cl_cr_/9, cl_inner_dn_/5, cl_inner_up_/5, cl_inner_rt_/5,
cl_inner_lt_/5, cl_apply_changes_/3, cl_new_row_/4, cl_new_cell_/5.
File: Mentova/src/mentova/games/arc_benchmark_2.pl
Task solved: 3e6067c3. Score: 20/120 = 16.67% -> 21/120 = 17.50%.

ARC-AGI-2 Wave 22: legend_veto rule specification (2026-06-29)
Rule name: legend_veto. The top-left 4x4 area of the grid is a legend frame
bordered by 3s on its right column (col 3, rows 0-3) and bottom row (row 3,
cols 0-3). The non-3, non-7, non-0 values inside this 4x4 area form the legend
set S. All 4-connected components of non-7 cells are found, ignoring color
differences (any non-7 cell is part of a component). Components that overlap the
legend area (any cell with row <= 3 AND col <= 3) are excluded from processing.
Each remaining data component is checked: if its value set (all non-7, non-0
colors present in the component) is a superset of S, the entire component is
erased by replacing all its cells with 7; otherwise the component is kept
unchanged.
New predicates: arc2_lv_legend_set_/2, arc2_lv_is_leg_comp_/1,
arc2_lv_any_comps_/3, arc2_lv_comps_/5, arc2_lv_bfs_/7,
arc2_lv_comp_vals_/4, arc2_lv_all_in_/2, arc2_lv_erase_comp_/4.
File: Mentova/src/mentova/games/arc_benchmark_2.pl
Task solved: d59b0160. Score: 21/120 = 17.50% -> 22/120 = 18.33%.
